# M10b Phase 9 — Cluster Synthesis — structural input

**Date:** 2026-05-25
**Cluster:** M10b — Wickedness, Evil and Abomination

---

## §1 — Cluster overview

M10b (Wickedness, Evil and Abomination) holds 6 inner-being characteristics:

| Char | Short name | One-line definition |
|---:|---|---|
| 1 | Wickedness as settled person-identity | The wicked person as an inner-being type — the individual whose core moral character is defined by wickedness. |
| 2 | Evil as constitutional inner nature | Evil as the structural condition of the inner person — not primarily the choice of the will moment by moment, but the constitutive nature from which corrupt choices flow. |
| 3 | Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character | The category of evil that violates divine holiness and provokes God's active revulsion — directed specifically at corrupt moral character and ethical failure rather than idolatry. |
| 4 | Idolatrous abomination | The specific form of abomination rooted in idolatrous devotion — the will's conformity to detestable practices, the heart going after idol-objects, worship corrupted through false devotion. |
| 5 | Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation | Evil as an ongoing active inner process — devised, cultivated, generated, and enacted from within. |
| 6 | Evil expressed through speech | The inner character of wickedness expressed through the instrument of speech — the defiant will that generates contemptuous blasphemy against God even under judgment, the hostile slander that falsely charges the innocent as evildoers, the deceptive misrepresentation that inverts moral reality through verbal manipulation. |

Each characteristic produced 189 findings in its Phase 9 Stage A batch (1134 rows total in `cluster_finding`).

---

## §2 — Open cluster observations (raised at Phase 8.7)

These 3 observations were raised at characteristic-mapping time and link to VCG-level polysemy splits / cross-register signals from Phase 7. All remain `status='open'`; the Stage B synthesis should address each (confirm or refine).

### Observation #80 — INTEGRATION_NOTE (linked to Char 47)

**Title:** ra.sha forensic-verdict register — VCG-level cross-register signal

**Description:**

> M10b-A-VCG-01 (5V — Exo 23:7, Deu 25:1, 25:2, 1Ki 8:32, 2Ch 6:23) carries ra.sha as a legal-status label in forensic/judicial contexts ('the wicked = the legally condemnable') rather than naming inner moral character. Phase 9 T6 (Structural Relationships) findings should attend to this M10 (act-of-moral-failure) cross-register relationship. The VCG is structurally separated from the inner-moral-character VCGs within M10b-A.

---

### Observation #81 — INTEGRATION_NOTE (linked to Char 48)

**Title:** ponēros cosmic-evil-agent sub-corpus — VCG-level cross-register signal

**Description:**

> M10b-B-VCG-01 (13V — Mat 13:19, 13:38, Joh 17:15, Eph 6:16, 2Th 3:3, 1Jn 2:13, 2:14, 5:18, 5:19, Gal 1:4, Eph 5:16, 6:13, and Eph 6:12 ponēria) carries the 'evil one' / 'evil age' / cosmic-evil-agent register — supra-personal evil rather than the personal constitutional-evil register of the remaining ~77 VCG-2/3/4/5/6 verses. Phase 9 T6 findings should attend to this M27 (idolatry/cosmic-evil/concrete-evil) cross-register relationship. The VCG is structurally separated within M10b-B.

---

### Observation #82 — INTEGRATION_NOTE (linked to Char 51)

**Title:** a.ven trouble-suffered sub-corpus — VCG-level cross-register signal

**Description:**

> M10b-E-VCG-01 (7V) carries a.ven in the trouble/distress/affliction-suffered register — the harm that befalls the victim rather than the iniquity-scheming of the agent. Phase 9 T6 findings should attend to the M03 (grief/sorrow) and M27 (calamity/ruin) cross-register relationships. The VCG is structurally separated from the iniquity-scheming and evil-deeds VCGs within M10b-E. (The brief estimated ~18V for this sub-corpus; the AI's per-verse read identified 7 cleaner trouble-register cases.)

## §3 — Per-prompt synthesis matrix

For each of the 189 prompts (T0.1.1 … T7.3.4), all 6 characteristics' findings are stacked verbatim below. Read all 6 before authoring the cluster-scope row in your output.

### T0

#### T0.1 — Divine Nature Reflected

##### T0.1.1 — What does the verse evidence reveal about the nature or character of God that this characteristic reflects or images?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Wickedness as settled person-identity is definitionally structured against the divine nature rather than derived from it. Job 34:10 states explicitly that it is "far be it from God that he should do wickedness, and from the Almighty that he should do wrong" (re.sha) — God's nature is declared the absolute structural opposite of what wickedness names. This structural opposition is the primary theological datum: wickedness does not reflect or image any divine attribute; it reveals the divine character by negation and contrast. Psa 11:5 reinforces this — "his soul hates the wicked" — establishing that wickedness is specifically the object of divine loathing, not a divine attribute. What the evidence reveals about God through this characteristic is therefore apophatic: God's righteousness, justice, and wholeness are defined in part by their absolute incompatibility with the inner orientation that wickedness describes. The wicked person is the anti-image of what God is, and the universe of 190 verses sustains this polarity throughout.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Evil as constitutional inner nature is definitionally opposed to God's nature rather than derived from it. Rom 9:14 (vc=65872 — VCG-06) poses and immediately rejects the charge of unrighteousness (adikia) against God — divine sovereign choice is explicitly not constitutionally evil. The verse establishes that God's nature is the structural antithesis of constitutional inner evil. Rom 12:9 (vc=14417 — VCG-06) commands the community to "abhor what is evil" — this command reflects the divine moral character that stands against evil as constitutional nature. 1Cor 13:6 (vc=14341 — VCG-06) frames love (the divine character) as refusing to "rejoice at wrongdoing" — unrighteousness is what love's opposite produces. The evidence collectively reveals God as constitutionally righteous and the human constitutional evil as an inversion of that righteousness.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The characteristic reveals God's nature primarily through the divine response: active revulsion, loathing, and rejection directed at specific inner moral conditions. Pro 6:16 (vc=65952 — VCG-05) frames God as the one who "hates" and finds "abomination" in seven specific attitudes and acts — establishing that God's holiness is not merely a passive state of purity but an active repugnance toward moral corruption. Pro 3:32 (vc=1686 — VCG-02) contrasts the abomination of the devious person with divine intimacy: "the devious person is an abomination to the Lord, but the upright are in his confidence" — revealing that God's moral character involves both rejection of the crooked and intimate sharing with the upright. Pro 11:20 (vc=1677 — VCG-01) and Pro 16:5 (vc=1689 — VCG-02) confirm that God's revulsion is specifically directed at inner-being conditions (crooked heart, arrogant heart). Luk 16:15 (vc=21 — VCG-02) reveals that what humans exalt as admirable is an abomination in God's sight — God's evaluative standard is categorically different from human social evaluation. The evidence collectively reveals God as morally sensitive at the inner-being level, responding to the quality of the heart with either revulsion or delight.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Idolatrous abomination reveals God's character primarily through the divine-jealousy and divine-exclusivity dimensions: God is a moral being whose holiness cannot coexist with false devotion. Deu 32:16 (vc=65938 — VCG-02): "They stirred him to jealousy with strange gods; with abominations they provoked him to anger" — the divine response is jealousy and anger, revealing that God's character includes a morally serious covenantal exclusivity that is violated by idolatrous attachment. Eze 5:11 (vc=65969 — VCG-05): because the sanctuary was defiled with abominations "I will withdraw. My eye will not spare, and I will have no pity" — God's holiness is incompatible with idolatrous defilement; the divine presence is forced to withdraw. Jer 44:4 (vc=65966 — VCG-04): "do not do this abomination that I hate" — God's character involves intense moral hatred of idolatrous devotion. The evidence reveals God as a relational being whose holiness is covenantally exclusive — he cannot share devotion with idol-objects without responding with jealousy, anger, and withdrawal.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The characteristic reveals God's nature primarily through the divine response to iniquity as an active inner process: God perceives, hates, and judges it. Psa 5:5 (vc=38237 — VCG-03): "you hate all evildoers" — God's active moral hatred is directed at those whose inner character is constituted by the working of iniquity; the hating is not passive disapproval but a settled divine stance toward those who persistently generate evil from within. Job 11:11 (vc=38206 — VCG-04): "For he knows worthless men; when he sees iniquity, will he not consider it?" — God perceives and registers iniquity even when hidden from others, revealing his character as omniscient moral witness. Psa 94:23 (vc=38249 — VCG-03): "He will bring back on them their iniquity and wipe them out for their wickedness" — God's character includes active retributive justice that returns the inner scheming of iniquity upon those who practise it. The evidence reveals God as the moral pole against which active inner scheming is measured and judged.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The characteristic reveals God's nature primarily through what the characteristic attacks: God's name, his dwelling, and his glory — the very realities that blasphemy targets. Rev 13:6 (vc=14356 — VCG-01): the beast "opened its mouth to utter blasphemies against God, blaspheming his name and his dwelling, that is, those who dwell in heaven" — God's name and dwelling are the specific objects of blasphemous contempt, revealing God as a named, dwelling, glory-bearing being whose character and presence are the pole against which defiant speech defines itself. Rev 16:9 (vc=14352 — VCG-01): "they cursed the name of God who had power over these plagues. They did not repent and give him glory" — the withheld glory reveals that God's character warrants and invites glory; blasphemy is precisely the refusal to render what is due. Rom 2:24 (vc=14357 — VCG-02): God's name is "blasphemed among the Gentiles" — his name exists to be honoured and known, not dishonoured. The characteristic reveals God as the morally serious, glory-bearing, name-holding personal being whose honour is the target of evil expressed through speech.

---

##### T0.1.2 — Does Scripture explicitly attribute this characteristic to God — and if so, what does that attribution reveal about its significance in the human person?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Scripture explicitly and forcefully denies this characteristic to God. Job 34:10 declares God incapable of wickedness (re.sha); Psa 36:1 portrays transgression as speaking within the wicked person "deep in his heart" while "there is no fear of God before his eyes" — structuring the wicked person's inner life as the space where God is absent. The absence of attribution to God is analytically significant: it means wickedness as settled person-identity is a purely creaturely failure-mode, with no divine analogue. Its significance in the human person is therefore as a measure of departure from the divine pattern — the further the inner person is from God (Psa 36:1; Mal 3:18 defines the wicked as "one who does not serve him"), the more completely this characteristic defines them.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Scripture explicitly denies constitutional inner evil to God. Rom 9:14 (vc=65872 — VCG-06) raises and immediately rejects the charge: "Is there injustice on God's part? By no means!" The denial is forceful and categorical. Heb 8:12 (vc=14342 — VCG-06) contrasts God's mercy toward human iniquities ("I will remember their sins no more") with the human constitutional condition — God stands over against human constitutional evil as the one who covers it by grace, not as one who shares it. The evidence is entirely consistent: constitutional inner evil is attributed exclusively to humans (Mat 7:11: "you who are evil"; Luk 11:13: the same), never to God.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Scripture does not attribute the experience of being abominable to God — God is not the one who becomes an abomination. But Scripture does explicitly attribute the response-side of the characteristic to God: God is the primary agent of the revulsion that names and constitutes something as abominable. Pro 8:7 (vc=65953 — VCG-02): "wickedness is an abomination to my lips" — spoken in Wisdom's voice, implying a divine-moral faculty of revulsion. Pro 11:1 (vc=65954 — VCG-01): "a false balance is an abomination to the Lord" — God's reaction is the defining standard. The divine attribution reveals that the characteristic's constitutive element (the revulsion response) is divine in origin: what makes something an abomination is specifically God's active moral response to it. This is analytically significant — the characteristic is not self-certifying in the human sphere but is defined by reference to the divine inner response. God's revulsion is the measure.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Scripture explicitly denies this characteristic to God: the divine cannot become an idolater or be abominable. However, Scripture does attribute God's intense revulsion-response to the characteristic: Jer 44:4 (vc=65966 — VCG-04): "this abomination that I hate" — God's hatred of idolatrous abomination is directly stated. Deu 12:31 (vc=1683 — VCG-02): "every abominable thing that the Lord hates they have done for their gods" — the Lord's hatred is the defining relational context within which idolatrous abomination is identified. Deu 7:25 (vc=1682 — VCG-02): idols are "an abomination to the Lord your God" — the relational identity of God is the standard. The non-attribution of the characteristic to God reveals that idolatrous attachment is exclusively a creaturely failure — the creature who was designed to give exclusive devotion to God has redirected that devotion to created objects. God's own character (exclusive, morally serious, jealous for undivided allegiance) is the positive standard against which idolatrous abomination is measured.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Scripture explicitly denies iniquity to God. Isa 55:7 (vc=38200 — VCG-02): the unrighteous man is called to forsake "his thoughts" and "return to the Lord" — the Lord is the party toward whom the iniquity-shaped person must turn; God is the structural opposite of the iniquity-scheming inner life. Psa 66:18 (vc=38182 — VCG-04): "If I had cherished iniquity in my heart, the Lord would not have listened" — the conditional structure implies that God, as the one who listens, is characterised by the absence of cherished iniquity. Psa 5:5 (vc=38237 — VCG-03): God hates evildoers — the hating posture is the divine stance against what God does not possess. The non-attribution reveals that iniquity as active inner scheming is exclusively a creaturely failure — specifically, the misuse of the mind, heart, and will faculties that God designed for generation of good.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Scripture does not attribute blasphemy or defamatory evil speech to God. God is consistently the object of blasphemy (Rev 13:6; 16:9; 16:11; 16:21 — VCG-01) and the one whose name is blasphemed by others' conduct (Rom 2:24 — VCG-02), never its subject. The non-attribution is emphatic: the entire VCG-01 corpus (6V) positions God as the one against whom defiant blasphemy is directed. This active non-attribution reveals that the characteristic is the polar inversion of the speech that God's nature calls forth — which is worship, glory, and honest testimony. Attributing evil speech to God would be a logical impossibility in the evidence's framework: God cannot blaspheme himself. The silence reveals the characteristic as exclusively creaturely, specifically as the misuse of the creaturely speech-faculty that was designed for truthful testimony about and toward God.

---

##### T0.1.3 — Where Scripture is silent about God's possession of this characteristic, what does that silence suggest about the characteristic's place in the divine image?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Scripture is not silent but actively declarative on this point (Job 34:10). Nevertheless, the analytical question about the divine image remains important: because wickedness-as-settled-person-identity is constitutionally absent from God, it cannot be an aspect of the divine image that the human is designed to reflect. The verse evidence suggests that the human capacity for this characteristic represents a corruption or inversion of the image, not an expression of it. Psa 9:17 defines the wicked by their forgetting of God; Gen 18:23–25 presupposes that wickedness and righteousness are distinct moral statuses that map onto just and unjust outcomes respectively — the whole structure presupposes a divine moral order the wicked person violates. Wickedness-as-settled-identity is therefore the image-bearer in a state of image-corruption or image-inversion.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Scripture is not merely silent but actively declarative in opposing this characteristic to God (T0.1.2). The analytical significance: evil as constitutional inner nature belongs exclusively to the creaturely sphere as a post-creation failure-condition. Its absence from God is not accidental silence but the positive ground from which the characteristic's seriousness is assessed. That humans are "constitutionally evil" (Mat 7:11 — VCG-02) while God is not means the characteristic represents the precise site where creaturely nature has departed from its original orientation toward the divine. The silence about God's possession is the theological ground for why the characteristic requires transformation (Act 3:26 — VCG-05 — turning from wickedness through divine blessing).

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Scripture is not silent but actively declarative: God is the one who reviles, not the one who is reviled. The relevant silence concerns the human experience of being abominable to oneself — the characteristic's subjective inner dimension is almost entirely framed from the divine-perspective side (what God finds abominable) rather than as a first-person inner experience of the abominable person. Where the human inner experience does appear — Eze 36:31 (vc=1681 — VCG-04): "you will loathe yourselves for your iniquities and your abominations" — it appears as an awakened human conscience finally registering the divine verdict. The silence about God possessing the experience of abomination (being repugnant) reveals the characteristic as a purely creaturely failure-condition: God has no moral corruption that would make him abominable. What God has is the morally sensitive faculty of revulsion that names and responds to abomination in the creature.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Scripture is not silent but actively declarative (T0.1.2): God hates idolatrous abomination rather than possessing it. The silence about God's possession reveals the characteristic as the inversion of the designed God-devotion faculty in the human person. The human person was created with the capacity for exclusive devotion — a capacity designed for God. When that capacity is attached to idol-objects, idolatrous abomination results. God's non-possession of the characteristic is the negative space that defines the characteristic: what makes idolatry an abomination is precisely that the devotion-faculty is attached to what is not God. The silence about God possessing false devotion confirms that CHAR-4 is constitutively a departure from the relational orientation the created human was designed for.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Scripture is actively declarative (T0.1.2) rather than merely silent. God is consistently positioned as the moral authority who perceives, hates, and judges iniquity rather than as one who possesses it. The silence about God scheming iniquity reveals the characteristic as the image-bearer's misuse of the generative inner capacities (mind devising, heart conceiving, will executing) that are meant to produce what is good. Isa 32:6 (vc=38181 — VCG-02): "his heart is busy with iniquity" — the heart's busyness with iniquity names the corruption of a generative capacity; the divine image designed human persons with generative inner faculties precisely so that good could be conceived and enacted from within. The silence about God plotting trouble on beds or conceiving mischief (Psa 7:14 — vc=38245 — VCG-02; Psa 36:4 — vc=38235 — VCG-02) names the characteristic as the inversion of what those faculties were for.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Scripture is not merely silent but actively declarative (T0.1.2): God is the target of blasphemy, not its agent. The silence about God speaking evil through speech reveals the characteristic as the inversion of the image-bearing speech-capacity. The human person as image-bearer was equipped with speech specifically to name, testify, and render glory to God and to represent reality truthfully. Evil expressed through speech — blasphemy, slander, false accusation — inverts every dimension of that design. Rom 14:16 (vc=14359 — VCG-02): "do not let what you regard as good be spoken of as evil" — the possibility of good being spoken of as evil presupposes that speech was designed to name good as good; the inversion is the failure of the image-bearing speech-function.

---

#### T0.2 — Created Purpose

##### T0.2.1 — What does the verse evidence suggest about the purpose this characteristic serves in the human person as created — what does it equip the person to be, do, or become?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (S)

The evidence does not address what purpose wickedness as settled person-identity serves in the originally created human. This is analytically appropriate: the characteristic as defined is a settled inner orientation of moral corruption, which the evidence consistently presents as a failure-mode of creation, not a designed capacity. No verse in the corpus suggests that wickedness was part of original design or serves a constructive anthropological function. The evidence is silent about creative purpose precisely because wickedness-as-settled-identity is a description of the person after their inner orientation has turned against the created order. The purpose-question is not posed by the evidence; the evidence's universal testimony is that wickedness leads to instability, destruction, and divine judgment — not to any designed end.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (S)

The evidence does not address what purpose evil as constitutional inner nature serves in the originally created human. This is analytically expected: the characteristic is framed throughout as a post-creation condition from which humans need deliverance (Gal 1:4 — VCG-01: "deliver us from the present evil age"), transformation (Act 3:26 — VCG-05), and purging (1Cor 5:8 — VCG-05; 1Pe 2:1 — VCG-05). No verse in the 90-verse corpus presents this characteristic as serving a designed purpose. The evidence's consistent framing is remedial — the characteristic is what must be removed, not what was designed to be there.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (S)

The evidence does not address what purpose abomination as a category of inner moral failure serves in the originally designed human. The characteristic is framed entirely as a judgment on fallen moral conditions — the devious heart, the arrogant heart, dishonest commerce, silenced conscience — not as a designed element. The evidence's consistent framing is diagnostic and prophylactic: it names what is repugnant to God so that people may be warned away from it (Pro 6:16-19 listing the seven; the Proverbs antithetical contrasts). The purpose served by the characteristic in the created human is absent from the evidence — the evidence concerns what must be avoided and what happens when it is not, not what designed function it serves.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (S)

The evidence does not address what purpose idolatrous abomination serves in the originally created human. The characteristic is framed entirely as a corruption of the devotion-capacity that was designed for God: Deu 18:9 (vc=65931 — VCG-02): Israel is warned "not to learn to follow the abominable practices of those nations" — the framing is protective and remedial. Eze 37:23 (vc=65913 — VCG-05): restoration includes removing detestable things and abominations — the characteristic is what must be removed for restoration to occur, not what was designed. No verse presents idolatrous abomination as serving a positive designed function.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (S)

The evidence does not address what purpose iniquity as active inner scheming serves in the originally created human. The characteristic is consistently framed as a departure from, and inversion of, designed inner capacities rather than as a designed function. Psa 119:133 (vc=38227 — VCG-04): "let no iniquity get dominion over me" — the prayer against dominion presupposes that iniquity's dominion is an unwanted deviation from a right inner state, not an intended capacity. The evidence contains no verse presenting active inner scheming as serving a positive original-design purpose.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (S)

The evidence does not address what purpose evil speech serves in the originally created human. The characteristic is entirely framed as a departure from and corruption of the designed speech-capacity: the evidence describes blasphemy as what the hardened will generates under judgment (Rev 16:9/11/21 — VCG-01), as what false accusation does to the innocent (1Pe 2:12 — VCG-03), and as what conduct-caused dishonour does to God's name (Rom 2:24 — VCG-02). No verse presents evil expressed through speech as serving a positive designed function. This is explicitly noted.

---

##### T0.2.2 — Does the evidence indicate whether this characteristic is part of the original created design, a response to the fallen condition, or both?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The evidence consistently positions wickedness-as-settled-person-identity as a condition of the fallen human, not the original created design. The proverb "out of the wicked comes wickedness" (1Sa 24:13 — vc=42648) treats wickedness as an inner source from which corresponding actions inevitably flow, but without attributing this orientation to original design. Eze 18:20–27 (M10b-A-VCG-07) addresses wickedness as a volitional orientation the will has taken and can reverse — its reversibility implies it is not constitutionally fixed by creation. The question of how wickedness entered the inner person is not directly addressed in this corpus (that belongs to M10/sin-act clusters); what is evidenced is the condition in its settled form. The corpus addresses the wicked person as an existing type, not as an explanation of human origins.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The evidence presents evil as constitutional inner nature as a condition of fallen humanity, not the original created design. Mat 7:11 (vc=14438 — VCG-02) states "you who are evil" as a present fact about humans while simultaneously showing them capable of giving good gifts — the tension implies a baseline condition that is not original design but fallen reality. Mat 7:17-18 (vc=14439, 14440 — VCG-02) frames the diseased tree as the state the tree is in, not its designed condition. Tit 3:3 (vc=14367 — VCG-05) describes the former inner life as passing "days in malice and envy" and then being transformed by divine grace — the "former" framing implies a condition that can be and was departed from. The evidence consistently positions the characteristic as the fallen condition from which grace rescues, not a designed element.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The evidence presents abomination as a category of fallen moral failure, not original design. The Proverbs evidence identifies specific inner-being conditions that are abominable: the crooked heart (Pro 11:20 — VCG-01), the arrogant heart (Pro 16:5 — VCG-02), thoughts of the wicked (Pro 15:26 — VCG-02) — all of which presuppose a departure from an intended inner orientation. The conscience evidence (VCG-04 — Jer 6:15; Jer 8:12; Eze 9:4; Eze 36:31) shows a faculty (conscience) that should respond to abomination with shame and grief but has in some cases been wholly silenced — the designed conscience reacting to abomination is the original equipment; the silence of conscience is the fallen deviation. The characteristic therefore describes conditions that arise within the fallen human inner life, not conditions designed into the original person.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The evidence consistently presents idolatrous abomination as a fallen condition, not original design. Deu 7:26 (vc=65927 — VCG-02): bringing an abominable thing into the house "makes you devoted to destruction like it" — the contaminating quality of idolatrous abomination is a consequence of a volitional choice in the fallen condition, not an original design element. Eze 37:23 (vc=65913 — VCG-05): God will "cleanse them" from their detestable things and abominations — the divine cleansing implies these are departures from the intended condition, not original features. Hos 9:10 (vc=1632 — VCG-04): the people "consecrated themselves to the thing of shame, and became detestable like the thing they loved" — the transformation from the original condition ("like grapes in the wilderness, I found Israel") to the abominable state through attachment to idols shows a trajectory of departure, not of original design.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The evidence presents iniquity as active inner scheming as a fallen condition, not original design. Job 15:35 (vc=38208 — VCG-02): "they conceive trouble and give birth to evil, and their womb prepares deceit" — the generative metaphor of conceiving and birthing iniquity from within describes a faculty (the inner womb) that generates corruption; the faculty of inner generation is designed; its corrupt output is the fallen deviation. Isa 55:7 (vc=38200 — VCG-02): the call to "forsake his thoughts" and "return to the Lord" positions iniquity-shaped thoughts as a departure requiring return, not as original endowment. Job 36:21 (vc=38216 — VCG-04): "do not turn to iniquity, for this you have chosen rather than affliction" — the volitional choice framing confirms the characteristic as a departure freely chosen in the fallen condition.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The evidence presents evil expressed through speech as entirely a fallen condition, not original design. Jude 10 (vc=14355 — VCG-01): "these people blaspheme all that they do not understand, and they are destroyed by all that they, like unreasoning animals, understand instinctively" — the comparison to unreasoning animals shows the characteristic as a regression below the designed rational-moral speech capacity. Rev 16:9/11/21 (VCG-01): the hardened will's response to divine judgment is defiant blasphemy — this is not a designed response but the terminal expression of the fallen will's resistance to God. The characteristic presupposes and corrupts speech as a designed human capacity; the corruption is the fallen condition, not the design.

---

##### T0.2.3 — Is there evidence that this characteristic is oriented toward a future fullness — something the person is moving toward, not only what they currently are?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The evidence orients wickedness-as-settled-person-identity toward a future state, but that future state is one of judgment and termination rather than fullness. The Ezekiel corpus (M10b-A-VCG-07) repeatedly depicts wickedness as a "way" heading toward death (Eze 3:18; 33:8; 33:11). Psa 37:10 states "in just a little while, the wicked will be no more." Job 20:5 notes "the exulting of the wicked is short." Dan 12:10 describes the wicked acting wickedly and being unable to understand, while the wise are refined — pointing to an eschatological bifurcation. The trajectory of wickedness-as-settled-identity is therefore toward exhaustion and dissolution, not forward fullness. The one counter-note is the Ezekiel repentance sequence: Eze 18:21–27 and 33:12–19 show that the wicked person can turn from this trajectory, which opens a different future — but that future belongs to the characteristic's reversal, not its completion.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The evidence orients evil as constitutional inner nature toward dissolution and termination rather than positive fullness. 2Ti 3:13 (vc=14451 — VCG-06) describes evil people moving "from bad to worse" — a downward trajectory, not a forward fullness. Mat 13:49 (vc=14459 — VCG-04) names the eschatological separation of the evil from the righteous — their future is separation from the righteous community, not a positive eschatological destination. The characteristic's future is anticipated only in terms of removal and judgment. The one counter-trajectory is in the evidence's consistent call for departure from the characteristic: Act 3:26 (VCG-05 — turning from wickedness), Jam 1:21 (VCG-05 — putting away rampant wickedness), Eph 4:31 (VCG-05 — putting away malice) — these envision a human future in which the constitutional inner evil is replaced, not fulfilled.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The evidence orients the characteristic toward eschatological exclusion rather than forward fullness. Rev 21:27 (vc=22 — VCG-05): "nothing unclean will ever enter it, nor anyone who does what is detestable or false, but only those who are written in the Lamb's book of life" — the eschatological end-state is one in which abomination is permanently excluded from the divine presence. The trajectory of the characteristic is toward final separation, not toward a positive fulfillment. Rev 17:5 (vc=65878 — VCG-05): the identity constituted by generating abominations ends in judgment. The one redemptive trajectory in the evidence is Eze 36:31 (vc=1681 — VCG-04): restored memory producing self-loathing, which is the conscience-awakening that enables repentance — but that trajectory moves toward departure from the characteristic, not its fulfillment.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The evidence orients idolatrous abomination toward eschatological judgment and removal rather than positive fullness. Dan 9:27 (vc=65914 — VCG-06): the abomination that brings desolation is an eschatological event leading to decreed judgment — "until the decreed end is poured out on the desolator." Dan 12:11 (vc=65916 — VCG-06): the abomination that makes desolate is set up at a specific apocalyptic moment pointing toward final judgment. The redemptive trajectory (Eze 37:23 — VCG-05: "they shall not defile themselves anymore… I will save them… and will cleanse them") points toward a future where the characteristic is entirely removed, not fulfilled. The eschatological trajectory is toward removal and restoration, not toward the characteristic's completion or fullness.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The evidence orients iniquity as active scheming toward eventual irrecoverable ruin rather than any positive fullness. Psa 36:12 (vc=38233 — VCG-04): "There the evildoers lie fallen; they are thrust down, unable to rise" — the trajectory ends in total and permanent collapse. Psa 92:7 (vc=38246 — VCG-03): "though the wicked sprout like grass and all evildoers flourish, they are doomed to destruction forever" — apparent flourishing precedes inevitable destruction. Psa 94:23 (vc=38249 — VCG-03): "He will bring back on them their iniquity and wipe them out" — the iniquity returns on the schemer as judgment. The trajectory of the characteristic is toward its own undoing: the scheming generates ruin for the schemer. No verse presents the characteristic as moving toward a positive fullness.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The evidence orients the characteristic toward eschatological judgment and elimination rather than positive fullness. Rom 3:8 (vc=14358 — VCG-02): "their condemnation is just" — the slanderous misrepresentation carries a certain future condemnation. Rev 16:9-21 (VCG-01): the hardened blasphemers under eschatological judgment — scorched, in pain, struck by hailstones — with no repentance, only continued cursing: the trajectory terminates in destruction without reversal. 1Pe 2:12 (vc=14377 — VCG-03): those who falsely accuse believers as evildoers "may see your good deeds and glorify God on the day of visitation" — the day of visitation brings the false accusation's end and the reversal of the defamation. The characteristic's eschatological fullness is judgment and exposure, not any positive future state.

---

#### T0.3 — Image-Bearer Expression

##### T0.3.1 — In what way does this characteristic express the divine image in the human person — what aspect of being made in God's likeness does it instantiate?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Wickedness-as-settled-person-identity does not express the divine image; it suppresses and corrupts it. The evidence from M10b-A-VCG-02 (practical atheism) is definitional: Psa 10:4 describes the wicked person whose "every thought is 'There is no God'" — the most direct inversion of the image-bearing faculty by which the human is constitutionally oriented toward God. Psa 36:1 shows transgression speaking within the wicked person as an internal voice displacing the fear of God. Mal 3:18 defines the wicked as those who "do not serve him." The divine image in the human is corrupted precisely where the wicked person suppresses the God-directed orientation of their inner life. What the image-bearer was designed to be — morally directed toward God, capable of justice and righteousness — is inverted in the wicked person. The evidence does not suggest any positive expression of the divine image through wickedness; the characteristic is the image in suppression.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Evil as constitutional inner nature does not express the divine image — it suppresses and corrupts it. Heb 3:12 (vc=14423 — VCG-06) defines an evil heart as an unbelieving heart "leading you to fall away from the living God" — this is the image-bearing person moving away from God, the inverse of the image's orientation. Col 1:21 (vc=14424 — VCG-06) names the condition as "hostile in mind" and "doing evil deeds" — the mind, which in the image-bearing human should be oriented toward God, is here alienated. Mat 6:23 (vc=14458 — VCG-03) names the corrupted eye flooding the whole inner being with darkness — the perceptive faculty through which the image-bearer apprehends God is darkened. The characteristic represents the divine image in a state of corruption at the constitutional level — not expressing but suppressing it.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Abomination as a category of moral failure does not express the divine image — it violates it. The evidence consistently frames the abominable inner conditions as antithetical to the relational intimacy with God that image-bearing enables: Pro 3:32 (vc=1686 — VCG-02) explicitly contrasts the devious person as abomination (excluded from divine confidence) with the upright who are in God's confidence — the image-bearing relational intimacy is foreclosed by the abominable inner condition. Rev 21:27 (vc=22 — VCG-05) names the abominable as permanently excluded from the city of the divine presence — the characteristic represents the image-bearer in a state of incompatibility with the God in whose image they were made. Luk 16:15 (vc=21 — VCG-02): what humans exalt (self-justifying pride) is abomination in God's sight — the characteristic marks the inversion of the image's proper orientation from God-exalting to self-exalting.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Idolatrous abomination does not express the divine image — it inverts it. The human person as image-bearer was created with a devotion-capacity oriented toward God. Eze 11:21 (vc=1631 — VCG-05): "those whose heart goes after their detestable things and their abominations" — the heart, which as image-bearer should go after God, goes after idol-objects. Isa 66:3 (vc=1633 — VCG-04): "their soul delights in their abominations" — the soul's delight faculty, designed for the divine, is attached to what is abominable. Hos 9:10 (vc=1632 — VCG-04): "they became detestable like the thing they loved" — the image-bearing person was shaped by what they devoted themselves to, but that shaping produced abomination rather than image-likeness to God. The characteristic reveals the image-bearing faculties (heart, soul, devotion-capacity) redirected away from God toward created objects, producing a corrupted image.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Iniquity as active inner scheming does not express the divine image — it inverts and corrupts the generative inner faculties that are image-bearing capacities. Psa 7:14 (vc=38245 — VCG-02): "the wicked man conceives evil and is pregnant with mischief and gives birth to lies" — the conception, gestation, and birth metaphor names precisely the generative inner faculty that, as an image-bearing capacity, should generate good from within. Job 15:35 (vc=38208 — VCG-02): "they conceive trouble and give birth to evil, and their womb prepares deceit" — the inner womb as generative centre is present and active, but its output is iniquity rather than good. The characteristic reveals the image-bearing generative faculty (heart and mind as creative-moral producers) operating in the wrong direction: producing scheming and harm instead of good plans and righteous deeds.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Evil expressed through speech does not express the divine image — it corrupts the speech-faculty that is the primary image-bearing capacity for naming, testifying, and rendering glory. Rev 16:9 (vc=14352 — VCG-01): people under judgment "did not repent and give him glory" — the withholding of glory through defiant blasphemy is the antithesis of the image-bearer's speech-function (to glorify God). 1Pe 2:12 (vc=14377 — VCG-03): false accusation of the innocent as evildoers shows the image-bearing testimony-capacity (to name moral reality accurately) inverted to produce false testimony. Rom 2:24 (vc=14357 — VCG-02): God's name blasphemed because of believers' moral failure — the image-bearer whose conduct should honour God's name instead dishonours it. The characteristic reveals the image-bearing speech-capacity operating in reverse: naming wrongly, testifying falsely, defying rather than glorifying.

---

##### T0.3.2 — Does the evidence suggest that this characteristic is shared between God and the human person, or is it exclusively a creaturely analogue to something in God?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The evidence is unambiguous: wickedness-as-settled-person-identity is exclusively a creaturely failure-state with no divine analogue and no creaturely-analogue relationship to God. Job 34:10 forecloses any shared possession. The closest the evidence comes to a divine parallel is in God's response to wickedness — his loathing of the wicked (Psa 11:5), his refusal to acquit them (Exo 23:7), his judgment that terminates their way (Psa 9:5). These divine responses show God acting as the moral antithesis to wickedness, not as its mirror. The structural opposition between God's righteousness and the wicked person's inner orientation (Gen 18:23–25; Mal 3:18) confirms that this characteristic belongs exclusively to the creaturely sphere as a form of failure.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The evidence establishes this characteristic as exclusively a creaturely failure-condition with no divine analogue. Rom 9:14 (vc=65872 — VCG-06) explicitly denies any form of this characteristic to God. The terms ponēros, kakia, adikia, ponēria, faulos are applied throughout the 90-verse corpus exclusively to human persons, human communities, and cosmic-adversarial powers (VCG-01) — never to God. The command of Rom 12:9 (VCG-06) to "abhor what is evil" presupposes God's own posture of abhorrence toward evil, confirming that the characteristic belongs entirely to the creaturely domain as failure.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The characteristic as experienced by the person (being abominable) is exclusively creaturely — God has no moral corruption that would make him an abomination. What the evidence shows shared is the capacity for moral revulsion: Eze 9:4 (vc=1698 — VCG-04) marks those who "sigh and groan over all the abominations" — humans who share in the divine moral response of revulsion and grief at abomination. Pro 29:27 (vc=65959 — VCG-01): "an unjust man is an abomination to the righteous" — the righteous person shares the divine response of moral revulsion toward abominable inner conditions. This suggests that the capacity for moral revulsion at abomination (as opposed to being abominable) is a shared capacity between God and image-bearing humans, particularly those whose conscience is functioning rightly.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The characteristic is exclusively creaturely — God cannot be an idolater. The evidence confirms this by locating idolatrous abomination entirely in the human will's attachment to non-divine objects: Eze 11:21 (vc=1631 — VCG-05): the heart goes after detestable things; Isa 66:3 (vc=1633 — VCG-04): the soul delights in abominations — both are specifically human inner-being orientations. The divine position in the evidence is always that of the offended party (Deu 32:16 — VCG-02: God's jealousy provoked; Eze 5:11 — VCG-05: God's withdrawal). God has no analogue to false devotion — his devotion is always truthfully directed toward himself and toward his covenant people. The characteristic is exclusively a creaturely failure of the devotion-capacity.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The characteristic is exclusively creaturely. God is consistently positioned as the perceiver and judge of iniquity (Job 11:11 — VCG-04: "he sees iniquity, will he not consider it?"; Psa 5:5 — VCG-03: "you hate all evildoers"), never as its practitioner. The structural parallel that would be shared is the capacity for intentional inner generation — God devises plans (positive), the iniquity-schemer devises evil. But the iniquity-schemer's devising is entirely creaturely: Mic 2:1 (vc=38217 — VCG-02): "those who devise wickedness and work evil on their beds" — the devising is human inner activity. The characteristic belongs exclusively to the creaturely sphere of misused generative faculty.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The characteristic is exclusively creaturely. God is the target of blasphemy (VCG-01 — Rev 13:6; 16:9/11/21) and the one whose name is dishonoured by others' speech and conduct (VCG-02 — Rom 2:24). The human person is both the agent of evil speech (Rev 16:9 — those who curse God's name) and the victim (1Pe 2:12/3:16 — VCG-03: falsely accused as evildoers; 1Cor 4:13 — vc=14351 — VCG-02: slandered). God has no analogue to the characteristic — he cannot blaspheme himself and he does not falsely accuse. The characteristic belongs exclusively to the creaturely sphere as the misuse of the creaturely speech-gift.

---

##### T0.3.3 — What does the presence or absence of this characteristic in a person reveal about the condition of the divine image in that person?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The presence of wickedness-as-settled-person-identity reveals the divine image in a state of advanced corruption. The evidence from multiple VCGs maps this corruption: the wicked person excludes God from their mind (Psa 10:4 — VCG-02 — practical atheism), the transgression-voice displaces the God-voice in their heart (Psa 36:1 — VCG-02), their soul actively desires evil (Pro 21:10 — VCG-09 — "the soul of the wicked desires evil"), their moral compass is inverted (Pro 10:32 — VCG-08 — "the mouth of the wicked knows what is perverse"), and even their acts of mercy are cruel (Pro 12:10 — VCG-09). The image-bearing faculties — soul, heart, mind, will, moral perception — are all present but all maloriented. The absence of this characteristic (the righteous person) correspondingly reveals the divine image more fully functional — the Psa 1 contrast (VCG-04) structures the whole pattern. The presence of wickedness therefore maps the degree of image-corruption with granular precision.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The presence of evil as constitutional inner nature reveals the divine image in a state of deep structural corruption. Heb 10:22 (vc=14426 — VCG-06) names "an evil conscience" as the barrier that makes approach to God impossible — the image-bearer whose conscience is constitutionally defiled cannot access the God in whose image they were made. Luk 11:39 (vc=14407 — VCG-05) names the inner person as "full of greed and wickedness" while the outward appearance is clean — the image's inner core is corrupted while the exterior remains formally intact. The absence of this characteristic (when it is departed from through repentance and divine renewal) reveals the image becoming functional again: Act 3:26 (VCG-05 — "turning every one of you from your wickedness" through divine blessing) implies restoration of the image's correct orientation when the constitutional evil is addressed.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The presence of the abominable inner conditions (crooked heart, arrogant heart, silenced conscience, dishonest dealings) reveals the divine image in a state of severe corruption — specifically at the moral-relational interface with God. Pro 3:32 (vc=1686 — VCG-02) reveals the consequence: the devious person (whose inner character is abominable) is excluded from God's confidence — the relational intimacy of the image-bearing relationship is severed. The absence of abominable conditions (the upright, the blameless) reveals the image more functional: Pro 11:20 (vc=1677 — VCG-01) — "those of blameless ways are his delight" — the image in its intended orientation toward God produces delight rather than revulsion. Tit 1:16 (vc=27 — VCG-02): those who profess God but deny him by their works are "detestable" — the gap between verbal profession and inner/practical reality is the specific image-corruption this characteristic diagnoses.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The presence of idolatrous abomination reveals the divine image in a state of radical misdirection — the devotion-capacity that should orient the heart toward God is instead directing the heart toward idol-objects. Eze 11:21 (vc=1631/65982 — VCG-05): "those whose heart goes after their detestable things and their abominations" — the heart's directional faculty (the image-bearing centre) is perverted. Hos 9:10 (vc=1632 — VCG-04): "they became detestable like the thing they loved" — the image-formation principle is operative but producing a corrupted image of the idol rather than a true image of God. The absence of this characteristic (Eze 37:23 — VCG-05: restored people no longer defiling themselves with detestable things) reveals the image functioning as designed — the heart oriented toward God, the devotion-capacity correctly attached.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The presence of iniquity as active inner scheming reveals the divine image in a state of severe inner corruption at the generative level — the faculty designed to conceive and produce good from within is instead producing evil. Isa 32:6 (vc=38181 — VCG-02): "his heart is busy with iniquity" — the heart's busyness (its generative activity) is wholly occupied with scheming harm, revealing an image whose central productive faculty is inverted. Pro 6:18 (vc=38224 — VCG-02): "a heart that devises wicked plans" — the heart as the image-bearing productive centre devises wrongly. The absence of this characteristic — the person whose heart devises good, whose thoughts are righteous — reveals the image more functional and intact. Isa 55:7 (vc=38200 — VCG-02): returning to God and forsaking iniquitous thoughts is the movement toward image-restoration.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The presence of evil expressed through speech reveals the divine image in a state of severe speech-faculty corruption — the capacity for naming, testifying, and glorifying is inverted. Rev 16:9 (vc=14352 — VCG-01): the hardened will curses God's name rather than glorifying it — the image's speech-faculty is entirely reversed in its orientation. Jude 10 (vc=14355 — VCG-01): blaspheming what is not understood shows the image's cognitive-speech capacity (to understand and name accurately) replaced by contempt filling the void of ignorance. The absence of the characteristic — speech that names God's glory, testifies truthfully, and represents moral reality accurately — reveals the image functioning more as designed. 1Pe 2:12 (vc=14377 — VCG-03): honourable conduct that contradicts false accusation and eventually silences it through good deeds represents the image-functioning alternative.

---

#### T0.4 — Typological Significance

##### T0.4.1 — Does Scripture use this characteristic typologically — deploying it to point toward or participate in a reality beyond the immediate (covenantal, eschatological, christological)?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The evidence contains limited but present typological use. The most analytically significant instance is Dan 12:10's eschatological frame (M10b-A-VCG-05): "the wicked shall act wickedly and none of the wicked shall understand" — here the wicked person is a type of those who will harden in the final purification rather than being refined. Isa 53:9 (M10b-A-VCG-04) is typologically important in the opposite direction: the servant is buried "among the wicked" despite having no wickedness in him — the wicked person's category functions typologically here as a contrast-type that reveals the servant's inner purity by negation. The Ezekiel repentance-corpus (VCG-07) does not function typologically in the strict sense but does prefigure the prophetic call to inner turning that the NT develops. The wicked-as-type is primarily eschatological (those destined for judgment) and contrast-typological (the negative against which the righteous, the servant, and the Messiah are defined).

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The evidence contains limited but present typological use. Mat 12:45 (vc=65879 — VCG-06) is the most concentrated typological instance: spirits more evil filling a vacated inner space, and the generation mirroring this increasing inner wickedness — the individual's inner dynamics are typological of the generation's collective condition. Mat 13:49 (vc=14459 — VCG-04) deploys the evil/righteous distinction eschatologically — the separation at the end of the age functions as a typological culmination of the present moral category. Gal 1:4 (vc=14466 — VCG-01) names "the present evil age" as what Christ's self-giving rescues from — here the cosmic frame of evil is typological, pointing beyond the present age to the coming age of liberation. The typological use is primarily eschatological.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The evidence contains significant typological use. Rev 17:4-5 (vc=23, 65878 — VCG-02/05) is the most concentrated typological deployment: Babylon the Great as the "mother of prostitutes and of earth's abominations" — the abomination category is deployed at a cosmic typological scale where historical Babylon/Rome becomes the type of all earthly systems constituted by abomination. Rev 21:27 (vc=22 — VCG-05): the eschatological city's exclusion of the abominable is a typological culmination, pointing from the OT's ritual exclusion of the defiled beyond the sacred boundary toward the final eschatological separation. Eze 9:4 (vc=1698 — VCG-04): the mark on those who grieve over abominations prefigures the Lamb's book of life distinction (Rev 21:27). The typological direction is primarily from OT moral-character abomination categories toward NT/Revelation eschatological and cosmic deployment.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Yes. VCG-06 (5V — Dan 9:27; 11:31; 12:11; Mat 24:15; Mar 13:14) is the typological corpus: the "abomination of desolation" is the most explicit typological use, where present idolatrous abomination patterns (sanctuary desecration) point toward an eschatological peak-evil event. Mat 24:15 (vc=65876 — VCG-06): "when you see the abomination of desolation spoken of by the prophet Daniel, standing in the holy place" — the historical desecration of Daniel's prophecy is typologically extended to future sacrilege. Hos 9:10 (vc=1632 — VCG-04): consecration to Baal-peor and becoming detestable like the idol is typological of the idolatry pattern throughout Israel's history. The Ezekiel VCG-05 corpus is typologically significant as the concentrated portrait of how accumulated abominations drive the divine presence away — a pattern the NT echoes in its understanding of defilement and divine departure.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The evidence shows typological use primarily in the prophetic projection of iniquity as scheming toward its own judgment endpoint. Isa 10:1 (vc=38191 — VCG-02): "Woe to those who decree iniquitous decrees" — the institutionalised scheming of the oppressive ruler is deployed as a prophetic type of the kind of inner evil that draws divine woe. The Psalms' evildoer corpus (VCG-03) establishes the evildoer as a type — a recurring figure whose inner scheming and ultimate defeat function typologically across the Psalter to express the certainty of divine justice. Psa 92:7-9 (vc=38246/38247 — VCG-03): "evildoers flourish… doomed to destruction forever… enemies shall perish; all evildoers shall be scattered" — this pattern functions as a typological teaching about the trajectory of all iniquity. The typological use is primarily didactic-judicial: iniquity as scheming functions as the type of what incurs divine judgment.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Yes. The Revelation VCG-01 corpus is the most concentrated typological use: Rev 13:6 (vc=14356 — VCG-01): the beast's sustained blasphemy against God's name and dwelling is a typological figure — the beast-figure represents the concentrated eschatological expression of all blasphemous defiance. The three Rev 16 verses (vc=14352; 14350; 14353 — VCG-01) show the human population under judgment as instances of the same blasphemous-will pattern at eschatological scale. Jude 8-10 (vc=14354; 14355 — VCG-01) deploys the dreamers as a typological figure linking to Sodom and past instances of rebellion. The VCG-03 false-accusation corpus (Joh 18:30 — vc=14378) has clear christological typological significance: the false charge against the accused as an evildoer participating in the pattern of false accusation against the righteous that culminates in the trial of Jesus.

---

##### T0.4.2 — If typological use is present, what is the direction of the typology — does the human instance point toward the divine, or does the divine instance establish the pattern for the human?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The typological direction is primarily from the human instance outward to the eschatological reality: the wicked person as encountered in the present evidence base is a type of those whose hardened inner orientation will persist into and be finalised at eschatological judgment (Dan 12:10; Isa 11:4 — "he shall kill the wicked"). The contrast-typological use in Isa 53:9 runs in the reverse direction — the divine servant establishes the pattern of inner purity against which the wicked serve as contrast. No typology runs from a divine instance to the human wicked person: since God is incapable of wickedness (Job 34:10), there is no divine pattern for wickedness that the human instantiates.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The typological direction runs from present creaturely experience toward eschatological and cosmic reality. Mat 13:49 (vc=14459 — VCG-04) points from the present sorting of evil and righteous persons toward the eschatological separation — the human instances point toward the divine eschatological act. Gal 1:4 (vc=14466 — VCG-01) points from the present experience of the "evil age" toward the rescue that transcends it — the present age as type points to its transcendence. The VCG-01 cosmic-evil evidence (evil one, evil age) also introduces a typological direction from the cosmic domain downward to the personal: 1Jo 5:19 (vc=14433 — VCG-01 — "the whole world lies in the power of the evil one") frames the cosmic evil as the context that explains the constitutional human condition.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The typological direction runs from present human moral conditions toward eschatological divine verdict. The OT Proverbs and Prophets identify specific inner-being conditions as abominable (crooked heart, silenced conscience, dishonest practice) — these present human instances point toward the eschatological separation of Rev 21:27 (nothing abominable enters the holy city). The Revelation material takes the moral-character abomination category and deploys it at cosmic scale (Rev 17:5 — Babylon as mother of abominations), showing that present moral abomination patterns ultimately find their fullest expression and judgment in cosmic-eschatological terms. The typological movement is from the particular (this heart, this act) toward the universal (all abomination excluded from the divine presence). No typological use points from a divine instance downward to the human.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The typological direction runs from historical idolatrous abomination patterns (OT) toward eschatological and cosmic sacrilege events (Daniel's prophecy → NT apocalyptic). Dan 9:27 and Dan 11:31 (VCG-06 — historical desecration under Antiochus) are taken up in Mat 24:15 and Mar 13:14 (VCG-06) as pointing toward a future eschatological event. The typological movement is from the particular historical instances (Baal-peor — Hos 9:10; Manasseh's idolatry — 2Ki 21:2; Ezekiel's vision of the sanctuary — VCG-05) toward a culminating eschatological abomination-of-desolation event. The direction is from human instances of idolatrous abomination in the present, pointing forward and upward toward an eschatological-cosmic fulfillment of the pattern.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The typological direction runs from specific human instances of scheming iniquity toward the general theological assertion about divine justice. The particular instances (those who devise iniquitous decrees — Isa 10:1 — VCG-02; those who plot treachery — Psa 59:5 — vc=38242 — VCG-03; those who lay snares — Psa 141:9 — vc=38231 — VCG-03) function as instances of a pattern that points toward the universal divine verdict on all such scheming. The direction is from the human-particular upward to the divine-universal: each specific act of inner scheming participates in a type whose full meaning is the certainty of divine judgment on all iniquity. No typology runs from divine instance downward to human.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The typological direction is from present/historical instances toward eschatological culmination, and from human instances toward christological revelation. Rev 13:6 (VCG-01): the beast's blasphemy as the concentrated eschatological type of all human blasphemous defiance — present instances of cursing God (Rev 16:9/11/21 — VCG-01) participate in and anticipate this eschatological beast-blasphemy. Joh 18:30 (VCG-03): the false charge against the innocent man as evildoer — the human instance of false accusation is typologically loaded in the christological context; the one falsely charged as an evildoer is the one who is in fact the righteous one. The direction is: present human instances of evil speech → eschatological beast-type concentration of blasphemy (Rev 13:6); and historical false accusation → christological revelation of its wrongness (Joh 18:30).

---

##### T0.4.3 — If no typological use is evidenced, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Typological use is evidenced (T0.4.1 above) and its direction described (T0.4.2). This prompt is satisfied by the findings at T0.4.1–T0.4.2.

## T1 — Inner Being Faculty in Operation (24 prompts)

---

### T1

#### T1.1 — Name and Naming

##### T1.1.1 — What is this characteristic called in the programme — and what does the name itself signal about its essential nature?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The characteristic is named "Wickedness as settled person-identity." The name has three components, each analytically significant. "Wickedness" signals a moral-character category — not a discrete act but a quality of the inner person. "Settled" signals a stable, consolidated state rather than a transient condition or a series of episodes — it has become definitional for the person who possesses it. "Person-identity" signals that the characteristic names a type of inner-being person rather than an experience that passes through the person. The name as a whole communicates that the evidence concerns the human being whose moral character has been organised around wickedness as its centre of gravity — it is who the person is, not merely what they have done. This contrasts with M10 (sin-act, the doing) and M10c (defilement, the contagion effect) to which M10b-A is a sibling.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The characteristic is named "Evil as constitutional inner nature." Three components matter analytically. "Evil" (ponēros / kakia / adikia / ponēria) names a moral-quality designation — not a specific act but a characterisation of what the person is at their inner core. "Constitutional" signals that this is not a transient state or episodic failure but a structural condition of the inner person — what they are constituted as. "Inner nature" signals that the characteristic concerns the generative architecture of the person's moral being, not its surface expressions. The name as a whole communicates that the evidence addresses the person whose inner generative nature is structurally oriented toward evil — not merely who has done evil things but from whom evil things necessarily flow. This differs from CHAR-1 (wickedness as settled person-identity) by emphasising structural-generative condition over settled directional orientation.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The characteristic is named "Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character." Three components carry analytical weight. "Abomination" signals a category of extreme moral repugnance that violates a sacred boundary — not merely wrongdoing but a quality of inner being or conduct that produces active revulsion. "Divine revulsion" specifies the agent of the response: the revulsion is God's, not merely human social disapproval, establishing the characteristic as a relational category defined at the God-human interface. "On moral character" limits the scope: this is the moral-character sub-register of abomination, distinct from M10b-D (idolatrous abomination). The name signals that the characteristic operates at the intersection of divine holiness (God's capacity for revulsion) and human moral character (the inner conditions that trigger it): Pro 11:20 (vc=1677 — VCG-01 — "those of crooked heart are an abomination"), Pro 16:5 (vc=1689 — VCG-02 — "everyone who is arrogant in heart is an abomination").

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The characteristic is named "Idolatrous abomination." Two components carry analytical weight. "Idolatrous" specifies the register: this is abomination rooted in false devotion — the attachment of the heart/soul/will to idol-objects rather than to God. This distinguishes CHAR-4 from CHAR-3 (moral-character abomination), where the abominable quality resides in inner moral conditions (pride, dishonesty). "Abomination" signals the divine-relational verdict: the characteristic provokes God's active revulsion. The name as a whole signals that idolatrous abomination is the specific form of abomination arising from the devotion-capacity's misdirection: Eze 11:21 (vc=1631 — VCG-05): "those whose heart goes after their detestable things and their abominations" — the heart's directional faculty is what goes after idols; Isa 66:3 (vc=1633 — VCG-04): "their soul delights in their abominations" — the soul's delight-faculty is what is engaged. The name names the specific inner-being dynamics of false devotion.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The characteristic is named "Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation." Three components carry analytical weight. "Iniquity" names the moral category — wrongdoing conceived and produced from within. "Active inner scheming" specifies the generative mode: this is not passive moral failure but deliberate, premeditated inner activity. "Evil generation" names the output: the inner scheming produces evil as its child. The name signals that the characteristic is constitutively generative: Psa 7:14 (vc=38245 — VCG-02): "conceives evil… pregnant with mischief… gives birth to lies" — the birth metaphor is embedded in the characteristic's definitional core. Mic 2:1 (vc=38217 — VCG-02): "those who devise wickedness and work evil on their beds! When the morning dawns, they perform it" — the devising (inner) and performing (outer) sequence names both dimensions the name covers. The name orients toward the inner generative process, not merely the outer wicked act.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The characteristic is named "Evil expressed through speech." Three components signal its essential nature. "Evil" names the inner moral source — wickedness that originates from within the person. "Expressed through" signals the medium: speech is the instrument, not the source; the evil precedes its expression and uses speech as its vehicle. "Speech" specifies the mode of operation — the characteristic is constitutively verbal. The name signals that the characteristic is an expression-phenomenon: it requires the inner evil to exist before speech can express it, and requires speech as the specific channel through which inner wickedness becomes socially operative. This distinguishes CHAR-6 from characteristics where speech is incidental; here speech is constitutive. Rev 13:6 (vc=14356 — VCG-01): the beast "opened its mouth to utter blasphemies" — the opening of the mouth is the act through which inner defiant orientation becomes operational blasphemy.

---

##### T1.1.2 — What do the primary Hebrew and Greek terms reveal at the definitional level — before deeper lexical analysis begins?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The primary Hebrew term ra.sha (H7563, 179 of 190 verses) is an adjective/noun designating the wicked person as a type — one constitutionally oriented toward evil. Its root covers both the moral-character meaning (the wicked person) and the forensic-legal meaning (the guilty, legally condemnable party — M10b-A-VCG-01's 5V carry this polysemy with M10 cross-register flag). re.sha (H7562, 9V) is the abstract noun counterpart: wickedness as a condition, state, and coercive force. mir.sha.at (H4849, 1V) names the collective — the wicked woman as type. The definitional revelation at this level is that Hebrew constructs an entire person-type vocabulary: the wicked person (ra.sha), wickedness as their condition (re.sha), and the wicked collective (mir.sha.at). This vocabulary suite is unusually complete, signalling that Scripture treats wickedness-as-person-identity as a coherent, classifiable inner-being category requiring multiple lexical tools to name adequately.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Four primary Greek terms carry this characteristic. ponēros (G4190, 63V): the most comprehensive term — spanning evil as a quality of persons, deeds, thoughts, and cosmic powers; at root it names what is characteristically bad or corrupt in a moral sense. kakia (G2549, 11V): specifically names settled inner badness — malice, ill-will, wickedness as an entrenched inner residue; the term's usage in Eph 4:31 (VCG-05), Col 3:8 (VCG-05), 1Pe 2:1 (VCG-05) consistently addresses it as something deeply seated requiring deliberate stripping off. adikia (G0093, 8V): unrighteousness — the condition of being structurally not-right, especially in relation to moral and legal norms; Rom 1:18 (VCG-05) names it as actively suppressing truth. ponēria (G4189, 7V): wickedness, villainy — typically naming active malicious intent; Mar 7:22 (VCG-05) lists it as an inner vice emerging from the heart. faulos (G5337, 1V): a term for what is cheap, bad, or worthless — applied to deeds in 2Cor 5:10 (VCG-06). Collectively the terms map evil across quality (ponēros), residual badness (kakia), structural wrongness (adikia), active malice (ponēria), and evaluative worthlessness (faulos).

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Primary Hebrew: to.e.vah (H8441, ~35V in this characteristic) — the term names that which is ritually or morally abhorrent; its root may connect to a verb of loathing or turning away in disgust. At the definitional level, to.e.vah designates a category of violation so severe that it provokes active revulsion rather than mere disapproval. The term is consistently relational — "an abomination to the Lord" or "to the righteous" — signalling that abomination is defined in relationship (the revulsion of the other), not self-referentially. Primary Greek: bdelugma (G0946, 4V — Luk 16:15; Rev 17:4; 17:5; 21:27) — from bdeo, to stink; the root names what is repugnant through its putrid, offensive quality. bdeluktos (G0947, 1V — Tit 1:16) — the adjectival form: the detestable or loathsome person. The Greek root's derivation from the concept of stench adds a sensory-disgust dimension: abomination is that which morally stinks in the divine nostrils.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Two primary Hebrew terms and one Greek. to.e.vah (H8441, ~72V idolatry sub-corpus) — the general abomination term: see CHAR-3 for root analysis. Applied to the idolatrous register it names: idol-practices as abominable to God (Deu 7:25 — VCG-02: idols "an abomination to the Lord"), the person who practises divination as abominable (Deu 18:12 — VCG-02), and accumulated idolatrous acts as abominations (Eze 5:9 — VCG-05). shiq.quts (H8251, 25V) — from a root of loathing/abhorrence; specifically names detestable idolatrous objects — the idol-things themselves as objects of abhorrence. 1Ki 11:5 (vc=65898 — VCG-03): "Milcom the abomination of the Ammonites" — the foreign deity is named a shiq.quts. Eze 20:7 (vc=1634 — VCG-05): "the detestable things your eyes feast on" — the idol-objects as shiq.quts. bdelugma (G0946, 2V — Mat 24:15; Mar 13:14 — VCG-06): the sacrilegious desecration-event in the holy place. Definitionally: to.e.vah names the quality of divine revulsion toward idolatrous practice; shiq.quts names the specific idol-objects that are abhorrent; bdelugma names the event of sacrilegious desolation.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Two primary Hebrew terms carry this characteristic. a.ven (H0205G, 66V) — its root denotes emptiness, nothingness, and trouble; at the definitional level it names iniquity as a morally empty-but-troublesome quality — wrongdoing that is both hollow (without genuine moral substance) and actively harmful. The term covers the scheming agent's inner state and the trouble their scheming generates. ro.a (H7455, 13V evil-deeds sub-corpus) — from the root r-'-' (to be bad, evil, harmful); names the badness-quality of deeds. At the definitional level, ro.a names evil as a quality of deeds that flows from inner moral corruption. Deu 28:20 (vc=38439 — VCG-05): "the evil of your deeds" — ro.a names the moral quality attached to the acts. No NT Greek terms appear in this characteristic's corpus — it is exclusively OT Hebrew, which T7.1.8 will address. Definitionally: a.ven names the emptiness-that-troubles; ro.a names the badness-quality of the resulting deeds.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

No primary Hebrew terms appear in the 17-verse corpus (exclusively NT Greek). Three Greek terms carry the characteristic. blasfēmeō (G0987, 11V) — the primary term: from blapto (to harm, injure) + phēmē (speech, reputation). At the definitional level, blasfēmeō names harmful speech — speech that injures a person's or God's reputation by misrepresentation. The harm is carried in the speech act itself. Rev 13:6 (VCG-01): blasphemies against God's name — the injury is to the divine name's honour. kakopoios (G2555, 5V) — from kakos (evil, bad) + poieo (to do, make): "evil-doer" or "one who does evil." As used in VCG-03, it names the identity attributed through hostile accusation — the charge that someone is an evil-doer. atopos (G0824, 1V — Act 25:5 — VCG-03) — from a (not) + topos (place): literally "out of place," hence irregular, improper, wrong. In legal context it names verifiable wrongdoing. These three terms span: harmful speech directed at God/persons (blasfēmeō), the evil-doer as charged identity (kakopoios), and legally defined wrongdoing (atopos).

---

##### T1.1.3 — Does the name carry directional, relational, or constitutional implications that orient the enquiry from the outset?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The name carries all three implications. Directional: the Ezekiel corpus (M10b-A-VCG-07, 22V) uses ra.sha consistently with "way" (Eze 3:18; 33:8; 33:11) — wickedness is a direction the will has taken, a trajectory the inner person is on. Isa 55:7 reinforces: "let the wicked forsake his way."
