Relational: the evidence locates wickedness relationally against the righteous (Gen 18:23; Psa 1:1; Mal 3:18), against God (Psa 10:4; 9:17 — forgetting God), and against the vulnerable (Psa 10:2; 37:14). Constitutional: Pro 21:10 ("the soul of the wicked desires evil") and the VCG-02 practical-atheism cluster show the characteristic lodged at the constitutional level of the inner person — soul, heart, and the deepest thought-life (Psa 10:4: "all his thoughts are 'There is no God'"). The name therefore is accurate to the evidence in all three registers.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The name "constitutional inner nature" carries constitutional implications most prominently. Mat 7:11 (vc=14438 — VCG-02): "you who are evil" — the "are" is constitutive, not episodic. Mat 7:17-18 (vc=14439-14440 — VCG-02): "a diseased tree cannot bear good fruit" — the constitutional metaphor directly names the inner generative architecture. Mar 7:23 (vc=14422 — VCG-03): "all these evil things come from within" — the inside is the constitutional source. The name also carries relational implications: the constitutional evil produces relational harm (3Jo 10 — VCG-04 — domineering malice against community; 2Jo 11 — VCG-04 — communicated through association; 2Th 3:2 — VCG-06 — faithlessness grounding moral depravity). The directional implication is that the characteristic generates evil outward (from the treasury — Mat 12:35, Luk 6:45 — VCG-03) rather than being received from outside.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The name carries all three, with the relational dimension most prominent. Relational: to.e.vah is structurally relational — it names the inner condition from the perspective of the one who is revolted (God or the righteous). Every instance is "an abomination to the Lord" or "an abomination to the righteous" — the characteristic is defined by the divine-relational response, not by an internal self-assessment. Pro 29:27 (vc=65959 — VCG-01): the mutual repulsion of wicked and righteous confirms the relational definition. Constitutional: Pro 11:20 (vc=1677 — VCG-01) and Pro 16:5 (vc=1689 — VCG-02) locate abomination in the heart (crooked heart, arrogant heart) — constitutional inner conditions, not merely surface acts. Directional: Eze 14:6 (vc=65984 — VCG-04): "turn away your faces from all your abominations" — the characteristic names the direction the will is currently facing, and repentance requires a directional reversal.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The name carries all three implications. Directional: Eze 11:21 (vc=1631 — VCG-05): "whose heart goes after their detestable things" — the characteristic is directional; the heart is moving toward idol-objects. Eze 20:7 (vc=1634 — VCG-05): "the detestable things your eyes feast on" — the eyes are oriented toward the idolatrous objects. Jer 4:1 (vc=65903 — VCG-04): "remove your detestable things from my presence" — the call to repentance is directional (remove from before the divine presence). Relational: Deu 32:16 (vc=65938 — VCG-02): "they stirred him to jealousy" — idolatrous abomination is a relational betrayal that provokes divine jealousy. Eze 5:11 (vc=65969 — VCG-05): the divine presence withdraws — the characteristic produces relational breakdown. Constitutional: Hos 9:10 (vc=1632 — VCG-04): "they became detestable like the thing they loved" — sustained idolatrous devotion transforms the person's inner character at the constitutional level.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The name carries all three implications. Directional: "active inner scheming" implies a direction — from within outward. Mic 2:1 (vc=38217 — VCG-02): iniquity devised inward at night → performed outward at dawn. The characteristic moves in a consistent inside-to-outside direction. Constitutional: "evil generation" places the characteristic at the generative heart of the person — in the heart (Isa 32:6 — vc=38181 — VCG-02: "heart is busy with iniquity") and in the thought-life (Isa 59:7 — vc=38203 — VCG-02: "their thoughts are thoughts of iniquity"). Relational: VCG-03 (24V — evildoer class) shows the characteristic as relational in its harm — Psa 14:4 (vc=38229 — VCG-03): "evildoers who eat up my people" — the scheming targets other persons; Psa 28:3 (vc=38232 — VCG-03): "speak peace with their neighbors while evil is in their hearts" — the relational dimension of deception is constitutive of the characteristic's expression.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

All three implications are present. Directional: "expressed through speech" names an outward direction — from inner evil through the speech-faculty into the social-relational world. Rev 16:9 (vc=14352 — VCG-01): people "cursed the name of God" — the inner hardened-will state moves outward through cursing speech. Relational: the characteristic is constitutively targeted at another — blasphemy is directed at God (VCG-01) or at persons through false accusation (VCG-03). Rom 2:24 (vc=14357 — VCG-02): God's name blasphemed "among the Gentiles" — the relational audience (Gentiles) is part of the characteristic's definition. Constitutional: Jude 8 (vc=14354 — VCG-01): the dreamers "reject authority and blaspheme the glorious ones" — the blasphemy arises from a constitutional inner posture of authority-rejection; the inner constitutional orientation (rejection of authority, sensory self-indulgence) produces the speech expression.

---

#### T1.2 — Kind

##### T1.2.1 — What kind of inner-being phenomenon does this characteristic appear to be — an act, a disposition, a condition, a quality, or something else?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The evidence establishes wickedness-as-settled-person-identity as primarily a disposition — a stable, habitual inner orientation of the whole person toward evil, away from God, and toward harm to others. It is not primarily an act (that register belongs to M10 sin-act); it is not primarily a condition imposed from outside; it is the inner person's characteristic directional bent. Evidence: Psa 36:1 (transgression speaking as an inner voice, displacing God-fear — the disposition as an interior governance structure), Pro 4:19 (the way of the wicked characterised by moral blindness — a perceptual consequence of the disposition), 1Sa 24:13 ("out of the wicked comes wickedness" — the disposition as generative source). The characteristic also has qualities of a condition (it is stable and self-perpetuating) and a quality (it marks the person morally). But "disposition" is the primary classification: it is something the person habitually is in their inner orientation.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Evil as constitutional inner nature is primarily a condition — a structural state of the inner person — rather than primarily an act, a disposition, or a quality. The constitutional-condition classification is supported by the tree-nature metaphor (Mat 7:17-18 — VCG-02): a tree's nature determines its fruit; the condition precedes and generates the output. It also has quality aspects (ponēros as a moral-quality term — Mat 5:45 — VCG-04) and disposition aspects (kakia as settled inner badness — Eph 4:31 — VCG-05; Col 3:8 — VCG-05). But the defining evidence for "condition" is the constitutional-baseline framing: Mat 7:11 (VCG-02) — "you who are evil" as a fact about human nature, not a description of a specific volitional alignment. The condition is what makes the dispositions and acts possible; it is the underlying structural reality from which they emerge.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The characteristic is analytically a compound phenomenon: it is simultaneously a quality of the inner person (what makes them abominable), a condition of the inner person (the state of their heart/conscience), and a relational judgment (the divine verdict of revulsion). The Proverbs evidence (VCG-01, VCG-02) treats abomination primarily as a quality — the quality of dishonest practice (Pro 11:1 — vc=65954), of the crooked heart (Pro 11:20 — vc=1677), of the arrogant heart (Pro 16:5 — vc=1689). The VCG-04 conscience evidence treats it as a condition — a state the inner person is in relative to their conscience's engagement with abominable acts (Jer 6:15 — vc=1680: conscience wholly silenced). The relational verdict (divine revulsion as response) is the frame within which both quality and condition are assessed. The most analytically precise classification is: a quality of the inner moral character that provokes divine relational revulsion, constituting a sacred-boundary violation.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The characteristic is primarily a dispositional-attachment phenomenon — the sustained inner orientation of the devotion-faculty (heart, soul, will) toward idol-objects. It is not primarily an act (individual acts of idolatrous worship belong to M10c cultic defilement) but a dispositional condition: the habitual going-after of the heart (Eze 11:21 — VCG-05 — "heart goes after their detestable things") and the active delight of the soul (Isa 66:3 — VCG-04 — "soul delights in their abominations"). The Ezekiel VCG-05 corpus (43V) documents this characteristic as an accumulated communal disposition — "all your abominations" — not individual episodic acts. The characteristic also has a constitutional quality dimension: Hos 9:10 (VCG-04) — "became detestable like the thing they loved" — the sustained attachment transforms character quality. The best single classification is: a dispositional inner attachment of the devotion-capacity to idolatrous objects, producing accumulated abomination as its characteristic output.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The characteristic is primarily a generative-dispositional phenomenon — an active, ongoing inner process of producing evil from within. It is not merely a static condition or quality but a process: Psa 36:4 (vc=38235 — VCG-02): "He plots trouble while on his bed" — plotting is an active inner cognitive-volitional act. Isa 32:6 (vc=38181 — VCG-02): "his heart is busy with iniquity" — "busy" confirms ongoing inner activity. Job 15:35 (vc=38208 — VCG-02): "they conceive trouble and give birth to evil" — the conception-to-birth arc is processual. Alongside this generative dimension, the characteristic also presents as a stored condition in VCG-04 (23V): Psa 66:18 (vc=38182 — VCG-04): "cherished iniquity in my heart" — iniquity is harboured as an inner holding. The characteristic therefore has two aspects: generative process (VCG-02) and stored condition (VCG-04), unified by the same a.ven vocabulary.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The characteristic is primarily an expressive-dispositional phenomenon: an expressive act (speech) that flows from and reveals an inner moral disposition (wickedness, hardened will, malicious false judgment). It is not merely an act (individual utterances) but the expression of a constitutive inner posture. Rev 13:6 (vc=14356 — VCG-01): "a total inner orientation of defiant contempt toward the divine" expressed through the opened mouth. Jude 8 (vc=14354 — VCG-01): the dreamers' blasphemy flows from their wilful inner rejection of authority and sensory self-indulgence — the speech is expressive of a settled inner disposition. The characteristic also has a social-perlocutionary dimension: the speech acts cause harm to others — defamation reduces the slandered to refuse (1Cor 4:13 — VCG-02) and causes God's name to be dishonoured (Rom 2:24 — VCG-02). It is an inner-moral-disposition expressed through speech with harmful social consequences.

---

##### T1.2.2 — Is this characteristic simple in structure or does it appear to have constituent elements at first encounter?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The VCG structure reveals multiple constituent elements within the characteristic. At minimum, the evidence maps: (a) practical atheism — the God-exclusion mechanism (VCG-02, 8V: Psa 10:4, 9:17, 36:1, etc.); (b) pride as the inner engine of directed hostility (VCG-03, 22V: Psa 10:2, 37:12-14, Isa 13:11); (c) moral hollowness — the soul oriented toward evil and the desires corrupted (VCG-09, 33V: Pro 21:10, 10:20, 12:10); (d) inner instability — the self-undermining momentum of wickedness (VCG-06, 21V: Pro 5:22, 10:24-30); (e) the directional-orientation — wickedness as a "way" the will can turn from (VCG-07, 22V: Eze 3:18, 33:11). These are not separate characteristics but constituent structural elements of the one characteristic. The characteristic is composite in this analytical sense — it has identifiable sub-structures within the settled person-identity.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The 6-VCG structure reveals multiple constituent elements. The characteristic has: (a) the constitutional baseline — human inner nature as evil by default (VCG-02, 8V: Mat 7:11-18; Luk 11:13; Mat 12:39; Mat 16:4; Luk 11:29); (b) the heart-as-treasury — the inner generative organ from which evil flows (VCG-03, 8V: Mat 6:23; Mat 9:4; Mat 12:34-35; Mat 15:19; Luk 6:45; Mar 7:23; Jam 2:4); (c) settled deep character of persons (VCG-04, 17V); (d) the cosmic-evil/evil-one dimension (VCG-01, 13V — cross-register); (e) saturating inner vices — kakia, ponēria, adikia filling the person (VCG-05, 20V); (f) evil conscience, progressive deterioration, and the command to abhor evil (VCG-06, 24V). These are not separate characteristics but constituent structural registers within the one constitutional-condition characteristic.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The 5-VCG structure reveals multiple constituent elements. The characteristic has: (a) the commercial/ethical-practice register — dishonest weights, false balances, perverted judgment (VCG-01, 10V: Deu 25:16; Pro 11:1; Pro 11:20; Pro 15:9; Pro 16:12; Pro 17:15; Pro 20:10; Pro 20:23; Pro 24:9; Pro 29:27); (b) the inner-character register — pride, crooked heart, hidden corruption, lying lips, wicked thoughts (VCG-02, 9V: Pro 3:32; Pro 8:7; Pro 12:22; Pro 15:26; Pro 16:5; Pro 26:25; Luk 16:15; Tit 1:16; Rev 17:4); (c) the corrupt worship register — religious acts offered by the inwardly corrupt person (VCG-03, 4V: Pro 15:8; Pro 21:27; Pro 28:9; Isa 1:13); (d) the conscience register — silenced, awakening, and grieving conscience in relation to abomination (VCG-04, 11V); (e) the identity-constituted register — choice, identity, and being wholly constituted by abomination (VCG-05, 6V: Pro 6:16; Pro 13:19; Isa 41:24; Isa 44:19; Rev 17:5; Rev 21:27). These are constituent registers within a single characteristic.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The 6-VCG structure reveals multiple constituent elements. (a) The category-violation boundary register (VCG-01, 6V — Levitical): acts declared abominable as violations of created order distinctions — the boundary itself is the content; (b) the volitional-resistance register (VCG-02, 14V — Deuteronomic): the will that must actively resist adopting abominable practices; (c) the historical-institutionalization register (VCG-03, 17V — reform narratives): kings installing or purging idolatrous abominations — the characteristic as political-institutional embeddedness; (d) the prophetic-stubbornness register (VCG-04, 14V — Jeremiah/Prophets): the inner stubbornness that continues in abomination despite warnings; (e) the divine-presence-driving register (VCG-05, 43V — Ezekiel): accumulated abominations progressively driving the divine presence from the sanctuary; (f) the apocalyptic-desolation register (VCG-06, 5V): eschatological peak-sacrilege. These registers address different inner-being aspects: the will (VCG-02), the heart/soul (VCG-05), the stubbornness (VCG-04), and institutional/communal expression (VCG-03).

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The 5-VCG structure reveals multiple constituent registers. (a) Active inner generation (VCG-02, 14V): the scheming and conceiving mode — Psa 7:14 (vc=38245); Mic 2:1 (vc=38217); Eze 11:2 (vc=38193); Isa 32:6 (vc=38181) etc. (b) Evildoer as character-type (VCG-03, 24V): iniquity as habitual inner-character orientation defining a class of persons — Psa 5:5 (vc=38237); Psa 28:3 (vc=38232); Pro 17:4 (vc=38219) etc. (c) Stored/harboured iniquity (VCG-04, 23V): iniquity as accumulated inner moral condition — Psa 66:18 (vc=38182); Psa 41:6 (vc=38236); Psa 119:133 (vc=38227) etc. (d) Evil deeds as expressed moral quality (VCG-05, 11V): the outward expression of the inner condition — ro.a evil-deeds sub-corpus. (e) Trouble-suffered (VCG-01, 7V): the INTEGRATION_NOTE carry-forward polysemy VCG — a.ven in trouble-received-by-victim register. These five registers constitute the characteristic's full range.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The 3-VCG structure reveals three constituent registers. (a) Direct defiant blasphemy against God (VCG-01, 6V): the hardened will generating contemptuous speech against God himself — Rev 13:6; 16:9/11/21; Jude 8/10. The inner content is wilful defiance of God's authority. (b) Social defamation causing dishonour (VCG-02, 5V): the social consequence of moral failure (Rom 2:24) or the false attribution of wrong teaching (Rom 3:8) or speaking ill of the good (Rom 14:16) or slandering the apostle (1Cor 4:13) or denouncing thankful freedom (1Cor 10:30). Here the inner content ranges from conduct-failure to malicious misrepresentation. (c) False accusation as hostile legal charge (VCG-03, 6V): charging the innocent as evildoers through hostile social-legal processes — Joh 18:30; 1Pe 2:12/14/3:16/4:15; Act 25:5. These three registers constitute the full range of the characteristic.

---

##### T1.2.3 — What is the current best working description of this characteristic — encapsulating its constitutional location, the faculties it primarily engages, and its impact on the person?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Based on the 190-verse corpus, the working description is: Wickedness-as-settled-person-identity is a stable inner-being disposition in which the human person's constitutive faculties — will, soul, heart, moral perception — are organised around an orientation away from God and toward evil, injustice, and harm. The disposition is habitual and identity-defining: it generates the person's characteristic conduct, determines their relationship to God (non-service, Mal 3:18; forgetting, Psa 9:17; relational estrangement, Pro 15:29), shapes their relationships with others (exploitation, concealment, predation — VCGs 03, 08, 09), and carries within itself an inherent instability that moves toward dissolution and judgment. It is a constitutional orientation of the whole person, not a momentary state, distinguishable from the righteous person at the deepest inner level (Psa 7:9: "you who test the minds and hearts").

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Evil as constitutional inner nature is the structural condition of the human inner person in which the generative architecture of the heart, mind, and soul is oriented toward the production of evil as its default output. The heart is a treasury from which evil is actively drawn (Mat 12:35 — VCG-03; Luk 6:45 — VCG-03), all evil things come from within (Mar 7:23 — VCG-03), and the inner nature is diseased in a way that makes good fruit constitutionally impossible without transformation (Mat 7:17-18 — VCG-02). The condition saturates the person at multiple levels — the soul is filled with vice clusters (Rom 1:29 — VCG-05), the conscience is defiled (Heb 10:22 — VCG-06), and the mind is hostile (Col 1:21 — VCG-06). The characteristic is NT-distinctive: the Hebrew OT (Characteristic 1) identified the wicked person by their inner orientation; the NT (Characteristic 2) identifies the constitutional evil as the baseline condition of human nature from which that orientation flows.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Abomination as divine revulsion on moral character is the verdict and response of divine holiness to specific inner moral conditions and their expressions — a verdict of active revulsion that names certain qualities of the heart, will, conscience, and conduct as fundamentally incompatible with the divine moral order. The evidence shows the characteristic operating at two poles: the divine-inner response (God's revulsion — Pro 11:1; Pro 16:5; Luk 16:15) and the human-inner state (the abominable condition — crooked heart, arrogant heart, silenced conscience, dishonest dealing). Between these poles lies the three-part mechanism: the act or inner condition that defiles, the sacred boundary it transgresses, and the divine revulsion that responds. The 40-verse corpus documents the characteristic across commercial practice (VCG-01), inner character (VCG-02), worship (VCG-03), conscience (VCG-04), and identity (VCG-05), showing it as a comprehensive category of divine moral response to human inner-being failure.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Idolatrous abomination is the dispositional condition of the inner person in which the devotion-capacity — heart, soul, eyes, will — is attached to and oriented toward idol-objects rather than God, producing an accumulated inner-and-outer pattern of abominable practices that provokes divine revulsion, drives the divine presence away, and progressively transforms the person's character toward the likeness of what they love. The evidence documents this across: the heart going after idols (Eze 11:21 — VCG-05), the soul delighting in abominations (Isa 66:3 — VCG-04), the eyes feasting on detestable things (Eze 20:7 — VCG-05), and the will persistently refusing to turn from them (Eze 20:8 — VCG-05: "none of them cast away the detestable things their eyes feasted on"). The divine response is withdrawal (Eze 5:11 — VCG-05) and eventually unprecedented judgment (Eze 5:9 — VCG-05: "what I have never yet done").

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation is an ongoing inner-moral process in which the mind, heart, and will generate evil from within — devising harmful schemes, harbouring accumulated iniquity, and expressing a settled character-type whose habitual pattern is the working of evil against others and against God. The 79-verse corpus documents this across: active inner generation (devising, conceiving, plotting — VCG-02, 14V); habitual character-definition of the evildoer class (VCG-03, 24V); the stored-and-harboured inner condition (VCG-04, 23V); the evil quality of the deeds that express the inner condition (VCG-05, 11V); and the trouble the characteristic inflicts on victims (VCG-01, 7V). The primary inner-being location is the heart and thought-life (Isa 32:6 — VCG-02: "heart busy with iniquity"; Isa 59:7 — VCG-02: "thoughts are thoughts of iniquity"); the primary impact is harmful scheming directed against others and the severing of the divine-human relationship (Psa 66:18 — VCG-04: cherished iniquity forecloses divine hearing).

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Evil expressed through speech is the socially operative expression of inner wickedness through the instrument of speech — spanning three modes: (1) direct defiant contempt for God uttered verbally by the hardened will under judgment (VCG-01); (2) harmful speech that dishonours God's name or damages persons' reputations through misrepresentation (VCG-02); (3) hostile false accusation that charges the innocent as evildoers through legal-social processes (VCG-03). The characteristic's inner content varies by VCG — from total will-defiance against God (Rev 16:9 — VCG-01) to malicious hostile judgment (Joh 18:30 — VCG-03) to reckless denunciation (1Cor 10:30 — VCG-02) — but the common thread is inner wickedness finding its socially operative form through speech: blasphemy, slander, false accusation, or harmful denunciation.

---

#### T1.3 — Boundary

##### T1.3.1 — What is the structural opposite of this characteristic — the inner-being reality that stands against or excludes it?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The structural opposite is righteousness (tsaddiq / righteous person), which appears as the constant explicit contrast throughout the corpus. Gen 18:23–25 (VCG-04) is foundational: wickedness and righteousness are distinct inner conditions requiring distinct judgments. The contrast is sustained through the entire Psalms and Proverbs corpus (VCG-04, 18V of moral contrast; VCG-09, 33V of wickedness against divine justice). Psa 1:6 names the opposition structurally: "the Lord knows the way of the righteous, but the way of the wicked will perish." Isa 53:9 (VCG-04) provides the most concentrated single contrast: the servant buried among the wicked has "no violence in will, no deceit in speech" — righteousness defined against the wicked person's constitutive characteristics. M26 (Righteousness) is the primary cluster-scope structural opposite; the M10b-A evidence base is saturated with this relationship.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The structural opposite is righteous/good inner nature, sincerity, and a cleansed conscience. 1Cor 5:8 (vc=14363/14412 — VCG-05) contrasts the old leaven of malice and evil with "the unleavened bread of sincerity and truth" — sincerity and truth are the constitutional opposite. Heb 10:22 (vc=14426 — VCG-06) contrasts an evil conscience with the heart "sprinkled clean from an evil conscience" — the cleansed conscience is the opposed condition. Jam 1:21 (vc=14368 — VCG-05) contrasts "rampant wickedness" with receiving the implanted word — the word-receiving state is the structural opposite of constitutional inner evil. Rom 12:9 (vc=14417 — VCG-06) contrasts evil with good: "abhor what is evil; hold fast to what is good." The structural opposite is constitutionally good inner nature — the person from whom good things flow (Mat 12:35: "the good person out of his good treasure brings forth good").

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The evidence names the structural opposite explicitly and consistently in antithetical form. Pro 11:20 (vc=1677 — VCG-01): "those of crooked heart are an abomination to the Lord, but those of blameless ways are his delight." Pro 11:1 (vc=65954 — VCG-01): "a false balance is an abomination to the Lord, but a just weight is his delight." Pro 15:8 (vc=1678 — VCG-03): "the sacrifice of the wicked is an abomination to the Lord, but the prayer of the upright is acceptable to him." The structural opposite is consistently "delight" (ratson) and "acceptability" (ratsah) — what is abominable provokes revulsion; what is its opposite provokes divine delight and acceptance. The person-type opposite of the abominable is "the upright" (Pro 3:32 — vc=1686 — VCG-02: "the upright are in his confidence"), "the blameless" (Pro 11:20 — VCG-01), and "him who pursues righteousness" (Pro 15:9 — vc=1688 — VCG-01). The structural opposite is moral integrity that attracts divine delight rather than revulsion.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The structural opposite is exclusive covenant devotion to God — the devotion-capacity correctly attached. 2Ch 34:33 (vc=65946 — VCG-03): after Josiah removed all the abominations "all who were present in Israel serve the Lord their God. All his days they did not turn away from following the Lord" — the removal of idolatrous abomination produces sustained following of the Lord, its structural opposite. Jer 4:1 (vc=65903 — VCG-04): "if you return, O Israel…to me you should return. If you remove your detestable things from my presence" — the return to God is the structural opposite, made possible by removal of the abomination. Deu 18:9 (vc=65931 — VCG-02): the opposite of following abominable practices is following the Lord's ways. Eze 37:23 (vc=65913 — VCG-05): "they shall be my people, and I will be their God" — the covenantal relationship restored is the structural opposite of abomination-driving-God-away. The structural opposite is: will aligned with God, heart following God, soul delighting in God rather than abominations.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The structural opposite is named directly in the antithetical Psalm and Proverbs evidence. Psa 5:5 (vc=38237 — VCG-03) contrasts evildoers with the blameless who can stand before God. Psa 92:7/12 (VCG-03): evildoers flourish briefly then are destroyed; the structural opposite is the righteous who flourish like the palm tree. Psa 10:29 (vc=38218 — VCG-03): "the way of the Lord is a stronghold to the blameless, but destruction to evildoers" — the blameless way is the structural opposite. Job 4:8 (vc=38186 — VCG-04): "those who plow iniquity and sow trouble reap the same" implies the structural opposite: plowing righteousness, sowing good. Isa 55:7 (vc=38200 — VCG-02): "let the wicked forsake his way, and the unrighteous man his thoughts; let him return to the Lord" — the structural opposite is the righteous mind/thoughts and the path toward God. In person-type terms: the blameless, the upright, and those who call on the Lord (Psa 14:4 — VCG-03: evildoers "do not call upon the Lord") are the structural opposites.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The structural opposite is speech that glorifies God, testifies truthfully, and honours persons. Rev 16:9 (vc=14352 — VCG-01): "they did not repent and give him glory" — giving glory is the structural opposite of cursing the name. The withheld glory specifies exactly what the opposite would look like. 1Pe 2:12 (vc=14377 — VCG-03): "honorable conduct among the Gentiles" that causes people "to glorify God on the day of visitation" — honourable conduct producing God-glorifying recognition is the structural opposite of both evildoing and the false accusation that accompanies it. Rom 2:24 (vc=14357 — VCG-02): the opposite of "God's name blasphemed among the Gentiles" is God's name glorified by the conduct of those who represent him. The structural opposite is: repentance producing glory-speech toward God (VCG-01), honest representation of truth about persons and teaching (VCG-02), and truthful testimony that names the innocent as innocent (VCG-03).

---

##### T1.3.2 — What does this characteristic explicitly exclude or resist?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The evidence shows wickedness-as-settled-person-identity explicitly excluding and resisting: (1) God — the God-exclusion mechanism is definitional (Psa 10:4; 9:17; 10:13 "renounce God from within their heart"; Mal 3:18 non-service; Pro 15:29 "the Lord is far from the wicked"); (2) moral correction — Pro 9:7 ("whoever corrects a scoffer gets himself abuse") and Isa 26:10 ("if favor is shown to the wicked, he does not learn righteousness") show resistance to correction as structural; (3) justice — the wicked pervert justice (Isa 5:23; Pro 17:23; Hab 1:4) and the Ezekiel corpus shows wickedness explicitly resisting the turn toward what is just (Eze 33:9: "he does not turn from his way"); (4) the righteous — active hostility toward the righteous is a structural feature (Psa 37:12-14; 11:2; 34:21 — VCG-03).

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The evidence shows constitutional inner evil explicitly excluding and resisting: (1) truth — Rom 1:18 (vc=14336 — VCG-05): unrighteousness "suppresses the truth" — active resistance to truth is definitional for adikia; (2) faith — 2Th 3:2 (vc=14450 — VCG-06): "wicked and evil men" are those for whom "not all have faith" — faithlessness is the ground of constitutional moral depravity; Heb 3:12 (vc=14423 — VCG-06) fuses evil heart with unbelieving heart; (3) the implanted word — Jam 1:21 (vc=14368 — VCG-05): rampant wickedness must be "stripped away before the implanted word can take root"; (4) genuine approach to God — Heb 10:22 (vc=14426 — VCG-06): the evil conscience makes approach to God impossible; (5) love — 1Cor 13:6 (vc=14341 — VCG-06): love refuses to rejoice in unrighteousness — evil's presence resists the orientation love requires.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The abominable inner conditions explicitly exclude and resist: (1) divine intimacy — Pro 3:32 (vc=1686 — VCG-02): the devious person is an abomination and therefore excluded from divine confidence — the characteristic forecloses the relational proximity with God; (2) divine acceptance of worship — Pro 15:8 (vc=1678 — VCG-03), Pro 21:27 (vc=1693 — VCG-03), Isa 1:13 (vc=1695 — VCG-03): the inner corruption renders religious approach unacceptable; (3) sacred space — Rev 21:27 (vc=22 — VCG-05): nothing abominable enters the holy city; Eze 44:13 (vc=66003 — VCG-04): those who committed abominations are barred from sacred service; (4) moral turning — Pro 13:19 (vc=1687 — VCG-05): fools find turning from evil to be abominable — the characteristic in fools resists its own correction; (5) shame as inner corrective — Jer 6:15 (vc=1680 — VCG-04): the silenced conscience resists shame as the natural inner response to abomination.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The characteristic explicitly excludes and resists: (1) the divine presence — Eze 8:6 (vc=65976 — VCG-05): abominations "drive me far from my sanctuary" — the characteristic is incompatible with divine presence; (2) covenant separation from the nations — Ezr 9:1 (vc=65949 — VCG-03): "have not separated themselves from the peoples of the lands with their abominations" — the characteristic is expressed through the refusal of covenant separation; (3) divine instruction — Eze 20:8 (vc=65911 — VCG-05): "not willing to listen to me. None of them cast away the detestable things" — the characteristic resists hearing and obeying; (4) the will to turn — Jer 44:4 (vc=65966 — VCG-04): persistent prophetic warnings ignored; (5) cleansing — Eze 37:23 (vc=65913 — VCG-05) shows that divine cleansing is required precisely because the characteristic resists self-generated departure.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The characteristic explicitly excludes and resists: (1) divine hearing — Psa 66:18 (vc=38182 — VCG-04): "If I had cherished iniquity in my heart, the Lord would not have listened" — cherished iniquity closes the divine ear; (2) calling on God — Psa 14:4 (vc=38229 — VCG-03): evildoers "do not call upon the Lord" — the characteristic resists the person's movement toward God; Psa 53:4 (vc=38238 — VCG-03): same — "do not call upon God"; (3) justice — Isa 59:4 (vc=38192 — VCG-02): "No one enters suit justly; no one goes to law honestly" — iniquity as inner scheming subverts the justice system; (4) wisdom — Psa 36:3 (vc=38234 — VCG-04): "he has ceased to act wisely and do good" — iniquity displaces wisdom; (5) moral instruction — Job 36:10 (vc=38215 — VCG-04): God opens ears to return from iniquity — the characteristic resists the instruction that would produce departure.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The characteristic explicitly excludes and resists: (1) repentance — Rev 16:9 (vc=14352 — VCG-01): "they did not repent and give him glory"; Rev 16:11 (vc=14350 — VCG-01): "they did not repent of their deeds" — under direct divine judgment, the hardened blasphemer refuses the repentance that would arrest the characteristic; (2) glory-giving — Rev 16:9 (VCG-01): glory is withheld; (3) truthful testimony — 1Pe 2:12 (vc=14377 — VCG-03): false accusation resists accurate naming of the person's actual character; (4) rational understanding — Jude 10 (vc=14355 — VCG-01): "blaspheme all that they do not understand" — blasphemy fills the void left by the refusal or inability to understand; (5) submission to authority — Jude 8 (vc=14354 — VCG-01): "reject authority and blaspheme the glorious ones" — authority-rejection is the precondition of the blasphemous speech.

---

##### T1.3.3 — What is this characteristic not — where does it end and something else begin?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The forensic-verdict VCG (M10b-A-VCG-01, 5V — Exo 23:7, Deu 25:1, 25:2, 1Ki 8:32, 2Ch 6:23) marks the boundary between wickedness-as-settled-person-identity and the legal-status use of ra.sha. In these verses, "wicked" is a judicial label applied to the guilty party in a legal dispute — it describes a socially adjudicated status rather than an inner moral orientation. This is a cross-register boundary with M10 (sin-act / forensic). Beyond this, the characteristic ends where the falling-away of a righteous person begins (Eze 18:24: "when a righteous person turns to wicked ways" — this is the moment of transition, not yet the settled condition). The characteristic is also distinct from isolated sinful acts (M10): the corpus's primary terms (ra.sha as person-type) consistently describe the person-type rather than the act-instance.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The VCG-01 cosmic-evil sub-corpus (13V — Mat 6:13, 13:19, 13:38, Joh 17:15, Eph 6:16, 2Th 3:3, 1Jo 2:13, 2:14, 5:18, 5:19, Gal 1:4, Eph 5:16, 6:13) marks the most important boundary: these verses name the evil one / evil age as supra-personal powers, which is the M27 cross-register. The evil one is external to the person's constitutional condition; the constitutional condition is internal. The INTEGRATION_NOTE carry-forward applies here: VCG-01 is structurally separated from the personal-constitutional VCGs. The characteristic also ends where the legal-forensic register begins (Act 18:14 — vc=14462; Act 25:18 — vc=14463; Act 28:21 — vc=14464 — VCG-06 minimal inner-being content — these are barely within the characteristic and mark its outer edge at the legal-category boundary, where ponēros names a crime-category rather than an inner condition). Mat 6:34 (vc=14371 — VCG-02 — kakia as "trouble" — M03 cross-register flag-only) marks the edge where kakia's semantic range intersects circumstantial distress rather than moral evil.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The characteristic ends at the boundary with M10b-D (idolatrous abomination). The §2 VCG descriptions explicitly separate moral-character abomination (M10b-C = CHAR-3) from idolatry-based abomination (M10b-D = CHAR-4). Within the present corpus, Deu 27:15 (vc=65937 — VCG-04 here) and Isa 41:24 (vc=65960 — VCG-05) and Isa 44:19 (vc=65961 — VCG-05) touch the idolatrous boundary — they are assigned to M10b-C because their primary inner-being content concerns the conscience (Deu 27:15 — secret idol with knowing heart) or the inner faculty of reflection/discernment (Isa 44:19 — absence of discernment). The characteristic also ends where mere sin-act begins (M10): an act of dishonesty is a sin-act (M10); the dishonest practice becoming an abomination specifically requires the divine-revulsion verdict and the inner-character dimension (the habitual dishonest dealer — Deu 25:16: "all who act dishonestly, are an abomination"). Abomination names the registration of the sin-act as provoking divine revulsion at the inner-character level.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The characteristic ends at the boundary with CHAR-3 (moral-character abomination) — CHAR-4 specifically roots abomination in idolatrous devotion, not in moral-character failures like dishonesty or pride. Within CHAR-4's own corpus, VCG-01 (Levitical — 6V) marks the inner boundary with M10c (cultic/ritual defilement): Lev 18:22-30 (VCG-01) addresses specific acts whose primary content is category-boundary violation rather than inner idolatrous attachment — these verses are at the edge of the characteristic. VCG-06 (5V — Dan 9:27; 11:31; 12:11; Mat 24:15; Mar 13:14) marks the inner boundary with M27 (concrete abomination/idol-object): these verses have minimal inner-being content (the abomination-of-desolation is an objective sacrilegious event rather than an inner devotion pattern). The characteristic's core (VCGs 02-05) is most clearly CHAR-4; the margins (VCGs 01 and 06) share vocabulary and category with adjacent clusters.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The characteristic ends at the boundary with: (1) CHAR-1 (wickedness as settled person-identity): CHAR-1 addresses the settled ra.sha inner orientation using H7563/H7562 vocabulary; CHAR-5 addresses the active generative scheming process using a.ven vocabulary. Both involve the evildoer-type but CHAR-5 emphasises the active inner process of devising and generating evil, while CHAR-1 emphasises the settled dispositional identity. (2) CHAR-3/4 (abomination): CHAR-3 is a divine-verdict category; CHAR-5 is an inner-process category — the scheming produces what may then be named abominable, but the scheming itself is CHAR-5. (3) VCG-01's trouble-suffered register (7V — Psa 55:3; 55:10; 94:16; Hab 1:3; Zec 10:2; Neh 2:2; Ecc 7:3): these verses carry a.ven in the victim/affliction-received sense — the harm that falls on a person from outside — which borders on M03 (grief/sorrow) and M27 (calamity). The characteristic's core is the agent's inner scheming; VCG-01 marks the boundary where a.ven names the trouble received rather than perpetrated.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The characteristic ends at the boundary with M06 (contempt/hostile speech/defiant rejection of authority) — the §2 VCG description notes the M06 cross-register flag on blasfēmeō. CHAR-6 names the evil expressed through speech as an inner-being characteristic; M06 names the contempt and hostile speech as the relational and communicative act. The overlap is real but the primary focus differs: CHAR-6 analyses the inner wickedness finding expression through speech; M06 analyses the contemptuous relational act itself. Within CHAR-6, the characteristic ends where speech is not primarily evil-expressive: Rom 14:16 (vc=14359 — VCG-02) and 1Cor 10:30 (vc=14360 — VCG-02) involve speech that calls good things evil — the evil here is in the misrepresentation, not in a directly wicked inner state of the speaker. The characteristic also does not include all harmful speech — only speech that is the instrument of inner wickedness (blasphemy, slander, false accusation).

---

#### T1.4 — Modes of Operation

##### T1.4.1 — In what distinct ways does this characteristic operate within the inner person?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The evidence maps at least four distinct modes of inner operation. (1) As a voice — Psa 36:1: "transgression speaks to the wicked deep in his heart" — wickedness operates as an internal governance voice that displaces the divine fear. (2) As a treasury — the wicked person's soul and heart function as a store of evil from which conduct flows (Pro 21:10 "the soul of the wicked desires evil"; implied in VCG-08 speech-revealing cluster — Pro 12:6, 10:6). (3) As a way — wickedness operates as a directional orientation of the will (Eze 3:18; 33:11; Isa 55:7; Pro 4:14) — the inner person is on a trajectory. (4) As a self-generating bondage — Pro 5:22 "the iniquities of the wicked ensnare him, and he is held fast in the cords of his sin" — wickedness feeds itself through the acts it generates, creating a closed inner feedback loop. These four modes are distinct but co-present in the settled wicked person.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The evidence maps four distinct modes of inner operation. (1) As a treasury — the inner person actively draws from an inner store of evil (Mat 12:35 — VCG-03: "out of his evil treasure brings forth evil"; Luk 6:45 — VCG-03: "out of his evil treasure produces evil"). (2) As leaven — the characteristic spreads and corrupts the whole from within (1Cor 5:8 — VCG-05: "the old leaven, the leaven of malice and evil"). (3) As saturation — the inner person is filled with the characteristic (Rom 1:29 — VCG-05: "filled with all manner of unrighteousness, evil, covetousness, malice"; Luk 11:39 — VCG-05: "inside you are full of greed and wickedness"). (4) As a generative source — all evil things come from within the person (Mar 7:23 — VCG-03: "all these evil things come from within, and they defile a person"). These four modes — treasury, leaven, saturation, and generative-source — describe different aspects of the same constitutional condition.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The evidence maps four distinct modes of inner operation. (1) As a heart-level inner condition — the abominable quality is located in the heart itself: Pro 11:20 (vc=1677 — VCG-01 — crooked heart), Pro 16:5 (vc=1689 — VCG-02 — arrogant heart), Pro 26:25 (vc=1694 — VCG-02 — seven abominations in his heart). (2) As a cognitive-inner operation — the thoughts of the wicked are abominable (Pro 15:26 — vc=1679 — VCG-02 — "the thoughts of the wicked are an abomination to the Lord"), meaning cognition itself, when wicked, enters the category of abomination. (3) As a conscience-silencing dynamic — the characteristic operates by suppressing the inner moral faculty of shame (Jer 6:15; Jer 8:12 — VCG-04): the conscience that should produce shame and blushing is rendered wholly non-functional. (4) As an identity-constituting dynamic — the characteristic moves beyond individual acts or states to constitute entire identity: Rev 17:5 (vc=65878 — VCG-05 — the mother of abominations) and Pro 13:19 (vc=1687 — VCG-05 — fools find departing from evil abominable) show abomination as a totalising identity orientation.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The evidence maps four distinct inner modes of operation. (1) As heart-attachment — the heart as the directional inner faculty goes after idol-objects (Eze 11:21 — vc=1631/65982 — VCG-05: "whose heart goes after their detestable things and their abominations"); (2) As soul-delight — the soul's delight-faculty is attached to abominations (Isa 66:3 — vc=1633 — VCG-04: "their soul delights in their abominations") — the appropriate affective faculty of delight, designed for the divine, is inverted; (3) As eye-feasting — the eyes as perceptive-desire faculty feed on detestable things (Eze 20:7 — vc=1634 — VCG-05: "the detestable things your eyes feast on"; Eze 20:8 — vc=65911 — VCG-05: "detestable things their eyes feasted on, nor did they forsake the idols"); (4) As will-stubbornness — the will that persistently refuses to cast away the detestable things (Eze 20:8 — VCG-05; Jer 44:4 — VCG-04: stubbornness despite repeated prophetic warning). These four modes — heart, soul, eyes, will — show the characteristic as engaging all the major inner-being faculties through the single channel of false devotion.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The evidence maps four distinct inner modes of operation. (1) As active cognitive scheming — the mind engaged in planning evil: Eze 11:2 (vc=38193 — VCG-02): "men who devise iniquity and who give wicked counsel"; Mic 2:1 (vc=38217 — VCG-02): "devise wickedness… on their beds"; Psa 36:4 (vc=38235 — VCG-02): "plots trouble while on his bed." (2) As heart-conceiving/generating — evil conceived as an inner birth: Psa 7:14 (vc=38245 — VCG-02): "conceives evil… gives birth to lies"; Job 15:35 (vc=38208 — VCG-02): "conceive trouble and give birth to evil." (3) As stored/harboured inner condition — iniquity held and accumulated: Psa 66:18 (vc=38182 — VCG-04): "cherished iniquity in my heart"; Psa 41:6 (vc=38236 — VCG-04): "his heart gathers iniquity"; Psa 119:133 (vc=38227 — VCG-04): iniquity seeking dominion. (4) As habitual character-orientation — the evildoer's settled way: Pro 17:4 (vc=38219 — VCG-03): "an evildoer listens to wicked lips" — the inner appetite drawn toward harmful content. These four modes — scheming, conceiving, storing, habituating — show iniquity as operating at multiple inner levels simultaneously.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Three distinct inner modes of operation emerge. (1) As defiant will expressing contempt through cursing — the hardened inner will venting its rebellion against God through verbal blasphemy: Rev 16:9/11/21 (VCG-01): scorched, in pain, struck — yet the will curses rather than yields; Rev 13:6 (VCG-01): sustained deliberate blasphemy as total inner orientation. (2) As malicious false judgment expressed through accusation — the hostile inner evaluation of another producing verbal charges: Joh 18:30 (vc=14378 — VCG-03): "if this man were not doing evil, we would not have delivered him over" — the accusers' malicious inner assessment expressed as verbal charge. (3) As conduct-shaped testimony — the inner moral state (of failure or faithfulness) producing speech consequences for others: Rom 2:24 (vc=14357 — VCG-02): the believer's moral failure causes God's name to be blasphemed; 1Pe 2:12 (vc=14377 — VCG-03): honourable conduct causes former accusers to glorify God. Mode 3 operates indirectly — the inner character shapes how others speak about God.

---

##### T1.4.2 — Does this characteristic operate differently depending on context, direction, or constitutional level?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The evidence shows variation by context and level. At the individual constitutional level, wickedness operates as the internal voice displacing God (Psa 36:1 — VCG-02) and the soul's desire-orientation (Pro 21:10 — VCG-09). At the social/relational level, it operates as directed hostility (VCG-03), predatory exploitation (Jer 5:26; Job 24:6), and the perversion of speech (VCG-08). At the institutional level, it operates as structural corruption of justice (Isa 5:23; Hab 1:4; Pro 17:23 — VCG-09). Eze 13:22 (VCG-07) shows it operating through prophetic enablement — false prophets encourage the wicked not to turn. The characteristic also operates differently in the phase of judgment versus the phase of apparent prosperity (Job 21:7 — VCG-10 — "why do the wicked live and grow mighty?" poses the paradox that under apparent prosperity the characteristic continues but its consequences are deferred).

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Yes. The evidence shows variation across contexts. At the individual constitutional level: the heart-as-treasury mode (VCG-03) and the constitutional-baseline mode (VCG-02) — the characteristic is the structural condition from which all else flows. At the social/communal level: the spreading-leaven mode (1Cor 5:8 — VCG-05 — spreading through the community), the relational-complicity mode (2Jo 11 — VCG-04 — whoever greets the wicked person shares in their works), and the community-destruction mode (3Jo 10 — VCG-04 — domineering malice against the church). At the legal-forensic level: ponēros operates in a reduced sense as a crime-category (Act 18:14; 25:18; 28:21 — VCG-06 — minimal inner-being content). At the cosmic level: VCG-01's evil-one/evil-age register addresses the characteristic's supra-personal dimension. The characteristic therefore operates more intensely in the personal constitutional register and diminishes toward the legal-categorical register.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Yes. The evidence shows variation by register. At the inner-character level (VCG-02), the characteristic operates as a quality of the heart/thoughts: Pro 16:5 (arrogant heart), Pro 15:26 (wicked thoughts) — the abomination resides in what the person is and thinks. At the commercial/social level (VCG-01), it operates as a quality of practice revealing inner character: Pro 11:1 (false balance), Deu 25:16 (dishonest practice) — the outward act reveals and expresses the inner moral deficiency. At the worship level (VCG-03), it operates as the contamination of religious approach by inner corruption: Pro 15:8 (wicked person's sacrifice), Isa 1:13 (incense alongside iniquity) — the inner condition renders outward worship repugnant. At the conscience level (VCG-04), it operates through the silence or awakening of the moral faculty. At the identity-eschatological level (VCG-05), it operates as total self-constitution by abomination (Rev 17:5) or fundamental incompatibility with the divine (Rev 21:27).

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Yes. The evidence shows variation by context. At the individual constitutional level: the heart going after idols (Eze 11:21 — VCG-05), the soul delighting in abominations (Isa 66:3 — VCG-04). At the communal-institutional level: VCG-03 (17V — kings institutionalizing or purging abominations — 1Ki 14:24; 2Ki 21:2; 2Ch 36:14 etc.): the characteristic is embedded in political structures and national practice. At the sanctuary/ritual level (VCG-05 — Ezekiel's vision of progressively greater abominations in the sanctuary — Eze 8:6-17): the characteristic operates in the sacred-space dimension, driving the divine presence away through its presence in the sanctuary. At the eschatological-sacrilegious level (VCG-06 — Dan 9:27; Mat 24:15): the characteristic reaches its most extreme outer-event form. The intensity and inner-being content vary: VCGs 04 and 05 have the richest inner-being content; VCG-06 has the least.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Yes. By context: the active-scheming mode (VCG-02) is most concentrated in prophetic and Psalm contexts that address specific acts of devising (Isa 10:1 — VCG-02: institutionalised iniquitous decrees; Eze 11:2 — VCG-02: counsel-giving). The habitual-character mode (VCG-03) operates across the Psalter's evildoer corpus as a generalised person-type. The stored-condition mode (VCG-04) is concentrated in wisdom and prayer contexts (Job 4:8; 11:14; 36:21; Psa 66:18). By constitutional level: the scheming-mode operates at the cognitive level (thoughts, devising — Isa 59:7; Jer 4:14 — VCG-02); the conceiving-mode at the heart level (Isa 32:6 — VCG-02); the stored-mode at the heart-and-hand level (Job 11:14 — VCG-04: "iniquity is in your hand"); the evil-deeds mode (VCG-05) at the deed-level expressing the inner orientation. The constitutional level of operation varies by VCG.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Yes. By direction: VCG-01 operates from the human will outward toward God (blasphemy against God's name/dwelling) — vertical-ascending direction of defiance. VCG-03 operates from one human agent outward toward another (false accusation against the innocent) — horizontal direction of hostile speech. VCG-02 operates in both directions — toward God (Rom 2:24: name dishonoured) and toward persons (Rom 3:8: false attribution of teaching; 1Cor 4:13: slandered to refuse). By constitutional level: VCG-01 evidences the deepest constitutional operation — the hardened will as the source of sustained blasphemy. VCG-03 evidences a more surface-cognitive operation — the malicious false judgment about another. VCG-02 spans from deep (moral failure producing God-dishonour — Rom 2:24) to reactive (denouncing thankful freedom — 1Cor 10:30).

---

##### T1.4.3 — Does this characteristic have a communicative or speech-based mode of operation — and if so, how does it function?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Yes. M10b-A-VCG-08 (12V) specifically evidences the speech-based mode. The wicked person's inner orientation expresses itself through the instrument of speech in multiple registers: concealment of violent intent (Pro 10:6, 10:11 — "the mouth of the wicked conceals violence"), lethal ambush (Pro 12:6 — "the words of the wicked lie in wait for blood"), active consumption of iniquity through speech (Pro 19:28), unreflective pouring out of evil (Pro 15:28), perverse speech as the signature of an inverted moral compass (Pro 10:32), and the social destruction of whole communities through speech (Pro 11:11 — "by the mouth of the wicked [a city] is overthrown"). Beyond VCG-08, Psa 36:1's internal voice of transgression is a speech-mode of the wickedness operating within the person before it expresses outward.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Yes. The speech-based mode is well-evidenced. Mat 12:34 (vc=14419 — VCG-03): "out of the abundance of the heart the mouth speaks" — the constitutionally evil heart overflows into corrupt speech as its most immediate outward expression. Luk 6:45 (vc=14421 — VCG-03): "the evil person out of his evil treasure produces evil, for out of the abundance of the heart his mouth speaks" — the same mechanism. Mat 5:37 (vc=14456 — VCG-04): "anything more than this comes from evil" — verbal elaboration beyond simple honesty signals constitutional inner evil at its communicative mode. 3Jo 10 (vc=14454 — VCG-04): "talking wicked nonsense against us" — the speech is the direct expression of domineering inner malice. Act 28:21 (vc=14464 — VCG-06): "evil" spoken about someone as harmful report. The speech mode operates as the primary mechanism through which constitutional inner evil moves from the internal to the relational and social sphere.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Yes. Two speech-based modes appear. (1) Lying lips as direct abomination: Pro 12:22 (vc=65955 — VCG-02): "lying lips are an abomination to the Lord" — deceptive speech is itself an abominable inner-being expression, not merely a surface act. The lying lips reveal and enact the inner character's deviation from truth. (2) Profession-works disconnect as the NT speech-register: Tit 1:16 (vc=27 — VCG-02): "they profess to know God, but they deny him by their works. They are detestable" — the verbal profession of knowledge combined with the denial through works creates a specifically speech-related abomination, where words claim what the inner being and conduct deny. Wisdom's speech also appears: Pro 8:7 (vc=65953 — VCG-02): "wickedness is an abomination to my lips" — Wisdom's lips as the divine-speech faculty that cannot utter evil. The speech mode reveals abomination as operative through the consistency or inconsistency between verbal claim and inner reality.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The speech-based mode appears primarily in the prophetic-declaration register. Eze 16:2 (vc=1699 — VCG-05): "make known to Jerusalem her abominations" — the prophetic declaration of abominations is speech-as-judgment-instrument. Eze 22:2 (vc=65995 — VCG-05): "declare to her all her abominations" — judicial speech as the instrument through which the accumulated abomination is named and confronted. Eze 12:16 (vc=65983 — VCG-05): survivors are preserved "that they may declare all their abominations among the nations" — the testimony of abominations is itself a communicative mode. The characteristic's own communicative mode is inverse: Jer 32:34 (vc=65907 — VCG-04): "they set up their abominations in the house that is called by my name" — the installation of idols in sacred space is a communicative act, a declarative statement of inner loyalty to idols over the divine covenant. The inner will's idolatrous attachment communicates itself through the physical placement of idols in sacred space.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Yes. Speech is a prominent expressive and constitutive mode. Psa 36:3 (vc=38234 — VCG-04): "the words of his mouth are trouble and deceit" — iniquity stored within flows out through words of trouble and deceit. Psa 10:7 (vc=38225 — VCG-04): "under his tongue are mischief and iniquity" — the iniquity is hidden beneath the tongue, positioned for deployment through speech. Pro 6:12 (vc=38223 — VCG-03): "a worthless person, a wicked man, goes about with crooked speech" — the evildoer's inner character expresses itself in crooked verbal output. Isa 59:4 (vc=38192 — VCG-02): "they speak lies, they conceive mischief and give birth to iniquity" — speech and inner generation are paired; the lies are both the output and the mechanism of iniquity's social propagation. Pro 19:28 (vc=38220 — VCG-03): "the mouth of the wicked devours iniquity" — the mouth actively consumes and thereby reinforces the inner orientation toward evil. Speech operates as both the vehicle through which iniquity is expressed and the channel through which the inner appetite for evil is fed.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Yes — speech is the constitutive mode of operation for this characteristic, not incidental to it. The characteristic is defined as "evil expressed through speech" — speech is the necessary instrument. Rev 13:6 (vc=14356 — VCG-01): "opened its mouth to utter blasphemies" — the mouth-opening and utterance is the characteristic's definitive act. Rev 16:9 (vc=14352 — VCG-01): "cursed the name of God" — the cursing is a speech act. Joh 18:30 (vc=14378 — VCG-03): "if this man were not doing evil, we would not have delivered him over to you" — the false charge is a verbal declaration. Rom 2:24 (vc=14357 — VCG-02): "blasphemed among the Gentiles" — the dishonour is carried through spoken/social communication. The characteristic cannot exist without the speech act: the inner evil must find verbal expression to be CHAR-6. Speech here is not merely expressive but constitutive: it is the operative form that makes the inner evil socially real.

---

#### T1.5 — Immediate Response

##### T1.5.1 — What is the first or most immediate inner-being response to receiving or encountering this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The evidence addresses the response to encountering the wicked person from the outside rather than the inner experience of adopting the characteristic from within. From the outside: the evidence shows immediate moral recoil and avoidance as the appropriate response. Psa 26:5 (VCG-03): "I hate the assembly of evildoers, and I will not sit with the wicked" — deliberate moral separation as the will's first response. Psa 1:1 (VCG-04): the blessed person "walks not in the counsel of the wicked" — avoidance of the wicked person's counsel-register as the first step. Gen 18:25 (VCG-04) and Exo 23:7 (VCG-01) show the first response of the just judge: separation between wicked and righteous (the judicial impulse to name and distinguish). The response from the wicked person's own inner life to correction is the opposite: Pro 9:7 shows the immediate response is injury and abuse — wickedness resists its own naming.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The evidence addresses two types of encounter: encountering the command to abhor evil, and encountering the wicked person who embodies it. For the righteous community encountering the constitutionally evil: Rom 12:9 (vc=14417 — VCG-06) calls for "abhorring" evil — a deep moral revulsion as the first inner response. 1Pe 2:1 (vc=14369 — VCG-05) calls for immediately "putting away" malice as the first act of the community that receives the word. Jam 1:21 (vc=14368 — VCG-05) calls for stripping away rampant wickedness. The immediate response to the characteristic's presence is therefore a call to active repugnance and removal. For the constitutionally evil person encountering truth or testimony: Joh 7:7 (vc=14449 — VCG-04) shows the world hating the one who testifies that its works are evil — the immediate response of the constitutionally evil to exposure is hatred of the witness.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The evidence addresses two distinct immediate-response patterns. From the perspective of the one who perceives abomination in another: Eze 9:4 (vc=1698 — VCG-04) shows the immediate response as sighing and groaning — a conscience-driven, grief-laden inner recoil at encountered abomination. Pro 29:27 (vc=65959 — VCG-01): "an unjust man is an abomination to the righteous" — the righteous person's immediate inner response is moral revulsion mirroring the divine response. From the perspective of the person who has committed abomination without conscience engagement: Jer 6:15 (vc=1680 — VCG-04) and Jer 8:12 (vc=1696 — VCG-04) show no immediate response — the conscience is wholly silenced and produces no shame or blushing. The immediate response therefore varies radically depending on whether conscience is functional (grief and recoil) or silenced (complete inner non-response).

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The evidence shows two distinct immediate-response patterns. From the outside (the reforming king or the prophet): the immediate response to encountering idolatrous abomination is an act of will to remove it — 2Ch 15:8 (vc=65902 — VCG-03): Asa "took courage and put away the detestable idols from all the land"; 2Ki 23:24 (vc=65901 — VCG-03): Josiah "put away the mediums and necromancers and the household gods and the idols and all the abominations." The immediate response of the reforming agent is decisive volitional removal. From inside the characteristic (the community already practising it): the immediate response to prophetic warning is stubborn continuation — Eze 20:8 (vc=65911 — VCG-05): "they rebelled against me and were not willing to listen to me. None of them cast away the detestable things their eyes feasted on" — the immediate inner response to the call to remove is refusal.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Two distinct immediate-response patterns emerge. From the perspective of the victim encountering iniquity from another: Psa 55:3 (vc=38188 — VCG-01): "they drop trouble upon me, and in anger they bear a grudge against me" — the immediate experience of iniquity directed at the victim is crushing pressure and sustained anger from the oppressor. Psa 64:2 (vc=38244 — VCG-03): the psalmist prays for protection from "the secret plots of the wicked" — the immediate response to encountering scheming iniquity is the need for divine covering. From the perspective of the prayer not to receive iniquity's dominion: Psa 119:133 (vc=38227 — VCG-04): "let no iniquity get dominion over me" — the immediate concern is volitional resistance against the characteristic's pull. The evidence shows two distinct encounter-types: the victim's crushing experience and the pray-er's self-protective resistance.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The evidence reveals two distinct immediate-response patterns depending on the position of the encountering person. For the one targeted by false accusation (VCG-03 and VCG-02): 1Cor 4:13 (vc=14351 — VCG-02): "when slandered, we entreat" — the immediate response to receiving slander is non-retaliatory appeal; 1Pe 3:16 (vc=14380 — VCG-03): good conscience maintained amid slander — the immediate response is inner-integrity maintenance. For the recipient of blasphemous speech directed at God: the evidence does not directly document the inner response of the observer who hears blasphemy — the focus is on the blasphemer and the effect. What is evidenced is the non-response of the blasphemer under judgment: Rev 16:9 (VCG-01): no repentance — the characteristic has foreclosed the corrective inner response.

---

##### T1.5.2 — Is the immediate response consistent across the verse evidence, or does it vary?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The immediate response varies significantly by direction. For those outside the characteristic who encounter the wicked person: the evidence shows avoidance, separation, and appeal to divine judgment (Psa 3:7; 17:13; 26:5; 31:17 — VCGs 03, 05). For the wicked person themselves when confronted: the immediate response is aggression, defensive hardening, and rejection of correction (Pro 9:7; Isa 26:10 — VCG-09 and VCG-05). The variation is therefore consistent in pattern: the wicked person's characteristic inner response to any encounter that threatens their orientation is resistance and hardening. The evidence from Eze 33:9 generalises this: "if you warn the wicked to turn from his way, and he does not turn from his way, that person shall die in his iniquity" — the prototypical immediate response is non-turning.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The response varies by the perspective of the encountering person. From outside the characteristic (the righteous community or the believer): the consistent first response is abhorrence and separation — Rom 12:9 (abhor), 1Pe 2:1 (put away), Jam 1:21 (strip away), 1Cor 5:13 (vc=14465 — VCG-04: purge the evil person from among you). From within the characteristic (the constitutionally evil person encountering truth): the consistent first response is resistance — Joh 7:7 (hatred of testimony), Joh 3:19 (vc=14448 — VCG-04: loving darkness rather than light because works are evil). The variation is directional rather than random: the outside perspective consistently generates immediate repugnance and separation; the inside perspective consistently generates resistance to exposure.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The response varies significantly by the state of the encountering person's conscience. The VCG-04 corpus reveals two poles: (1) awakened conscience — Eze 9:4 (vc=1698): sighing and groaning immediately upon perceiving abomination; Eze 36:31 (vc=1681): restored memory producing immediate self-loathing. (2) silenced conscience — Jer 6:15 (vc=1680); Jer 8:12 (vc=1696): committed abomination with no shame or blushing — the immediate response is no response. The variation is therefore not random but is a function of the person's inner state: functional conscience produces immediate grief/revulsion; silenced conscience produces complete inner non-response. This makes the immediate-response variation diagnostically significant — the presence or absence of shame upon encounter with abomination is a direct indicator of the conscience's functional state.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The response varies by the inner state of the encountering person. For those not deeply embedded in the characteristic (reforming kings, the prophets): immediate decisive removal and rejection (VCG-03 reform narratives). For those whose will and heart are already embedded in idolatrous attachment: immediate resistance and refusal (Eze 20:8 — VCG-05; Jer 44:4 — VCG-04: persistent warnings ignored). The variation is consistent in pattern: the functional conscience and uncompromised will respond with removal; the hardened, deeply attached will responds with stubborn continuation. This variation is diagnostically significant — the immediate response to the prophetic call reveals the state of the inner person's attachment.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The response varies by the position of the encountering person. For victims of iniquity (VCG-01 trouble-suffered register): Psa 55:3 (vc=38188 — VCG-01) and Psa 94:16 (vc=38248 — VCG-01): the immediate experience is oppression and isolation — "who rises up for me against the wicked?" For those who witness iniquity: Hab 1:3 (vc=38194 — VCG-01): "Why do you make me see iniquity, and why do you idly look at wrong?" — the immediate response is distress at forced witness of evil. For those praying against the characteristic's grip: Psa 141:4 (vc=38230 — VCG-04): "do not let my heart incline to any evil" — the immediate response is the prayer for inner resistance. Variation is consistent with the person's relational position to the characteristic: the victim suffers; the witness protests; the person who has not yet been captured prays for protection.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The response varies by position. For the slandered/falsely accused (VCG-02/03): 1Cor 4:13 (VCG-02): immediate non-retaliatory entreaty; 1Pe 3:16 (VCG-03): maintained good conscience. For the blasphemer encountering divine judgment (VCG-01): no repentance — the immediate response is further defiance: Rev 16:11 (vc=14350 — VCG-01): "in pain and sores they cursed God rather than repent" — suffering deepens the defiance rather than breaking it. The variation is between the victim's non-retaliatory resilience and the perpetrator's escalated defiance when confronted. The VCG-03 false-accusation context (Joh 18:30 — VCG-03: Jesus delivered over) does not document an immediate inner response of the falsely accused in this corpus.

---

##### T1.5.3 — Where the verse evidence is silent on immediate response, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The evidence is not silent; it is addressed above (T1.5.1–T1.5.2). The evidence does not address the inner phenomenology of initially adopting wickedness (the transition moment) — that is silent. What the evidence richly documents is the response of the established wicked person when encountered, corrected, or threatened.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The evidence is not silent on immediate response; it is addressed in T1.5.1–T1.5.2. What remains unaddressed is the phenomenology of first-person inner experience of the characteristic in the moment of its formation or initial adoption — the evidence does not describe what it feels like to become constitutionally evil. The evidence addresses the established state and responses to it, not the process of its initial emergence. This silence is noted.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The evidence is not silent on immediate response — it is richly documented in VCG-04 (T1.5.1–T1.5.2 above). What is silent is the phenomenological description of the inner experience of the abominable person who is aware of their condition. The evidence describes consequences, verdicts, and responses but not the first-person inner phenomenology of recognition. This silence is noted.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The evidence is not silent on immediate response; it is documented above (T1.5.1–T1.5.2). What is silent is the phenomenological description of the moment of first attachment — the inner experience of first turning the heart toward an idol-object. The evidence documents the established state and responses to it, not the initiation phenomenology. This is noted.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The evidence is not globally silent on immediate response; specific patterns are documented (T1.5.1–T1.5.2). What is silent is the phenomenological description of the immediate inner experience of the person who has just begun scheming iniquity — the first-person experiential account of what it feels like to conceive evil for the first time. The evidence documents the practitioner's established state and the responses of those around them, not the initiation phenomenology. This silence is noted.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The immediate inner response of the observer who witnesses blasphemy is silent in this corpus. The evidence documents the blasphemer's response (further defiance — VCG-01) and the falsely accused's response (non-retaliatory maintenance — VCG-02/03), but not the inner experience of third-party witnesses to blasphemous speech. This silence is noted.

---

#### T1.6 — Sustained Effect

##### T1.6.1 — What does this characteristic produce in the inner being over time?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The sustained operation of wickedness-as-settled-person-identity produces multiple inner consequences documented across VCG-06 (instability) and VCG-09 (moral hollowness). Over time: (1) inner instability intensifies — Pro 10:24 ("what the wicked dreads will come upon him"), Pro 10:25 (no lasting foundation), Pro 10:28 (expectation of the wicked perishing); (2) moral perception degrades — Pro 4:19 ("the way of the wicked is like deep darkness; they do not know over what they stumble") — wickedness progressively blinds the inner faculty of moral sight; (3) the soul's unsatisfied craving deepens — Pro 13:25 ("the belly of the wicked suffers want") — sustained wickedness produces chronic inner want; (4) relational distance from God becomes structural and irreversible without repentance — Pro 15:29 ("the Lord is far from the wicked"); (5) the inner bondage tightens — Pro 5:22 ("ensnared by his own iniquities, held fast in the cords of his sin") — wickedness generates the constraints that deepen it.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The evidence from VCG-06 documents sustained inner consequences. (1) Progressive deterioration: 2Ti 3:13 (vc=14451 — VCG-06): "evil people and impostors will go on from bad to worse, deceiving and being deceived" — deterioration is self-reinforcing and progressive. (2) A defiled conscience: Heb 10:22 (vc=14426 — VCG-06) names the evil conscience as the sustained inner state that makes approach to God impossible. (3) Evil suspicions and relational corruption: 1Ti 6:4 (vc=14470 — VCG-06): evil suspicions arising from conceit and devoid understanding — the characteristic produces a paranoid-suspicious cognitive state. (4) Faithlessness as a settled inner condition: 2Th 3:2 (vc=14450 — VCG-06): faithlessness grounds moral depravity — this is the sustained inner state from which the characteristic's outward expressions flow. (5) Expanding inner darkness: Mat 12:45 (vc=65879 — VCG-06): spirits more evil filling the vacated inner space, the last state worse than the first — the characteristic deepens its hold.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The sustained operation of abominable inner conditions produces: (1) permanent exclusion from divine intimacy — Pro 3:32 (vc=1686 — VCG-02): the devious person is an abomination and excluded from divine confidence, a structural relational consequence that persists; (2) the progressive silencing of the conscience — Jer 6:15 and Jer 8:12 (VCG-04) describe a state of total conscience-silencing where even abomination produces no shame — this is the result of sustained abomination without inner resistance; (3) the permanent weight of shame — Eze 44:13 (vc=66003 — VCG-04): those who committed abominations "shall bear their shame and the abominations that they have committed" — the abominations become a permanent inner weight they carry; (4) identity-constitution by abomination — Rev 17:5 (vc=65878 — VCG-05): sustained generation of abomination produces an identity that is wholly constituted by it. The sustained effect is deepening relational exclusion and identity corruption.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

VCG-05 (Ezekiel — 43V) documents the sustained inner consequences in detail. (1) Progressive deepening: Eze 8:13 (vc=65978 — VCG-05): "You will see still greater abominations than these" — each stage surpasses the last; (2) Constitutional transformation: Hos 9:10 (vc=1632 — VCG-04): "they became detestable like the thing they loved" — the devotion-to-idols transforms the person's own inner character toward the image of what they worship; (3) Moral numbness: Eze 8:17 (vc=65980 — VCG-05): "is it too light a thing for the house of Judah to commit the abominations that they commit here" — they treat abomination as a minor matter, showing deepening moral insensitivity; (4) Memory loss: Eze 16:22 (vc=65985 — VCG-05): "in all your abominations and your whorings you did not remember the days of your youth" — the faculty of covenantal memory is suppressed; (5) Divine-presence loss: Eze 5:11 (vc=65969 — VCG-05): God withdraws from the defiled sanctuary.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The evidence documents a trajectory of progressive inner degradation. (1) Wisdom displaced: Psa 36:3 (vc=38234 — VCG-04): "he has ceased to act wisely and do good" — over time, the characteristic crowds out wisdom from the inner life.
