(2) Conscience deadened: Pro 30:20 (vc=38222 — VCG-04): the adulteress "wipes her mouth and says, 'I have done no wrong'" — the conscience that should register iniquity has been entirely silenced through habitual commission. (3) Inner appetite increasingly attuned to evil: Pro 17:4 (vc=38219 — VCG-03): "an evildoer listens to wicked lips" — the inner ear becomes preferentially attuned to evil speech; Pro 19:28 (vc=38220 — VCG-03): "the mouth of the wicked devours iniquity" — the appetite actively feeds on wrongdoing. (4) Irrecoverable collapse: Psa 36:12 (vc=38233 — VCG-04): "there the evildoers lie fallen; they are thrust down, unable to rise" — the sustained trajectory terminates in total ruin.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The VCG-01 corpus documents the sustained inner consequences with particular intensity. Rev 16:9 → 16:11 → 16:21 (VCG-01): the sequence across three plague events shows escalating defiance — each judgment produces not repentance but more cursing. The sustained effect is progressive hardening of the will against God: the more judgment falls, the more the characteristic deepens. Rev 13:6 (vc=14356 — VCG-01): "a total inner orientation of defiant contempt toward the divine" — sustained blasphemy establishes a comprehensive inner stance of contempt that defines the person's entire orientation toward God. For those falsely accused (VCG-03): 1Pe 2:12 (vc=14377 — VCG-03) and 1Pe 3:16 (vc=14380 — VCG-03): the sustained effect on the target of false accusation is the patient maintenance of good conscience and honourable conduct — the opposite of the characteristic producing counter-formation in the victim.

---

##### T1.6.2 — What states, qualities, capacities, or orientations does sustained exposure to or possession of this characteristic establish?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Sustained possession of wickedness-as-settled-person-identity establishes: (a) moral blindness as a perceptual state (Pro 4:19; Isa 26:10 — even grace cannot penetrate; Dan 12:10 — the wicked "cannot understand"); (b) spiritual restlessness as a persistent condition (Isa 57:20–21 — "like the tossing sea… there is no peace for the wicked"); (c) hardened defiance as an inner posture (Eze 3:19 — refusing to turn even when warned; Isa 26:10 — incorrigibility under favour); (d) an appetite for evil as a soul-level orientation (Pro 21:10 — "the soul of the wicked desires evil"); (e) a corrupted deliberative faculty (Job 21:16 — "the counsel of the wicked is far from me" — wickedness generates a morally alien mode of reasoning). These are stable states, not transient reactions.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Sustained possession of evil as constitutional inner nature establishes: (a) defiled conscience as a permanent inner state (Heb 10:22 — VCG-06 — making approach to God structurally impossible); (b) a hostile, alienated mind (Col 1:21 — VCG-06 — "hostile in mind, doing evil deeds" — a stable cognitive orientation of enmity); (c) inner saturation with vice clusters (Rom 1:29 — VCG-05 — "filled with all manner of unrighteousness, evil, covetousness, malice" — the saturation state is a stable condition of the whole inner person); (d) moral deterioration as a trajectory (2Ti 3:13 — VCG-06 — "from bad to worse" — the trajectory of sustained possession is downward); (e) the suppression of truth as a stable inner operation (Rom 1:18 — VCG-05 — "suppress the truth" as a sustained act of the unrighteous inner person). These are not episodic but stable states established over time.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Sustained possession of abominable inner conditions establishes: (a) a conscience wholly non-functional with respect to shame — Jer 6:15 (vc=1680 — VCG-04): "they did not know how to blush" — the sustained abomination has rendered the shame-faculty inoperative; (b) a will inverted regarding moral departure — Pro 13:19 (vc=1687 — VCG-05): "to turn away from evil is an abomination to fools" — the sustained character finds the very idea of departure from evil repugnant; (c) a hidden interior packed with multiple corrupt motivations — Pro 26:25 (vc=1694 — VCG-02): "seven abominations in his heart" behind gracious speech — the inner life becomes layered with multiple concurrent corrupt drives; (d) the accumulated weight of shame and disgrace — Eze 44:13 (vc=66003 — VCG-04): the abominations become an inner burden preventing sacred service.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Sustained possession of idolatrous abomination establishes: (a) constitutional transformation toward the image of idols — Hos 9:10 (vc=1632 — VCG-04): "became detestable like the thing they loved" — the person's inner character is re-shaped by sustained idolatrous attachment; (b) moral numbness toward the gravity of abomination — Eze 8:17 (vc=65980 — VCG-05): treating abomination as a light matter; (c) the suppression of covenantal memory — Eze 16:22 (vc=65985 — VCG-05): forgetting; Eze 16:43 (vc=65987 — VCG-05): failure to remember youth — the covenantal-gratitude memory is silenced; (d) an inverted affective delight — Isa 66:3 (vc=1633 — VCG-04): the soul delights in abominations rather than recoiling; (e) the acceleration of moral deterioration — Eze 16:47-48 (vc=65988 — VCG-05): "within a very little time you were more corrupt than they in all your ways" — the trajectory is one of deepening beyond comparable models.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Sustained possession of iniquity as active scheming establishes: (a) iniquity's dominion over the will — Psa 119:133 (vc=38227 — VCG-04): "let no iniquity get dominion over me" — the sustained inner presence of iniquity seeks to control the will's direction; (b) the old way of wicked men as an ingrained moral trajectory — Job 22:15 (vc=38210 — VCG-04): "the old way that wicked men have trod" — a worn inner path that becomes habitual and difficult to leave; (c) the inner capacity for self-deception about one's own iniquity — Pro 30:20 (vc=38222 — VCG-04): "I have done no wrong" — moral self-blindness as a settled orientation; (d) the severing of the prayer-relationship with God — Psa 66:18 (vc=38182 — VCG-04): cherished iniquity forecloses divine listening; (e) an appetite that actively seeks evil input — Pro 19:28 (vc=38220 — VCG-03): mouth devouring iniquity.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Sustained possession of evil expressed through speech establishes: (a) the hardened will as a fixed inner orientation — Rev 16:9/11/21 (VCG-01): across three separate divine judgments, the will maintains its defiant posture; the sustained characteristic has solidified the will against God; (b) the foreclosure of repentance — Rev 16:9 (VCG-01): "they did not repent"; Rev 16:11 (VCG-01): "they did not repent of their deeds" — sustained blasphemy has rendered the will incapable of the repentance that would reverse it; (c) contempt as the primary inner stance toward the divine and toward authority — Jude 8 (vc=14354 — VCG-01): authority-rejection and glorious-ones-blasphemy as settled dispositions; (d) instinct-level operation without rational comprehension — Jude 10 (vc=14355 — VCG-01): "blaspheme all that they do not understand, destroyed by all that they… understand instinctively" — the characteristic has reduced operation to pre-rational instinct.

---

##### T1.6.3 — Does the sustained effect differ from the immediate response — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Yes. The immediate response (T1.5.1–T1.5.2) is characterised by resistance, aggression, and rejection of correction. The sustained effect is deeper: it is constitutional degradation — the progressive reduction of the person's capacity for moral perception (Pro 4:19; Dan 12:10), the establishment of chronic inner want (Pro 13:25), and the intensification of inner bondage (Pro 5:22). The immediate response is behavioural; the sustained effect is constitutional. The difference is between the wicked person hitting back when confronted (immediate) and the wicked person becoming progressively less capable of moral sight and inner peace over the course of their life (sustained). Job 15:20 ("the wicked man writhes in pain all his days") is the sustained-effect statement.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Yes. The immediate response (T1.5.1) is characterised by resistance to exposure (Joh 7:7 — hatred of testimony) and, from the outside, calls to abhorrence and separation. The sustained effect is deeper constitutional degradation: the conscience is defiled (Heb 10:22), the mind becomes habitually hostile (Col 1:21), progressive deterioration advances (2Ti 3:13), and inner saturation solidifies (Rom 1:29). The immediate response is reactive; the sustained effect is structural. The difference is analogous to the distinction Mat 7:17-18 (VCG-02) draws: the immediate bad fruit is the immediate response (an episodic bad act), but the diseased tree (sustained effect) is the structural condition that makes every episode of bad fruit inevitable.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Yes, markedly. The immediate response (T1.5.1) ranges from grief/recoil (awakened conscience) to complete non-response (silenced conscience). The sustained effect is always deteriorating: even for those whose conscience was initially functional, sustained proximity to or commission of abomination without address produces the conscience-silencing trajectory (Jer 6:15; 8:12). The immediate grieving response (Eze 9:4) is the response of those who have not yet committed the abominations themselves — their conscience remains functional. The sustained effect on the person who commits abominations is the progressive silencing of the very conscience that would produce the immediate-grief response. The difference is between the immediate moral recoil (possible early) and the settled non-response (the outcome of sustained unaddressed abomination).

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Yes, markedly. The immediate response to initial idolatrous temptation (Deu 20:18 — vc=65932 — VCG-02: "that they may not teach you to do according to all their abominable practices") is resisted at the volitional level — the Deuteronomic warnings address the will before the attachment is formed. The sustained effect, once attachment has formed and deepened, is the progressive loss of the inner capacities that would enable departure: moral numbness (Eze 8:17 — VCG-05), memory loss (Eze 16:22 — VCG-05), constitutional transformation (Hos 9:10 — VCG-04). The immediate-response stage is volitional and addressable by warning; the sustained-effect stage has transformed the inner faculties themselves, requiring divine intervention (Eze 37:23 — VCG-05: divine cleansing) rather than merely a renewed volitional choice.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Yes, markedly. The immediate response (T1.5.1) ranges from the victim's experience of crushing pressure to the self-aware person's prayer for protection. The sustained effect is the progressive corruption of the inner person's own faculties: wisdom displaced (Psa 36:3 — VCG-04), conscience deadened (Pro 30:20 — VCG-04), appetite re-oriented toward evil (Pro 17:4; 19:28 — VCG-03), will increasingly dominated by iniquity (Psa 119:133 — VCG-04). The immediate-response stage still involves some self-awareness (the prayer of Psa 119:133 — VCG-04 is possible); the sustained-effect stage has progressively eroded the very faculties that would enable self-awareness. The difference is between the moment of first encounter and the settled habitual condition.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Yes. The immediate response to divine judgment (Rev 16:9 — first plague) is defiant cursing — already showing a hardened will. The sustained effect across multiple judgments (Rev 16:9 → 16:11 → 16:21 — VCG-01) is not a change in kind but an intensification and solidification: the same pattern repeated under increasingly severe judgments shows the will becoming more fixed rather than softened. The sustained effect is thus the entrenchment of what began as the immediate response. For the slandered apostle (1Cor 4:13 — VCG-02): the immediate response is non-retaliatory entreaty; the sustained effect implies continued maintenance of this posture — the counter-formation of the victim is equally sustained.

---

#### T1.7 — Conditions of Reception

##### T1.7.1 — What inner conditions or orientations enable genuine reception of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The evidence is not framed around "receiving" wickedness as though it is something bestowed. The question is better addressed as: what inner conditions enable the settling of this characteristic in a person? The evidence suggests: (a) the pre-existing exclusion of God from the mind (Psa 10:4 — the wicked's practical atheism pre-exists and enables the settled orientation); (b) the abandonment of counsel from the righteous (Psa 1:1 — alignment with wicked counsel); (c) the decision to enter "the path of the wicked" (Pro 4:14 — VCG-07 — wickedness is entered as a path); (d) the silencing of the internal voice of God-fear (Psa 36:1 — the replacement of God-fear with transgression's voice is the enabling inner event). The characteristic settles where the God-orientation of the inner person has been abandoned.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The question "reception" is analytically unusual for this characteristic since it is framed as a constitutional baseline condition rather than something received from outside. The evidence addresses the conditions under which the characteristic deepens and consolidates rather than its initial reception. Deepening conditions: (1) the absence of faith — Heb 3:12 (vc=14423 — VCG-06): the evil, unbelieving heart leads to apostasy; (2) the absence of the received word — Jam 1:21 (vc=14368 — VCG-05): rampant wickedness must be stripped away before the word can take root — the presence of wickedness blocks reception of the word, and presumably the absence of the word enables the wickedness to consolidate; (3) vacated inner space — Mat 12:45 (vc=65879 — VCG-06): the swept but unoccupied inner space invites deeper evil; (4) self-seeking and obedience to unrighteousness — Rom 2:8 (vc=14338 — VCG-05): the self-seeking person who "does not obey the truth but obeys unrighteousness" is in a state enabling the characteristic's deepening.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The characteristic is not primarily a received condition but an inner moral condition that develops from within. The enabling conditions for its development are: (1) the prior erosion or silencing of the conscience — Jer 6:15 (vc=1680 — VCG-04) describes the state where conscience has already been silenced, which is both a symptom and an enabling condition for further abomination; (2) the crooked heart as a settled inner condition — Pro 11:20 (vc=1677 — VCG-01) and Pro 3:32 (vc=1686 — VCG-02): the devious inner orientation enables the specific inner qualities named as abominable; (3) the absence of hearing the law — Pro 28:9 (vc=65958 — VCG-03): "if one turns away his ear from hearing the law, even his prayer is an abomination" — the deliberate rejection of divine instruction opens the person to abominable inner conditions by removing the corrective that would otherwise check them; (4) the absence of discernment — Isa 44:19 (vc=65961 — VCG-05): no consideration, no knowledge or discernment allows abomination without recognition.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The enabling conditions for idolatrous abomination to take root are: (1) proximity to peoples who practice it — Deu 20:18 (vc=65932 — VCG-02): the nations "may not teach you to do according to all their abominable practices" — proximity and relational exposure enables reception; (2) the absence of active covenant separation — Ezr 9:1 (vc=65949 — VCG-03): failure to separate from peoples with abominations opens the inner person to their influence; (3) the coveting of what is attractive in the idol — Deu 7:25 (vc=1682 — VCG-02): "you shall not covet the silver or gold on them or take it for yourselves, lest you be ensnared by it" — inner coveting of what is on the idol is the mechanism of reception; (4) marital-relational entanglement — Ezr 9:14 (vc=65950 — VCG-03): intermarriage with abomination-practicing peoples as the relational channel through which inner attachment is received.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The enabling conditions are: (1) chosen association with evildoers — Job 34:8 (vc=38214 — VCG-04): "who travels in company with evildoers and walks with wicked men" — chosen relational proximity shapes inner character toward iniquity; Psa 141:4 (vc=38230 — VCG-04): the prayer against "busy myself with wicked deeds in company with men who work iniquity" shows that association is the primary entry vector; (2) the heart's susceptibility to incline — Psa 141:4 (vc=38230 — VCG-04): "do not let my heart incline to any evil" — the heart's inclination capacity is what is at risk; (3) the will's preference for iniquity over affliction — Job 36:21 (vc=38216 — VCG-04): "this you have chosen rather than affliction" — volitional choice of the easier/more attractive iniquitous path over the hard righteous one; (4) the absence of active volitional resistance — Psa 119:133 (vc=38227 — VCG-04): the prayer for steadiness implies its absence would enable reception.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The enabling inner conditions for generating evil expressed through speech: (1) the hardened will that refuses to yield to divine authority — Rev 16:9/11/21 (VCG-01): the will hardened against repentance enables defiant blasphemy; (2) the rejection of legitimate authority — Jude 8 (vc=14354 — VCG-01): "relying on their dreams, they reject authority and blaspheme the glorious ones" — authority-rejection is the enabling inner condition for the blasphemous expression; (3) incomprehension — Jude 10 (vc=14355 — VCG-01): "blaspheme all that they do not understand" — the absence of cognitive understanding leaves contempt as the inner substitute; (4) moral failure in those representing God — Rom 2:24 (vc=14357 — VCG-02): moral failure enables the social defamation of God's name; (5) malicious hostile evaluation of another — Joh 18:30 (vc=14378 — VCG-03): the accusers' inner evaluation ("if this man were not doing evil") enables the false charge.

---

##### T1.7.2 — What inner conditions block, distort, or prevent reception?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The evidence from VCG-04 (moral contrast) and VCG-07 (directional orientation) shows that the conditions blocking wickedness-as-settled-person-identity are: (a) active fear of God (its absence is definitional for the wicked — Psa 36:1; its presence in Psa 1:1 is the blessed person's condition); (b) the counsel of the righteous (Psa 1:1 — the blessed person avoids the wicked's counsel); (c) responsiveness to the prophetic call to turn (Eze 3:18–19; 33:8–19 — the wicked who turns is specifically the one who has not settled into the characteristic). The primary blocking condition is the sustained orientation of the inner person toward God — sustained non-service (Mal 3:18 defines the wicked by their non-service, so service is the blocking condition).

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The evidence names specific inner conditions that block the characteristic's deepening and expression: (1) genuine love — Rom 12:9 (vc=14417 — VCG-06): love actively abhors evil and holds fast to good — love's orientation structurally opposes the characteristic; (2) the implanted word — Jam 1:21 (vc=14368 — VCG-05): the received word blocks rampant wickedness from remaining; (3) faith and the word of God — 1Jo 2:14 (vc=14430 — VCG-01): "the word of God abides in you, and you have overcome the evil one" — the word's abiding in the person is the primary blocking condition; (4) the cleansed conscience through Christ — Heb 10:22 (vc=14426 — VCG-06): the conscience "sprinkled clean from an evil conscience" is the transformed state that blocks the characteristic's access to the relational dimension; (5) divine armor — Eph 6:16 (vc=14428 — VCG-01): faith as shield extinguishing the evil one's flaming darts.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The blocking conditions are: (1) a functional, shame-producing conscience — Eze 9:4 (vc=1698 — VCG-04): those who sigh and groan over abominations are marked for protection — their operative conscience is what prevents them from committing abomination themselves; (2) the hearing and keeping of law — Pro 28:9 (vc=65958 — VCG-03): the inverse of turning away the ear from the law; (3) the upright inner way — Pro 3:32 (vc=1686 — VCG-02): the upright person is in God's confidence precisely because their inner orientation is not crooked, meaning uprightness of inner way is the blocking condition; (4) discernment and reflection — Isa 44:19 (vc=65961 — VCG-05): the one who "considers" and has "knowledge or discernment" would perceive the abomination before committing it.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Blocking conditions: (1) active covenant separation — Deu 18:9 (vc=65931 — VCG-02): "you shall not learn to follow the abominable practices of those nations" — proactive non-learning is a blocking condition; (2) immediate destruction of idol-objects — Deu 7:25 (vc=1682 — VCG-02): "you shall burn with fire" — the removal of the physical object removes the attraction-mechanism; (3) hearing and responding to the prophetic word — Eze 20:8 (vc=65911 — VCG-05) shows the alternative: the command to "cast away the detestable things your eyes feast on" — compliance with this command would have blocked the characteristic; (4) the active removal of abominable objects from the inner community — 2Ch 15:8 (vc=65902 — VCG-03): Asa's reform — the act of purging protects the community's inner space from idolatrous influence.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Blocking conditions: (1) open ears to instruction — Job 36:10 (vc=38215 — VCG-04): "He opens their ears to instruction and commands that they return from iniquity" — receptivity to divine instruction is the primary inner block; (2) maintained steps according to divine promise — Psa 119:133 (vc=38227 — VCG-04): "keep steady my steps according to your promise" — volitional steadiness following the divine word blocks iniquity's dominion; (3) active releasing of iniquity held in the hand — Job 11:14 (vc=38207 — VCG-04): "if iniquity is in your hand, put it far away" — volitional distance from held iniquity as a blocking act; (4) forsaking iniquitous thoughts and returning to the Lord — Isa 55:7 (vc=38200 — VCG-02): the prescribed internal blocking movement; (5) cleansing the heart — Jer 4:14 (vc=38205 — VCG-02): "O Jerusalem, wash your heart from evil, that you may be saved" — the commanded inner cleansing as the blocking act.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Blocking conditions: (1) repentance — Rev 16:9 (VCG-01): "they did not repent" — its presence would have arrested the characteristic; the absence of repentance enables continued blasphemy; (2) good conscience — 1Pe 3:16 (vc=14380 — VCG-03): "having a good conscience" — the inner integrity of conscience protects against both generating false accusation and being undone by it; (3) honourable conduct — 1Pe 2:12 (vc=14377 — VCG-03): honourable conduct prevents the generation of justified accusations; (4) accurate understanding — Jude 10 (vc=14355 — VCG-01): the contrary of not-understanding; if they understood, they would not blaspheme; (5) submission to authority — Jude 8 (vc=14354 — VCG-01): the contrary of authority-rejection; authority-submission blocks the blasphemy that flows from authority-rejection.

---

##### T1.7.3 — What is the inner-being state of the person who encounters this characteristic but does not receive it?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The person who encounters the wicked but does not adopt the characteristic maintains deliberate moral separation and inner integrity. Psa 26:5 (VCG-03) is the clearest evidence: "I hate the assembly of evildoers, and I will not sit with the wicked" — the maintenance of moral separation requires an active internal stance of refusal. Psa 1:1 (VCG-04) describes the blessed person as defined by what they refuse to enter. The wicked's social-corrosive power (Num 16:26 — VCG-04 — "proximity risks being swept away") indicates that the person who does not receive the characteristic must actively distance; the inner state is one of maintained integrity against a contagious force. 2Ch 19:2 (VCG-03) warns that helping the wicked even without adopting their wickedness draws divine displeasure — the inner state of the non-receiver must include practical separation, not merely internal distinction.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The person who encounters evil as constitutional inner nature in another but does not absorb it maintains a posture of active moral abhorrence and protective separation. Rom 12:9 (vc=14417 — VCG-06): the commanded inner state is "abhorrence" of evil combined with holding fast to the good — the non-receiver's inner state is one of active moral revulsion maintained as a deliberate orientation. 1Cor 5:13 (vc=14465 — VCG-04): the community that expels the evil person is the community whose own constitutional condition is healthy enough to recognise and reject the invasive one. 1Cor 14:20 (vc=14364 — VCG-05): "be infants in evil" — the non-receiver is characterised by moral inexperience in the domain of evil — an inner state of preserved moral simplicity in this domain.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The person who encounters abominable conditions (in others or as an inner temptation) and does not receive them maintains a state of active moral revulsion and grief. Eze 9:4 (vc=1698 — VCG-04): those who "sigh and groan over all the abominations committed in it" — the inner state is one of conscience-driven grief that mirrors the divine revulsion. Pro 29:27 (vc=65959 — VCG-01): "an unjust man is an abomination to the righteous" — the righteous person's inner response to the abominable is moral revulsion. This is the functionally conscience-alive person: their inner moral faculty identifies the abominable, recoils from it in grief or revulsion, and marks them as distinct from those who commit it without response. The non-receiving state is one of inner moral perceptiveness and affective-moral recoil.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The non-receiving person maintains a state of active moral revulsion and decisive removal. 2Ch 15:8 (vc=65902 — VCG-03): Asa "took courage and put away the detestable idols" — courage and decisive action characterise the non-receiver. 2Ki 23:24 (vc=65901 — VCG-03): Josiah's comprehensive purge — the non-receiving community leader actively removes every form of the characteristic. The inner state is one of covenant loyalty that finds idolatrous abomination repugnant (mirroring the divine revulsion) and is moved to decisive corrective action. This mirrors Eze 9:4 (from CHAR-3's corpus) — the grieving conscience that marks the person for protection by refusing to participate.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The non-receiving person maintains a state of active rejection and volitional distance from iniquity. Psa 101:8 (vc=38226 — VCG-03): the royal psalmist "morning by morning will destroy all the wicked in the land, cutting off all the evildoers" — the non-receiver is actively engaged in removing the characteristic from the communal space. Psa 141:9 (vc=38231 — VCG-03): prayer for protection from evildoers' snares — the non-receiver maintains a state of watchful protection. Job 11:14 (vc=38207 — VCG-04): "if iniquity is in your hand, put it far away" — the non-receiver is one who has actively distanced themselves from held iniquity. The inner state of non-reception is characterised by active rejection, volitional distancing, and the willingness to call on the Lord (contrasted with evildoers who "do not call upon the Lord" — Psa 14:4 — VCG-03).

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The non-receiving person (the one who does not generate evil speech when provoked) maintains: (1) non-retaliatory inner orientation — 1Cor 4:13 (vc=14351 — VCG-02): "when slandered, we entreat" — the inner state is one of constrained, non-retaliatory appeal rather than counter-blast; (2) good conscience — 1Pe 3:16 (vc=14380 — VCG-03): "having a good conscience, so that when you are slandered, those who revile your good behavior in Christ may be put to shame" — the inner integrity of good conscience is the foundation of the non-receiving state; (3) honourable-conduct orientation — 1Pe 2:12 (vc=14377 — VCG-03): the non-receiver lives honorably, producing good deeds that eventually silence the false accusation. The inner state of non-reception is: good conscience + non-retaliatory entreaty + honourable conduct orientation.

---

#### T1.8 — Dimension Classification

##### T1.8.1 — What is the primary inner-being dimension of this characteristic from the programme's dimension vocabulary?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The primary dimension is volitional-dispositional: wickedness-as-settled-person-identity is fundamentally a settled orientation of the will — a direction the will has taken and consolidated. The evidence is concentrated here: Eze 3:18; 33:8; 33:11 use "way" (derek) as the primary metaphor, consistently indicating a volitional direction. Isa 55:7 calls for the wicked to "forsake his way and the unrighteous man his thoughts" — the volitional dimension is the primary address for potential reversal. Pro 4:14 ("do not enter the path of the wicked") frames the characteristic as a volitional entry. The God-exclusion (Psa 10:4; 10:13) is volitional — the wicked "renounce God" from within their heart. This is a dimension of active will, not merely a passive condition imposed from outside.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The primary dimension is constitutional-structural: evil as constitutional inner nature is first and foremost a structural condition of the inner person — the state the inner architecture is in by default. The evidence from VCG-02 and VCG-03 is definitional: the tree-nature metaphor (Mat 7:17-18) names a constitutional-structural condition that determines output; the heart-as-treasury (Mat 12:35; Luk 6:45) names a structural reservoir from which evil is actively drawn. This differs from the volitional-dispositional primary dimension of CHAR-1: CHAR-2's primary reference is not "the direction the will has taken" but "the structural condition from which all output flows." The constitutional-condition classification is the most analytically accurate primary dimension.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The primary dimension is relational-moral: the characteristic is constitutively defined by the divine-human relational verdict of revulsion in response to inner moral conditions. Every to.e.vah statement is framed relationally — "an abomination to the Lord," "an abomination to the righteous" — the characteristic cannot be defined without reference to the responding other. This is distinct from the volitional-dispositional primary of CHAR-1 or the constitutional-structural primary of CHAR-2. CHAR-3's primary dimension is the relational-evaluative encounter between divine holiness and human inner moral character, in which divine revulsion is the constitutive response. Supporting evidence: Pro 3:32 (vc=1686 — VCG-02): the devious person is an abomination and excluded from divine confidence — the relational consequence is definitional; Luk 16:15 (vc=21 — VCG-02): what is exalted among men is an abomination in the sight of God — the divine sight/relational perspective is what defines the category.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The primary dimension is volitional-devotional: idolatrous abomination is fundamentally the will's directional choice and sustained commitment to idol-objects as the object of the devotion-capacity. The Ezekiel VCG-05 corpus (43V) consistently frames the characteristic as a directional volitional commitment: Eze 11:21 (vc=1631 — VCG-05): "heart goes after" — directional volitional movement; Eze 20:8 (vc=65911 — VCG-05): "not willing to listen… none of them cast away" — volitional refusal to depart; Eze 14:6 context parallel: "turn away your faces from all your abominations" — the volitional turn is the prescribed address. The Deuteronomic VCG-02 corpus (14V) addresses the will directly: Deu 18:9 (VCG-02 — "shall not learn to follow"), Deu 7:25 (VCG-02 — "shall not covet"). The characteristic's primary dimension is the will's devotional direction.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The primary dimension is cognitive-volitional-generative: iniquity as active inner scheming operates primarily through the combined engagement of the cognitive faculty (devising, planning, thinking) and the volitional faculty (choosing, refusing to reject evil, executing at dawn). VCG-02 (14V — the deliberate inner generation register) is the most definitionally central sub-corpus. Isa 59:7 (vc=38203 — VCG-02): "their thoughts are thoughts of iniquity" — the cognitive dimension. Mic 2:1 (vc=38217 — VCG-02): "devise wickedness… when the morning dawns, they perform it" — the volitional execution following the cognitive devising. Isa 32:6 (vc=38181 — VCG-02): "his heart is busy with iniquity" — the heart's generative activity as the productive centre. The primary dimension is thus: volitional-generative (the will's deliberate commitment to producing evil from within through cognitive scheming).

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The primary dimension is volitional-expressive: the characteristic is constitutively the will's expression of wickedness through the speech-instrument. The will is the primary faculty — VCG-01 is the definitional core: Rev 16:9 (vc=14352 — VCG-01): "they did not repent" — the will's refusal is the central inner-being reality; Rev 16:11 (vc=14350 — VCG-01): "they did not repent of their deeds" — the will is the faculty whose orientation produces or refuses to produce the characteristic-reversing act of repentance. Jude 8 (vc=14354 — VCG-01): "reject authority" — the will's authority-rejection is the inner source of the blasphemous speech. The expression through speech is the characteristic's defining mode — speech is not incidental but essential. The primary dimension is therefore volitional-expressive: will-wickedness enacted through the speech faculty.

---

##### T1.8.2 — What evidence from the verse evidence supports this classification?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Supporting the volitional-dispositional classification: (1) the "way" metaphor throughout VCG-07 (22V) — Eze 3:18; 33:8, 11, 12, 14, 15, 19; Pro 4:14, 4:19; Isa 55:7 — consistently locating the characteristic as a direction one travels; (2) the Ezekiel repentance corpus (Eze 18:21–27; 33:12–19) shows that reversal occurs at exactly the volitional level — "turns away from all his sins and does what is just and right"; (3) Pro 21:10 ("the soul of the wicked desires evil") — even the soul-level desire is oriented, not merely inert; (4) the practical-atheism cluster (VCG-02, 8V) uses volitional language — "does not seek" (Psa 10:4), "renounces God" (Psa 10:13), "forgetting God" (Psa 9:17). The act of exclusion is consistently volitional.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Supporting the constitutional-structural classification: (1) Mat 7:17-18 (vc=14439-14440 — VCG-02): the tree-nature language — "a diseased tree cannot bear good fruit" — is constitutional, not volitional; (2) Mat 7:11 and Luk 11:13 (vc=14438, 14445 — VCG-02): "you who are evil" — the use of "are" addresses a constitutive state, not a chosen direction; (3) Mar 7:23 (vc=14422 — VCG-03): "all these evil things come from within" — the inside-out direction of causation is constitutional; (4) Rom 1:29 (vc=14337 etc. — VCG-05): "filled with all manner of unrighteousness" — saturation is a structural condition, not a volitional act; (5) Heb 10:22 (vc=14426 — VCG-06): "evil conscience" as a structural inner-faculty state that blocks approach to God. The constitutional evidence is the dominant framing of the characteristic's 90-verse corpus.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Supporting the relational-moral primary: (1) every instance of the characteristic in the corpus is framed as "abomination to the Lord / to the righteous" — never as "this is abominable in itself" without reference to a responding subject; (2) Pro 3:32 (vc=1686 — VCG-02): the relational consequence (exclusion from divine confidence) is presented as co-definitional with the abomination category; (3) Pro 29:27 (vc=65959 — VCG-01): the mutual abomination of wicked and righteous shows the characteristic as constitutively relational — each is an abomination to the other, showing that abomination names a relationship of fundamental moral incompatibility; (4) Luk 16:15 (vc=21 — VCG-02): the explicit reference to God's sight as the defining perspective confirms the relational-evaluative framing; (5) Eze 9:4 (vc=1698 — VCG-04): those who grieve over abominations mirror the divine relational response — the characteristic propagates through the relational chain of moral revulsion.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Supporting the volitional-devotional primary: (1) the Deuteronomic volitional language (VCG-02) — "shall not covet" (Deu 7:25), "shall not learn to follow" (Deu 18:9), "shall not worship" (Deu 12:31) — all addressing the will directly; (2) Eze 11:21 (vc=1631 — VCG-05): "heart goes after their detestable things" — the heart's directional faculty as the primary location; (3) Eze 20:8 (vc=65911 — VCG-05): "not willing to listen; none of them cast away" — volitional refusal as the characteristic's defining inner stance; (4) Isa 66:3 (vc=1633 — VCG-04): "they have chosen their own ways" — volitional choice is the stated mechanism; (5) the reform narratives (VCG-03): kings' wills are what install or purge the abominations — the characteristically volitional-institutional dimension.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Supporting the cognitive-volitional-generative primary: (1) the bed-plotting evidence (Psa 36:4 — VCG-02: "plots trouble while on his bed"; Mic 2:1 — VCG-02: "devise wickedness… on their beds") shows deliberate premeditated inner planning; (2) the conceive-and-birth metaphor (Psa 7:14 — VCG-02; Job 15:35 — VCG-02; Isa 59:4 — VCG-02) frames iniquity as the generative output of deliberate inner process; (3) the "heart busy with" evidence (Isa 32:6 — VCG-02) names the heart's productive activity as the locus; (4) the volitional choice evidence (Job 36:21 — VCG-04: "for this you have chosen rather than affliction"; Isa 29:20 — VCG-02: "all who watch to do evil") shows deliberate volitional commitment; (5) the warning-to-the-will evidence (Job 36:10 — VCG-04: return from iniquity; Psa 119:133 — VCG-04: resist dominion) confirms the will as the primary faculty the characteristic inhabits.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Supporting the volitional-expressive primary: (1) VCG-01's repeated "did not repent" (Rev 16:9; 16:11 — VCG-01) shows the volitional refusal as the characteristic's constitutive inner reality; (2) Jude 8 (vc=14354 — VCG-01): "reject authority" — explicit volitional rejection as the source of blasphemous expression; (3) Rev 13:6 (vc=14356 — VCG-01): the beast "opened its mouth" — the deliberate opening of the speech-instrument is a volitional act; (4) Joh 18:30 (vc=14378 — VCG-03): the accusers' deliberate verbal charge — a volitional speech act expressing malicious inner judgment; (5) Rom 3:8 (vc=14358 — VCG-02): the false attribution is "slanderously charged" — a deliberate verbal act. All primary evidence confirms the characteristic as volitionally enacted through speech.

---

##### T1.8.3 — Does this characteristic carry secondary dimensions — and if so, what are they, and do they compete with the primary classification?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Secondary dimensions present in the evidence: (1) affective — the wicked person's soul actively desires evil (Pro 21:10; VCG-09), their inner hostility is visceral (Psa 37:12 — "gnashes his teeth"), their joy is momentary and unstable (Job 20:5; VCG-10) — the affective faculty is engaged and corrupted; (2) cognitive — the deliberative faculty is characterised by deceit (Pro 12:5; VCG-08), practical atheism (VCG-02), moral blindness (Pro 4:19), and morally alien counsel (Job 21:16; VCG-10) — cognition is a secondary dimension; (3) self-perpetuating momentum — a quasi-mechanical dimension in which the characteristic generates its own fuel (Pro 5:22; Pro 10:16 "the gain of the wicked leads to sin" — self-perpetuating momentum). These secondary dimensions do not displace the primary volitional-dispositional classification but are its consequences in the affective and cognitive sphere.

## T2 — Constitutional Location (31 prompts)

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Secondary dimensions present in the evidence: (1) volitional — Rom 2:8 (vc=14338 — VCG-05): "obey unrighteousness" — the will's active obedience to unrighteousness shows a volitional secondary dimension; Joh 3:19 (vc=14448 — VCG-04): "loved the darkness" — the will's preference is engaged; (2) affective — Jam 4:16 (vc=14472 — VCG-06): boasting from arrogance — the affective dimension of pride expressing outward as evil; Mat 20:15 (vc=14460 — VCG-06): the evil eye as inner envy and grudging resentment — the affective dimension of the characteristic; (3) cognitive — Col 1:21 (vc=14424 — VCG-06): "hostile in mind" — the cognitive faculty as the seat of evil's hostile orientation; 1Ti 6:4 (vc=14470 — VCG-06): evil suspicions from a conceited, understanding-devoid mind. These secondary dimensions do not displace the primary constitutional-structural classification but show the characteristic's engagement with other inner-being faculties as consequences of the constitutional condition.

These secondary dimensions do not displace the primary relational-moral classification but show the characteristic's engagement with inner-being faculties as the content of what is relationally judged abominable.

## T2 — Constitutional Location (31 prompts)

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Secondary dimensions: (1) affective — Isa 66:3 (vc=1633 — VCG-04): "soul delights in their abominations" — the affective delight-faculty is secondarily engaged and inverted; Deu 32:16 (vc=65938 — VCG-02): divine jealousy as the responding affect; (2) perceptive — Eze 20:7 (vc=1634 — VCG-05): "eyes feast on" detestable things — the perceptive-desire faculty is a secondary mode; (3) constitutional-transformative — Hos 9:10 (vc=1632 — VCG-04): "became detestable like the thing they loved" — the sustained volitional attachment produces secondary constitutional transformation of character. These secondary dimensions do not displace the volitional-devotional primary but show the characteristic's engagement with other inner-being faculties as consequences of the will's directional choice.

Verse-corpus check:  ✓ (Eze 11:21 vc=1631/65982, Isa 66:3 vc=1633, Eze 20:7 vc=1634, Eze 20:8 vc=65911, Deu 7:25 vc=1682, Deu 7:26 vc=65927, Deu 18:9 vc=65931, Deu 18:12 vc=1685, Deu 12:31 vc=1683, Deu 32:16 vc=65938, Eze 5:9 vc=65968, Eze 5:11 vc=65969, Eze 8:6 vc=65976, Eze 8:13 vc=65978, Eze 8:17 vc=65980, Eze 16:22 vc=65985, Eze 16:43 vc=65987, Eze 16:47 vc=65988, Eze 37:23 vc=65913, 2Ch 15:8 vc=65902, 2Ki 23:24 vc=65901, Ezr 9:1 vc=65949, Ezr 9:14 vc=65950, Jer 44:4 vc=65966, Jer 32:34 vc=65907, Eze 12:16 vc=65983, Eze 16:2 vc=1699, Eze 22:2 vc=65995, Hos 9:10 vc=1632, 2Ch 34:33 vc=65946 — all confirmed in §3)
  → PASS. Proceeding to Tier T2.


## T2 — Constitutional Location (31 prompts)

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Secondary dimensions: (1) dispositional-character — the evildoer class (VCG-03, 24V) shows iniquity as a settled character disposition: Pro 17:4 (vc=38219 — VCG-03): the evildoer's inner appetite for wicked speech; Psa 92:7 (vc=38246 — VCG-03): evildoers defined as a class. This dispositional secondary dimension is supported but does not displace the primary volitional-generative classification; (2) accumulated-condition — VCG-04's stored/harboured iniquity (Psa 66:18 — VCG-04: cherished in heart; Psa 41:6 — VCG-04: heart gathers iniquity) shows a secondary accumulated-condition dimension; (3) moral-quality-of-deeds — VCG-05's ro.a sub-corpus names the evil quality of expressed deeds as a secondary dimension. These secondary dimensions do not compete with the primary classification but show the characteristic's engagement with multiple inner-being faculties as the process of scheming matures into character.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Secondary dimensions: (1) social-relational — the characteristic is constitutively social; it requires a target (God or persons) and a social-relational context (VCG-02/03); Rom 2:24 (vc=14357 — VCG-02): blasphemy "among the Gentiles" — the social audience is part of the characteristic's operational reality; (2) cognitive — Jude 10 (vc=14355 — VCG-01): "blaspheme all that they do not understand" — cognitive incomprehension as a secondary enabling condition; (3) affective — the contempt and hostility embedded in blasphemy are affective inner states that accompany the volitional expression; Rev 13:6 (VCG-01): sustained defiant contempt as an affective inner orientation. These secondary dimensions do not displace the volitional-expressive primary but show the characteristic's engagement with other inner faculties as the speech expression is generated.

## T2 — Constitutional Location (31 prompts)

---

### T2

#### T2.1 — Spirit-Level Location

##### T2.1.1 — Is this characteristic explicitly located at the spirit level in the verse evidence?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (S)

The verse evidence does not explicitly locate wickedness-as-settled-person-identity at the spirit level (ruach). No verse in the 190-verse corpus uses spirit-level language as the primary locus of wickedness. The vocabulary is heart (lev), soul (nephesh), thoughts (machashavot), and "way" (derek) — none of which are the programme's spirit-level designations.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (S)

The 90-verse corpus does not explicitly use spirit-level (pneuma) language to locate evil as constitutional inner nature. The dominant constitutional vocabulary is heart (kardia), mind (nous/dianoia), conscience (syneidēsis), and the whole inner person (the "inside" — Luk 11:39). No verse in the corpus names the spirit faculty as the primary site of this constitutional evil.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (S)

The 40-verse corpus does not explicitly locate abomination at the spirit (ruach) level. The primary constitutional vocabulary is heart (lev) — Pro 11:20 (crooked heart), Pro 16:5 (arrogant heart), Pro 26:25 (seven abominations in his heart) — and conscience (the shame/blush faculty of VCG-04). No verse uses spirit-level language as the primary locus.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (S)

The 99-verse corpus does not explicitly use spirit (ruach) vocabulary to locate idolatrous abomination. The dominant constitutional vocabulary is heart (lev/kardia), soul (nephesh), and eyes — not the spirit faculty specifically. Eze 6:9 (vc=1697 — VCG-05) addresses the "whoring heart that has departed from me" — the heart's faculty, not the spirit.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (S)

The 79-verse corpus does not explicitly locate iniquity as active scheming at the spirit (ruach) level. The dominant constitutional vocabulary is heart (lev), thought/mind, and hand — not spirit specifically. 1Sa 15:23 (vc=38185 — VCG-02): presumption as iniquity engages the will but does not use spirit vocabulary. No verse uses ruach to locate this characteristic.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (S)

The 17-verse corpus does not explicitly locate evil expressed through speech at the spirit (pneuma) level. The constitutional vocabulary is primarily volitional (will refusing to repent — Rev 16:9/11 — VCG-01) and cognitive (not understanding — Jude 10 — VCG-01) rather than spirit-level. No verse uses pneuma vocabulary to locate this characteristic.

---

##### T2.1.2 — Does the evidence indicate that this characteristic originates in or is primarily a spirit-level phenomenon?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (S)

The evidence does not address spirit-level origin for wickedness-as-settled-person-identity. The deepest constitutional location evidenced is the heart (Psa 36:1 — "transgression speaks deep in his heart"; Psa 10:13 — "renounce God and say in his heart"). Whether this constitutes spirit-level depth in the programme's taxonomy is not directly evidenced; the verse corpus consistently uses heart and soul vocabulary, not spirit vocabulary.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (S)

The evidence does not indicate spirit-level origin. The constitutional framing (Mat 7:17-18 — VCG-02 — tree-nature determining fruit; Mar 7:23 — VCG-03 — all evil coming from within) does not specify the spirit as the originating faculty. The heart and the "inside" of the person are the specified constitutional loci. Spirit-level origin is not evidenced in this corpus.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (S)

Spirit-level origin is not indicated in this corpus. The evidence roots abomination in the heart (VCG-02 and VCG-01) and in the state of the conscience (VCG-04), not in the spirit faculty specifically. The constitutional depth implied (Pro 26:25 — seven abominations in the heart; Pro 11:20 — crooked heart) suggests the characteristic reaches the innermost integrating centre, but this is named as heart rather than spirit in the Hebrew vocabulary.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (S)

Spirit-level origin is not indicated. The evidence roots the characteristic in the heart (Eze 11:21 — heart going after idols — VCG-05), the soul (Isa 66:3 — soul delighting in abominations — VCG-04), and the eyes (Eze 20:7 — eyes feasting — VCG-05) — all of which are soul-level or sub-soul-level faculties in the programme's taxonomy. Spirit-level origin is not specifically evidenced.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (S)

Spirit-level origin is not indicated. The evidence roots the characteristic in the heart and thought-life (Isa 32:6 — VCG-02: "heart is busy with iniquity"; Isa 59:7 — VCG-02: "thoughts are thoughts of iniquity") and in the hand (Job 11:14 — VCG-04: "iniquity is in your hand") — all soul-level or expressive-level locations. Spirit-level origin is not specifically evidenced.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (S)

Spirit-level origin is not indicated. The characteristic originates in the hardened will (VCG-01 — "did not repent"), in authority-rejection (Jude 8 — VCG-01), and in moral failure affecting social testimony (VCG-02 — Rom 2:24). These are will and cognitive-moral locations, not spirit-level designations.

---

##### T2.1.3 — What does spirit-level location reveal about the nature and depth of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (S)

Spirit-level location is not directly evidenced for this characteristic (T2.1.1–T2.1.2). The analytical significance of this silence is that wickedness-as-settled-person-identity, while deep (reaching the heart's innermost register per Psa 36:1), is not presented in Scripture as a disruption of the spirit-level communion with God in the specific vocabulary of spirit-disruption. The characteristic is primarily named at the level of moral orientation, soul-desire, and heart-governance rather than spirit.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (S)

Spirit-level location is not directly evidenced for this characteristic (T2.1.1–T2.1.2). The absence of spirit-level location does not preclude it analytically — the constitutional condition evidenced at heart and mind level could have spirit-level implications — but the evidence does not directly address this. The depth the evidence does name is the whole inner being: Mat 6:23 (vc=14458 — VCG-03) — the evil eye floods "the whole body" with darkness; Mar 7:23 (vc=14422 — VCG-03) — "all these evil things come from within." The depth is whole-person constitutional but not specifically spirit-located.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (S)

Spirit-level location is not evidenced (T2.1.1–T2.1.2). The depth the evidence does name is the heart level, where abomination resides as the crooked or arrogant inner orientation (Pro 11:20; Pro 16:5 — VCG-02), and the whole inner person's saturation with multiple abominations (Pro 26:25 — VCG-02: "seven abominations in his heart"). The depth is heart-constitutional without specific spirit-vocabulary.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (S)

Spirit-level location is not evidenced for this characteristic (T2.1.1–T2.1.2). The depth the evidence does name is the heart-level (the directional faculty) and the soul-level (delight). The characteristic reaches into these deep constitutional levels without explicit spirit-level vocabulary in the corpus.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (S)

Spirit-level location is not evidenced for this characteristic (T2.1.1–T2.1.2). The depth the evidence does name is the heart level — the inner generative centre — where iniquity is "busy" (Isa 32:6 — VCG-02) and "cherished" (Psa 66:18 — VCG-04). The characteristic reaches to the deepest evidenced inner-being level without using spirit-specific vocabulary.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (S)

Spirit-level location is not evidenced for this characteristic (T2.1.1–T2.1.2). The depth the evidence does name is the will-level: the hardened will that persists in cursing through multiple divine judgments (Rev 16:9/11/21 — VCG-01). This will-level depth is the constitutional depth the evidence reaches without spirit-vocabulary.

##### T2.1.4 — If the evidence is silent on spirit-level location, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The evidence is silent on spirit-level location for wickedness-as-settled-person-identity. No verse in the 190-verse corpus explicitly places this characteristic at the spirit level or uses ruach in relation to wickedness as this characteristic defines it. This is noted explicitly as directed.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The evidence is silent on spirit-level location for evil as constitutional inner nature. No verse in the 90-verse corpus locates this characteristic at the spirit level using pneuma vocabulary. This is noted explicitly as directed.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The evidence is silent on spirit-level location for abomination as divine revulsion on moral character. No verse in the 40-verse corpus uses ruach (spirit) vocabulary to locate this characteristic. This is explicitly noted.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The evidence is silent on spirit-level location for idolatrous abomination. No verse in the 99-verse corpus uses ruach (spirit) vocabulary to locate this characteristic. This is explicitly noted.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The evidence is silent on spirit-level location for iniquity as active scheming. No verse in the 79-verse corpus uses ruach (spirit) vocabulary to locate this characteristic. This is explicitly noted.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The evidence is silent on spirit-level location for evil expressed through speech. No verse in the 17-verse corpus uses pneuma (spirit) vocabulary to locate this characteristic. This is explicitly noted.

#### T2.2 — Soul-Level Location

##### T2.2.1 — Is this characteristic identified in the verse evidence as a soul-level phenomenon?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Yes. Pro 21:10 (VCG-09) is the most direct soul-level location: "the soul of the wicked desires evil" — the Hebrew nephesh (soul) is the explicit locus of the wicked person's desire-orientation. Psa 17:13 (VCG-03) names the threat to the soul: "deliver my soul from the wicked" — the wicked person endangers the soul itself, presupposing that the wicked person's inner force operates at the level where the soul is at stake. Psa 11:5 states "his soul hates the wicked" — God's soul-level response to wickedness by contrast confirms the soul as the appropriate level of engagement. The characteristic is not only soul-located in the wicked person but is recognised as a soul-level threat to those the wicked endanger.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (S)

The corpus does not explicitly use soul (psychē) language to locate constitutional inner evil. The closest soul-level reference is in the purpose clauses: Jam 1:21 (vc=14368 — VCG-05): "receive with meekness the implanted word, which is able to save your souls" — the rampant wickedness being stripped away is what blocks soul-salvation; this implies soul-level stakes but does not explicitly locate the characteristic in the soul faculty. The verse evidence locates the characteristic primarily in the heart and the whole inner person rather than the soul faculty specifically.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Pro 13:19 (vc=1687 — VCG-05) provides the clearest soul-level reference: "A desire fulfilled is sweet to the soul, but to turn away from evil is an abomination to fools." The soul-level desire (sweet to the soul) is placed in explicit contrast with the fool's inverted appetite (finding departure from evil abominable). This verse shows the characteristic engaging the soul's desire-faculty — the fool's soul has an inverted desire orientation that finds departure from abomination itself to be abominable. The soul's desire capacity is the site of this radical inversion.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Yes. Isa 66:3 (vc=1633 — VCG-04) is the primary soul-level evidence: "their soul delights in their abominations." The soul (nephesh) is the explicit locus of the characteristic's affective-attachment dimension — the soul's delight-faculty is attached to abominations rather than to God. This is the most direct soul-level location statement in the corpus and is analytically significant: the nephesh as the seat of deepest desire and delight is the constitutional location of the inverted affective attachment that characterises idolatrous abomination.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Yes. Isa 66:3 (vc=38204 — VCG-04): "their soul delights in their abominations" — the soul (nephesh) is the affective-desire faculty that is attached to and delights in the abominable iniquitous ways. This is the clearest soul-level evidence in the corpus. The soul-level location reveals iniquity as reaching the deepest desire-centre of the person: the nephesh that should find delight in God instead finds delight in its own chosen abominable ways, of which iniquity is a key component.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (S)

The 17-verse corpus does not use explicit soul (psychē) vocabulary to locate this characteristic. The inner-being content is primarily accessed through volitional and cognitive language rather than soul-level designation. This silence is noted.

---

##### T2.2.2 — What does soul-level location reveal about this characteristic's place in the innermost personal experience?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Soul-level location (Pro 21:10 — nephesh) reveals that wickedness-as-settled-person-identity reaches the innermost faculty of personal desire and appetite. The soul's desire being directed toward evil (rather than toward God, nourishment, or blessing) means the characteristic has penetrated to the person's deepest seat of longing. This explains why the characteristic is "settled" — it is not a surface preference but a desire-level orientation. The soul's craving in the wicked person is for evil (Pro 21:10) and its craving remains structurally unsatisfied (Pro 13:25 — "the belly of the wicked suffers want") — wickedness as a soul-level disposition generates an insatiable appetite that works against the person's own wellbeing.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

While explicit soul-level location is limited (T2.2.1), Jam 1:21 (vc=14368 — VCG-05) reveals that the constitutional inner evil is the primary obstacle to soul-salvation — its removal is the precondition for the word to take root and save the soul. This implies the characteristic operates at the level that determines the soul's ultimate trajectory. The stakes of the characteristic being present or absent are soul-level stakes. The characteristic therefore has soul-level significance even without being explicitly located in the soul faculty — it determines whether the soul is reachable by the saving word.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Pro 13:19 (vc=1687 — VCG-05) reveals that in the most deeply corrupted state, the characteristic has reached the soul's desire faculty and inverted it. The soul that should desire good and find the fulfillment of righteous desire sweet (the first half of the verse) now finds the moral opposite abominable. This soul-level inversion is analytically significant: abomination has not merely occupied the heart and thoughts but has penetrated to the soul's desire-orientation, corrupting the faculty that governs what the person fundamentally wants. Soul-level location reveals the characteristic at its deepest penetration into the inner person.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Isa 66:3 (vc=1633 — VCG-04) reveals that idolatrous abomination has penetrated to the soul's delight faculty — not merely the surface behaviour or the will's momentary choice but the deepest affective centre. The soul that should delight in God (the designed delight-orientation of the nephesh) now delights in abominations. This soul-level penetration explains why the characteristic is so resistant to surface reform: it has reached the level where the person's fundamental affective orientation is attached to the idol. Soul-level location reveals the characteristic as an inner-being corruption that has reached the person's deepest motivational spring.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Isa 66:3 (vc=38204 — VCG-04) reveals that sustained iniquity penetrates to the soul's delight-faculty — the nephesh's capacity for deep affective attachment is redirected toward the iniquitous self-chosen ways. This soul-level penetration shows the characteristic at its deepest development: not merely cognition scheming or will choosing, but the soul itself finding pleasure in what is iniquitous. Soul-level location reveals the characteristic as having corrupted the motivational spring of the person when fully established.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (S)

Soul-level location is not evidenced in this corpus (T2.2.1). The inner-being depth the evidence reaches is the will's settled refusal to repent (Rev 16:9/11/21 — VCG-01) and the authority-rejection that precedes blasphemous expression (Jude 8 — VCG-01) — both of which engage the person's deepest motivational centre without using psychē vocabulary.

---

##### T2.2.3 — If the evidence is silent on soul-level location, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The evidence is not silent; soul-level location is confirmed (T2.2.1–T2.2.2). This prompt is satisfied by the positive finding above.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The evidence is largely silent on explicit soul-level location, though soul-level stakes are implied by Jam 1:21 (vc=14368 — VCG-05). This nuance is noted. The finding at T2.2.2 addresses the analytical significance.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Soul-level location is evidenced via Pro 13:19 (vc=1687 — VCG-05) (T2.2.1–T2.2.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Soul-level location is evidenced (T2.2.1–T2.2.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Soul-level location is evidenced (T2.2.1–T2.2.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The evidence is silent on explicit soul-level location. This is noted. The characteristic's inner depth is accessed through volitional and will-level language rather than soul-vocabulary.

---

#### T2.3 — Heart

##### T2.3.1 — Does the verse evidence locate this characteristic in the heart?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Yes. Heart-location is among the richest evidential sites for this characteristic. Psa 36:1 (VCG-02): "transgression speaks to the wicked deep in his heart" — the heart is the location of the inner voice of wickedness. Psa 10:13 (VCG-02): the wicked "renounce God and say in his heart" — the heart's internal speech is the primary site of God-exclusion. 1Sa 17:28 (VCG-08 — ro.a): Eliab accuses David of "evil of your heart" — locating the projected inner disposition explicitly in the heart. Pro 12:5 (VCG-08): "the counsels of the wicked are deceitful" — the deliberative function of the heart is corrupted. Pro 26:25 (in M10b-C, but the ra.sha corpus shares this register): "seven abominations fill their heart." The heart is both the location of the characteristic's inner voice (Psa 36:1) and the organ whose moral compass has inverted (Pro 10:32: "the mouth of the wicked knows what is perverse" — the mouth revealing the heart).

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Yes. Heart-location is the most densely evidenced constitutional site for this characteristic. VCG-03 (8V) is specifically named "The heart as treasury — the inner source and generative organ of evil." Primary evidence: Mat 9:4 (vc=14418 — VCG-03): "Why do you think evil in your hearts?" — heart as the site of evil cognition. Mat 12:34 (vc=14419 — VCG-03): "out of the abundance of the heart the mouth speaks" — the heart's abundance produces speech. Mat 12:35 (vc=14420 — VCG-03): "the evil person out of his evil treasure" — the heart as treasury. Mat 15:19 (vc=14414 — VCG-03): "out of the heart come evil thoughts, murder, adultery…" — the heart as the originating generative organ of the vice catalogue. Luk 6:45 (vc=14421 — VCG-03): the same treasury-and-mouth mechanism. Act 8:22 (vc=14361 — VCG-05): "the intent of your heart" as the seat of the moral evil requiring repentance. Heb 3:12 (vc=14423 — VCG-06): "an evil, unbelieving heart."

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Yes. Heart-location is the most richly evidenced constitutional site for this characteristic. VCG-02 is the primary evidence cluster. Pro 11:20 (vc=1677 — VCG-01): "those of crooked heart are an abomination to the Lord" — the heart's inner moral curvature is the abominable condition. Pro 16:5 (vc=1689 — VCG-02): "everyone who is arrogant in heart is an abomination to the Lord" — the heart's pride is specifically named. Pro 26:25 (vc=1694 — VCG-02): "there are seven abominations in his heart" — the heart as the repository of multiple abominable inner drives hidden beneath gracious speech. Pro 15:26 (vc=1679 — VCG-02): "the thoughts of the wicked are an abomination" — the cognitive function of the heart (thoughts) is included. Luk 16:15 (vc=21 — VCG-02): "God knows your hearts. For what is exalted among men is an abomination in the sight of God" — the heart is explicitly the locus God knows and responds to with revulsion.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Yes. Heart-location is the richest constitutional site. Eze 11:21 (vc=1631 — VCG-05): "whose heart goes after their detestable things and their abominations" — the heart as the directional faculty is the primary seat of the characteristic. Eze 11:21 (vc=65982 — VCG-05 second occurrence): "the heart that goes after abominations makes the inner faculty of desire the driver of spiritual defection." Eze 6:9 (vc=1697 — VCG-05): "their whoring heart that has departed from me and over their eyes that go whoring after their idols" — the heart is specifically named as having "departed" — a directional language for the heart's volitional-relational abandonment of God. Eze 16:36 (vc=65986 — VCG-05): "lust was poured out" in idolatrous whorings — inner desire is the heart-level driver.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Yes. Heart-location is the richest and most directly evidenced constitutional site. Isa 32:6 (vc=38181 — VCG-02): "his heart is busy with iniquity" — the heart as the productive generative centre is fully occupied with scheming evil. Psa 66:18 (vc=38182 — VCG-04): "if I had cherished iniquity in my heart" — the heart as the site where iniquity is harboured. Psa 7:14 (vc=38245 — VCG-02): "the wicked man conceives evil" — the heart as the conceiving-faculty (implied by the birth metaphor). Psa 28:3 (vc=38232 — VCG-03): "workers of evil, who speak peace with their neighbors while evil is in their hearts" — the heart as the hidden repository of evil contrasted with outward peace-speech. Jer 4:14 (vc=38205 — VCG-02): "wash your heart from evil, that you may be saved. How long shall your wicked thoughts lodge within you?" — heart and thoughts both named as the location of lodging iniquity. Psa 41:6 (vc=38236 — VCG-04): "his heart gathers iniquity" — the heart actively collecting evil.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (S)

The 17-verse corpus does not use explicit heart (kardia) vocabulary to locate this characteristic. The hardened-will evidence in VCG-01 (Rev 16:9/11/21) describes the will's stance without naming the heart as the constitutional locus. The characteristic's inner location is the will and the cognitive faculties, named without heart-vocabulary in this specific corpus.

---

##### T2.3.2 — What does the heart-location reveal — what aspect of the heart's integrating function (knowing, willing, feeling, moral awareness) does this characteristic engage?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Heart-location reveals that wickedness-as-settled-person-identity specifically engages the heart's integrating and self-governing function. The heart in Scripture is the integrating centre of the person — where knowing, willing, feeling, and moral awareness converge. In the wicked person: (1) the knowing function is corrupted — the heart's moral compass is inverted (Pro 10:32); (2) the willing function is misoriented — the heart renounces God actively (Psa 10:13); (3) the governing function is occupied — transgression speaks as an internal voice in the heart (Psa 36:1), displacing the God-fear that should govern. The heart is not merely the location of wickedness — it is the site where wickedness has replaced the rightful governance structure of the person with its own alternative governance (transgression-as-inner-voice).

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Heart-location reveals that evil as constitutional inner nature engages the heart's generative and integrating function — the heart as the source from which all inner-being outputs flow. The treasury metaphor (Mat 12:35 — VCG-03) captures this precisely: the heart does not merely host the characteristic but actively generates outputs from it. The knowing function is corrupted (Mat 9:4 — evil in your hearts as corrupt cognition), the willing function is misoriented (Heb 3:12 — unbelieving heart leading to apostasy), and the generative function is redirected (Mat 15:19 — out of the heart come the vice list). The heart-location reveals the characteristic as occupying the central integrating organ of the person — not a peripheral faculty but the generative core from which speech, thought, and action all flow.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Heart-location reveals that abomination engages three of the heart's integrating functions simultaneously. (1) The moral-orientation function — the heart's basic directional bent (crooked — Pro 11:20; straight/blameless as opposite) determines whether the person is abominable or delightful to God. (2) The affective-pride function — arrogance in heart (Pro 16:5 — VCG-02) is an affective orientation of self-elevation that the heart harbours. (3) The cognitive-hidden function — seven abominations in the heart (Pro 26:25 — VCG-02) describes the heart as the location of concealed corrupt motivations that the person hides beneath smooth speech. The heart-location reveals the characteristic as operating at the central integrating point of the person — the place where orientation, affect, and hidden motivation converge, all of which God perceives directly (Luk 16:15 — "God knows your hearts").

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Heart-location reveals that idolatrous abomination engages specifically the heart's directional-devotional function — the function by which the heart orients itself toward an object of worship and allegiance. Eze 11:21 (vc=1631 — VCG-05): "heart goes after" — the going-after is the heart's directional function misdirected. Eze 6:9 (vc=1697 — VCG-05): "whoring heart that has departed from me" — the departure is the directional function moving away from God. The characteristic does not engage the heart's cognitive function (knowing) or the moral-awareness function (right and wrong) primarily; it engages the allegiance-devotion function — the capacity by which the heart binds itself to an object of ultimate loyalty. This is the heart's most fundamental function as image-bearer: the choice of what to love and worship.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Heart-location reveals that iniquity as scheming engages all three of the heart's primary integrating functions simultaneously. (1) Cognitive/planning function: Isa 32:6 (vc=38181 — VCG-02): the heart "busy with iniquity" in a planning, scheming mode — the heart's knowing-planning capacity generates the schemes. (2) Moral awareness function — inverted: Psa 28:3 (vc=38232 — VCG-03): "evil is in their hearts" while speaking outward peace — the heart knows the evil it harbours, enabling the deception; the moral awareness is present but co-opted for concealment. (3) Volitional function: the heart as chooser — Psa 36:4 (vc=38235 — VCG-02): "he sets himself in a way that is not good; he does not reject evil" — the heart's willing is the faculty through which iniquity is retained. Heart-location shows the characteristic as engaging the full integrating centre of the person.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (S)

Heart-location is not explicitly evidenced in this corpus (T2.3.1). The nearest equivalent to heart-location is the hardened-will evidence in VCG-01 — Rev 16:9 (vc=14352): "they did not repent and give him glory" — the refusal is at the deepest volitional-moral centre, which in the programme's framework corresponds to heart-level function even without the explicit vocabulary. This engagement is with the heart's volitional-moral function (the will's choice of orientation) without heart-vocabulary being used.

---

##### T2.3.3 — If the evidence is silent on heart-location, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The evidence is not silent; heart-location is richly evidenced (T2.3.1–T2.3.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The evidence is not silent; heart-location is richly evidenced (T2.3.1–T2.3.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Heart-location is richly evidenced (T2.3.1–T2.3.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Heart-location is richly evidenced (T2.3.1–T2.3.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Heart-location is richly evidenced (T2.3.1–T2.3.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Explicit heart-location vocabulary is absent from the 17-verse corpus. This is noted. The functional equivalent (volitional-moral centre) is present in the hardened-will evidence of VCG-01.

---

#### T2.4 — Mind

##### T2.4.1 — Does the verse evidence locate this characteristic in the mind?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Yes, though the vocabulary is primarily thought-life rather than "mind" as a discrete faculty. The most direct mind-location is Psa 10:4 (VCG-02): "all his thoughts are 'There is no God'" — the wicked person's entire thought-life is organised around the practical exclusion of God. Pro 12:5 (VCG-08): "the counsels of the wicked are deceitful" — the deliberative/advisory faculty (the moral reasoning of the heart-as-mind) is oriented toward deception. Job 21:16 (VCG-10): "the counsel of the wicked is far from me" — wickedness generates a morally alien cognitive framework (a distinct mode of reasoning). Pro 4:19 (VCG-07): "they do not know over what they stumble" — cognitive blindness as a consequence of the wicked way.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Yes. Mind-location is present though less dominant than heart-location. Col 1:21 (vc=14424 — VCG-06): "hostile in mind, doing evil deeds" — the mind as the seat of hostile enmity that produces evil conduct. 1Ti 6:4 (vc=14470 — VCG-06): "a mind inflated with conceit and devoid of understanding" producing evil suspicions — the cognitive faculty as the site from which the characteristic's suspicious and divisive outputs emerge. Mat 6:23 (vc=14458 — VCG-03): "if your eye is bad" — the eye metaphor for the faculty of inner perception/intent, which is a cognitive-perceptive function.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Yes, in the cognitive register. Pro 15:26 (vc=1679 — VCG-02): "the thoughts of the wicked are an abomination to the Lord" — the thought-life (machashevot — deliberate thoughts/plans) is explicitly named as the site of the abominable quality. Isa 44:19 (vc=65961 — VCG-05): "no one considers, nor is there knowledge or discernment" — the absence of cognitive reflection (consideration, knowledge, discernment) enables abomination without recognition. Eze 44:7 (vc=66002 — VCG-04): "uncircumcised in heart" — the heart's knowing function, when uncircumcised (not inwardly responsive to the divine), is the root defilement.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Mind-location appears in the cognitive-failure registers.
