## T3 — Inner Faculties (33 prompts)

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Constitutional movement is extensively evidenced (T2.10.1–T2.10.2). This prompt is satisfied.

---

T2 self-evaluation:
  1. Prompt count:        31/31 ✓
  2. Scope marker:        31× [CHAR-5] ✓
  3. Citation discipline: S findings (T2.1.1–T2.1.4) correctly note spirit-level silence; all E findings cite specific verses/VCGs ✓
  4. No cross-tier refs:  ✓
  5. Distinct openings:   ✓
  6. Verse-corpus check:  ✓ (all citations confirmed in §3)
  → PASS. Proceeding to Tier T3.


## T3 — Inner Faculties (33 prompts)

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Constitutional movement is evidenced (T2.10.1–T2.10.2). This prompt is satisfied.

## T3 — Inner Faculties (33 prompts)

---

### T3

#### T3.1 — Perception

##### T3.1.1 — Does this characteristic engage the perceptive faculty — the inner senses including hearing, sight, taste, touch, smell, and spiritual discernment — and if so, which inner sense and how?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Yes. The perceptive faculty (inner sight) is significantly engaged. The primary engagement is through moral-spiritual sight, which wickedness corrupts. Pro 4:19 (VCG-07): "the way of the wicked is like deep darkness; they do not know over what they stumble" — inner moral sight is disabled by the wicked way. Isa 26:10 (VCG-05): "he does not see the majesty of the Lord" — the wicked person is specifically blind to the divine presence even when surrounded by uprightness. Dan 12:10 (VCG-05): "none of the wicked shall understand" — the eschatological equivalent of perceptive closure. Pro 21:4 (VCG-03): "haughty eyes" — the outer eyes are the expressive instrument of the inner disposition of pride, which itself distorts the perceptive faculty. Psa 10:4 (VCG-02): "In the pride of his face the wicked does not seek" — pride actively inhibits the seeking that perception requires. The inner sense most engaged is spiritual-moral sight; the engagement is through impairment and disablement.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Yes. The perceptive faculty (inner sight) is directly engaged and corrupted. Mat 6:23 (vc=14458 — VCG-03): "if your eye is bad, your whole body will be full of darkness" — the eye as the perceptive faculty expresses the constitutional evil inner condition by flooding the whole person with moral darkness. The "bad eye" is the perceptive faculty corrupted at its root — not merely a perception error but a constitutional state of the perceptive organ. Joh 3:19 (vc=14448 — VCG-04): "people loved the darkness rather than the light because their works were evil" — the constitutionally evil person's perceptive preference is for moral concealment over exposure; the characteristic shapes what the person chooses to see and value.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Yes. Spiritual discernment and moral-spiritual sight are directly engaged. Isa 44:19 (vc=65961 — VCG-05): "no one considers, nor is there knowledge or discernment" — the perceptive faculty of spiritual discernment is specifically absent, enabling the person to bow before wood without perceiving the abomination they perform. The absence of the perceptive-discernment faculty is what allows abomination to proceed unrecognised. Eze 9:4 (vc=1698 — VCG-04): those who "sigh and groan over all the abominations" are those who perceive the abominations morally and spiritually — their inner sight is functional, seeing what others ignore. Pro 17:15 (vc=1690 — VCG-01): perverted judgment — the moral-evaluative perceptive faculty is inverted in those who justify the wicked and condemn the righteous.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Yes. Visual perception/desire is the most directly evidenced perceptive mode. Eze 20:7 (vc=1634 — VCG-05): "the detestable things your eyes feast on" — the eyes are the perceptive channel through which the idolatrous objects attract and sustain inner attachment. Eze 20:8 (vc=65911 — VCG-05): "none of them cast away the detestable things their eyes feasted on, nor did they forsake the idols of Egypt" — the continued feasting of the eyes shows a perceptive-desire faculty actively sustaining the inner attachment. Eze 6:9 (vc=1697 — VCG-05): "eyes that go whoring after their idols" — the eyes are personified as going after the idols, showing visual perception as the dominant sense through which the characteristic operates. The characteristic engages visual perception through a desire-loop: idol-objects attract the eyes → eyes feed the inner attachment → attachment reinforces visual seeking.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Yes. Moral-spiritual perception is engaged through its impairment and misdirection. Psa 14:4 (vc=38229 — VCG-03): "Have they no knowledge, all the evildoers who eat up my people" — the perceptive faculty of moral knowledge is absent in those who work iniquity; their inner sight cannot register what they are doing as wrong. Psa 53:4 (vc=38238 — VCG-03): same — "no knowledge" among those who work evil. Isa 29:20 (vc=38198 — VCG-02): "all who watch to do evil shall be cut off" — the perceptive faculty of watching/looking is specifically directed toward opportunities for evil; the eyes are used as surveillance tools in service of scheming. Pro 17:4 (vc=38219 — VCG-03): "an evildoer listens to wicked lips" — the inner hearing is preferentially oriented toward harmful content.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Yes. Moral and spiritual perception is engaged through its comprehensive failure in VCG-01. Jude 10 (vc=14355 — VCG-01): "these people blaspheme all that they do not understand" — the perceptive faculty of spiritual comprehension has failed entirely; what they cannot perceive they blaspheme. The inner perceptive faculty that should apprehend spiritual reality (the "glorious ones" of Jude 8 — VCG-01) is so non-functional that contempt fills the void. The contrast with unreasoning animals who "understand instinctively" shows that even sub-rational instinct operates where human moral-spiritual perception has collapsed. Additionally, Rev 16:9/11/21 (VCG-01): under direct physical judgment (scorching, pain, hailstones), the perceptive faculty that should register divine power and respond is present — "who had power over these plagues" (Rev 16:9) — but the will refuses to respond despite perceiving divine causation.

---

##### T3.1.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair the perceptive faculty in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Wickedness-as-settled-person-identity impairs the perceptive faculty. The evidence is consistent: Pro 4:19 (blindness to the cause of stumbling), Isa 26:10 (blindness to God's majesty), Dan 12:10 (inability to understand). The impairment is not merely incidental — it is described as constitutive of the wicked way: the darkness of the wicked person's way (Pro 4:19) is the condition from which their perceptive blindness flows. The characteristic does not enable or deepen perception. It bypasses moral-spiritual discernment in the sense that the wicked person acts without the check that clear moral perception would impose.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The characteristic impairs the perceptive faculty by constitutionally orienting it toward darkness. Mat 6:23 (vc=14458 — VCG-03) is the most direct statement: the bad eye produces darkness rather than light — the perceptive faculty no longer illuminates but obscures. Joh 3:19 (vc=14448 — VCG-04): the constitutionally evil person's works align their perceptive preference toward darkness — they prefer not to see the truth (Joh 7:7 — VCG-04: the world hates the one who testifies to evil works, because testimony forces perception of what the constitution prefers to ignore). The characteristic impairs perception specifically by orienting the whole inner person toward moral concealment and away from honest moral sight.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The characteristic impairs and bypasses the perceptive faculty in those who commit abomination. Isa 44:19 (vc=65961 — VCG-05): no discernment — the abominable inner condition has disabled the perceptive faculty of moral discernment. Pro 17:15 (vc=1690 — VCG-01): perverted judgment — the moral-perceptive faculty is not absent but inverted (justifying wrong, condemning right). In contrast, for those whose conscience is awakened, the characteristic deepens moral perception: Eze 9:4 (vc=1698 — VCG-04): those who grieve have a heightened perceptive sensitivity to the abominations around them. The characteristic's relationship to perception is thus dual: it impairs/bypasses perception in the abominable person and deepens it in those who grieve.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The characteristic enables and deepens the perceptive faculty in its misdirected form (toward idol-objects) while impairing it in its correctly directed form (toward God and moral reality). Eze 20:7-8 (VCG-05): the eyes actively feast on detestable things — the perceptive faculty is heightened in its idol-directed mode. Simultaneously, the characteristic impairs the moral-spiritual perceptive faculty: Eze 8:17 (vc=65980 — VCG-05): treating abomination as "too light a thing" shows that the moral-perceptive faculty cannot accurately assess the gravity of what is happening. The characteristic produces a perceptive split: enhanced idol-directed perception, diminished God-directed moral perception.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The characteristic impairs the perceptive faculty's moral-knowledge function (Psa 14:4; 53:4 — VCG-03: no knowledge in evildoers) while redirecting and enabling the surveillance-for-evil function (Isa 29:20 — VCG-02: "watch to do evil"). It also impairs the hearing faculty's responsiveness to moral instruction: Job 36:10 (vc=38215 — VCG-04): "He opens their ears to instruction and commands that they return from iniquity" — the need for divine ear-opening implies the characteristic has closed the inner ear to instruction. The characteristic thus produces a split in perceptive function: enhanced perception for opportunities to scheme harm, diminished perception of moral reality.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The characteristic impairs the perceptive faculty for moral-spiritual reality (Jude 10 — VCG-01: not understanding what they blaspheme) while leaving the physical perceptive faculty operational (Rev 16:9 — VCG-01: they know who has power over the plagues). The impairment is specifically moral-spiritual discernment — the capacity to perceive the value, authority, and holiness of what is blasphemed. The physical pain and heat are perceived but their spiritual significance is not: this is a spiritually selective perceptive impairment — physical pain is registered but its meaning (divine judgment calling for repentance) is not received.

---

##### T3.1.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with perception reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The consistent perceptive impairment reveals that wickedness-as-settled-person-identity involves a systematic closure of the inner faculty through which God and moral reality are apprehended. This is not accidental — it is the functional consequence of the practical atheism at the characteristic's core (VCG-02: Psa 10:4). The person who excludes God from their thought-life (Psa 10:4) necessarily loses the capacity to perceive the divine perspective on their situation (Isa 26:10). The perceptive pattern reveals that wickedness is self-reinforcing through this perceptual closure: the less the wicked person can perceive moral reality, the more deeply settled the characteristic becomes. This is a diagnostic finding about the characteristic's internal dynamics.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The perceptive engagement pattern reveals that evil as constitutional inner nature has corrupted the person's evaluative and orientational perception — they see, but are constitutionally inclined to evaluate what they see according to a darkened standard. Mat 6:23 (VCG-03) reveals the constitutive link: the eye's badness is not merely a failure of individual perceptions but a constitutional state of the perceptive faculty that determines what the whole person apprehends. This reveals the characteristic as a condition that has compromised the primary incoming-orientation faculty — before the person acts, before they speak, the perceptive faculty through which they receive and assess reality is already constitutionally corrupted.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The dual pattern — impaired perception in the abominable, heightened perception in the grieving — reveals that the characteristic's relationship to moral perception is a diagnostic indicator of the conscience's state. Isa 44:19 (vc=65961 — VCG-05) identifies the absence of discernment as what enables abomination without self-recognition. Eze 9:4 (vc=1698 — VCG-04) shows that the capacity to perceive abomination in others is the mark of a functioning moral-perceptive conscience. The pattern reveals the characteristic as one that progressively closes moral perception in the person who practises abomination, while it sharpens moral perception in those whose conscience remains functional and responsive.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The perceptive pattern reveals a distinctive feature of idolatrous abomination: the characteristic operates through the visual-desire appetite more than other M10b characteristics. The idolatrous object is presented as visually attractive — Eze 7:20 (vc=65909 — VCG-05): "his beautiful ornament" converted into idols — the beauty of the material is what draws. This visual-attractiveness mechanism explains the Deuteronomic emphasis on destroying the idol-objects (Deu 7:25 — VCG-02: "burn with fire") and not coveting what is on them — the perceptive-desire faculty is the primary entry-point for the characteristic. The perceptive pattern reveals CHAR-4 as operating through visual desire in a way that distinguishes it from CHAR-1 (which operates through inner voice) and CHAR-2 (which operates through the heart's treasury).

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The perceptive pattern reveals that iniquity as scheming specifically requires a particular perceptive orientation — the "watching to do evil" (Isa 29:20 — VCG-02) and listening to wicked lips (Pro 17:4 — VCG-03) show the characteristic as actively deploying the perceptive faculties in the service of harm-generation. The concomitant moral-knowledge blindness (Psa 14:4 — VCG-03) is not accidental but functionally linked: the inner sight directed toward opportunities for evil cannot simultaneously attend to moral reality. The perceptive pattern reveals the characteristic as perceptively focussed and functionally selective — able to spot opportunities for harm while blind to moral truth.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The perceptive pattern reveals a distinctive split in the characteristic: the physical perceptive faculty is intact (pain and judgment are felt — Rev 16:9/11/21 — VCG-01) while the moral-spiritual perceptive faculty has failed (Jude 10 — VCG-01: not understanding). This split confirms that the characteristic is primarily a will-phenomenon, not a perception-phenomenon: the hardened will can perceive the divine power behind the judgment (Rev 16:9: "who had power over these plagues") yet refuse to respond rightly to what it perceives. The perceptive pattern reveals the characteristic as a post-perceptual failure — not a failure to see but a refusal to respond rightly to what is seen.

---

#### T3.2 — Cognition

##### T3.2.1 — Does this characteristic engage the cognitive faculty — knowing, understanding, discerning — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Yes. Cognition is significantly engaged and corrupted. Pro 12:5 (VCG-08): "the counsels of the wicked are deceitful" — the deliberative cognitive function is oriented toward deceptive output. Job 21:16 (VCG-10): "the counsel of the wicked is far from me" — wickedness generates a morally alien cognitive framework. Psa 10:4 (VCG-02): "all his thoughts are 'There is no God'" — the cognitive contents of the wicked person are systematically God-excluding. Pro 4:19 (VCG-07): the wicked "do not know over what they stumble" — cognitive self-knowledge is impaired. Isa 5:23 (VCG-05): the corrupt judicial will "acquitting the guilty for a bribe" — the judicial cognitive faculty (discernment of right from wrong) is deliberately perverted. Dan 12:10 (VCG-05): "none of the wicked shall understand" — cognitive capacity for understanding is closed at the eschatological level.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Yes. Cognition is significantly engaged. Mat 9:4 (vc=14418 — VCG-03): "Why do you think evil in your hearts?" — evil cognition is directly named; the heart as the site of morally corrupt thought. Mat 12:35 (vc=14420 — VCG-03): the evil person draws from an inner treasury — this is an active cognitive act of retrieval. Col 1:21 (vc=14424 — VCG-06): "hostile in mind, doing evil deeds" — the mind as the cognitive-evaluative faculty is the seat of the constitutionally hostile orientation that produces evil deeds. 1Ti 6:4 (vc=14470 — VCG-06): evil suspicions arising from a mind inflated with conceit and devoid of understanding — cognitive corruption producing relational damage.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Yes. Cognition is directly engaged. Pro 15:26 (vc=1679 — VCG-02): "the thoughts of the wicked are an abomination to the Lord" — deliberate inner thought is named as the site of abomination; the cognitive faculty generates abominable content. Pro 17:15 (vc=1690 — VCG-01): perverted judgment — the cognitive faculty of moral assessment has been inverted. Isa 44:19 (vc=65961 — VCG-05): the absence of "consideration" (a reflective cognitive act) enables abomination; cognitive reflection would prevent the abominable act by naming it for what it is. Luk 16:15 (vc=21 — VCG-02): "God knows your hearts" — divine cognition penetrates the human heart's self-justifying cognitive constructions.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Yes. Cognition is engaged primarily through its failure modes. Eze 16:22 (vc=65985 — VCG-05): "in all your abominations and your whorings you did not remember the days of your youth" — the cognitive-memorial faculty fails to retrieve covenantal history. Eze 8:17 (vc=65980 — VCG-05): treating abomination as a "light thing" — the cognitive evaluative faculty has lost the capacity to assess moral gravity. Eze 20:4 (vc=65994 — VCG-05): "let them know the abominations of their fathers" — the command to know implies they don't currently understand the weight of what they inherited. Deu 13:14 (vc=65928 — VCG-02): the commanded diligent inquiry before acting on reports of communal apostasy — cognition is here applied as the appropriate investigative check.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Yes. Cognition is the primary faculty engaged in the characteristic's most definitionally central VCG. Eze 11:2 (vc=38193 — VCG-02): "men who devise iniquity and give wicked counsel" — devising is a deliberate cognitive act of planning. Mic 2:1 (vc=38217 — VCG-02): "those who devise wickedness… on their beds" — nocturnal deliberate planning. Isa 32:6 (vc=38181 — VCG-02): "his heart is busy with iniquity" — cognitive busyness as the mode. Isa 59:7 (vc=38203 — VCG-02): "their thoughts are thoughts of iniquity" — the entire thought-content is colonised by iniquitous cognitive material. Psa 64:2 (vc=38244 — VCG-03): "secret plots of the wicked" — plotting as a cognitive-scheming act.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Yes. Jude 10 (vc=14355 — VCG-01) directly addresses cognitive failure: "these people blaspheme all that they do not understand" — the cognitive faculty of understanding has failed or been bypassed entirely. The cognitive failure is comprehensive: everything not understood is blasphemed. Rev 13:6 (vc=14356 — VCG-01): blaspheming God's name, dwelling, and heaven's inhabitants — the scope of the blasphemy (everything connected with God and heaven) suggests a total cognitive inversion: instead of understanding leading to acknowledgment, incomprehension leads to contemptuous rejection. Rom 3:8 (vc=14358 — VCG-02): the false attribution of teaching ("do evil that good may come") requires the cognitive act of misrepresentation — a cognitive distortion applied to another's position.

---

##### T3.2.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair cognition in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Wickedness-as-settled-person-identity impairs cognition by corrupting the deliberative faculty (Pro 12:5), generating morally alien reasoning (Job 21:16), systematically excluding God from the thought-life (Psa 10:4), and progressively closing the capacity for moral understanding (Dan 12:10). It also bypasses discernment — the wicked person acts without the cognitive check of moral discernment (Isa 5:23). The characteristic does not enable or deepen cognition in any positive sense; it subverts cognition by replacing truth-oriented reasoning with deception-oriented deliberation.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The characteristic impairs cognition by corrupting its evaluative and relational functions. Col 1:21 (vc=14424 — VCG-06) shows cognition becoming hostile — the mind evaluates others and God through a lens of enmity rather than receptivity. 1Ti 6:4 (vc=14470 — VCG-06) shows cognition producing "evil suspicions" — a cognitive state that generates false, damaging assessments of others. The characteristic does not eliminate cognitive capacity (the person still thinks, still reasons) but it redirects and corrupts cognitive output toward hostile and suspicious assessments. Mat 9:4 (VCG-03) shows the cognitive faculty actively generating "evil thoughts" — the cognitive engagement is active, not passive.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The characteristic impairs the cognitive faculty's evaluative function by inverting it (Pro 17:15 — VCG-01: perverted judgment) and bypasses reflective cognition in those who proceed into abomination without consideration (Isa 44:19 — VCG-05). Pro 15:26 (vc=1679 — VCG-02) shows the cognitive faculty actively generating abominable content — the thoughts themselves are corrupt — showing cognition operating but producing wrong output. Luk 16:15 (vc=21 — VCG-02) reveals the self-justifying cognitive construction ("justifying yourselves before men") as itself an abomination — the abominable condition has co-opted the reasoning faculty to produce self-justification rather than honest assessment.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The characteristic impairs cognition in two specific functions: (1) the evaluative function — the capacity to assess moral gravity (Eze 8:17 — VCG-05: abomination treated as light matter); (2) the memorial function — the capacity to recall covenantal history (Eze 16:22 — VCG-05: not remembering the days of youth). The characteristic does not enhance cognitive capacity in any direction; it specifically degrades the cognitive functions that would enable the person to recognise the gravity of their idolatrous attachment and recall the covenantal relationship it betrays.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The characteristic corrupts the cognitive faculty by redirecting its capacity for deliberate planning toward evil production. The deliberative-planning function is not impaired in its operational capacity — the nocturnal deviser (Mic 2:1 — VCG-02) and the counsel-giver (Eze 11:2 — VCG-02) are cognitively active and skilled. The characteristic bypasses the cognitive faculty's evaluative function: Psa 14:4 (vc=38229 — VCG-03): "no knowledge" — the cognitive evaluation of moral reality is absent. The planning capacity is enabled and deepened for scheming purposes; the moral-evaluative function is bypassed.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The characteristic impairs and bypasses the higher cognitive faculties. Jude 10 (vc=14355 — VCG-01): "blaspheme all that they do not understand, and they are destroyed by all that they, like unreasoning animals, understand instinctively" — the cognitive faculty of rational understanding is bypassed; instinctual understanding replaces rational comprehension. The characteristic reduces cognitive operation to the pre-rational instinctual level, below the level of the image-bearing rational speech-capacity. Rom 3:8 (VCG-02): the false attribution requires active cognitive distortion — the cognitive faculty is engaged but producing false outputs (misrepresenting another's position).

---

##### T3.2.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with cognition reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The cognitive engagement pattern reveals that wickedness-as-settled-person-identity has occupied the reasoning faculty and redirected it toward the person's corrupt ends. The wicked person is not cognitively absent — they plot (Psa 37:12: "the wicked plots against the righteous"), devise (Jer 5:26: "wicked men… set a trap; they catch men"), and counsel (Pro 12:5) — the cognitive faculty is active. But it is active in the service of wickedness rather than truth. This reveals that wickedness is not a passive deficit but an active redirection of the person's cognitive resources toward corrupt ends. The characteristic co-opts the reasoning faculty rather than simply eliminating it.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The cognitive pattern reveals that constitutional inner evil co-opts the thinking faculty and redirects it toward three specific corruptions: hostile assessment (Col 1:21), suspicious reasoning (1Ti 6:4), and evil thought-generation (Mat 9:4). The pattern confirms that the characteristic is not a passive inner state but an active generator — it actively produces evil thoughts through the cognitive faculty. This explains why the NT's remedial commands are so often cognitive: Col 1:21's "hostile in mind" context requires a transformed mind (Rom 12:2 — though outside this corpus); the active cognitive generation of evil requires active cognitive renewal.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The cognitive pattern reveals that abomination operates within the cognitive faculty in three specific corruptions: deliberate thought-generation of abominable content (Pro 15:26 — VCG-02), perversion of the moral-evaluative cognitive faculty (Pro 17:15 — VCG-01 — justifying/condemning inverted), and cognitive bypass of reflective consideration that would name the abomination (Isa 44:19 — VCG-05). These three show the characteristic as corrupting the cognitive faculty at the levels of content (what thoughts are generated), assessment (how moral reality is evaluated), and reflection (whether the person considers what they are doing). Cognition is present and active in abomination but systematically misdirected.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The cognitive pattern reveals that idolatrous abomination specifically suppresses the two cognitive functions most needed to arrest it: gravity-assessment and covenantal memory. The person who cannot assess the gravity of their abomination (Eze 8:17 — VCG-05) and cannot remember the covenantal origins that would motivate departure (Eze 16:22 — VCG-05) is cognitively disarmed against the characteristic. This explains why external prophetic intervention (naming the abominations — Eze 16:2 — VCG-05; confronting with the knowledge of fathers' abominations — Eze 20:4 — VCG-05) is the necessary corrective — the person's own cognitive faculties can no longer perform this function.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The cognitive pattern reveals that iniquity as active scheming specifically co-opts the highest-level cognitive faculties (deliberate planning, premeditated devising, counsel-giving — Eze 11:2 — VCG-02; Mic 2:1 — VCG-02) while leaving the moral-evaluative cognitive function non-functional (Psa 14:4 — VCG-03: no knowledge). This creates an inner cognitive profile distinctive to the characteristic: high planning-scheming capacity, low moral-knowledge capacity. The person is cognitively sophisticated in evil production but cognitively blind to moral reality. This explains why the characteristic is so damaging: it weaponises the most capable cognitive faculties against others.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The cognitive pattern reveals that the characteristic exploits cognitive gaps — where understanding fails, blasphemous contempt fills the void (Jude 10 — VCG-01). This is analytically significant: the characteristic is not primarily a product of cognitive error (misunderstanding) but of the refusal to acknowledge what might be understood, and of contempt substituting for the understanding that is absent. The cognitive bypass (Jude 10 — VCG-01) reveals that the characteristic operates at a level below rational moral comprehension — it is a sub-rational expression of inner moral rejection, not a rationally considered position.

---

#### T3.3 — Memory

##### T3.3.1 — Does this characteristic engage the memory faculty — the holding and retrieving of inner-being reality across time — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The memory faculty is engaged through its absence and its consequences. The core practical-atheism evidence (Psa 9:17 — VCG-02 — "the wicked… all the nations that forget God") explicitly identifies forgetting as the wicked person's defining cognitive-memorial act. God-forgetting is the characteristic's memorial mode: the wicked person's memory retains everything except the orientation toward God. The legacy of the wicked is also addressed through memory's inverse: Pro 10:7 (VCG-09): "the name of the wicked will rot" — their memory is corrupted at the social level; what will be remembered of them is dishonour. Psa 9:5 (VCG-05): "you have blotted out their name forever and ever" — divine judgment is described as the ultimate erasure of the wicked person's memorial existence. The characteristic engages memory by displacing the God-memory that should be foundational and corrupting the social memory that will survive the person.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The evidence engages memory primarily through its consequences rather than the memory faculty directly. Heb 8:12 (vc=14342 — VCG-06): "I will remember their sins no more" — God's gracious choice not to remember the iniquities (adikia) implies that the iniquities exist as a moral record; the constitutional inner evil generates a record of offenses that divine memory could hold. Rom 1:18 (vc=14336 — VCG-05): unrighteousness "suppresses the truth" — the suppression implies a knowing that is actively being denied, which involves a form of distorted memorial function (the person knows truth but refuses to remember it or act on it). The characteristic engages memory through suppression (denying what is known) rather than through positive memorial content.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Yes. Memory is engaged through a specific restoration dynamic in VCG-04. Eze 36:31 (vc=1681 — VCG-04): "Then you will remember your evil ways and your deeds that were not good, and you will loathe yourselves for your iniquities and your abominations." The memory faculty is the mechanism through which the awakened conscience re-engages with past abominations — restored memory produces self-loathing. The verse shows memory not merely as a neutral cognitive recall but as the morally laden faculty that, when restored to function, enables genuine conscience engagement with past abominable acts.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Yes. Memory is engaged through its systematic failure. Eze 16:22 (vc=65985 — VCG-05): "in all your abominations and your whorings you did not remember the days of your youth, when you were naked and bare, wallowing in your blood" — the covenantal memory of origins (the founding divine care) is precisely what is suppressed. Eze 16:43 (vc=65987 — VCG-05): "because you have not remembered the days of your youth" — the memorial failure is stated as the cause of enraging the divine. Eze 6:9 (vc=1697 — VCG-05): "those of you who escape will remember me among the nations" — post-judgment restoration of memory is what produces conscience-reactivation and self-loathing. Memory's engagement with the characteristic is through its suppression: the characteristic operates by preventing the recall of what would arrest it.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Yes. Memory appears primarily in the context of iniquity's accumulation and the divine record of it. Job 21:19 (vc=38209 — VCG-04): "God stores up their iniquity for their children" — God's moral memory retains accumulated iniquity beyond the individual's lifespan. Psa 94:23 (vc=38249 — VCG-03): "He will bring back on them their iniquity" — the divine memory brings the person's own iniquity back as judgment; the judgment is precisely the return of what was done, implying a stored moral record. Psa 125:5 (vc=38382 — VCG-03): those who turn aside "to their crooked ways" — the crooked ways as a remembered moral trajectory that has been followed. The human memory faculty also appears in the evidence for the suppression of instruction-memory: Job 22:15 (vc=38210 — VCG-04): "the old way that wicked men have trod" — the memory of this worn path perpetuates the characteristic.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (S)

The 17-verse corpus does not directly evidence the memory faculty's engagement with this characteristic. No verse addresses what the blaspheming or falsely accusing person remembers or fails to remember in the course of the characteristic's operation. This silence is noted. The closest proximity to memory appears in the VCG-01 sequence (Rev 16:9/11/21) where repeated divine judgments apparently fail to leave a corrective moral memory — but this is inferential rather than directly evidenced.

---

##### T3.3.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair memory in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The characteristic impairs the memory faculty specifically in its God-directed function. The forgetting of God (Psa 9:17) is not simple cognitive absence — it is an active orientation away from what should be most memorable. The wicked person's memory functions in selective dis-orientation: they retain plans for harm (Psa 37:12), strategies of deception (Pro 12:5), and personal gain (Pro 17:23), but suppress the God-memory that would constitute their reference for moral reality. The characteristic bypasses the normative memorial function of keeping God in view.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The characteristic impairs the truth-retaining function of memory through active suppression. Rom 1:18 (vc=14336 — VCG-05): the constitutionally unrighteous person "suppresses the truth" — this is an active act of memory-distortion in which what is known is denied through the will's refusal. The characteristic therefore does not destroy the cognitive-memorial capacity to know truth but deploys the will to actively prevent that truth from operating in the person's inner life. The memory faculty is present but systematically prevented from generating its designed output (truth-orientation).

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The characteristic impairs the morally functioning memory when the conscience is silenced. The absence of shame (Jer 6:15 — vc=1680 — VCG-04; Jer 8:12 — vc=1696 — VCG-04) implies a suppression of the memory of abominable acts that would otherwise produce shame. The person who does not know how to blush is not recalling and registering the moral weight of their acts. Conversely, the restoration of memory (Eze 36:31 — vc=1681 — VCG-04) is the instrument through which conscience is reactivated — memory-restoration is the mechanism of conscience-awakening. The characteristic impairs morally functional memory in its settled state and can be addressed through the restoration of that memory.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The characteristic impairs covenantal memory — specifically the memory of divine care and covenant origins. Eze 16:22 (vc=65985 — VCG-05) and 16:43 (vc=65987 — VCG-05) both name the failure to remember as causally related to the continuation of abominations. The characteristic bypasses the covenantal-memory faculty, preventing the retrieval of the moral history that would constrain the inner person's idolatrous attachment. Eze 6:9 (vc=1697 — VCG-05) shows that the restoration of memory (post-judgment) is what enables self-loathing and conscience-engagement — confirming that the characteristic's suppression of memory is the mechanism through which conscience is bypassed.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The characteristic bypasses the human memory faculty's moral-corrective function: the person who has cherished iniquity in the heart (Psa 66:18 — VCG-04) or ceased to act wisely (Psa 36:3 — VCG-04) is no longer retrieving and applying the moral memories that would correct the trajectory. Job 36:10 (vc=38215 — VCG-04): divine instruction opens the ears to "return from iniquity" — the return-metaphor implies a memory of where one came from, which the characteristic suppresses. The divine memory operates in the opposite direction: it retains the person's iniquity for eventual return (Psa 94:23 — VCG-03), showing that what the human memory forgets or suppresses, the divine memory retains.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (S)

The evidence is silent on the memory faculty's specific engagement with this characteristic (T3.3.1). The inference from the Rev 16 sequence (VCG-01) is that the characteristic bypasses moral memory — previous judgments do not accumulate as corrective memorial evidence — but this is not directly stated in the corpus. This silence is noted.

---

##### T3.3.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with memory reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The God-forgetting pattern reveals that wickedness-as-settled-person-identity has reorganised the memory faculty around the self and its projects rather than God. Memory in biblical anthropology functions covenantally — to remember God is to orient the self toward covenant reality. The wicked person's forgetting of God (Psa 9:17) is therefore not a cognitive failure but a dispositional orientation: the memory faculty has been redirected toward the person's own projects at the expense of the covenantal orientation. The consequence — their name will rot (Pro 10:7) and be blotted out (Psa 9:5) — reveals a divine irony: the person who refuses to remember God is themselves forgotten or erased.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The suppression of truth (Rom 1:18 — VCG-05) reveals that the constitutional evil's engagement with memory is an act of active inner violence against the person's own truth-knowing capacity. The person constitutionally evil knows truth (the suppression implies there is something to suppress) but the constitutional evil generates a persistent act of will that prevents the truth from functioning. This reveals the characteristic as not merely an absence of good but a positive counter-force that actively works against the person's own better knowing. The memory pattern confirms the characteristic's active and aggressive nature even at the deepest cognitive-memorial level.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The memory pattern (Eze 36:31 — VCG-04) reveals a distinctive aspect of this characteristic: the conscience's awakening is mediated specifically through remembered moral history. The person "will remember your evil ways" — the memory of specific past acts is the route through which abomination becomes self-loathing. This reveals memory as the faculty through which the divine verdict on abomination is personalised and made inner — the person must remember what they did before they can own the verdict on it. The pattern shows memory as a morally therapeutic faculty when it is restored to function; its suppression (the silenced conscience that does not remember in a morally weighted way) enables continued abomination without inner arrest.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The memory pattern reveals that idolatrous abomination requires the suppression of covenantal memory to sustain itself. The person who remembers the "days of their youth" — the founding divine care — would be constrained by that memory from continuing in abomination. The characteristic's survival depends on not-remembering. This makes memory restoration (Eze 6:9 — VCG-05 — survivors remembering God) the mechanism of conscience-reactivation and the beginning of departure from the characteristic. The memory pattern also shows the characteristic as specifically a covenantal-fidelity failure: what is forgotten is not a generic past but the specific history of divine care that grounds covenant obligation.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The memory pattern reveals a significant asymmetry: the person practising iniquity operates with suppressed moral-corrective memory (no longer retrieving the instruction that would produce return — Job 36:10 — VCG-04) while the divine memory retains their iniquity for eventual judgment (Psa 94:23 — VCG-03; Job 21:19 — VCG-04). This asymmetry means the iniquity-schemer cannot escape the moral record even through forgetting. The memory pattern also reveals Job 22:15 (VCG-04) — the worn path of wicked men — as a collective memory of trajectory that perpetuates the characteristic: the person remembers the path walked by predecessors and follows it.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (S)

Memory engagement is not directly evidenced in this corpus (T3.3.1–T3.3.2). The silence is analytically significant: the characteristic's relationship to moral memory (whether the blasphemer carries or suppresses the memory of what should constrain their speech) is not addressed in the 17-verse corpus. This is a gap where further investigation of the broader blasphemy context would be needed.

---

#### T3.4 — Affect

##### T3.4.1 — Does this characteristic engage the affective faculty — feeling and emotional experience — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Yes. The affective faculty is engaged and corrupted. Evidence across VCGs: (1) Pride as an affective disposition — Pro 21:4 (VCG-03): "haughty eyes and a proud heart" name an affective posture of self-elevation; (2) inner hostility — Psa 37:12 (VCG-03): "gnashes his teeth" — a visceral affective expression of hostility toward the righteous; (3) exultation that is momentary — Job 20:5 (VCG-10): "the exulting of the wicked is short" — an affective high that cannot sustain itself; (4) soul-level desire as affect — Pro 21:10 (VCG-09): "the soul of the wicked desires evil" — desire is the affective dimension of this soul-level orientation; (5) inner fear — Pro 10:24 (VCG-06): "what the wicked dreads will come upon him" — the characteristic produces chronic inner dread; (6) inner anguish — Job 15:20 (VCG-06): "the wicked man writhes in pain all his days."

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Yes. Affective engagement is documented across multiple VCGs. Mat 20:15 (vc=14460 — VCG-06): the evil eye as inner envy and grudging resentment — envy is a direct affective expression of the constitutional evil. Jam 4:16 (vc=14472 — VCG-06): boasting from arrogance declared evil — the affective disposition of pride expressing outward through self-aggrandizing speech. Joh 3:19 (vc=14448 — VCG-04): people "loved the darkness" — love is here an affective orientation toward moral concealment; the characteristic has corrupted the affective faculty of love to attach to darkness. 1Cor 13:6 (vc=14341 — VCG-06): unrighteousness is something that could draw "inner delight" — the affective capacity for delight is capable of being attracted to wrongdoing.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Yes, extensively. The characteristic is constitutively affective on the divine side (revulsion, loathing, hatred — Pro 6:16: "hates"; Pro 11:20 — VCG-01: contrasted with "delight") and generates specific human affective responses. On the human side, when conscience is functional: Eze 9:4 (vc=1698 — VCG-04): "sigh and groan" — grief and anguish as the affective response to perceived abomination; Eze 36:31 (vc=1681 — VCG-04): "you will loathe yourselves" — self-loathing as the affective response to remembered abomination. When conscience is silenced: the affective faculty of shame is entirely absent — Jer 6:15; 8:12 (VCG-04): no shame, no blushing — the affective moral faculty that should register the abomination produces nothing. Pro 13:19 (vc=1687 — VCG-05): the fool experiences turning from evil as affectively abominable — an inverted moral affect.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Yes. The affective faculty is centrally and definitionally engaged. Isa 66:3 (vc=1633 — VCG-04): "their soul delights in their abominations" — the delight faculty is inverted: attached to abominations rather than to God. Deu 32:16 (vc=65938 — VCG-02): "they stirred him to jealousy with strange gods; with abominations they provoked him to anger" — the relational affect of jealousy on the divine side and of provocative betrayal on the human side. Eze 7:20 (vc=65909 — VCG-05): "His beautiful ornament they used for pride" — pride as an affective disposition drives the characteristic. Eze 16:36 (vc=65986 — VCG-05): "your lust was poured out" — intense desire as the affective fuel of idolatrous abomination.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Yes. The affective faculty appears in its inverted form. Isa 66:3 (vc=38204 — VCG-04): "their soul delights in their abominations" — the delight-faculty is attached to their iniquitous self-chosen ways. Pro 19:28 (vc=38220 — VCG-03): "the mouth of the wicked devours iniquity" — devouring implies an inner craving and appetite for iniquity; this is an affective desire-state, not merely a cognitive or volitional choice. Pro 21:15 (vc=38221 — VCG-03): "when justice is done, it is a joy to the righteous but terror to evildoers" — the evildoer's affective response to justice is terror (dread), revealing that the inner affective faculty is so aligned with iniquity that right judgment produces fear rather than relief. Psa 55:3 (vc=38188 — VCG-01): enemies "in anger they bear a grudge" — the affective state of sustained anger and grudge-bearing sustains the iniquity directed at others.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Yes. The affective faculty appears in the contempt-register of VCG-01. Rev 13:6 (vc=14356 — VCG-01): sustained deliberate blasphemy against God's name and dwelling — the sustained quality of the blasphemy reveals contempt as a deep affective inner orientation, not a momentary emotional outburst. Rev 16:9/11/21 (VCG-01): people under catastrophic judgment curse God — the cursing carries intense affective hostility: anger and defiance directed toward God. Jude 8 (vc=14354 — VCG-01): "defile the flesh" alongside authority-rejection and blasphemy — the sensory/fleshly self-indulgence accompanies the blasphemous expression, showing that affective self-indulgence and contemptuous speech are paired inner states.

---

##### T3.4.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair affect in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The characteristic corrupts and distorts the affective faculty. The affect of the wicked person is not absent but maloriented: pride produces self-elevation (Pro 21:4), desire produces craving for evil (Pro 21:10), exultation is momentary and founded on what cannot sustain itself (Job 20:5), and the deeper sustained affect is anguish and inner torment (Job 15:20; Pro 32:10 — "many are the sorrows of the wicked"). The characteristic does not simply impair affect — it redirects it toward corrupt objects and corrupt postures, producing a characteristic emotional signature of momentary exultation, chronic inner want, dread of coming consequences, and sustained torment.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The characteristic corrupts and redirects affect toward wrong objects. Joh 3:19 (vc=14448 — VCG-04) shows love corrupted — the affective capacity for love is present but attached to darkness rather than light. 1Cor 13:6 (vc=14341 — VCG-06) implies the possibility of "rejoicing in" unrighteousness — the affective capacity for joy is capable of being wrongly attached to wrongdoing. The characteristic does not eliminate the affective faculty but redirects its primary attachments toward what is constitutionally evil. The corrective commands (Rom 12:9 — VCG-06: "abhor what is evil; hold fast to what is good") presuppose that the affective faculty of abhorrence must be actively redirected — indicating the characteristic has redirected it wrongly.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The characteristic impairs the morally appropriate affective responses (shame, self-loathing, grief) when the conscience is silenced (Jer 6:15; 8:12 — VCG-04: no shame or blushing). It inverts affect in the fool who finds departure from evil affectively repugnant (Pro 13:19 — VCG-05). When conscience is restored, the characteristic produces and deepens the appropriate affective responses: Eze 36:31 (vc=1681 — VCG-04) — self-loathing; Eze 9:4 (vc=1698 — VCG-04) — sighing and groaning. The characteristic is thus affectively ambiguous in its effect: it suppresses appropriate affect in the hardened abominable person and intensifies appropriate affect in the awakened conscience.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The characteristic corrupts and inverts the affective faculty by redirecting it toward wrong objects. Isa 66:3 (vc=1633 — VCG-04): the soul's delight is attached to abominations — the affective capacity for delight is present and functioning but attached wrongly. Eze 16:36 (vc=65986 — VCG-05): "lust poured out" through idolatrous whorings — the affective-desire capacity is intensified but misdirected. The characteristic does not impair the affective faculty in the sense of reducing its intensity; rather, it inverts the faculty's attachment — making what should be repugnant delightful, and detaching affect from what should inspire delight (the divine).

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The characteristic inverts and redirects the affective faculty. Isa 66:3 (VCG-04): the soul's delight is attached to abominable ways — delight is functional but misdirected. Pro 19:28 (VCG-03): the devouring mouth — appetite/craving is functional and intensified but toward evil. Pro 21:15 (VCG-03): terror at justice — the appropriate affective response to justice (joy) is inverted to terror. The characteristic does not impair affect in terms of reducing its intensity; rather, it redirects affect toward wrong objects (delight in evil) and inverts appropriate responses (terror at justice rather than joy). The affective faculty is thus deepened in its attachment to iniquity and impaired in its orientation toward the good.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The characteristic intensifies and inverts the affective faculty. Rev 16:9/11/21 (VCG-01): under judgment the cursing intensifies — the affliction deepens the hostile affective state rather than breaking it. Rev 13:6 (VCG-01): sustained blasphemy shows affect deepening over time in the direction of contempt. The characteristic inverts the appropriate affective response to judgment (contrition, grief) into defiant hostility (cursing, contempt). The affective faculty that should move toward God in grief and repentance is redirected into sustained contemptuous hostility. The characteristic thus deepens the wrong affective orientation while impairs the capacity for appropriate affective response (contrition).

---

##### T3.4.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with affect reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The affective pattern reveals a fundamental inner contradiction within the wicked person: they exult (Job 20:5), boast of their soul's desires (Psa 10:3 — VCG-02), and pursue what they crave — but the affect produced is ultimately one of inner desolation (Isa 57:20-21 — "like the tossing sea… there is no peace for the wicked"). The wicked person's affective life is characterised by the short-circuit: the affect of momentary exultation and craving is present, but the capacity for the stable positive affect of shalom is structurally foreclosed by the characteristic. This reveals that wickedness-as-settled-person-identity is affectively self-defeating: it promises inner gratification but produces inner want and torment.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The affective pattern reveals a profound inner contradiction: the constitutional evil person has not lost their affective capacity but has attached it to wrong objects. They love darkness (Joh 3:19 — VCG-04), hate the truthful witness (Joh 7:7 — VCG-04), experience envy (Mat 20:15 — VCG-06), and can delight in wrongdoing (1Cor 13:6 — VCG-06). The characteristic's affective engagement reveals it as a comprehensive corruption of the person's evaluative-affective apparatus — what they love, hate, envy, and delight in are all constitutionally misdirected. The affective faculty is fully operational but systematically oriented toward wrong objects.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The affective pattern reveals that the characteristic is deeply connected to the shame faculty as its primary inner-being diagnostic. Shame and self-loathing are the appropriate affective responses to abomination (Eze 36:31 — VCG-04); their absence (Jer 6:15; 8:12 — VCG-04) signals a conscience wholly silenced. This makes the affect of shame the diagnostic test for the characteristic's inner-being engagement: shame present = conscience alive; shame absent = conscience silenced; shame experienced at turned-from-evil = conscience inverted. The affective pattern reveals the characteristic as one whose inner diagnostic is specifically shame — a datum that distinguishes CHAR-3 from other characteristics in the M10b cluster.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The affective pattern reveals that idolatrous abomination involves a specific inversion of the delight-faculty: Isa 66:3 (vc=1633 — VCG-04) — "soul delights in their abominations." This is the affective signature of the characteristic: the soul's delight is attached to what is abominable. This affective inversion distinguishes CHAR-4 from CHAR-3's shame-diagnostic: CHAR-3's inner diagnostic is the presence or absence of shame; CHAR-4's inner diagnostic is the presence or absence of delight in abominations. The soul that delights in abominations rather than recoiling has completed the affective inversion that defines idolatrous abomination at its deepest level.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The affective pattern reveals that iniquity as scheming, when fully established, produces an inverted affective world: the person delights in what is abominable (Isa 66:3 — VCG-04), craves what is harmful (Pro 19:28 — VCG-03), and dreads what is righteous (Pro 21:15 — VCG-03). This affective inversion is analytically significant: it shows the characteristic as not merely a cognitive-volitional disorder but a comprehensive inner-being transformation in which the affective faculty has been fully re-calibrated toward evil. The inverse of this pattern — joy at justice, delight in righteousness — is the goal toward which Isa 55:7 (vc=38200 — VCG-02) calls: returning to the Lord involves returning the affective faculty to its rightful orientation.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The affective pattern reveals that the characteristic is not affectively neutral speech — it is charged with intense contemptuous hostility (VCG-01). The cursing under judgment (Rev 16:9/11/21 — VCG-01) shows an affective state of active hostility that divine pressure intensifies rather than reduces. This affective pattern distinguishes the characteristic from mere cognitive error or careless speech: the blasphemy is affectively loaded with contempt, making it a deeply motivated inner-being expression rather than incidental wrongdoing. The characteristic reveals contempt as the affective signature of the hardened will's relationship to God.

---

#### T3.5 — Creativity

##### T3.5.1 — Does this characteristic engage the creative faculty — imagination and the capacity to originate — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The creative-imaginative faculty is engaged but subverted. The evidence from VCG-03 and VCG-08 shows the wicked person deploying originative capacity toward harmful ends: Jer 5:26 (VCG-03): "they lurk like fowlers lying in wait; they set a trap; they catch men" — tactical imagination applied to predation. Psa 37:12 (VCG-03): "the wicked plots against the righteous" — plotting as the creative-planning faculty directed toward harm. Pro 12:5 (VCG-08): "the counsels of the wicked are deceitful" — the deliberative-creative faculty generating deceptive plans. Pro 12:6 (VCG-08): "the words of the wicked lie in wait for blood" — speech as a weaponised creative construct. The wicked person's creativity is operational; it is redirected toward harm rather than toward the building of shalom.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The creative-imaginative faculty is engaged through its redirection toward harmful origination. Mat 12:35 (vc=14420 — VCG-03): "the evil person out of his evil treasure brings forth evil" — the bringing-forth is an active generative act; the person draws creatively from the inner treasury to produce evil outputs. Mat 15:19 (vc=14414 — VCG-03): "out of the heart come evil thoughts" — the origination of evil thoughts is a creative-generative act of the heart. 1Ti 6:4 (vc=14470 — VCG-06): evil suspicions from a mind inflated with conceit — the generation of suspicious thoughts is an imaginative-creative act in the negative direction. The creative faculty is engaged but redirected toward generating evil rather than good.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The creative faculty is engaged primarily in the service of concealment and deception. Pro 26:25 (vc=1694 — VCG-02): "when he speaks graciously, believe him not, for there are seven abominations in his heart" — the gracious speech is a creative performance constructed to conceal the heart's multiple corrupt motivations; imagination and artful presentation are deployed to mask abomination. Pro 17:15 (vc=1690 — VCG-01): perverted judgment — the cognitive-creative act of justifying the wicked and condemning the righteous requires the creative construction of inverted moral arguments. Deu 27:15 (vc=65937 — VCG-04): "makes a carved or cast metal image" and "sets it up in secret" — the craftsman's creative act produces the abominable object; creativity is here deployed in abominable service.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Yes. The creative faculty is engaged through its redirection toward idol-making. Eze 7:20 (vc=65909 — VCG-05): "His beautiful ornament they used for pride, and they made their abominable images and their detestable things of it" — the creative act of making is the primary creative engagement. Deu 29:17 (vc=65897 — VCG-02): "idols of wood and stone, of silver and gold" — the material diversity of idol-crafting shows sustained creative investment. The construction of high places for foreign deities (1Ki 11:7 — vc=65899 — VCG-03: "Solomon built a high place for Chemosh") involves architectural creativity deployed in idolatrous service. The creative faculty is fully operational in the characteristic — producing elaborate idol-objects, sacred spaces, and cultic practices in service of false devotion.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Yes. The creative-imaginative faculty is engaged through its specific co-optation for scheming. Psa 7:14 (vc=38245 — VCG-02): "conceives evil… pregnant with mischief… gives birth to lies" — the birth metaphor for iniquity names a creative process: conception, gestation, birth. The inner person imagines, develops, and produces iniquity as a creative act. Eze 11:2 (vc=38193 — VCG-02): "men who devise iniquity and who give wicked counsel in this city" — devising and counsel-giving require creative mental construction of plans and scenarios. Isa 10:1 (vc=38191 — VCG-02): "those who decree iniquitous decrees, and the writers who keep writing oppression" — the institutional creative act of writing and decreeing oppression shows creative capacity deployed in the service of systematised harm.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Yes, partially. The creative faculty appears in VCG-02's false attribution. Rom 3:8 (vc=14358 — VCG-02): "why not do evil that good may come? — as some people slanderously charge us with saying" — the false attribution requires creative construction of a teaching position never held; the slanderers invented or distorted a position to misrepresent Paul. The creative faculty is engaged in the service of misrepresentation: producing a false verbal portrait of another's position. VCG-03: Joh 18:30 (vc=14378 — VCG-03): "if this man were not doing evil, we would not have delivered him over to you" — the false charge requires the creative construction of a justificatory narrative for the hostile action.

---

##### T3.5.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair creativity in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The characteristic co-opts the creative faculty for destructive ends rather than impairing it. The wicked person plans (Psa 37:12), constructs traps (Jer 5:26), generates deceptive counsel (Pro 12:5), and weaponises speech (Pro 12:6) — all creative operations. The faculty is operational but redirected. The impairment is of the faculty's orientation toward its designed purpose (the creation of good, the building of just community), not of the faculty itself. The evidence does not show the wicked person as creatively disabled; rather, their creative capacity is fully deployed in the service of wickedness.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The characteristic co-opts the creative faculty for evil production rather than impairing it. The evil person "brings forth evil" (Mat 12:35 — VCG-03) — the bringing-forth is the creative act. The characteristic does not disable origination but redirects what is originated. 3Jo 10 (vc=14454 — VCG-04) shows creative energy directed toward domineering community control — active, organized, and persistent social harm requiring the creative deployment of speech and obstruction. The characteristic enables and directs the creative faculty toward evil; it does not empty or disable it.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The characteristic co-opts the creative faculty for the production of concealment and deception rather than impairing it. Pro 26:25 (vc=1694 — VCG-02): the gracious speech covering seven inner abominations requires considerable creative social performance — the creative faculty is fully operational in the service of masking the abominable inner state. The characteristic does not eliminate creativity but redirects it toward concealment and moral inversion. The act of making idols (Deu 27:15 — VCG-04) shows creativity deployed in abominable service — the craftsman's skill is present, but the product is an abomination.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The characteristic redirects and energises the creative faculty toward idolatrous production. The Eze 7:20 (VCG-05) example is most revealing: the person takes "beautiful ornament" — already a product of creative care — and converts it into idol-material, showing creative repurposing in the service of abomination. The creativity is fully present and resourced; it is not impaired but redirected. The energy and ingenuity of idol-making (Deu 29:17 — VCG-02: wood, stone, silver, gold — diverse material engagement) show creative capacity fully deployed in the characteristic's service.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The characteristic redirects and enables the creative faculty for evil production. The nocturnal deviser (Mic 2:1 — VCG-02: lying on the bed devising wickedness) is exercising sustained imaginative planning; the counsel-giver (Eze 11:2 — VCG-02) is producing creative social strategies. Psa 64:2 (vc=38244 — VCG-03): "secret plots of the wicked" — the secrecy implies creative concealment alongside the scheming. The creative faculty is not impaired but fully operational and redirected toward harm-generation. Isa 10:1 (vc=38191 — VCG-02): "writers who keep writing oppression" — the professional creative act of writing is co-opted for institutional harm.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The characteristic redirects the creative faculty toward misrepresentation and false narrative construction. Rom 3:8 (VCG-02): the creative capacity deployed to construct a falsely attributed teaching. Joh 18:30 (VCG-03): the creative capacity deployed to construct a justificatory false charge. In VCG-01 (the direct blasphemy register), the creative faculty appears less prominently — the hardened will expressing contempt through cursing does not require the same creative construction as false attribution. The characteristic thus engages creativity differently by VCG: VCG-01 is more directly hostile without requiring creative fabrication; VCG-02/03 require active verbal construction of false representations.

---

##### T3.5.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with creativity reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The creative engagement pattern reveals that wickedness-as-settled-person-identity does not destroy the inner-being faculties — it subverts and redirects them. This is analytically important: the wicked person remains a fully equipped image-bearer in terms of faculty-presence (they can plan, reason, speak, desire, imagine) — but every faculty is oriented away from its designed end toward wickedness. The creative faculty's subversion into harm-planning confirms that wickedness is not a reduction of the person's inner capacities but a reorientation of them.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The creative engagement pattern reveals that evil as constitutional inner nature is not a passive absence of good — it is an active generating condition. The evil treasury (Mat 12:35 — VCG-03) is not empty but full, and the person actively draws from it. This confirms the characteristic as a structural source of active evil production, not merely a deficiency. The creative pattern also reveals why the NT's remedial commands focus on filling and renewal rather than merely emptying: Jam 1:21 (vc=14368 — VCG-05) calls for receiving the implanted word — the creative faculty needs a new treasury to draw from, not merely the old one removed.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The creative pattern reveals the characteristic as particularly threatening in the social sphere because the creative faculty is deployed to mask and perpetuate it. Pro 26:25 (vc=1694 — VCG-02) shows that the person with seven abominations in their heart can generate gracious and convincing social performance — the creative faculty is the tool of concealment. This explains the emphasis on divine perception penetrating social performance: Luk 16:15 (vc=21 — VCG-02): "God knows your hearts" — the divine faculty sees through the creative social construct to the abominable inner condition beneath.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The creative pattern reveals that idolatrous abomination co-opts human creative capacity as the vehicle through which false devotion is embodied. The idol is not a discovery but a creation — it is made (Eze 7:20 — VCG-05; crafted from materials). This means the characteristic redirects the image-bearing creativity that should produce images of God's glory toward the production of rival god-images. The pattern confirms that idolatrous abomination is not a passive deficiency but an active creative project — the inner attachment to idols expresses itself through the creative construction of the objects of devotion.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The creative pattern reveals that iniquity as active scheming specifically requires and deploys the creative faculty — the characteristic is not merely passive or reactive but generatively productive. The birth metaphor (Psa 7:14 — VCG-02; Job 15:35 — VCG-02) positions the characteristic as the output of a creative inner process. This makes iniquity-as-scheming distinctively different from moral failure through weakness or impulse: it involves sustained, creative, premeditated inner activity. The creative pattern reveals the characteristic as an anti-creation: the image-bearing creative capacity redirected from good generation to harm generation.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The creative pattern reveals a distinction within the characteristic's three registers. VCG-02/03's false-attribution and false-charge modes engage the creative faculty through verbal construction of misrepresentations (Rom 3:8 — VCG-02; Joh 18:30 — VCG-03). VCG-01's direct blasphemy mode bypasses elaborate creative construction — the defiant cursing (Rev 16:9/11/21 — VCG-01) is direct, unelaborate hostile speech. The creative engagement pattern thus reveals that false accusation and defamation (VCG-02/03) require creative verbal fabrication, while direct hardened-will blasphemy (VCG-01) is more raw and immediate.

---

#### T3.6 — Volition

##### T3.6.1 — Does this characteristic engage the volitional faculty — the capacity to choose — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Yes. Volition is the primary faculty engaged by wickedness-as-settled-person-identity (confirming T1.8.1). The Ezekiel corpus (VCG-07, 22V) is the definitive evidence: wickedness is consistently addressed as a "way" the wicked person is "on" and can "turn from" (Eze 3:18; 18:21; 33:11-19). The volitional faculty is engaged by: (1) the initial directional choice ("enter the path of the wicked" — Pro 4:14 — a volitional entry); (2) the sustained volitional refusal to turn (Eze 3:19; 33:9 — "he does not turn from his way"); (3) the active inner renunciation of God (Psa 10:13 — "renounce God"; Psa 9:17 — "forget God"); (4) the willed entry into alliance with the wicked (Psa 1:1 — walking, standing, sitting — three progressively deeper volitional stages of alignment). The characteristic is constituted and sustained by volitional acts.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Yes, though the volitional dimension is secondary to the constitutional-structural primary classification (T1.8.1). The will is engaged in several registers: (1) active preference — Joh 3:19 (vc=14448 — VCG-04): people "loved the darkness" — the will chose moral concealment; (2) active suppression — Rom 1:18 (vc=14336 — VCG-05): "suppress the truth" — the will is actively engaged in preventing truth's operation; (3) obedience to unrighteousness — Rom 2:8 (vc=14338 — VCG-05): "do not obey the truth, but obey unrighteousness" — the will's allegiance is given to the constitutional evil rather than truth; (4) knowing non-compliance — Luk 19:22 (vc=14447 — VCG-04): "you knew…and still refused" — the will operates despite knowledge to withhold faithful action.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Yes. Volition is directly engaged across multiple VCGs. Deu 25:16 (vc=65936 — VCG-01): "all who act dishonestly" — the abominable quality arises from chosen habitual behaviour. Eze 14:6 (vc=65984 — VCG-04): "repent and turn away from your idols, and turn away your faces from all your abominations" — the call to repentance addresses the will directly: the abominations are things the will is currently oriented toward, and repentance requires volitional redirection. Pro 13:19 (vc=1687 — VCG-05): "to turn away from evil is an abomination to fools" — the will's resistance to departure from evil is the distinctive volitional engagement; the fool's will is so bonded to evil that the idea of turning is experienced as repugnant. Deu 27:15 (vc=65937 — VCG-04): the person "makes" and "sets it up in secret" — volitional acts producing abomination while knowing it is wrong.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Yes. Volition is the primary faculty engaged (confirming T1.8.1). The Deuteronomic VCG-02 (14V) addresses the will directly throughout: "you shall not covet" (Deu 7:25 — VCG-02), "you shall not learn to follow" (Deu 18:9 — VCG-02), "you shall not worship" (Deu 12:31 — VCG-02). The Ezekiel corpus (VCG-05) shows the will in its hardened state: Eze 20:8 (vc=65911 — VCG-05): "they rebelled against me and were not willing to listen to me. None of them cast away the detestable things" — volitional refusal is the precise characterisation. Isa 66:3 (vc=1633 — VCG-04): "they have chosen their own ways" — volitional choice as the constitutive act of the characteristic.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Yes. Volition is the primary faculty engaged, as confirmed by the characteristic's primary classification. Job 36:21 (vc=38216 — VCG-04): "do not turn to iniquity, for this you have chosen rather than affliction" — volitional choice is the stated mechanism of the characteristic's entry and persistence. Psa 36:4 (vc=38235 — VCG-02): "he sets himself in a way that is not good; he does not reject evil" — the refusal to reject evil is a volitional act of sustained commitment. Mic 2:1 (vc=38217 — VCG-02): "when the morning dawns, they perform it, because it is in the power of their hand" — the "power of their hand" shows the will's execution capacity aligned with the scheming. 1Sa 15:23 (vc=38185 — VCG-02): "presumption" called iniquity — self-assertive will elevating its own judgment above the divine word.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Yes. Volition is the primary faculty — the characteristic is constituted by the will's expression of wickedness through speech. Rev 16:9 (vc=14352 — VCG-01): "they did not repent and give him glory" — the refusal to repent is the defining volitional act; the cursing of God's name is the positive volitional expression. Jude 8 (vc=14354 — VCG-01): "reject authority and blaspheme the glorious ones" — authority-rejection is explicitly volitional. Rev 13:6 (vc=14356 — VCG-01): "opened its mouth to utter blasphemies" — the deliberate opening of the mouth is a volitional act. Joh 18:30 (vc=14378 — VCG-03): the accusers deliberately formulate and deliver the false charge — a volitional speech act. The characteristic is volitionally active throughout: it requires deliberate choice at multiple levels (refusing repentance, choosing the speech act, choosing the content of the false accusation).

---

##### T3.6.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair volition in the person — including its three aspects: capacity, interaction with other characteristics, and the constraints under which it operates?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The characteristic progressively impairs the full range of volitional freedom. Volition is initially engaged (Pro 4:14 — the choice to enter the path) but the sustained operation of the characteristic restricts the scope of volitional capacity: Pro 5:22 ("ensnared, held fast in the cords of his sin") — wickedness generates its own volitional constraints; Isa 26:10 ("he does not learn righteousness") — the volitional capacity to receive righteous instruction is impaired by the settled characteristic. The evidence presents volition as both the primary faculty by which the characteristic is adopted and the primary faculty the characteristic eventually constrains. This is the trajectory: volitional entry → sustained volitional refusal to turn → progressive volitional bondage.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The characteristic constrains volitional freedom while keeping the will active. The will is present (the person suppresses truth, chooses darkness, obeys unrighteousness — all volitional acts), but the constitutional condition narrows the range within which the will operates freely. Mat 7:18 (vc=14440 — VCG-02): "a diseased tree cannot bear good fruit" — the word "cannot" indicates a constitutional constraint on volitional possibility. The will is not eliminated but is structurally constrained by the constitutional evil condition: it can choose among evil options but cannot choose good fruit from an evil tree without the tree's nature being changed. This is distinct from CHAR-1's volitional orientation: CHAR-2 describes a constitutional constraint on what the will can produce; CHAR-1 describes the direction the will has chosen.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The characteristic progressively constrains volitional freedom. In its settled state, the fool's will is so oriented toward evil that departure is experienced as repugnant (Pro 13:19 — VCG-05) — the will's range of choice has narrowed to within the abominable. Eze 14:6 (vc=65984 — VCG-04) reveals that the will is currently "facing" abominations — the volitional direction requires the commanding divine call to reverse. The characteristic does not eliminate volition (the commands to repent and turn presuppose volitional capacity) but it constrains and misdirects the will toward abominable orientations and away from departure.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The characteristic progressively constrains volitional freedom. Initially, the characteristic enters through a volitional choice (Isa 66:3 — VCG-04: "chosen their own ways"). Sustained attachment then constrains the will: Eze 20:8 (vc=65911 — VCG-05) shows a community "not willing" to cast away the idols — the will has become bound by the attachment. Deu 7:26 (vc=65927 — VCG-02): bringing the abominable thing into the house "makes you devoted to destruction like it" — the act of proximity re-orients the will toward the abominable object.
