The will is not eliminated but progressively aligned with the idol's pull, narrowing the person's volitional freedom to depart.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The characteristic progressively constrains volitional freedom. Initially the characteristic is entered through volitional choice (Job 36:21 — VCG-04). As it deepens, the will becomes bound by the characteristic: Psa 119:133 (vc=38227 — VCG-04): iniquity seeking "dominion over me" — the will's governing function is at risk of being displaced by iniquity's control. Job 36:10 (vc=38215 — VCG-04): God must open their ears to enable return — the will cannot independently reverse the trajectory without divine intervention at an advanced stage. The characteristic does not eliminate volition (the commands to return and put far away are addressed to the will) but progressively constrains its range of free movement toward departure.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The characteristic progressively constrains and hardens the volitional faculty. Rev 16:9/11/21 (VCG-01): across three escalating divine judgments, the will maintains and deepens its defiant posture — each judgment compounds the hardening. The volitional refusal to repent becomes more absolute rather than weakening. This progressive constraint shows the characteristic as self-reinforcing in its volitional dimension: each act of defiant speech entrenches the will more deeply in the direction it has chosen. The will is not eliminated (the choice to speak remains deliberate) but its range of genuine choice toward repentance progressively narrows.

---

##### T3.6.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with volition reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The volitional engagement pattern reveals a crucial diagnostic: because wickedness-as-settled-person-identity is primarily a volitional phenomenon (entered, sustained, and potentially reversed by the will), it is the will that must be addressed in any transformation of the characteristic. The Ezekiel corpus's consistent call for the wicked to "turn from his way" (Eze 18:21-27; 33:11-19) confirms this: the therapeutic address is volitional ("turn," "forsake" — Isa 55:7). This also explains why the characteristic cannot be overcome by external reform alone — Isa 26:10 demonstrates that even a favourable environment does not produce change in the wicked person without the volitional turn. The characteristic is, at its root, a volitional commitment.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The volitional pattern reveals the most analytically significant distinction between CHAR-2 and CHAR-1. CHAR-1 (wickedness as settled person-identity) is primarily volitional — the will has chosen a direction and settled into it. CHAR-2 (evil as constitutional inner nature) is primarily constitutional — the will operates within a structural constraint that the tree-nature metaphor (Mat 7:17-18 — VCG-02) names precisely: the nature constrains the will's productive range. The will can still choose how to express the constitutional evil (choice of specific evil acts), but it cannot produce good fruit from the constitutional condition without a transformation of the condition itself. The volitional engagement reveals the characteristic as deeper than willful choice — it is the condition that shapes what the will can choose to produce.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The volitional pattern reveals an important distinction from CHAR-1 (wickedness as settled person-identity): in CHAR-1, the volitional-directional dimension is primary. In CHAR-3, volition is the faculty through which the abominable inner conditions are expressed and maintained (Eze 14:6 — the will facing the abominations; Pro 13:19 — the will bonded to evil), but the primary dimension is the relational-moral verdict rather than the volitional direction per se. The volitional engagement shows that abomination is not merely incidental or passive — it requires sustained volitional commitment to the abominable inner conditions. The call to repent (Eze 14:6) shows that volitional reversal is both possible and required.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The volitional pattern reveals that idolatrous abomination is fundamentally a will-phenomenon: it begins with a volitional choice and ends with a bound will. This explains the Deuteronomic preventive strategy (VCG-02): address the will before the attachment forms (don't covet, don't learn, don't worship) because once the attachment is formed, the will is progressively constrained. The Ezekiel restoration trajectory (Eze 14:6 context: "repent and turn away from your abominations") also addresses the will — the therapeutic address is volitional. The volitional pattern confirms the characteristic's primary dimension (T1.8.1) and shows that volitional intervention is the primary address at both the preventive and therapeutic stages.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The volitional pattern reveals that iniquity as scheming is both constituted by the will (it is chosen — Job 36:21 — VCG-04) and eventually dominates the will (Psa 119:133 — VCG-04: seeking dominion). This paradox — the will creates what then masters it — is a defining feature of the characteristic's inner-being mechanism. The trajectory of the will is: free choice of iniquity → progressive constraint of the will by iniquity's hold → potential dominion of iniquity over the will → required divine intervention to re-open the ear and enable return (Job 36:10 — VCG-04). The volitional pattern confirms the characteristic as a will-phenomenon that turns against the will's own freedom.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The volitional pattern reveals the characteristic as the most extreme form of will-hardening in the M10b cluster: VCG-01's blasphemy under divine judgment (Rev 16:9/11/21 — VCG-01) shows a will that persists in defiance through maximum external pressure. The will's refusal to repent is not merely passive (failing to change) but active (generating defiant speech as its expression of continued refusal). This active-volitional defiance under judgment is the characteristic's most analytically distinctive feature: the will is not merely wrong but actively self-asserting against the divine in the moment of judgment. The volitional pattern reveals CHAR-6 as the characteristic of the maximally hardened will.

---

#### T3.7 — Agency

##### T3.7.1 — Does this characteristic engage the agency faculty — the capacity to act, initiate, and make happen — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Yes. Agency is strongly engaged, primarily in the form of directed harmful action. VCG-03 (pride and directed hostility, 22V) is the primary evidence base: the wicked actively pursue the poor in arrogance (Psa 10:2), plot and gnash teeth against the righteous (Psa 37:12), arm themselves with destructive intent (Psa 37:14), lurk as predatory trappers (Jer 5:26), surround the righteous and pervert justice (Hab 1:4). VCG-09 also shows agency in economic harm: the wicked accepts bribes to pervert justice (Pro 17:23), sweeps others away through violence (Pro 21:7), and covets the spoil of evildoers (Pro 12:12). The agency of the wicked person is consistently productive — they act, initiate, and bring harm into being.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Yes. Agency is engaged and fully operational in the constitutionally evil person. The characteristic does not impair the capacity to act — it redirects it. Mat 12:35 (vc=14420 — VCG-03): the evil person "brings forth evil" — active originating agency. 3Jo 10 (vc=14454 — VCG-04): Diotrephes "talking wicked nonsense against us, and not content with that, he refuses to welcome the brothers, and also stops those who want to and puts them out of the church" — multiple layered agency acts (speech, refusal, obstruction, expulsion) all expressing the constitutional inner malice. Act 17:5 (vc=14452 — VCG-04): wicked men "formed a mob, set the city in an uproar, and attacked" — organized active agency in service of constitutional inner disposition.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Yes. Agency is engaged both in the production of abomination and in the called-for response. Deu 25:16 (vc=65936 — VCG-01): "all who act dishonestly" — agency in practice produces abomination. Deu 27:15 (vc=65937 — VCG-04): "makes a carved image" and "sets it up in secret" — active creative-constructive agency producing abomination. Pro 21:27 (vc=1693 — VCG-03): "how much more when he brings it with evil intent" — agency in religious offering compounded by intentional corrupt motivation. Eze 44:6 (vc=66001 — VCG-04): "O house of Israel, enough of all your abominations" — the accumulated acts of the rebellious inner disposition are the corporate agency that has generated the abominable state.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Yes. Agency is fully engaged and oriented toward idolatrous production and installation. VCG-03 (17V — historical reform narratives) documents the most concentrated agency evidence: Solomon "built a high place" (1Ki 11:7 — vc=65899 — VCG-03 — constructive agency); kings "did according to the abominations of the nations" (2Ki 21:2 — vc=65941 — VCG-03 — comprehensive agency conformity); Josiah "took away all the abominations" (2Ch 34:33 — vc=65946 — VCG-03 — reforming agency). Jer 32:34 (vc=65907 — VCG-04): "they set up their abominations in the house" — deliberate placement as an act of bold agency. Eze 7:20 (vc=65909 — VCG-05): "they made their abominable images" — creative-productive agency.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Yes. Agency is extensively evidenced and actively engaged in executing iniquity. Mic 2:1 (vc=38217 — VCG-02): "when the morning dawns, they perform it, because it is in the power of their hand" — agency (the power to make things happen) is the executing faculty. Isa 10:1 (vc=38191 — VCG-02): "those who decree iniquitous decrees, and the writers who keep writing oppression" — institutional agency producing systematic harm. Isa 59:7 (vc=38203 — VCG-02): "swift to shed innocent blood" — agency directed toward violent harm. Job 4:8 (vc=38186 — VCG-04): "those who plow iniquity and sow trouble reap the same" — agricultural agency metaphor: iniquity is sown with active effort, like farming.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Yes. Agency is directly engaged through the speech acts. Rev 13:6 (vc=14356 — VCG-01): "opened its mouth to utter blasphemies" — the utterance is an agentive act. Rev 16:9 (vc=14352 — VCG-01): "cursed the name of God" — cursing as an agentive act. Joh 18:30 (vc=14378 — VCG-03): the accusers "delivered him over" — the false charge is part of an agentive process of handing Jesus over to Pilate. Jude 8 (vc=14354 — VCG-01): "blaspheme the glorious ones" — an agentive targeting of specific beings through speech. The characteristic requires agency for its operation: the speech act must be initiated, formulated, and delivered through deliberate agency.

---

##### T3.7.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair agency in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The characteristic enables and directs agency toward harmful ends. It does not impair the capacity to act — the wicked person is consistently active in the evidence. The enablement is through the removal of the moral check that would otherwise constrain agency: because the wicked person has excluded God from their mind (Psa 10:4) and suppressed conscience (T3.9), they act with a kind of unimpeded boldness. Pro 21:29 (VCG-08): "a wicked man puts on a bold face" — the boldness is the characteristic's agency-enabling effect. Eventually, however, agency is terminated by divine judgment: Job 38:15 ("their uplifted arm is broken"), Isa 14:5 (VCG-03 — "the staff of the wicked broken"), Psa 37:17 ("the arms of the wicked shall be broken"). The characteristic enables harmful agency in the present and ensures its termination in judgment.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The characteristic enables and directs agency toward harmful ends. The constitutionally evil person is consistently active in the evidence — they bring forth evil (Mat 12:35), they set cities in uproar (Act 17:5), they talk wicked nonsense and obstruct (3Jo 10), they form mobs (Act 17:5). Agency is not impaired — it is fully deployed in the service of the constitutional condition. The characteristic provides the motivational source from which agency draws its drive: the treasury of evil (Mat 12:35 — VCG-03) is the inner resource from which action is energised.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The characteristic enables and energises agency toward abominable ends. The dishonest dealer (Deu 25:16 — VCG-01), the idol-maker (Deu 27:15 — VCG-04), and the Babylon of Rev 17:5 (vc=65878 — VCG-05) are all active agents — the characteristic does not impair their capacity to act. Rather, it channels their agency into abominable production. The commanded response (Eze 14:6 — VCG-04: "repent and turn") shows that agency must be redirected — from abomination-generating action toward repentance-action. The characteristic thus actively engages and enables agency in the service of abominable production.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The characteristic energises and enables agency in the service of idolatrous devotion. The evidence consistently shows active, intentional, organised agency: Solomon constructing high places (1Ki 11:7 — VCG-03), the people setting idols in the temple (Jer 32:34 — VCG-04), the crafting of idol-objects from beautiful ornament (Eze 7:20 — VCG-05). The characteristic does not impair agency; it redirects it comprehensively. The reform-agency (Josiah purging — 2Ch 34:33; 2Ki 23:24 — VCG-03; Asa removing — 2Ch 15:8 — VCG-03) shows that decisive volitional agency is required to resist and reverse the characteristic — confirming that agency is the faculty at stake.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The characteristic energises and directs agency toward harm-production. Mic 2:1 (vc=38217 — VCG-02): "when the morning dawns, they perform it, because it is in the power of their hand" — the dawn-execution shows agency fully operational and eagerly deployed in service of the nightly-devised schemes. Isa 59:7 (VCG-02): "swift to shed innocent blood" — swiftness reveals agency heightened and accelerated toward evil. The characteristic does not impair agency; it maximally energises it in the wrong direction. This confirms that iniquity as scheming is not a passive condition but an actively agentive one.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The characteristic enables and energises agency toward defiant speech production. Rev 16:9/11/21 (VCG-01): under escalating judgment, the agency for cursing is maintained and deployed — the characteristic does not reduce the ability to act but directs full agency toward defiant expression. Rev 13:6 (VCG-01): "sustained, deliberate blasphemy" — the sustained quality shows agency operating consistently over time in the service of the characteristic. The characteristic does not impair agency but fully co-opts it for the production of defiant, harmful speech.

---

##### T3.7.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with agency reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The agency pattern reveals that wickedness-as-settled-person-identity is not a passive condition — it is an active posture that generates harm in the social world. The wicked person is not merely morally deficient in their inner being; they produce measurable damage in their communities (Pro 11:11 — cities overthrown), legal systems (Isa 5:23 — justice perverted), and interpersonal relationships (Psa 28:3 — speaking peace while harboring evil). The characteristic's agency-activation pattern explains its social dangerousness and why the corpus addresses it with divine judgment: an active harmful agency that shapes communities requires termination, not merely internal correction.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The agency pattern reveals that evil as constitutional inner nature is not a passive state but an active generative engine that produces ongoing social harm through fully operational agency. The constitutionally evil person is not incapacitated — they are energised by their constitutional condition toward harm. This explains the NT's urgency about the characteristic: a fully agentic person constitutionally oriented toward evil is not merely a passive problem but an active danger to communities (1Cor 5:13 — VCG-04: the community must expel the evil person precisely because their active agency is corrupting the whole). The agency pattern confirms the need for transformation at the constitutional level, not merely behavioural restraint.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The agency pattern reveals that abomination requires active sustained agency for its production. It is not a passive inner state — it is actively generated by the dishonest dealer (Deu 25:16 — VCG-01), the offering-bringer (Pro 15:8 — VCG-03), the idol-maker (Deu 27:15 — VCG-04). The characteristic therefore has a sustained-agency component: the abominable inner condition is continuously enacted through habitual practice, not merely held as a static quality. This accounts for the evidence's emphasis on turning from abominations (Eze 14:6 — VCG-04) — the agency must be actively redirected rather than merely the inner state addressed.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The agency pattern reveals that idolatrous abomination is sustained through organised, persistent, publicly visible agency: high places constructed, idols installed in temples, national practices reformed. The characteristic is not a private inner state but an energetically enacted social phenomenon. This explains why the evidence so consistently frames the response as equally active and public: reform requires removing, destroying, and purging with equal organising energy to what installed the abomination (2Ki 23:24 — VCG-03: comprehensive Josiah reform). The agency pattern confirms that CHAR-4 is a characteristically activist deviation — driven by the same inner-being capacity for agency as the reforms that must oppose it.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The agency pattern reveals that iniquity as active scheming is constitutively agentive: it requires and deploys full agency for its realisation. Job 4:8 (VCG-04): "plow iniquity and sow trouble" — the agricultural labour metaphor shows that iniquity requires sustained effort, like farming. The characteristic is therefore not a passive moral failure but an energetically sustained practice. The agency pattern also reveals why the characteristic is so harmful to others: the full agency of the person (power to make things happen, institutional authority in Isa 10:1 — VCG-02) is directed against the weak and innocent. Addressing the characteristic must therefore involve the redirection of agency, not its elimination.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The agency pattern reveals that evil expressed through speech is an agentive choice at every level: choosing to open the mouth (Rev 13:6 — VCG-01), choosing the content of the speech (cursing God's name — Rev 16:9 — VCG-01), choosing to formulate the false charge (Joh 18:30 — VCG-03). The characteristic is not an involuntary expression but an agentively produced and delivered speech act. This full-agency character makes the characteristic specifically morally culpable — it is not the overflow of emotion beyond the person's control but a deliberate, agentively executed expression of inner wickedness. Rom 3:8 (vc=14358 — VCG-02): "their condemnation is just" — the justness of condemnation presupposes the agentive character of the slanderous speech.

---

#### T3.8 — Moral Evaluation

##### T3.8.1 — Does this characteristic engage the moral evaluation faculty — the capacity to assess against a standard of right, wrong, good, and true — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Yes. The moral evaluation faculty is engaged and inverted. The wicked person retains the capacity for moral assessment but has reversed its polarity: Pro 10:32 (VCG-08): "the mouth of the wicked knows what is perverse" — the wicked person is fluent in perversity, which implies they have the moral evaluation faculty but have calibrated it toward what is twisted rather than toward the right. Pro 12:5 (VCG-08): "the counsels of the wicked are deceitful" — the deliberative moral faculty generates deceptive output. Isa 5:23 (VCG-05): acquitting the guilty and condemning the righteous for a bribe — the judicial moral-evaluation faculty is deliberately inverted for personal gain. The wicked person therefore is not without moral evaluation capacity — they evaluate, but according to an inverted standard.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Yes. The moral evaluation faculty is engaged and systematically inverted. The constitutionally evil person evaluates moral reality through a corrupted lens. Joh 3:19 (vc=14448 — VCG-04): works are evaluated as worth concealing (loved darkness), not as worth exposing — moral evaluation prefers concealment. 1Cor 13:6 (vc=14341 — VCG-06): unrighteousness is something that could "draw inner delight" — moral evaluation is capable of assessing wrongdoing as delightful. Joh 7:7 (vc=14449 — VCG-04): the world hates the truthful witness — moral evaluation has assessed the truth-teller as the threat rather than the evil as the threat. The moral evaluation faculty is inverted: what is truly bad is evaluated as acceptable or pleasurable; what is truly good is evaluated as threatening.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Yes. Moral evaluation is centrally engaged, particularly in its capacity for inversion. Pro 17:15 (vc=1690 — VCG-01) is the definitive evidence: "he who justifies the wicked and he who condemns the righteous are both alike an abomination to the Lord" — the moral evaluation faculty (the capacity to assess and render moral verdicts) has been inverted: what is wrong is justified, what is right is condemned. This is not the absence of moral evaluation but its systematic perversion. Pro 29:27 (vc=65959 — VCG-01): the mutual abomination of the unjust and the righteous shows that their moral evaluation faculties render opposite verdicts on each other — the unjust person evaluates the righteous as abominable, and vice versa.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Yes. The moral evaluation faculty is engaged through its systematic failure in the characteristic. Eze 8:17 (vc=65980 — VCG-05): "is it too light a thing for the house of Judah to commit the abominations that they commit here" — the evaluative faculty has assessed abomination as a light, trivial matter. Deu 18:12 (vc=1685 — VCG-02): "whoever does these things is an abomination to the Lord" — the divine moral evaluation (this is abominable) is the standard against which the human inner evaluation is being measured; the human community evaluates the same practices as acceptable. The moral evaluation faculty is present but its assessments are systematically inverted.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Yes. The moral evaluation faculty is engaged through its systematic failure and co-optation. Psa 14:4 (vc=38229 — VCG-03): "Have they no knowledge, all the evildoers" — the moral evaluation faculty (knowledge of right and wrong) is absent. Pro 30:20 (vc=38222 — VCG-04): "I have done no wrong" — the moral evaluation faculty is present but producing inverted verdicts: the adulteress evaluates her wrong as not-wrong. Isa 59:4 (vc=38192 — VCG-02): "No one enters suit justly; no one goes to law honestly" — the social-institutional moral evaluation mechanisms (courts) have been subverted by iniquity, producing false verdicts.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Yes. The moral evaluation faculty is engaged through systematic inversion. Rom 14:16 (vc=14359 — VCG-02): "do not let what you regard as good be spoken of as evil" — speaking good as evil is the characteristic's moral-evaluation operation: the faculty of moral assessment is employed but producing inverted verdicts (naming good as evil). Rom 3:8 (vc=14358 — VCG-02): false attribution of "do evil that good may come" — a moral-evaluative framework ("good ends") is deployed to misrepresent another's position. Joh 18:30 (vc=14378 — VCG-03): "if this man were not doing evil" — the accusers' moral evaluation of the innocent as evildoers shows the moral-evaluative faculty producing inverted verdicts.

---

##### T3.8.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair moral evaluation in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The characteristic inverts moral evaluation rather than simply impairing it. The inversion is active and sustained: the wicked person's moral compass has not disappeared but has been rotated so that what is perverse is known and chosen (Pro 10:32), what is unjust is rewarded (Isa 5:23), and what is good is despised (Psa 10:3 — "renounces the Lord"). This inversion is itself a form of deep impairment — the faculty is present but systematically misdirected. It also bypasses the corrective function of moral evaluation: the wicked person's moral assessment does not serve as a corrective to their conduct because the assessment itself is corrupted.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The characteristic inverts moral evaluation rather than simply eliminating it. The constitutionally evil person evaluates — they make moral assessments — but the evaluations are systematically wrong because the constitutional condition has skewed the standard. Mat 22:18 (vc=14408 — VCG-05): Jesus perceives their "malice" (ponēria) as a calculated entrapment — they evaluate their entrapment scheme as cunning and justified (self-assessed as moral victory). 1Pe 2:16 (vc=14370 — VCG-05): evil as the corrupt aim that freedom can serve — they evaluate freedom as a legitimate cover for evil. The moral evaluation faculty is present, active, and systematically inverted by the constitutional condition.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The characteristic perverts the moral evaluation faculty rather than eliminating it. Pro 17:15 (vc=1690 — VCG-01): perverted judgment — the evaluative faculty is operative but systematically inverted. Luk 16:15 (vc=21 — VCG-02): "you justify yourselves before men" — the moral evaluation faculty is actively deployed in self-justification rather than honest assessment. Pro 26:25 (vc=1694 — VCG-02): seven abominations hidden beneath gracious speech — the person evaluates their own inner state and constructs a concealing performance, showing they know their inner evaluation is negative (hence the concealment). The moral evaluation faculty is present, operating, but systematically misdirected — assessing others wrong and oneself with self-justifying bias.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The characteristic impairs the moral evaluation faculty by reducing its capacity to assess the gravity of idolatrous acts. Eze 8:17 (vc=65980 — VCG-05): abomination treated as trivial — the evaluative severity-assessment is impaired. The characteristic bypasses the faculty in the sense that the person proceeds with idolatrous acts without the evaluative check that would declare them abominable. This is connected to the cognitive impairment of the gravity-assessment function (T3.2.2). The moral evaluation faculty has not disappeared — the person still evaluates (Deu 13:14 — VCG-02: the community is expected to evaluate carefully when reports of apostasy arise) — but the faculty no longer accurately assesses the idolatrous acts as abominable to God.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The characteristic impairs and inverts the moral evaluation faculty. Psa 14:4 (VCG-03): moral knowledge absent — the faculty is impaired. Pro 30:20 (VCG-04): moral wrong evaluated as not-wrong — the faculty is inverted. Isa 59:4 (VCG-02): courts subverted — the institutional moral evaluation is bypassed by the scheming of those in power. The characteristic does not eliminate the capacity for moral assessment — Pro 30:20 shows the person still evaluating and rendering a verdict; it inverts the verdicts that the faculty produces. This is not cognitive impairment but moral-evaluative inversion.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The characteristic inverts and perverts the moral evaluation faculty. Rom 14:16 (VCG-02): calling good things evil — the faculty is operational but producing inverted outputs. Joh 18:30 (VCG-03): the innocent named as evildoer — systematic moral inversion. Jude 10 (vc=14355 — VCG-01): "blaspheme all that they do not understand" — here the moral evaluation faculty is not just inverted but bypassed: contempt substitutes for moral assessment rather than corrupting it. The moral evaluation faculty is thus engaged differently by VCG: VCG-01 bypasses it (contempt replaces assessment); VCG-02/03 invert it (produce false verdicts naming evil as good or good as evil).

---

##### T3.8.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with moral evaluation reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The inverted moral evaluation reveals that wickedness-as-settled-person-identity does not leave the person without moral knowledge — it corrupts the use of that knowledge. The wicked person "knows what is perverse" (Pro 10:32) — they are morally knowledgeable but in a perverted direction. This is confirmed by the forensic-verdict VCG (M10b-A-VCG-01): the legal framework presupposes that the wicked person is morally accountable — their guilt is assessed against a standard they are presumed to know. The inverted moral evaluation pattern reveals the characteristic as a form of moral corruption rather than moral ignorance: the person knows but has chosen the wrong.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The inverted moral evaluation pattern reveals that the constitutionally evil person is not without moral judgement — they judge constantly — but their constitutional condition has corrupted the standard against which they judge. This makes the characteristic analytically distinct from moral ignorance: the person knows moral categories (they assess, they plan, they evaluate), but the constitutional evil has skewed what they assess as good or acceptable. The inversion is precisely the characteristic's most theologically dangerous aspect — it provides moral rationalisation for evil rather than moral awareness of it.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The moral evaluation pattern reveals that abomination operates within a systematically inverted evaluative framework. The person whose inner character is abominable evaluates moral reality through a lens that justifies what is wrong and condemns what is right (Pro 17:15 — VCG-01). This means the characteristic is self-sustaining: the inverted moral evaluation prevents the person from recognising their own abominable condition. Luk 16:15 (vc=21 — VCG-02) names the divine counter: God's moral evaluation bypasses the inverted human assessment and goes directly to the heart. This reveals the characteristic as specifically resistant to self-diagnosis — the same evaluative inversion that produces abomination also prevents its recognition.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The moral evaluation pattern reveals that the characteristic produces a specific cognitive-evaluative blindspot: the idolatrous acts are accessible to ordinary evaluation (they can be seen, known, and discussed) but are not assessed as abominable. Eze 8:17 (vc=65980 — VCG-05) shows this explicitly — the people know they are committing abominations (the prophet asks "do you see what they are doing?") but evaluate them as a light matter. The evaluative blindspot is not ignorance of the acts but misjudgment of their gravity. This explains why the prophetic naming of abominations (Eze 16:2; 22:2 — VCG-05) is the therapeutic corrective: it re-introduces the correct evaluative assessment that the inner faculty can no longer produce independently.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The moral evaluation pattern reveals that iniquity as scheming specifically corrupts the verdicting function of moral evaluation: the schemer can see what they are doing (the devising and planning presuppose some cognitive awareness of the scheme) but evaluates it as acceptable or even desirable. Pro 30:20 (VCG-04) is the most definitive: the adulteress knows she ate but denies she did wrong — the moral evaluation faculty has been subverted to produce self-exculpating verdicts. This makes the characteristic self-sustaining: the same inner inversion that generates iniquity also prevents its recognition as wrong, eliminating the internal brake.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The moral evaluation pattern reveals two distinct modes of failure within the characteristic. VCG-01 (Jude 10 — VCG-01): bypass — the faculty never engages; contempt operates in the vacuum. VCG-02/03 (Rom 14:16 — VCG-02; Joh 18:30 — VCG-03): inversion — the faculty engages but produces systematically false verdicts. These two modes show the characteristic as capable of corrupting moral evaluation at both the pre-evaluative level (bypass — contempt fills the gap before assessment occurs) and the post-evaluative level (inversion — assessment occurs but produces false results). The combination makes the characteristic particularly damaging in social contexts: it can either simply disregard moral reality or actively misrepresent it.

---

#### T3.9 — Conscience

##### T3.9.1 — Does this characteristic engage the conscience — the acute inner witness of sin, guilt, and conviction — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Yes. Conscience engagement is central to this characteristic. The primary evidence is Psa 36:1 (VCG-02): "transgression speaks to the wicked deep in his heart; there is no fear of God before his eyes" — the inner voice of transgression has displaced the voice of conscience (God-fear). This is the characteristic's definitive conscience-engagement pattern: the conscience has been replaced by an internal governance structure that speaks for wickedness rather than against it. Pro 10:24 (VCG-06): "what the wicked dreads will come upon him" — the inner dread is a conscience-residue that the wicked person cannot fully suppress; the conscience retains enough function to produce dread of the consequences the wicked person knows are coming. Job 34:18 (VCG-10): "who says to a king 'worthless one' and to nobles 'wicked man'" — divine authority applies the conscience-verdict to nobles regardless of social rank.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Yes. The conscience is centrally engaged. Heb 10:22 (vc=14426 — VCG-06) is the primary conscience evidence: "hearts sprinkled clean from an evil conscience" — the conscience is named as the specific faculty that has been constitutionally corrupted ("evil conscience") and that blocks approach to God. Act 8:22 (vc=14361 — VCG-05): "the intent of your heart may be forgiven you" — the heart's intent is addressed by repentance and prayer, implying a conscience-level reckoning with the constitutional evil. Rom 1:18 (vc=14336 — VCG-05): "suppress the truth" — suppression is the conscience's relationship to the truth it knows; the constitutional evil generates the suppressive act that prevents conscience from functioning.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Yes. The conscience is the central and most extensively evidenced faculty in this characteristic — VCG-04 (11 verses) is entirely devoted to the conscience's relationship with abomination. The conscience engages the characteristic across three states: (1) wholly silenced — Jer 6:15 (vc=1680 — VCG-04) and Jer 8:12 (vc=1696 — VCG-04): "not at all ashamed; they did not know how to blush" — complete conscience-silencing with no shame or blushing; (2) awakened and grieving — Eze 9:4 (vc=1698 — VCG-04): those who sigh and groan over others' abominations — a conscience responding with grief; (3) restored to full function — Eze 36:31 (vc=1681 — VCG-04): memory restored producing self-loathing; Eze 44:13 (vc=66003 — VCG-04): bearing shame permanently. The conscience is the defining inner faculty through which abomination is registered, shamed, or ignored.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Yes. The conscience is engaged primarily through its deadening and eventual reactivation. Eze 6:9 (vc=1697 — VCG-05): survivors "will be loathsome in their own sight for the evils they have committed, for all their abominations" — the post-judgment conscience generates self-loathing; this implies that during the period of abomination the conscience was suppressed. Eze 8:17 (vc=65980 — VCG-05): treating abomination as a light matter shows a conscience that no longer registers the gravity of idolatrous acts. Deu 27:15 (vc=65937 — VCG-02 — from CHAR-3's corpus but structurally parallel): the idol set up "in secret" implies a conscience that knows the act is wrong while the will proceeds — conscience still active but overridden.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Yes. The conscience is engaged through progressive deadening. Pro 30:20 (vc=38222 — VCG-04): "I have done no wrong" — the conscience that should register wrongdoing produces nothing; it has been entirely silenced through sustained iniquity. Psa 36:4 (vc=38235 — VCG-02): "he does not reject evil" — the failure to reject evil implies that the conscience no longer produces the rejection-impulse that would arrest the scheming. Psa 66:18 (vc=38182 — VCG-04): "if I had cherished iniquity in my heart, the Lord would not have listened" — the psalmist's awareness that cherished iniquity forecloses divine hearing shows a conscience still functional (warning against this state), while the person who has actually reached that state (Pro 30:20 — VCG-04) has a silenced conscience.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Yes. The conscience is engaged primarily through its foreclosure in VCG-01. Rev 16:9 (vc=14352 — VCG-01): "they did not repent" — the conscience's convicting function that should produce repentance has been entirely suppressed; the characteristic has silenced the conscience-induced impulse toward repentance. Rev 16:11 (vc=14350 — VCG-01): "they did not repent of their deeds" — the deeds-conscience link is specifically severed: consciousness of deeds does not produce conscience-engagement with them. For VCG-03: 1Pe 3:16 (vc=14380 — VCG-03): "having a good conscience, so that when you are slandered, those who revile your good behavior in Christ may be put to shame" — the good conscience of the falsely accused is specifically named as the counter-characteristic; its presence exposes the false accusers' lack of conscience-grounded behavior.

---

##### T3.9.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair conscience in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The characteristic suppresses and displaces conscience. Psa 36:1 is the mechanism: the voice of transgression within the heart displaces the God-fear that is conscience's foundation. Isa 26:10 (VCG-05): "if favor is shown to the wicked, he does not learn righteousness" — the conscience is not activated even by favourable conditions. The conscience is not fully eliminated — Pro 10:24 ("what the wicked dreads") suggests a residual conscience function — but its corrective voice is suppressed by the transgression-voice (Psa 36:1) and its regulatory capacity is disabled. The characteristic's relationship to conscience is therefore one of progressive displacement rather than total elimination.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The characteristic corrupts and disables the conscience. Heb 10:22 (vc=14426 — VCG-06) names the conscience as "evil" — the faculty itself has been constitutionally defiled, not merely silenced. This is stronger than suppression: the conscience is not merely prevented from speaking but is constitutionally corrupted so that it no longer functions as a reliable guide toward God. The suppression of truth (Rom 1:18 — VCG-05) shows the will actively preventing conscience from performing its truth-witnessing function. Together these evidence patterns show the conscience as: (1) constitutionally corrupted in its nature (Heb 10:22) and (2) actively suppressed in its function (Rom 1:18).

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The characteristic impairs and ultimately silences the conscience in the person who commits sustained abomination without arrest. Jer 6:15 (vc=1680 — VCG-04) and Jer 8:12 (vc=1696 — VCG-04) show the terminus of sustained abomination: conscience rendered wholly non-functional regarding shame. Deu 27:15 (vc=65937 — VCG-04): the person sets up the idol "in secret" — their heart knows the act is wrong (the secrecy implies inner moral knowledge) but the conscience's corrective voice is overridden by the will. The trajectory is: conscience initially protests → continued abomination suppresses the protest → conscience eventually silenced. Conversely, divine restoration can reactivate the conscience (Eze 36:31 — VCG-04), showing the silencing is not permanent.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The characteristic progressively deadens the conscience to the horror of idolatrous acts. The trajectory from the initial override (knowing the idol is wrong but proceeding in secret — implied by Deu 27:15 — VCG-02 structural parallel) to the terminus (treating abomination as a light matter — Eze 8:17 — VCG-05) shows progressive conscience-deadening. The Eze 6:9 (VCG-05) restoration of self-loathing among survivors shows that the conscience can be reactivated through divine judgment and memory-restoration — confirming that the deadening is a sustained process rather than a permanent extinction.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The characteristic progressively impairs and silences the conscience. The trajectory from initial awareness (the psalmist knows that cherished iniquity blocks prayer — Psa 66:18 — VCG-04) to the silenced state (Pro 30:20 — VCG-04: "I have done no wrong") shows progressive conscience-deadening. Job 36:10 (vc=38215 — VCG-04): "He opens their ears to instruction and commands that they return from iniquity" — the divine ear-opening implies the conscience-through-instruction had been closed. The characteristic bypasses the conscience's arresting function at advanced stages; at its terminus, the conscience produces no signal against ongoing iniquity.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The characteristic suppresses and bypasses the conscience. Rev 16:9/11/21 (VCG-01): three successive divine judgments fail to activate the conscience toward repentance — the conscience is not merely silent but actively suppressed by the hardened will. Jude 8 (vc=14354 — VCG-01): defiling the flesh + authority-rejection + blasphemy — the triple inner posture shows that conscience has been comprehensively bypassed at every level (sensory, volitional, verbal). For VCG-03 false accusers: Joh 18:30 (VCG-03): the accusers formulate the false charge without apparent conscience-engagement — the absence of conscience-checking enables the false accusation.

---

##### T3.9.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with conscience reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The conscience pattern reveals the most acute inner-being consequence of wickedness-as-settled-person-identity: the person is not without moral self-awareness — they dread what is coming (Pro 10:24) — but the conscience cannot generate repentance because it has been displaced from its governing role by the transgression-voice (Psa 36:1). The residual conscience produces dread without correction. This explains the characteristic's self-perpetuating nature: the wicked person experiences inner consequences (dread, inner torment — Job 15:20) but these do not become corrective because conscience's corrective function has been bypassed by the displacement mechanism. The conscience-pattern reveals the characteristic as a structure that silences the inner moral witness without eliminating it entirely.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The conscience pattern reveals the most theologically consequential effect of evil as constitutional inner nature: the faculty specifically designed to mediate the person's access to God (the conscience that enables approach — Heb 10:22 names its cleansed state as the precondition for drawing near) has been constitutionally corrupted. This reveals the characteristic as having disrupted the primary God-access faculty in the inner person. When the conscience is constitutionally evil, the person cannot draw near to God (Heb 10:22 implies this — the precondition for drawing near is a cleansed evil conscience); the approach-channel is blocked at the constitutional level. This is a deeper impairment than merely blocked access from outside — the corruption is in the access-faculty itself.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The conscience pattern reveals the characteristic's most diagnostically precise inner-being indicator: the presence or absence of shame upon commission of abomination is the direct indicator of the conscience's functional state. Jer 6:15 and 8:12 (VCG-04 — "did not know how to blush") represent the terminus of conscience-silencing. Eze 9:4 (VCG-04 — sighing and groaning) represents conscience at full function. The pattern reveals that CHAR-3 is uniquely linked to the conscience faculty in the programme — more so than any other characteristic in M10b — because the mechanism of abomination's inner arrest is specifically the shame-producing conscience, and the characteristic's most dangerous form is precisely when that conscience has been silenced.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The conscience pattern reveals an important distinction from CHAR-3: in CHAR-3, the primary conscience dynamic is the presence or absence of shame upon commission of abomination; in CHAR-4, the primary conscience dynamic is the progressive deadening of the capacity to register idolatrous acts as repugnant to God, and the eventual reactivation through judgment and memory-restoration (Eze 6:9 — VCG-05). CHAR-4's conscience pattern is characterised by the gradual loss of the faculty of horror at idolatrous acts — what begins as a known-to-be-wrong act proceeding in secret ends as an act regarded as trivial. The conscience reactivation (post-judgment self-loathing — Eze 6:9) is the beginning of the characteristic's reversal.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The conscience pattern reveals a progression parallel to CHAR-3's conscience-silencing but with distinctive features. The distinctive CHAR-5 feature is the conscience's relationship to the self-evaluation of the scheme: Pro 30:20 (VCG-04) — the evaluating "I have done no wrong" — is an active self-assessment by the silenced conscience, not merely a passive absence of shame. The conscience has been co-opted to produce false self-exculpating verdicts rather than merely going silent. This is a more active corruption than simple silence: the conscience is still functioning (producing verdicts) but those verdicts now exculpate the iniquity rather than convicting it.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The conscience pattern reveals that VCG-01 blasphemy under judgment is the most extreme conscience-suppression in the M10b cluster: the conscience is suppressed not merely in normal circumstances but under maximum divine pressure. This makes CHAR-6's VCG-01 the ultimate terminus of conscience-foreclosure: even catastrophic judgment (scorching, pain, hailstones) cannot activate a conscience that has been locked shut by the hardened will. The VCG-03 counter-evidence (good conscience as protection — 1Pe 3:16 — VCG-03) confirms by negation: the characteristic's opposite is good conscience; its presence is the absence of conscience's corrective function.

---

#### T3.10 — Conscientiousness

##### T3.10.1 — Does this characteristic engage conscientiousness — the integrated response of moral awareness, volition, and action — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Conscientiousness — the integrated, responsive combination of moral awareness, choice, and action toward good — is precisely what wickedness-as-settled-person-identity displaces. The characteristic produces its own false conscientiousness: the wicked person is consistently responsive to their own inner orientation (they act on their desires, plans, and hostile intent with full consistency — Psa 37:12-14; Jer 5:26; Pro 12:6) but this responsiveness is oriented toward wickedness rather than toward good. The integrated moral-awareness-volition-action loop is present and functional but pointed in the wrong direction. Pro 21:29 (VCG-08): "a wicked man puts on a bold face" — the boldness is the outer expression of an inner moral-volitional consistency in the service of wickedness.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Yes. Conscientiousness — the integrated response of moral awareness, volition, and action — is present but comprehensively misdirected. Luk 19:22 (vc=14447 — VCG-04): the wicked servant knew (moral awareness) and still refused (volition) — his conscientiousness is operating (he is morally aware, he chooses) but the constitutional evil ensures his integrated response is withholding rather than faithful service. Mat 18:32 (vc=14442 — VCG-06): the servant who received mercy yet refused to extend it — morally aware, volitionally refusing, acting with hardness. The characteristic produces a consistent, integrated inner-being response that is the inversion of genuine conscientiousness.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Conscientiousness — the integrated response of moral awareness, volition, and action — is engaged but systematically inverted. The dishonest dealer (Deu 25:16 — VCG-01) is conscientious in their commercial practice — consistently applying false weights — but their conscientiousness is in the service of dishonesty. Pro 26:25 (vc=1694 — VCG-02): the person with seven abominations in their heart maintains a consistently gracious outward performance — an integrated, sustained moral-social response, but one oriented toward concealment of abomination. Tit 1:16 (vc=27 — VCG-02): the profession-works disconnect shows conscientiousness split: professing God (verbal conscientiousness) while denying him through works (practical non-conscientiousness).

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Conscientiousness is engaged and comprehensively redirected toward idolatrous devotion. VCG-03 (17V — historical reform narratives) shows the characteristic as producing a sustained, organised, intentional pattern: kings consistently "doing according to the abominations of the nations" (2Ki 21:2 — VCG-03; 2Ch 33:2 — VCG-03) — an integrated moral-volitional-action pattern oriented toward idolatrous conformity. The community that "did according to all the abominations of the nations that the Lord drove out before the people of Israel" (1Ki 14:24 — vc=65939 — VCG-03) shows conscientiousness (integrated moral awareness, volition, action) operating fully in the service of idolatrous abomination.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Yes. Conscientiousness — the integrated response of moral awareness, volition, and action — is fully engaged and redirected toward the scheming of iniquity. Mic 2:1 (vc=38217 — VCG-02): nocturnal devising + dawn execution — a fully integrated moral-volitional-action pattern, conscientiously pursued (planning with care, executing on schedule). Isa 10:1 (vc=38191 — VCG-02): "the writers who keep writing oppression" — the sustained professional activity of writing oppression shows conscientiousness (habitual, integrated, sustained action pattern) fully operational in the service of iniquity.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Yes. The characteristic inverts conscientiousness toward defiant speech production. Rev 13:6 (vc=14356 — VCG-01): "sustained, deliberate blasphemy" — the sustained quality shows integrated moral-volitional-action consistency, but in the direction of defiant contempt rather than righteousness. The beast's sustained blasphemy is conscientious in its moral-volitional integration: consistently oriented, deliberately executed, sustained over time. VCG-03 false accusation (Joh 18:30 — VCG-03; 1Pe 2:12 — VCG-03): the deliberate and organised character of the false accusation (delivering Jesus over, community-level charge of believers as evildoers) shows conscientiousness — integrated moral-volitional-action patterns — in the service of hostile speech.

---

##### T3.10.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair conscientiousness in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The characteristic displaces and redirects conscientiousness rather than impairing it. The wicked person's inner moral awareness (inverted — T3.8), volitional orientation, and action are integrated and consistent — but integrated around wickedness rather than around the good. This is a form of conscientiousness-subversion: the faculty-integration that makes a person capable of consistent moral action remains, but its orientation is corrupted. The evidence does not show the wicked person as ethically incoherent or incapable of consistent action; they are consistently wicked — which is, paradoxically, a form of integrated conscientiousness in the wrong direction.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The characteristic perverts conscientiousness by supplying a constitutional evil standard to the integrated moral-volitional-action loop. The loop remains operational (the person has moral awareness, makes choices, takes action) but the input standard is constitutionally corrupted. Luk 11:39 (vc=14407 — VCG-05): the Pharisees' conscientious religious practice (cleaning the outside) is bypassed at the level of the inside — their conscientiousness operates at the surface while the constitutional inner evil remains unaddressed. The characteristic enables a form of false conscientiousness: surface compliance with external standards while the constitutional inner evil continues unaddressed.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The characteristic perverts conscientiousness by supplying an abominable standard for the moral-volitional-action integration loop. The consistently dishonest dealer (Deu 25:16 — VCG-01) and the consistently gracious-speaking hider of abominations (Pro 26:25 — VCG-02) are both integrated and consistent — they have a settled, habitual response pattern. But the integration is in the service of abomination rather than righteousness. The characteristic displaces genuine conscientiousness (integrated toward the good) with a false conscientiousness (integrated toward concealment and dishonesty). The Tit 1:16 (vc=27 — VCG-02) split between profession and works represents a fragmentation of conscientiousness rather than its integration.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The characteristic perverts conscientiousness by supplying an idolatrous devotional standard for the integrated moral-volitional-action loop. The person and community who conscientiously practise idolatrous abomination — consistently, habitually, with deliberate organisation — have not lost their conscientiousness but redirected it. The reform narratives (VCG-03) show that opposing the characteristic requires equally conscientious counteraction: 2Ki 23:24 (vc=65901 — VCG-03): Josiah's comprehensive and systematic reform is the conscientious opposition to the conscientious idolatrous installation.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The characteristic perverts conscientiousness by supplying an iniquitous standard for the integrated moral-volitional-action loop. The nocturnal deviser who consistently plans at night and executes at dawn (Mic 2:1 — VCG-02) is operating with a high degree of conscientiousness — integrated, habitual, consistent — in the service of harm. Job 4:8 (VCG-04): "plow iniquity and sow trouble" — the agricultural labour metaphor shows conscientiousness required (sustained effort, seasonal consistency) in the service of iniquity. The characteristic does not eliminate conscientiousness; it enlists it.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The characteristic perverts conscientiousness by supplying a wrong standard for the integrated moral-volitional-action loop. Rev 13:6 (VCG-01): sustained deliberate blasphemy shows the characteristic as conscientiously executed — the same integration of moral orientation, will, and action that would characterise righteous speech is present, but oriented toward contemptuous defiance. The characteristic does not impair the integrated functionality of conscientiousness; it redirects it toward defiant speech production and hostile false accusation.

---

##### T3.10.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with conscientiousness reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The pattern reveals that the wicked person's inner-being faculties are not in disarray — they are organised, integrated, and operationally consistent. The characteristic has not destroyed the architecture of the person's inner-being integration but has reoriented it. This makes wickedness-as-settled-person-identity a particularly dangerous form of inner corruption: it is not chaotic but ordered, not random but directed, not incapacitated but active. This accounts for the evidence's repeated emphasis on the wicked person's organised, premeditated harm (Psa 37:12 — "plots," Jer 5:26 — "sets a trap," Pro 12:5 — "counsels are deceitful").

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The conscientiousness pattern reveals the NT's characteristic critique of the characteristic: the constitutionally evil person can be superficially conscientious (cleaning the outside — Luk 11:39 — VCG-05) while remaining constitutionally evil within. This reveals the characteristic as capable of generating an appearance of moral seriousness while the generative inner condition remains unchanged. The NT's remedial strategy addresses this by calling for inner constitutional renewal (the implanted word — Jam 1:21 — VCG-05; the cleansed conscience — Heb 10:22 — VCG-06) rather than surface behavioural compliance.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The pattern reveals that the characteristic is compatible with a high degree of behavioural consistency and social performance — the person with seven abominations in their heart (Pro 26:25 — VCG-02) presents as gracious; the dishonest dealer is consistently dishonest (Deu 25:16 — VCG-01). The characteristic does not produce visibly chaotic or obviously disorderly behaviour — it produces consistent, integrated behaviour in the wrong direction. This makes it socially invisible (Luk 16:15 — VCG-02: exalted among men but abomination to God) and diagnostically difficult from the outside. The divine perception that sees through social performance to the heart (Luk 16:15 — VCG-02) is the only evaluative faculty that can penetrate the characteristic's social performance layer.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The conscientiousness pattern reveals that idolatrous abomination is not a disorganised or incidental moral failure — it is a systematic, institutionally embedded, conscientiously practised devotional pattern oriented wrongly. The evidence of VCG-03 (17V of reform narratives) shows that idolatrous abomination has the character of a rival religion: practised with the same consistency, institutional organisation, and social reinforcement as genuine worship. This explains why reform requires such comprehensive effort (2Ki 23:24 — VCG-03: Josiah purges everything from mediums to necromancers to household gods to idols to all abominations) — the conscientious integration of the characteristic into communal life makes its removal a conscientious whole-community project.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The conscientiousness pattern reveals that iniquity as active scheming is a characteristically disciplined, integrated moral failure — not chaotic or impulsive but planned, sustained, and habitually executed. Mic 2:1 (VCG-02): nocturnal planning → punctual dawn execution; Isa 10:1 (VCG-02): sustained writing of oppression. The characteristic is thus more analogous to a rival moral discipline than to a moment of weakness. This explains why the evildoer-type (VCG-03, 24V) is a stable, recognisable class of persons: their conscientiousness in the wrong direction has produced a consistent inner-character orientation. Opposing the characteristic requires equally sustained conscientiousness in the right direction.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The conscientiousness pattern reveals that evil expressed through speech is not impulsive but integrated and sustained. Rev 13:6 (VCG-01): sustained deliberate blasphemy; 1Pe 2:12 (vc=14377 — VCG-03): believers "speak against you as evildoers" — the speaking against believers is a sustained communal practice. The integrated, sustained character of the characteristic makes it a stable inner-character orientation rather than a momentary lapse. This explains why the counter-strategy in VCG-03 (1Pe 2:12; 3:16 — VCG-03) is equally sustained and integrated: "keep your conduct among the Gentiles honorable" — the good conscience and honourable conduct must match the sustained character of the hostile accusation.

---

#### T3.11 — Relational Capacity

##### T3.11.1 — Does this characteristic engage the relational capacity — the constitutional equipment for genuine connection with another person — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Yes. Relational capacity is severely engaged and distorted. The characteristic manifests primarily as relational predation and deception: Psa 28:3 (VCG-08) — "speak peace with their neighbors while evil is in their hearts" — the relational surface is deceptive; Psa 37:12 — "gnashes his teeth at him" — relational hostility is the authentic posture beneath the surface; Pro 12:6 — "the words of the wicked lie in wait for blood" — speech as a relational weapon. The relational distortion extends to the divine-human relationship: Psa 15:29 — "the Lord is far from the wicked" — the vertical relational capacity is foreclosed; Pro 15:8 (VCG-09) — the wicked person's religious approach (sacrifice) is repugnant to God — the relational approach mechanism is corrupted. The community-wide relational consequence is documented at Pro 11:11 (city overthrown by wicked speech) and Hab 1:4 (justice perverted).

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Yes. Relational capacity is damaged and redirected by the characteristic. 3Jo 10 (vc=14454 — VCG-04) is the most concentrated evidence: Diotrephes's domineering malice involves refusal to welcome, obstruction of others, and expulsion from the church — the characteristic has converted the relational faculty into an instrument of control and harm. 2Jo 11 (vc=14453 — VCG-04): association with the wicked person communicates their wickedness — the relational capacity becomes a vector for the characteristic's spread. Eph 4:31 (vc=14365 — VCG-05): the cluster of relational vices (bitterness, wrath, anger, clamor, slander, malice) all emerging from the constitutional kakia — the relational sphere is the primary location where the characteristic's damage is expressed. 2Th 3:2 (vc=14450 — VCG-06): faithlessness grounds depravity — the relational-covenantal dimension (faith) is the ground the characteristic has corrupted.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Yes. Relational capacity is extensively engaged. Pro 3:32 (vc=1686 — VCG-02): the devious person is excluded from divine confidence — the relational capacity for intimacy with God is foreclosed by the abominable inner character. Pro 29:27 (vc=65959 — VCG-01): "an unjust man is an abomination to the righteous" — the relational incompatibility between the abominable and the upright operates at the human-horizontal level; they are mutually repulsive. Mal 2:11 (vc=66004 — VCG-04): faithless mixed devotion — covenant betrayal as abomination — shows the covenantal relational bond shattered by abominable inner choice. Eze 44:13 (vc=66003 — VCG-04): those who committed abominations are barred from sacred service — their relational access to the holy is permanently curtailed.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Yes. Relational capacity is perverted and damaged. Deu 32:16 (vc=65938 — VCG-02): "they stirred him to jealousy with strange gods; with abominations they provoked him to anger" — the covenant relationship with God is the primary relational domain damaged. Eze 5:11 (vc=65969 — VCG-05): "I will withdraw" — the divine-human relational capacity is severed by idolatrous abomination. Mal 2:11 parallel structure (from CHAR-3 corpus but applicable): faithless devotion as a covenant-betrayal. Eze 6:9 (vc=1697 — VCG-05): "their whoring heart that has departed from me" — the relational language of marriage-covenant is used: idolatrous abomination is experienced as relational infidelity, a whoring away from God.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Yes. The relational capacity is comprehensively damaged and weaponised. Psa 28:3 (vc=38232 — VCG-03): "workers of evil, who speak peace with their neighbors while evil is in their hearts" — the relational capacity for authentic connection is replaced by deceptive surface-relational performance; the neighbor relationship is instrumentalised as cover for inner evil. Psa 14:4 (vc=38229 — VCG-03): "evildoers who eat up my people" — the relational capacity for care is inverted into predatory consumption. Psa 55:3 (vc=38188 — VCG-01): enemies "drop trouble upon me, and in anger they bear a grudge" — sustained grudge as the relational posture of sustained iniquity against others.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Yes. The relational capacity is comprehensively damaged or weaponised. For the God-human relationship (VCG-01): Rev 16:9/11/21 (VCG-01) — the divine-human relationship is the direct target of the cursing; the characteristic severs the person from any genuine movement toward God by converting encounter with God (even judgment) into an occasion for increased relational hostility. For the human-human relationship (VCG-02/03): 1Cor 4:13 (vc=14351 — VCG-02): slander reduces the slandered to "the scum of the world, the refuse of all things" — the relational capacity for honest mutual regard is destroyed through defamation; 1Pe 2:12 (vc=14377 — VCG-03): false accusation as evildoers — the relational capacity for accurate communal recognition of the person is perverted into false hostile identification.

---

##### T3.11.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair relational capacity in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The characteristic impairs and weaponises relational capacity simultaneously. Genuine relational connection requires transparency and goodwill; the characteristic corrupts both. The wicked person speaks peace while harbouring evil (Psa 28:3 — relational transparency impaired), uses words as weapons (Pro 12:6 — relational capacity weaponised), and is structurally unable to approach God in genuine worship (Pro 15:8; Pro 15:29 — vertical relational capacity foreclosed). The social-relational harm documented throughout VCGs 03, 08, and 09 shows the characteristic's comprehensive relational destructiveness.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The characteristic impairs genuine relational capacity while enabling relational harm. The constitutionally evil person can form relationships (2Jo 11 — association; 3Jo 10 — community involvement), but the constitutional condition ensures those relationships are vehicles for harm rather than genuine connection. Luk 11:39 (vc=14407 — VCG-05) shows the Pharisees engaged in social-religious community while "full of greed and wickedness within" — relational participation without relational integrity. The characteristic hollows out relational capacity at the constitutional level: the form of relationship is maintained while its interior quality is corrupted.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The characteristic impairs relational capacity at both the vertical (God-human) and horizontal (human-human) levels. Vertically: Pro 3:32 (vc=1686 — VCG-02) — exclusion from divine confidence; Eze 44:13 (vc=66003 — VCG-04) — barred from sacred service; Pro 15:8 (vc=1678 — VCG-03) — sacrifice rendered unacceptable. Horizontally: Pro 29:27 (vc=65959 — VCG-01) — mutual abomination between unjust and righteous creates relational incompatibility. The characteristic does not impair instrumental relational capacity (the abominable person can still relate socially — Pro 26:25 shows gracious speech) but impairs the genuine relational capacity for authentic covenant connection — with God and with the morally upright.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The characteristic impairs the covenant-relational capacity with God while enabling a false relational attachment to idol-objects. Eze 5:11 (vc=65969 — VCG-05): divine withdrawal — the relational access to God is foreclosed. Eze 6:9 (vc=1697 — VCG-05): the whoring heart has departed from God — the relational departure is the characteristic's defining relational event. Simultaneously, the characteristic enables attachment to idol-objects as pseudo-relational objects (the heart going after them — Eze 11:21 — VCG-05), filling the relational vacuum left by departure from God with idolatrous attachment.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The characteristic impairs the relational capacity for authentic connection while enabling a false relational performance (Psa 28:3 — VCG-03: speech of peace covering inner evil). Genuine relational capacity requires consistency between inner and outer — the characteristic produces a radical inner-outer split that makes authentic relating impossible. The predatory relational mode (Psa 14:4 — VCG-03: eating up the people; Psa 141:9 — VCG-03: laying traps and snares) inverts the relational capacity into a harm-delivery system. The characteristic does not eliminate relational engagement but corrupts it into instrumentalised deception and predation.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The characteristic impairs genuine relational capacity while weaponising the relational-communicative capacity for harmful purposes. The divine-human relational capacity is specifically and comprehensively severed by the characteristic (VCG-01): Rev 16:9 (VCG-01) — people perceive God's power but curse rather than draw near; the blasphemy creates relational hostility where approach should occur. The human-human relational capacity (VCG-02/03) is weaponised: the communicative ability that enables genuine relational connection (speech) is deployed for defamation (1Cor 4:13 — VCG-02) and false accusation (1Pe 2:12 — VCG-03). The relational capacity is impaired for genuine connection and redirected toward hostile relational aggression.

---

##### T3.11.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with relational capacity reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The relational pattern reveals that wickedness-as-settled-person-identity corrupts the person's relational capacity at both the vertical (God-ward) and horizontal (other-person-ward) levels simultaneously. The God-ward relational foreclosure (Psa 15:29; Pro 15:8; Mal 3:18 — non-service) and the person-ward relational predation (Psa 37:12-14; Jer 5:26; Pro 11:11) are structurally connected: the exclusion of God from the inner mind (VCG-02) is the root from which the corruption of all other relational capacity flows. The person who does not relate rightly to God cannot relate rightly to others — the two relational directions fail together. This is a significant structural finding about the characteristic's relational architecture.

---

## T4 — Relational Interfaces (24 prompts)

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The relational pattern reveals that the characteristic's most visible damage is in the relational sphere — this is where constitutional evil becomes social harm. The NT evidence (VCGs 04, 05, 06) is heavily concentrated in communal, ecclesial, and relational contexts: expulsion from church (3Jo 10), community complicity (2Jo 11), relational vices requiring communal address (Eph 4:31 — VCG-05), and the command to purge the evil person from the community (1Cor 5:13 — VCG-04). The relational pattern confirms that constitutional inner evil is not merely a personal spiritual condition — it is a social force that requires communal response and containment.

## T4 — Relational Interfaces (24 prompts)

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The relational pattern reveals that abomination operates specifically as a category of relational incompatibility — it names the state where two parties cannot be in genuine relational intimacy because one's inner moral character is fundamentally offensive to the other's. Pro 3:32 (vc=1686 — VCG-02): devious person vs. divine confidence. Pro 29:27 (vc=65959 — VCG-01): unjust vs. righteous. Rev 21:27 (vc=22 — VCG-05): abominable vs. the holy city. This relational pattern confirms the primary dimension identified in T1.8.1 — the characteristic is constitutively relational, defined by incompatibility and revulsion rather than merely by an inner quality assessed in isolation. The relational incompatibility is its essence.

The relational pattern reveals CHAR-4 as a specifically covenantal-relational failure — not merely an ethical violation but a betrayal of the primary relationship for which the devotion-capacity was designed.

## T4 — Relational Interfaces (24 prompts)

The relational pattern reveals that iniquity as active scheming is constitutively relational in its harm-direction: it specifically targets and exploits other persons through deception (Psa 28:3 — VCG-03: speaking peace), predation (Psa 14:4 — VCG-03: eating up the people), entrapment (Psa 141:9 — VCG-03: laying snares), and institutional oppression (Isa 10:1 — VCG-02: iniquitous decrees against the weak). The relational pattern shows the characteristic as not content with private inner corruption but as actively directed outward against others through the full range of social-relational mechanisms. This relational harm-direction is what generates VCG-01 (the trouble/distress/affliction suffered by victims): the inner scheming's relational expression is the trouble that falls on others.
