## T4 — Relational Interfaces (24 prompts)

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The relational pattern reveals that the characteristic is constitutively relational in its harm-direction: blasphemy is directed at God (VCG-01), defamation is directed at persons (VCG-02), and false accusation targets specific individuals or communities (VCG-03). The characteristic cannot exist without a target — it is constitutively a relational act of hostile speech directed at another. 1Pe 2:12 (vc=14377 — VCG-03): "when they speak against you as evildoers, they may see your good deeds and glorify God on the day of visitation" — the irony of the relational dynamic is that the false accusation intended to harm ultimately creates the occasion for the accusers to witness the truth and glorify God. The relational pattern reveals the characteristic as a comprehensively hostile-relational speech act.

---

T3 self-evaluation:
  1. Prompt count:        33/33 ✓
  2. Scope marker:        33× [CHAR-6] ✓
  3. Citation discipline: S findings (T3.3.1–T3.3.3) correctly note memory silence; all E findings cite specific verses/VCGs ✓
  4. No cross-tier refs:  ✓
  5. Distinct openings:   ✓
  6. Verse-corpus check:  ✓ (all citations confirmed in §3)
  → PASS. Proceeding to Tier T4.


## T4 — Relational Interfaces (24 prompts)

---

### T4

#### T4.1 — Divine Interface — God to Human

##### T4.1.1 — Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating from God toward the human person — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The evidence does not show wickedness operating from God toward the human person — God is incapable of wickedness (Job 34:10 — VCG-11). What operates from God toward the wicked person is the divine response to their wickedness: judgment, wrath, loathing, and the call to repentance. These divine responses shape the characteristic's relational frame significantly: God's soul hates the wicked (Psa 11:5 — VCG-04), God will not acquit the wicked (Exo 23:7 — VCG-01), God condemns the guilty by bringing their conduct back on their heads (1Ki 8:32; 2Ch 6:23 — VCG-01), and God desires the wicked to turn and live (Eze 18:23; 33:11 — VCG-07). The divine-to-human direction is characterised by judicial response (condemnation), moral loathing (Psa 11:5), relational distance (Pro 15:29 — "the Lord is far from the wicked"), and paradoxically by genuine desire for the wicked person's repentance and life (Eze 18:23; 33:11).

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The evidence does not show evil as constitutional inner nature operating from God toward humans — God is explicitly denied this characteristic (Rom 9:14 — VCG-06). What operates from God toward the constitutionally evil person is the divine response: (1) wrath — Rom 1:18 (vc=14336 — VCG-05): "the wrath of God is revealed against all ungodliness and unrighteousness"; (2) judgment — Mat 13:49 (vc=14459 — VCG-04): at the end of the age angels separate the evil from the righteous; (3) grace for transformation — Act 3:26 (vc=14410 — VCG-05): God's blessing turns people from their wickedness; Heb 10:22 (vc=14426 — VCG-06): the cleansed evil conscience through the sprinkled blood. God operates toward the constitutionally evil in judgment and redemptive transformation, not by extending the characteristic itself.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Yes. The divine-to-human direction is the constitutive direction of this characteristic: God's revulsion response is what defines something as an abomination. The characteristic operates from God toward the human person primarily as a verdict of relational rejection. Pro 3:32 (vc=1686 — VCG-02): the devious person is excluded from God's confidence — God's response moves from his moral character toward the human inner condition, rendering a verdict of exclusion. Pro 6:16 (vc=65952 — VCG-05): "there are six things that the Lord hates, seven that are an abomination to him" — God is the active subject whose hatred and revulsion constitute the category. Luk 16:15 (vc=21 — VCG-02): "God knows your hearts" — God's knowing penetrates the human inner life and issues the abomination verdict on what he finds there. The characteristic therefore operates from God toward the human person as a moral verdict, a relational exclusion, and a persistent divine response.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

God does not extend idolatrous abomination toward humans — he is the party offended by it. What operates from God toward the person in the context of this characteristic is the divine response: (1) jealousy — Deu 32:16 (vc=65938 — VCG-02): "stirred him to jealousy"; (2) hatred/anger — Jer 44:4 (vc=65966 — VCG-04): "this abomination that I hate"; Deu 12:31 (vc=1683 — VCG-02): "every abominable thing that the Lord hates"; (3) withdrawal — Eze 5:11 (vc=65969 — VCG-05): "I will withdraw"; (4) unprecedented judgment — Eze 5:9 (vc=65968 — VCG-05): "I will do with you what I have never yet done"; (5) desolation — Eze 33:29 (vc=65999 — VCG-05): "the land a desolation and a waste because of all their abominations." The characteristic's divine-to-human operation is therefore entirely a response: divine judgment, withdrawal, and desolation as consequences of the characteristic's human expression.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

God does not extend iniquity toward the human person — he is the moral authority who perceives and judges it. What operates from God toward the person in the context of this characteristic is: (1) active hatred — Psa 5:5 (vc=38237 — VCG-03): "you hate all evildoers" — God's settled moral hatred directed at those who work iniquity; (2) retributive return — Psa 94:23 (vc=38249 — VCG-03): "He will bring back on them their iniquity and wipe them out" — God returns the accumulated iniquity upon the schemer; (3) responsive judgment — Deu 28:20 (vc=38439 — VCG-05): "curses, confusion, and frustration… because of the evil of your deeds" — God's response to evil deeds; (4) instruction-through-opening — Job 36:10 (vc=38215 — VCG-04): "He opens their ears to instruction and commands that they return from iniquity" — the divine initiative in creating the possibility of departure.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

God does not extend evil speech toward the human person — he is its target (VCG-01) or the one whose name is dishonoured by others' speech and conduct (VCG-02). What operates from God toward the person in the context of this characteristic is the divine response: the plagues and judgments that the Rev 16 corpus (VCG-01) shows humans blaspheming rather than receiving correctly. Rev 16:9 (vc=14352 — VCG-01): "God who had power over these plagues" — the divine power directed toward the human person through judgment is the context within which the blasphemy occurs. Additionally, 1Pe 2:12 (vc=14377 — VCG-03): "glorify God on the day of visitation" — the day of visitation is the divine movement toward humanity that eventually exposes the false accusation. God's movement toward the person is through judgment and visitation, not through evil speech.

---

##### T4.1.2 — What does the evidence reveal about the basis on which God extends this characteristic — is it conditional, unconditional, covenantal, or responsive?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

God's response to wickedness is both principled-consistent and conditionally responsive. The principled-consistent dimension: God will not acquit the wicked (Exo 23:7 — VCG-01) — this is an absolute moral stance independent of circumstances. God's soul hates the wicked (Psa 11:5) — an ongoing disposition. God does not preserve the wicked alive (Job 36:6 — VCG-05) — a consistent structural consequence. The conditionally responsive dimension: Eze 18:23 and 33:11 (VCG-07) reveal that God's desire for the wicked is that they turn and live — his judgment is averted if the wicked person turns (Eze 18:21-22; 33:14-16). The basis is therefore moral-principled (consistent opposition to wickedness) combined with relational-responsive (real desire for the wicked person's return through repentance).

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

God's response to constitutional inner evil is responsive and principled. The wrath (Rom 1:18 — VCG-05) is responsive to the constitutional unrighteousness — the suppression of truth draws the divine response. The grace-for-transformation (Act 3:26 — VCG-05: "God, having raised up his servant, sent him to you first, to bless you by turning every one of you from your wickedness") is covenantal-mission: the divine initiative to address the constitutional evil is grounded in the Abrahamic-covenant mission ("to you first"). Heb 10:22 (VCG-06): the cleanising of the evil conscience is covenantal — grounded in the new covenant mercy that "remembers sins no more" (Heb 8:12 — VCG-06). The basis is both principled-responsive (wrath to unrighteousness) and covenantal-gracious (mission and mercy to the constitutionally evil).

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

God's revulsion-verdict is responsive and principled. It is responsive to specific inner moral conditions: Pro 11:20 (vc=1677 — VCG-01): crooked heart triggers the verdict; Pro 16:5 (vc=1689 — VCG-02): arrogant heart triggers the verdict. The verdict is not unconditional (it is tied to specific inner conditions) but it is also not arbitrarily conditional — it is principled: every abominable inner condition named in the corpus triggers the same divine response of revulsion. The covenantal dimension appears in Mal 2:11 (vc=66004 — VCG-04): faithless covenant-betrayal as abomination — the covenantal relationship defines the space within which certain acts are specifically abominable. The verdict is thus: principled-responsive (God's holiness responds consistently to specific inner moral conditions) with a heightened covenantal register where covenant defines what specifically is a betrayal that constitutes abomination.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

God's response to idolatrous abomination is covenantally responsive: responsive to specific acts of idolatrous betrayal within a covenantal relationship that defines what constitutes betrayal. Deu 32:16 (vc=65938 — VCG-02): "stirred him to jealousy" — jealousy is a covenantal response (the covenant defines the exclusivity within which jealousy is appropriate). Eze 5:11 (vc=65969 — VCG-05): "because you have defiled my sanctuary… I will withdraw" — the divine response is explicitly conditioned on the prior idolatrous act. Jer 44:22 (vc=65967 — VCG-04): "the Lord could no longer bear your evil deeds and the abominations that you committed" — a threshold was crossed; the divine response is proportional and escalating. The basis is covenantal-responsive: the covenant defines the relationship within which idolatrous abomination is a specific form of betrayal requiring response.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

God's response to iniquity as active scheming is responsive and principled: responsive to the specific inner conduct of scheming and harm-generation, and principled in that the response is consistent with the moral order. Deu 28:20 (vc=38439 — VCG-05): "because of the evil of your deeds, because you have forsaken me" — the basis is explicitly the evil deeds and the forsaking of covenant relationship. Psa 94:23 (VCG-03): "bring back on them their iniquity" — the response is proportional: the iniquity returns as the measure of judgment. Job 21:19 (vc=38209 — VCG-04): "God stores up their iniquity for their children" — the deferred-but-certain response shows the principled nature: the divine response is certain even if delayed. The basis is covenantal-responsive: the covenant defines the relationship within which iniquity is a betrayal, and the response is to that betrayal.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

God's judgment in the Rev 16 context (VCG-01) is responsive and proportional: the plagues are responses to accumulated sin and defiance. Rev 16:9 (vc=14352 — VCG-01): "they cursed the name of God who had power over these plagues" — the judgment precedes the blasphemy (the scorching provokes the cursing), showing that the divine judgment is responsive to prior condition and that the blasphemous response to it is an escalation. The basis is covenantal-responsive: God responds to the defiance of his created order and the rejection of his authority (Jude 8 — VCG-01) with escalating judgment that discloses the depth of the hardened will. 1Pe 2:12 (vc=14377 — VCG-03): the day of visitation — God's evaluation of conduct — is consistent and principled.

---

##### T4.1.3 — What does God's extension of this characteristic reveal about his disposition toward the human person?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

God's response to the wicked person reveals the conjunction of two dispositions: his moral loathing of wickedness and his genuine desire for the wicked person's turning. Eze 33:11 (VCG-07) is the most theologically concentrated statement: "I have no pleasure in the death of the wicked, but that the wicked turn from his way and live" — God's disposition is anti-wickedness and pro-life-for-the-wicked simultaneously. His soul hates the wicked as a type (Psa 11:5) but desires the wicked person as an individual to turn (Eze 18:23). This reveals that God's disposition toward the wicked human is not indifferent — it is actively engaged: with loathing of what they have become and with desire for what they might become through turning.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

God's response reveals a dual disposition: moral seriousness about the constitutional evil combined with transformative intent for the person. Wrath is revealed against the unrighteousness (Rom 1:18 — VCG-05) — this reveals God's non-neutrality about the constitutional condition. But Act 3:26 (vc=14410 — VCG-05) reveals a mission of transformation: God's servant is sent "to bless you by turning every one of you from your wickedness" — the blessing-intent is toward the person even while the condemnation is toward the condition. Heb 10:22 (VCG-06) reveals God's provision of a cleansed conscience for the constitutionally evil person through the new covenant — the divine disposition is toward making the impossible approach to God (blocked by the evil conscience) possible again.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

God's revulsion-verdict reveals his moral character as both actively rejecting and genuinely caring. The active rejection: Pro 11:20 (vc=1677 — VCG-01): "those of crooked heart are an abomination to the Lord" — God's holiness does not merely tolerate but actively responds with revulsion to the abominable inner condition. The genuine care: Eze 14:6 (vc=65984 — VCG-04): "repent and turn away from your idols, and turn away your faces from all your abominations" — God issues the command to turn, showing that the revulsion verdict does not mean abandonment; the call to repentance shows God's desire for the human person to depart from the abominable condition. Eze 36:31 (vc=1681 — VCG-04): the divine action of restoring memory that produces self-loathing is a gracious act enabling conscience-reawakening. God's disposition is thus one of active moral revulsion toward the abominable condition combined with active desire for the person to be transformed.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

God's response reveals a disposition of covenantal faithfulness that makes idolatrous betrayal genuinely painful and provocative. Deu 32:16 (vc=65938 — VCG-02): jealousy — this is the emotion of a covenant partner who experiences betrayal; it reveals that God's disposition toward the human person is one of genuine covenantal attachment that is hurt by infidelity. Eze 6:9 (vc=1697 — VCG-05): "I have been broken over their whoring heart that has departed from me" — the divine heart is "broken" — a personal, relational response to betrayal. Despite this, God's desire is for restoration: Eze 37:23 (vc=65913 — VCG-05): "I will save them from all the backslidings in which they have sinned, and will cleanse them; and they shall be my people, and I will be their God" — the restorative desire is present even through the judgment responses.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

God's response reveals a disposition that takes iniquity seriously as a moral-relational violation while maintaining the possibility of return. Psa 5:5 (VCG-03): active hatred of evildoers — God's holiness creates a disposition of settled moral revulsion toward those constituted by iniquity. Job 36:10 (vc=38215 — VCG-04): "He opens their ears to instruction" — the divine initiative in enabling return reveals that the hatred-posture does not preclude redemptive desire; God acts to create the possibility of departure from iniquity. Isa 55:7 (vc=38200 — VCG-02): "he will abundantly pardon" — the promise of abundant pardon for those who forsake iniquitous thoughts reveals God's disposition as willing to restore, even after prolonged iniquity-scheming, upon genuine return.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

God's disposition revealed through the characteristic is morally serious and relentlessly pursuing. The Rev 16 sequence (vc=14352; 14350; 14353 — VCG-01): God sends three successive judgments even as blasphemy follows each one — this reveals that God does not abandon the pursuit of response even in the face of sustained defiance. The persistent judgment is not indifference but a morally serious engagement with the hardened human will. 1Pe 2:12 (vc=14377 — VCG-03): the day of visitation reveals God as one who evaluates and will ultimately vindicate the falsely accused — his disposition toward the unjustly slandered is one of eventual public vindication. Rom 2:24 (vc=14357 — VCG-02): his name's dishonour among the Gentiles moves him — God cares about the testimony of his name through his people's conduct.

---

##### T4.1.4 — If the evidence is silent on God-to-human operation, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The evidence is not silent; God-to-human relational operation is richly evidenced (T4.1.1–T4.1.3). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The evidence is not silent; God-to-human relational operation is addressed in T4.1.1–T4.1.3. This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The evidence is not silent; God-to-human operation is the constitutive direction of this characteristic (T4.1.1–T4.1.3). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The evidence is not silent; God-to-human operation (as divine response) is extensively evidenced (T4.1.1–T4.1.3). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The evidence is not silent; God-to-human operation (as judgment, hatred, instruction, and pardon) is evidenced (T4.1.1–T4.1.3). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

God-to-human operation (as judgment, visitation, and eventual vindication) is evidenced (T4.1.1–T4.1.3). This prompt is satisfied.

---

#### T4.2 — Divine Interface — Human to God

##### T4.2.1 — Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating in the human person's movement toward God — in seeking, supplication, worship, or covenant — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Yes, but in a negative register: wickedness-as-settled-person-identity is specifically the state in which the human person's movement is away from God rather than toward him. Psa 9:17 (VCG-02): "the wicked… all the nations that forget God" — the characteristic's defining relational posture toward God is forgetting (absence of movement toward). Mal 3:18 (VCG-02): "one who does not serve him" — non-service as the defining relational stance. Psa 10:13 (VCG-02): "renounce God and say in his heart 'You will not call to account'" — active inner renunciation rather than movement toward. Pro 15:8 (VCG-09): "the sacrifice of the wicked is an abomination" — even the wicked person's nominal religious approach is corrupted by the inner state; the movement toward God is structurally disabled. The one redemptive signal is Eze 18:21-27 and 33:11-19 (VCG-07): the wicked person can turn toward God — the movement is possible but requires a volitional reversal of the characteristic itself.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Yes, in a negative register: the characteristic specifically blocks the human person's movement toward God. Heb 10:22 (vc=14426 — VCG-06) is the most direct statement: the evil conscience makes approach to God impossible — "draw near with a true heart in full assurance of faith, with our hearts sprinkled clean from an evil conscience" implies that the unsprinkled evil conscience prevents drawing near. Heb 3:12 (vc=14423 — VCG-06): the evil, unbelieving heart leads to "falling away from the living God" — movement is away from God rather than toward him. The one verse showing movement toward God in the context of this characteristic is Act 3:26 (vc=14410 — VCG-05): "turning every one of you from your wickedness" — the turn from the constitutional evil is the precondition for movement toward God.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Yes, in a negative register: the characteristic specifically describes what blocks or corrupts the human person's movement toward God. The worship evidence (VCG-03) is definitional: Pro 15:8 (vc=1678 — VCG-03): the wicked person's sacrifice — a movement toward God — is rendered an abomination by the abominable inner character of the one moving; Pro 28:9 (vc=65958 — VCG-03): turning the ear from the law renders even prayer an abomination. Pro 21:27 (vc=1693 — VCG-03): the sacrifice is abominable, and evil intent deepens the offense. Isa 1:13 (vc=1695 — VCG-03): "incense is an abomination to me. New moon and Sabbath…I cannot endure iniquity and solemn assembly." The human-to-God movement is structurally blocked at every point by the abominable inner condition: approach to God through prayer, sacrifice, or religious assembly is rendered repugnant when the inner person is abominable.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Yes, but exclusively in a negative register: idolatrous abomination specifically perverts and blocks the human person's movement toward God. Deu 17:1 (vc=1684 — VCG-02): offering a flawed animal is an abomination — the act of worship is corrupted by the inner failure to value God's worth rightly. Jer 7:10 (vc=65963 — VCG-04): "come and stand before me in this house… only to go on doing all these abominations?" — the human movement toward God (standing before him) is decoupled from inner transformation; outward religious presence is combined with continued inner idolatrous practice. This reveals that the characteristic produces a dissociated religious life: outward approach to God combined with inner idolatrous attachment — a form of double-allegiance worship that is itself abominable.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Yes, exclusively in the negative register: iniquity as active scheming specifically blocks the human person's movement toward God. Psa 66:18 (vc=38182 — VCG-04): "If I had cherished iniquity in my heart, the Lord would not have listened" — the iniquity-schemer's prayer channel is closed; the cherished iniquity breaks the prayer-relationship. Isa 1:13 (vc=38197 — VCG-04): "incense is an abomination to me. I cannot endure iniquity and solemn assembly" — religious worship performed while harbouring iniquity is intolerable to God; the characteristic corrupts the religious approach. Psa 14:4 (vc=38229 — VCG-03): evildoers "do not call upon the Lord" — the characteristic specifically excludes the act of calling on God; Psa 53:4 (VCG-03): same.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Yes, but entirely in the negative register: the characteristic is the inversion of movement toward God. Rev 16:9 (vc=14352 — VCG-01): "they did not repent and give him glory" — the withheld repentance and glory name exactly what genuine movement toward God would look like; the characteristic is the refusal of that movement even when under judgment. The characteristic thus defines the anti-movement-toward-God: instead of repentance, cursing; instead of glory-giving, name-cursing. Jude 8 (vc=14354 — VCG-01): "reject authority and blaspheme the glorious ones" — authority-rejection as the inner posture precludes the submission that genuine movement toward God requires.

---

##### T4.2.2 — What does the evidence reveal about the inner posture required for this movement?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The inner posture required for the wicked person to move toward God is the reversal of the characteristic's defining elements: the will must "turn from his way" (Eze 3:18; 33:11), the thoughts must be forsaken (Isa 55:7 — VCG-07 — "let the unrighteous man forsake his thoughts"), and the way must be abandoned ("let the wicked forsake his way"). The evidence shows that the required posture is one of active renunciation of the wicked orientation — not passive drift but deliberate departure from the settled inner direction. The one passage where the inner posture of movement toward God is evidenced in the wicked person is Jer 14:20 (re.sha — VCG-11): "we acknowledge our wickedness… for we have sinned against you" — a communal conscience-acknowledgment that opens the path toward God.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The posture required for the constitutionally evil person to move toward God is one of repentance and reception. Act 8:22 (vc=14361 — VCG-05): "Repent, therefore, of this wickedness of yours, and pray to the Lord that, if possible, the intent of your heart may be forgiven you" — the required posture is repentance (turning from the constitutional evil) combined with supplication (prayer for forgiveness of the heart's intent). Jam 1:21 (vc=14368 — VCG-05): "put away all filthiness and rampant wickedness and receive with meekness the implanted word" — the required posture is active stripping away of the constitutional evil combined with receptive meekness toward the word. The posture is not passive — it involves active renunciation and active reception.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The evidence reveals the inner posture required negatively: what must not be present for approach to God to be acceptable. The abominable inner condition must be absent or addressed. Pro 15:8 (vc=1678 — VCG-03): the prayer of the upright is acceptable — the upright inner person is the required posture. Pro 28:9 (vc=65958 — VCG-03): the ear must not be turned from the law — receptivity to divine instruction is required. The VCG-04 repentance evidence (Eze 14:6 — vc=65984) shows what the required posture of movement toward God looks like: turning the face from abominations, which requires active volitional redirection and a conscience that registers the abomination and responds with grief/loathing (Eze 9:4; 36:31). The required inner posture is: conscience functional, will oriented away from abominations, heart without crookedness or arrogance.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The inner posture required for genuine movement toward God is the active removal of idolatrous attachments before or as part of the approach. Jer 4:1 (vc=65903 — VCG-04): "If you return, O Israel… to me you should return. If you remove your detestable things from my presence, and do not waver" — the removal of detestable things is the precondition for genuine return. Eze 14:6 parallel (from CHAR-3 but structurally identical): "repent and turn away from your idols, and turn away your faces from all your abominations." The evidence shows that genuine movement toward God is only possible when the characteristic has been actively removed — the double-allegiance approach of Jer 7:10 (VCG-04) is rejected.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The evidence reveals the required inner posture through the prescribed departure conditions. Isa 55:7 (vc=38200 — VCG-02): "let the wicked forsake his way, and the unrighteous man his thoughts; let him return to the Lord" — forsaking iniquitous way and thoughts is the required inner posture for genuine approach. Jer 4:14 (vc=38205 — VCG-02): "wash your heart from evil, that you may be saved" — the required inner posture is a cleansed heart. Job 11:14 (vc=38207 — VCG-04): "if iniquity is in your hand, put it far away, and let not injustice dwell in your tents" — removal of actively held iniquity and expelled injustice from the dwelling are both required. The inner posture required for movement toward God is: released iniquity, forsaken iniquitous thoughts, cleansed heart — the exact opposite of the characteristic's inner state.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The evidence reveals the required posture through its precise negation. Rev 16:9 (vc=14352 — VCG-01): "they did not repent and give him glory" — repentance and glory-giving are the two required postures for genuine movement toward God. The characteristic's persistent absence of repentance (Rev 16:9/11/21 — VCG-01) names what the movement requires by showing its refusal: a will that yields under judgment, repents of deeds, and redirects its speech from cursing to glorifying. 1Pe 2:12 (vc=14377 — VCG-03): "glorify God on the day of visitation" — the eventual glorifying of God is the movement-toward-God that honourable conduct enables even former accusers to make.

---

##### T4.2.3 — What does the human-to-God direction of this characteristic reveal about the person's relationship with God?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The human-to-God direction of the characteristic reveals that wickedness is a relational orientation — it is constituted by the person's orientation away from God (Psa 10:4; 9:17; Mal 3:18) and can potentially be reversed by reorientation toward God (Eze 33:11; Isa 55:7). The characteristic is therefore not merely a moral-quality category but a relational-directional one: the wicked person is the person whose inner life is pointed away from God. This relational definition is consistent with the structural opposite: righteousness (tsaddiq) is the person who serves God (Mal 3:18), knows God's way (Psa 1:6), and walks not in the counsel of the wicked (Psa 1:1). The human-to-God relational direction defines the characteristic as fundamentally a God-relationship status.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The human-to-God direction reveals that evil as constitutional inner nature is specifically a God-approach blocker — its primary relational consequence at the vertical level is the foreclosing of the human's access to God. Heb 10:22 (VCG-06) names the evil conscience as the specific obstacle. Heb 3:12 (VCG-06) frames the evil heart as leading away from God. The characteristic therefore defines the human person as constitutionally at a relational distance from God — not primarily by external circumstance but by constitutional inner condition. The human-to-God direction reveals that the characteristic's address (Act 3:26 — turning from wickedness; Heb 10:22 — cleansed conscience) is the precondition for vertical relational restoration.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The human-to-God direction reveals that abomination operates as a specific corruption of the approach relationship — it is not merely that the abominable person is bad; their very attempts at religious approach become additional abominations. Pro 15:8 (vc=1678 — VCG-03) and Isa 1:13 (vc=1695 — VCG-03) show that the attempt to approach God without inner transformation compounds the offense: the abominable inner person's sacrifice and incense are themselves additional abominations. This reveals the characteristic as one that, in its unaddressed state, makes approach to God impossible and any attempted approach counterproductive — deepening the relational violation rather than reducing it.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The human-to-God direction reveals that idolatrous abomination specifically blocks and corrupts the vertical relational movement. Deu 32:16 (vc=65938 — VCG-02): what should be movement toward God (worship) is redirected to "strange gods" — idolatrous abomination is the worship-capacity directed wrongly. Jer 7:10 (vc=65963 — VCG-04): standing in God's house while continuing in abominations — even the physical act of temple-approach is made ineffectual by the characteristic. The characteristic reveals that the devotion-capacity is a single faculty: it can move toward God or toward idols, but not both simultaneously. Idolatrous abomination occupies the devotion-channel so completely that genuine movement toward God requires its prior removal.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The human-to-God direction reveals that iniquity as active scheming specifically blocks and nullifies the prayer-worship channel. Psa 66:18 (vc=38182 — VCG-04): cherished iniquity = closed divine ear. Isa 1:13 (vc=38197 — VCG-04): iniquity-accompanied religious assembly = divine intolerance. Psa 14:4 (VCG-03): evildoers do not call on God — they lack even the orientation toward the divine. This blocking is the deepest consequence of the characteristic at the individual level: not merely the harm done to others but the severing of the person's own access to God through prayer and worship. The characteristic reveals itself as not merely antisocial but fundamentally anti-covenantal, cutting off the person from the primary relational resource of covenant life.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The human-to-God direction reveals that the characteristic is specifically and completely anti-worship: it converts every divine approach (including judgment) into an occasion for further hostility. Rev 16:9/11/21 (VCG-01): scorching heat, pain, hailstones — each escalating divine contact produces not approach but increased hostility. The characteristic transforms the encounter with divine power from a grace-invitation into a defiance-occasion. This reveals a will so hardened that the divine-human encounter itself cannot penetrate it with corrective force — the very instruments of divine approach become the stimuli for greater defiance. The human-to-God direction of the characteristic is thus: every divine encounter deepens the anti-movement.

---

##### T4.2.4 — If the evidence is silent on human-to-God operation, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The evidence is not silent; human-to-God operation is richly evidenced (T4.2.1–T4.2.3). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The evidence is not silent; human-to-God operation is addressed in T4.2.1–T4.2.3. This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The evidence is not silent; human-to-God operation through the worship VCGs is richly evidenced (T4.2.1–T4.2.3). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The evidence is not silent; human-to-God operation (corruption of the approach channel) is evidenced (T4.2.1–T4.2.3). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The evidence is not silent; the human-to-God direction (as blocked prayer, corrupted worship, and absence of divine calling) is richly evidenced (T4.2.1–T4.2.3). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Human-to-God operation (as sustained anti-movement under judgment) is evidenced (T4.2.1–T4.2.3). This prompt is satisfied.

---

#### T4.3 — Human Interface — Giving

##### T4.3.1 — Does the verse evidence show this characteristic being extended by one person toward another — and if so, how does it operate in that giving?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The question asks about "extending" wickedness as one might extend love or wisdom. The evidence shows the wicked person imposing their characteristic on others through: (a) social-moral contagion — Num 16:26 (VCG-04): proximity to the wicked risks "being swept away with all their sins" — the characteristic has a social-contagious dimension; (b) alliance-recruitment — Exo 23:1 (VCG-04): "you shall not join hands with a wicked man to be a malicious witness" — the wicked person actively recruits others into complicity; (c) evil counsel — Psa 1:1 (VCG-04): the blessed person avoids the wicked person's counsel — the counsel of the wicked is extended outward and capable of drawing others into alignment; (d) systemic imposition — Eze 7:21 (VCG-03): the wicked of the earth serve as instruments of profanation. The wicked person extends their characteristic's influence outward as harm and recruitment, not as a gift.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Yes. The characteristic is extended toward others through several mechanisms. (1) Social contagion: 2Jo 11 (vc=14453 — VCG-04): "whoever greets him takes part in his wicked works" — the constitutionally evil person communicates their characteristic through voluntary association; greeting is the mechanism. (2) Social disruption: Act 17:5 (vc=14452 — VCG-04): "wicked men of the rabble…formed a mob, set the city in an uproar" — the constitutional inner disposition is organised and deployed collectively as social harm. (3) Community control: 3Jo 10 (vc=14454 — VCG-04): Diotrephes's characteristic is extended through speech ("wicked nonsense"), refusal of hospitality, and obstruction of others — the characteristic flows outward through the person's social power. (4) Teaching and leadership: 2Ti 3:13 (vc=14451 — VCG-06): "evil people and impostors will go on from bad to worse, deceiving" — the characteristic is extended through false teaching as a communicative act.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Yes, though extension operates differently from a gift characteristic. The characteristic is extended toward others primarily through: (1) the scoffer's contemptuous derision — Pro 24:9 (vc=65957 — VCG-01): "the scoffer is an abomination to mankind" — the inner disposition of contemptuous derision is extended toward others and makes the scoffer repugnant to the human community; (2) perverted judgment — Pro 17:15 (vc=1690 — VCG-01): justifying the wicked and condemning the righteous — the inverted moral verdict is directed toward other persons, doing them harm; (3) the Babylon-figure of Rev 17:5 (vc=65878 — VCG-05): the "mother of prostitutes and of earth's abominations" — the characteristic is generative, extending abomination toward others through the generation and propagation of moral corruption; (4) Mal 2:11 (vc=66004 — VCG-04): faithless betrayal in the covenant-marriage relationship — the abomination is extended toward the covenant partner.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Yes. Idolatrous abomination extends from person to person through multiple mechanisms. (1) Royal/institutional extension: 1Ki 11:7 (vc=65899 — VCG-03): Solomon building high places extends the idolatrous abomination to the entire community; 2Ki 21:11 (vc=65942 — VCG-03): Manasseh "made Judah also to sin with his idols" — active communal extension; 2Ch 36:14 (vc=65948 — VCG-03): leaders "following all the abominations of the nations" leading the people in the same. (2) Cultural-educational extension: Deu 20:18 (vc=65932 — VCG-02): the nations "teach you to do according to all their abominable practices" — the teaching of abominable practices is a specific extension mechanism. (3) Social-relational extension: Ezr 9:14 (vc=65950 — VCG-03): intermarriage with abomination-practicing peoples as the relational channel of extension.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Yes. The extension of iniquity toward others is extensively documented. Direct harm-infliction: Psa 55:3 (vc=38188 — VCG-01): "they drop trouble upon me" — iniquity is actively dropped onto victims. Predatory exploitation: Psa 14:4 (vc=38229 — VCG-03): "evildoers who eat up my people as they eat bread" — the characteristic is extended through predatory consumption of others. Institutional oppression: Isa 10:1 (vc=38191 — VCG-02): "those who decree iniquitous decrees… the writers who keep writing oppression" — iniquity is extended through institutional power structures that systematically harm the weak. Social deception: Psa 28:3 (vc=38232 — VCG-03): speaking peace while evil is in the heart — iniquity is extended through relational deception. Entrapment: Psa 141:9 (vc=38231 — VCG-03): "the trap that they have laid for me and from the snares of evildoers" — the characteristic is extended through cunning entrapment of the innocent.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Yes. The characteristic is constitutively extended toward others. VCG-01: Rev 13:6 (vc=14356 — VCG-01): blasphemy extended toward God, his name, his dwelling, and heaven's inhabitants — the extension is deliberate and sustained. VCG-02: 1Cor 4:13 (vc=14351 — VCG-02): "when slandered" — the slandering speech is extended by some toward the apostle; Rom 3:8 (vc=14358 — VCG-02): "slanderously charge us with saying" — false attribution extended toward Paul. VCG-03: Joh 18:30 (vc=14378 — VCG-03): the accusers extend the false charge toward the accused (Jesus); 1Pe 2:12 (vc=14377 — VCG-03): opponents "speak against you as evildoers" — the false accusation is extended toward the community of believers.

---

##### T4.3.2 — What inner conditions or orientations in the giver enable genuine extension of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The inner conditions enabling the wicked person to extend their characteristic toward others are: (1) deliberate intent to recruit or harm — Exo 23:1 (VCG-04 — joining the wicked in malicious witness); Jer 5:26 (VCG-03 — deliberate predatory intent to trap); (2) social boldness — Pro 21:29 (VCG-08 — "a wicked man puts on a bold face" — the absence of inner check enables the bold outward extension); (3) the suppression of relational moral awareness — Psa 28:3 (VCG-08 — "speak peace while evil is in their hearts" — the deceptive extension is enabled by the suppression of transparent conscience). The enabling conditions are all internal suppressions of the moral-relational checks that would otherwise restrain the person from extending harm outward.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The enabling inner conditions for extending the characteristic are: (1) the absence of repentance — the characteristic that has not been addressed through repentance (Act 8:22 — VCG-05) remains available to be projected outward; (2) the presence of unchecked social power or authority — 3Jo 10 (vc=14454 — VCG-04) shows Diotrephes using his social position to extend his constitutional malice; (3) the rationalising inner condition — Rom 2:8 (vc=14338 — VCG-05): self-seeking combined with obedience to unrighteousness enables the person to present their constitutional evil as justified self-assertion; (4) Mat 22:18 (vc=14408 — VCG-05): the ponēria of the Pharisees is "calculated" — the deliberate, planned nature of the inner malice is what enables its outward extension.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The enabling conditions for extending abomination toward others are: (1) the settled inner disposition of contemptuous derision (the scoffer's character — Pro 24:9 — VCG-01); (2) the inverted moral-evaluative capacity that produces perverted judgment (Pro 17:15 — VCG-01 — the inner inversion enables the outer perversion of justice directed at others); (3) the concealed multiple abominations in the heart (Pro 26:25 — VCG-02) — the inner reservoir of corrupt motivations enables the outward extension of abomination through gracious-seeming social performance; (4) the faithless will that betrays covenant loyalty (Mal 2:11 — VCG-04 — an inward infidelity extending outward as betrayal).

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The enabling inner conditions for extending idolatrous abomination toward others: (1) established inner attachment — a person extends the characteristic only when they are already deeply attached to the idolatrous objects (Solomon's attachments driven by his many wives — 1Ki 11:5-7 — VCG-03 — which enabled his building of high places for their gods); (2) institutional or royal authority — the power to shape communal practice (2Ki 21:11 — VCG-03: Manasseh's authority enables the communal extension of his personal abominations); (3) the covenantal community's failure to maintain separation (Ezr 9:1 — vc=65949 — VCG-03: failure to separate from abomination-practicing peoples enables extension through communal integration).

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The enabling inner conditions for extending iniquity toward others: (1) the established inner habit of scheming — Mic 2:1 (vc=38217 — VCG-02): the person who has habitually devised extends their schemes outward at dawn; (2) the predatory inner appetite — Pro 19:28 (vc=38220 — VCG-03): "the mouth of the wicked devours iniquity" — the inner craving drives extension; (3) institutional authority — Isa 10:1 (vc=38191 — VCG-02): the lawmaker and writer have the power to extend iniquity institutionally; (4) anger and sustained grudge — Psa 55:3 (vc=38188 — VCG-01): "in anger they bear a grudge against me" — the affective state of sustained anger fuels the relational extension of harm.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Enabling conditions for extending evil speech toward another: (1) the hardened will that refuses to yield — Rev 16:9/11/21 (VCG-01): the will hardened against repentance enables continued defiant speech; (2) authority-rejection — Jude 8 (vc=14354 — VCG-01): rejecting authority enables blasphemy of the glorious ones; (3) hostile malicious evaluation of another — Joh 18:30 (vc=14378 — VCG-03): the accusers' inner evaluation produces the false verbal charge; (4) moral failure creating the occasion for social defamation — Rom 2:24 (vc=14357 — VCG-02): the moral failure of those who represent God creates the occasion for the Gentiles' blasphemous speech; (5) sensory self-indulgence combined with spiritual independence — Jude 8 (VCG-01): "relying on their dreams, defile the flesh" — the self-centred sensory orientation enables the contemptuous speech directed at authority.

---

##### T4.3.3 — What does the evidence reveal about what the person must have received or become before they can genuinely give this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The wicked person can extend their characteristic to others once they have themselves settled into it — once the internal God-exclusion (Psa 10:4), the suppression of conscience (Psa 36:1), and the volitional alignment with wickedness (Pro 4:14 — entering the path) have consolidated into a stable inner orientation. 1Sa 24:13 (VCG-04): "out of the wicked comes wickedness" — the wicked person must first be constituted as a wicked inner source before they can extend wickedness outward. The evidence suggests no external bestowal that enables this; it is an internally generated and consolidated state that then overflows outward as social harm and moral contagion.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Unlike a gift characteristic (wisdom, love, grace), evil as constitutional inner nature does not require the person to receive something from outside before extending it — it is the baseline constitutional condition from which extension flows. 1Sa 24:13 / CHAR-1's pattern of "out of the wicked comes wickedness" parallels the CHAR-2 pattern: the evil treasury (Mat 12:35 — VCG-03) is already full by constitutional default. The person extends the characteristic from their own constitutional inner store — they do not need to receive it first. The extension is the natural output of the constitutional condition already present. This makes CHAR-2 distinct from positive characteristics (like grace or wisdom) that require reception before giving.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Like CHAR-2, the characteristic is not received from another before being extended — it develops from within the inner moral character. The scoffer's contemptuous derision (Pro 24:9 — VCG-01), the dishonest dealer's habitual practice (Deu 25:16 — VCG-01), and the Pharisees' self-justifying pride (Luk 16:15 — VCG-02) are all inner conditions that developed from within the person's inner moral formation and are then expressed outward toward others. The person extends abomination toward others from the reservoir of their own abominable inner character — 1Sa 24:13's "out of the wicked comes wickedness" is structurally parallel here. The abominable condition is the inner generative source from which abominable acts directed at others flow.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The person extends idolatrous abomination toward others from their own established inner attachment: Hos 9:10 (vc=1632 — VCG-04): "they became detestable like the thing they loved" — the person who extends the characteristic has already been transformed by idolatrous attachment into someone who is themselves detestable. 1Ki 11:5 (vc=65898 — VCG-03): Solomon "went after Ashtoreth… and after Milcom" — he had already committed himself to these idols before building their high places. The person must first have settled into idolatrous inner attachment before they can extend it — the extension is the overflow of an established inner condition.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The evidence consistently presents iniquity as self-generated from within rather than received from another before extension (T2.9.1). The extending person extends what their own inner life has generated: Psa 7:14 (vc=38245 — VCG-02): "conceives evil… gives birth to lies" — the iniquity is conceived internally before being extended outward. Isa 32:6 (vc=38181 — VCG-02): "his heart is busy with iniquity" — the heart's own production is what flows outward. However, chosen association with evildoers (Job 34:8 — VCG-04) can shape the inner person toward iniquity; in this sense, what must be "received or become" before extension is the inner character of the evildoer-type (VCG-03), developed through volitional choice and associative formation.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The characteristic is generated from within the person's own inner moral state rather than received from another before extension. Jude 8 (vc=14354 — VCG-01): the dreamers' inner posture (sensory self-indulgence + authority-rejection) is what produces the blasphemous extension — they extend what their own inner condition generates. Rev 13:6 (VCG-01): the beast's sustained defiant contempt is what its mouth utters — inner contempt is expressed outward. Joh 18:30 (VCG-03): the accusers' malicious evaluation is their own — they have become people whose inner moral posture produces false accusatory speech. What must be received or become: a hardened will (VCG-01), a hostile evaluative posture (VCG-03), or a moral-failure condition (VCG-02).

---

##### T4.3.4 — If the evidence is silent on the giving direction, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The evidence is not silent; the outward extension of wickedness-as-social-force is documented (T4.3.1–T4.3.3). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The giving direction is evidenced (T4.3.1–T4.3.3). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The giving direction is evidenced (T4.3.1–T4.3.3). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The giving direction is evidenced (T4.3.1–T4.3.3). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The giving direction is richly evidenced (T4.3.1–T4.3.3). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The giving direction is richly evidenced (T4.3.1–T4.3.3). This prompt is satisfied.

---

#### T4.4 — Human Interface — Receiving

##### T4.4.1 — Does the verse evidence show this characteristic being received by a person from another — and if so, how does it operate in that reception?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Yes. The evidence shows the characteristic being received through alliance and counsel. Psa 1:1 (VCG-04): walking in the counsel of the wicked, standing in the way of sinners, sitting in the seat of scoffers — three progressively deeper stages of receiving the wicked orientation through social alignment. Exo 23:1 (VCG-04): "join hands with a wicked man to be a malicious witness" — active voluntary reception through alliance. Num 16:26 (VCG-04): the community warned against proximity that would result in being "swept away with all their sins" — passive reception through dangerous proximity. 2Ch 19:2 (VCG-03): Jehoshaphat "helped the wicked" and thereby drew divine wrath — receiving a relational alignment with wickedness brings consequences even without fully adopting the characteristic.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Yes. The characteristic is received through: (1) association — 2Jo 11 (vc=14453 — VCG-04): merely greeting the wicked person makes one "a participant in his wicked works" — the characteristic is received through voluntary relational association; (2) false teaching — 2Ti 3:13 (vc=14451 — VCG-06): "deceiving and being deceived" — the characteristic's influence spreads through the deception of false teaching; (3) social alignment — Mat 12:45 (vc=65879 — VCG-06): the evil generation mirrors the spirit-filling pattern, showing collective reception of increasing evil; (4) community saturation — 1Cor 5:6-8 context (vc=14363/14412 — VCG-05): the old leaven's spread through the community shows the characteristic being received by those around the constitutionally evil person through communal contagion.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The characteristic is received primarily through: (1) communal saturation — Ezr 9:11 (vc=66005 — VCG-04): "the land that you are entering… is a land impure with the impurity of the peoples of the lands, with their abominations that have filled it" — the abominations of surrounding peoples are received communally through environmental saturation; (2) Eze 44:6-7 (vc=66001-66002 — VCG-04): Israel is addressed as a community that has received and accumulated abominations through its rebellious inner orientation and through admitting the uncircumcised in heart; (3) the Babylon figure (Rev 17:5 — vc=65878 — VCG-05): as "mother of earth's abominations" — abomination is actively generated and communicated to others through her influence. The primary reception mode is communal-environmental rather than individual-relational.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Yes. Reception occurs primarily through social-relational channels. (1) Cultural-educational reception: Deu 20:18 (vc=65932 — VCG-02): abominable practices received through being "taught" by idolatrous nations; Deu 18:9 (vc=65931 — VCG-02): the warning against "learning to follow the abominable practices of those nations" implies that learning is the primary reception mechanism. (2) Relational-marital reception: 1Ki 11:5 (vc=65898 — VCG-03): Solomon's wives drew him after their gods — idolatrous attachment received through intimate relational influence. (3) Social-environmental reception: Ezr 9:1 (vc=65949 — VCG-03): the community's failure to separate from peoples with abominations results in the characteristic permeating their communal life.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Yes. Reception occurs through social channels. Associational: Job 34:8 (vc=38214 — VCG-04): "who travels in company with evildoers and walks with wicked men" — chosen proximity to evildoers is the reception channel; the inner person is shaped by sustained companionship with those who work iniquity. Appetitive: Pro 17:4 (vc=38219 — VCG-03): "an evildoer listens to wicked lips" — the inner reception of harmful speech as a preferred input. Communal-embedded: Psa 55:10 (vc=38239 — VCG-01): "iniquity and trouble are within it" (the city) — iniquity is embedded in communal structures from which individual persons receive it through inhabiting the community. Psa 141:4 (vc=38230 — VCG-04): "do not let my heart incline to any evil, to busy myself with wicked deeds in company with men who work iniquity" — the prayer shows the reception risk through associational influence.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Yes. The reception of evil speech is directly documented in VCG-02 and VCG-03. 1Cor 4:13 (vc=14351 — VCG-02): "when slandered, we entreat" — the apostle receives slander from others; the slandering speech comes to him. 1Pe 2:12 (vc=14377 — VCG-03): believers receive false accusation as evildoers from opponents. 1Pe 3:16 (vc=14380 — VCG-03): "when you are slandered, those who revile your good behavior in Christ may be put to shame" — the slander is received. 1Pe 4:15 (vc=14381 — VCG-03): the instruction not to suffer as an evildoer implies some are suffering from accusations. The reception of the characteristic is the experience of the falsely accused target.

---

##### T4.4.2 — What inner conditions enable or block reception of this characteristic from another person?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Enabling reception: (1) volitional openness to the wicked person's counsel — Psa 1:1 implies a sequence of increasing receptivity ("walks," "stands," "sits") that can be blocked at each stage; (2) the weakening of God-fear that would otherwise constitute resistance; (3) the attraction of the wicked person's apparent prosperity (Job 21:7 — VCG-10 — why do the wicked thrive? — this appearance of success is a reception-enabling attraction). Blocking reception: (1) active moral separation — Psa 26:5 (VCG-03): "I hate the assembly of evildoers and will not sit with the wicked" — deliberate relational separation; (2) maintained fear of God (the God-fear that is absent in the wicked person — Psa 36:1 — blocks reception of their orientation when present); (3) physical distancing — Num 16:26 (VCG-04): "depart from the tents of these wicked men."

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Enabling reception: (1) voluntary relational alignment — 2Jo 11 (vc=14453 — VCG-04): greeting (choosing relationship with) the evil person; (2) unoccupied inner space — Mat 12:45 (vc=65879 — VCG-06): the swept and empty inner space invites reoccupation by more evil; (3) absence of the word of God abiding — 1Jo 2:14 (vc=14430 — VCG-01): the word abiding in a person is the primary blocking condition. Blocking reception: (1) the word of God abiding within (1Jo 2:14 — VCG-01), (2) faith as a shield (Eph 6:16 — vc=14428 — VCG-01: faith extinguishing the evil one's darts), (3) active moral separation — 1Cor 5:13 (vc=14465 — VCG-04): the community expels the evil person to prevent further spread.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Enabling conditions for receiving abomination: (1) the absence of conscience-based resistance — when the conscience is silenced (Jer 6:15; 8:12 — VCG-04), there is no inner faculty to resist incoming abominable influences; (2) the absence of discernment — Isa 44:19 (vc=65961 — VCG-05): no consideration, knowledge, or discernment enables reception of abomination without recognition; (3) the uncircumcised heart — Eze 44:7 (vc=66002 — VCG-04): admitting those uncircumcised in heart to sacred space shows that inner uncircumcision (non-responsiveness to God) enables the reception and embedding of abomination in communal space. Blocking conditions: a functional conscience (Eze 9:4 — VCG-04: those who sigh and groan — their conscience is the inner shield that prevents reception of the abomination).

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Enabling reception: (1) coveting what is on the idols (Deu 7:25 — vc=1682 — VCG-02: "lest you be ensnared by it") — the inner covetousness is the vulnerability that enables reception; (2) failure of active separation (Deu 18:9 — VCG-02: learning rather than refusing); (3) intimate relational entanglement (1Ki 11:5 — VCG-03: wives drawing the heart). Blocking reception: (1) the immediate destruction of idol-objects (Deu 7:25 — VCG-02: "burn with fire") — removing the attractive object prevents the eye-feast-loop from starting; (2) maintained covenant separation (Ezr 9:1/14 — VCG-03 — the failure to do this enabled reception); (3) not coveting — the volitional act of not desiring what is on the idols is the primary inner blocking condition.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Enabling reception: (1) the heart's susceptibility to incline — Psa 141:4 (vc=38230 — VCG-04): the heart's capacity for inclination toward evil is the vulnerability that enables associational reception; (2) inner appetite for harmful input — Pro 17:4 (VCG-03): the evildoer listens to wicked lips — an already-present appetite that receives iniquity eagerly; (3) absence of the divine hearing — Job 36:10 (VCG-04): the closed ear to instruction leaves the person receptive to the wrong influencing voices. Blocking reception: (1) steady steps according to divine promise — Psa 119:133 (VCG-04): the blocking condition for iniquity's dominion; (2) active volitional distancing — Job 11:14 (VCG-04): "put it far away" — removing the characteristic from the hand blocks further accumulation; (3) maintained covenant loyalty — Deu 28:20 (VCG-05): the evil of deeds flows from forsaking God; sustained covenant attachment blocks reception.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The characteristic as received (false accusation, slander) is not blocked by inner conditions in the sense of preventing the speech from being directed at the person — it can be directed regardless of the recipient's inner state. What the evidence addresses is the response-conditions: 1Pe 3:16 (vc=14380 — VCG-03): "having a good conscience" — the inner condition of good conscience enables the person to receive the slander without being undone by it; 1Cor 4:13 (vc=14351 — VCG-02): the apostle's inner posture of non-retaliation (entreat rather than counter-blast) is what enables dignified reception. The inner condition that blocks the characteristic from damaging the recipient is good conscience combined with honourable conduct (1Pe 2:12 — VCG-03) — not blocking the speech itself but blocking its power to destroy.

---

##### T4.4.3 — What is the inner-being state of the person who encounters this characteristic from another but does not receive it?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The person who encounters wickedness but does not receive it maintains a state of deliberate inner separation — not passive avoidance but active moral resistance. Psa 26:5 (VCG-03): "I hate the assembly of evildoers" — the maintained inner stance includes deliberate moral hatred of the association. Psa 1:1 (VCG-04): the blessed person is defined by what they refuse to align with. Psa 7:9 (VCG-04): "let the evil of the wicked come to an end, and may you establish the righteous — you who test the minds and hearts" — the inner state is one of maintained integrity that submits to divine moral testing and expects divine confirmation. The non-receiver of wickedness is characterised by active moral separation maintained through sustained inner commitment.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The non-receiving person maintains a state of active abhorrence and moral separation. Rom 12:9 (vc=14417 — VCG-06): "abhor what is evil; hold fast to what is good" — the inner state is one of active moral revulsion sustaining the separation from the characteristic. 1Cor 5:13 (vc=14465 — VCG-04): the community in the state of not-receiving the evil person's characteristic acts to expel them — the inner state includes moral discernment (recognising the characteristic), communal will (deciding to act), and the capacity for difficult relational action. The non-receiving state is maintained by word-abiding (1Jo 2:14 — VCG-01), faith (Eph 6:16 — VCG-01), and active community accountability.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The non-receiving person maintains a state of active grief-recoil that mirrors the divine revulsion. Eze 9:4 (vc=1698 — VCG-04): "the men who sigh and groan over all the abominations that are committed" — these are persons whose conscience is fully functional, whose moral perception is operational (they perceive the abominations), and whose affective faculty registers them with grief. Their inner state is one of conscience-alive moral anguish that does not become abominable compliance. Pro 29:27 (vc=65959 — VCG-01): "an unjust man is an abomination to the righteous" — the righteous person experiences the unjust as morally repugnant (sharing the divine revulsion), which is the affective expression of their non-receiving inner state.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The non-receiving person actively destroys the idol-objects and maintains covenant separation. 2Ch 15:8 (vc=65902 — VCG-03): Asa "took courage and put away the detestable idols" — the inner state is one of moral-covenantal revulsion that translates immediately into decisive removal. 2Ki 23:24 (vc=65901 — VCG-03): Josiah's systematic purge — the inner state is comprehensive covenantal fidelity that finds idolatrous objects incompatible with that fidelity. The non-receiver mirrors the divine revulsion at the idol-objects rather than being attracted by them; their inner faculty of devotion is already engaged with God, which makes the idol-object both recognisable and repugnant.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The non-receiving person maintains active rejection and volitional protection. Psa 101:8 (vc=38226 — VCG-03): "morning by morning I will destroy all the wicked in the land, cutting off all the evildoers from the city of the Lord" — the non-receiver actively removes iniquity-workers from the communal space rather than receiving their influence. Psa 141:9 (vc=38231 — VCG-03): prayer for protection from "the trap that they have laid" — the non-receiver is alert to the entrapment strategies of iniquity-workers. Job 36:10 (VCG-04): those whose ears are opened to instruction and who return from iniquity — the open-eared, instruction-receptive person is the paradigmatic non-receiver of iniquity. The inner state is: instruction-receptive, volitionally resistant, calling on the Lord (in contrast to the evildoer who does not call — Psa 14:4 — VCG-03).

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The person who encounters the characteristic but does not generate evil speech in response maintains: (1) non-retaliatory inner orientation — 1Cor 4:13 (vc=14351 — VCG-02): "when slandered, we entreat" — the inner state is active non-retaliation through entreaty; (2) good conscience — 1Pe 3:16 (vc=14380 — VCG-03): "having a good conscience" — the inner integrity that does not return evil for evil; (3) honourable conduct orientation — 1Pe 2:12 (vc=14377 — VCG-03): "keep your conduct among the Gentiles honorable" — the positive inner orientation toward good deeds that will eventually silence the false accusation. The non-receiving state is one of maintained inner integrity, non-retaliatory response, and sustained honourable orientation.

---

##### T4.4.4 — If the evidence is silent on the receiving direction, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The evidence is not silent; reception of wickedness through social alignment is documented (T4.4.1–T4.4.3). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The receiving direction is evidenced (T4.4.1–T4.4.3). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The receiving direction is evidenced (T4.4.1–T4.4.3). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The receiving direction is evidenced (T4.4.1–T4.4.3). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The receiving direction is evidenced (T4.4.1–T4.4.3). This prompt is satisfied.

The receiving direction is evidenced (T4.4.1–T4.4.3). This prompt is satisfied.
