#### T4.5 — Human Interface — Boundaries

##### T4.5.1 — Does the evidence indicate whether this characteristic operates differently within existing relational bonds versus across relational distance or difference?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The evidence shows the characteristic operating with particular intensity within close relational bonds. Psa 28:3 (VCG-08): "speak peace with their neighbors while evil is in their hearts" — the deception is maximally operative within close relational proximity where trust is assumed. Psa 37:12 (VCG-03): "the wicked plots against the righteous" — the plotting targets the nearby righteous, not a distant stranger. The social-destruction of Pro 11:11 (city overthrown by the wicked's speech) occurs in a communal context of shared civic life. However, the characteristic also operates across relational distance: Hab 3:13 (VCG-03) — the wicked as an entrenched institutional power structure — suggests the characteristic operates at scale beyond proximate bonds. The evidence does not show a fundamental qualitative difference by relational distance but does show that the characteristic's deceptive mode (Psa 28:3) is most operative within bonds of assumed trust.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The evidence shows the characteristic operating with particular intensity within relational proximity and community bonds. 2Jo 11 (vc=14453 — VCG-04): the transmission through greeting requires proximity. 3Jo 10 (vc=14454 — VCG-04): Diotrephes's constitutional malice is deployed through the specific institutional relationships of church membership and hospitality. 1Cor 5:8 (vc=14363/14412 — VCG-05): the old leaven's spreading effect specifically requires the communal batch it is mixed into — the leaven metaphor implies that close community proximity is the medium through which the characteristic spreads. The evidence does not suggest qualitatively different operation across relational distance — rather, it shows that the characteristic's social harm is most potent and most visible within existing relational bonds precisely because those bonds provide the channels through which it flows.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The evidence shows the characteristic operating with particular intensity within close relational bonds. Mal 2:11 (vc=66004 — VCG-04): faithless covenant-betrayal through mixed marriage — the abomination is specifically the violation of the intimate covenant bond. Pro 26:25 (vc=1694 — VCG-02): seven abominations hidden beneath gracious speech — the gracious speech implies close social relationship; the concealment is operative within relational proximity. The Ezekiel conscience-related abominations (VCG-04: Eze 44:6-7) concern the covenant community's internal violations. VCG-03's corrupt worship abominations concern the personal worship relationship — the most intimate directional bond. The characteristic's most intense expression is within existing bonds of intimacy (covenant, worship relationship, close social proximity) where the violation of trust is compounded by the closeness of the bond violated.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The evidence shows the characteristic operating most powerfully within intimate relational bonds. 1Ki 11:4-5 (vc=65898 — VCG-03): "his wives turned away his heart… Solomon went after Ashtoreth" — the king's intimate marital bonds were the primary mechanism of idolatrous influence. Ezr 9:14 (vc=65950 — VCG-03): intermarriage with abomination-practicing peoples — intimate covenantal bonds as the mechanism. The characteristic is more potent within existing relational bonds (marriage, cultural community, institutional authority) than across relational distance. The Deuteronomic warnings (VCG-02) consistently frame the hazard as relational proximity — being among the nations (Deu 18:9; 20:18 — VCG-02) rather than distance from them.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The evidence shows the characteristic operating with particular damage within close relational bonds. Psa 28:3 (vc=38232 — VCG-03): "workers of evil, who speak peace with their neighbors" — the neighbour-bond is specifically the relational context exploited by the inner-evil/outward-peace deception. Psa 41:6 (vc=38236 — VCG-04): "when one comes to see me, he utters empty words, while his heart gathers iniquity" — the visit (a close relational act) is exploited as cover for inward iniquity-gathering. The characteristic weaponises intimacy: the closer the bond, the more effectively deception operates (speaking peace while evil is in the heart — Psa 28:3 — VCG-03 — requires relational proximity to be plausible). The VCG-01 trouble-suffered register (Psa 55:3 — "they drop trouble upon me") also evidences the characteristic as operating within personal enemy relationships rather than anonymous contexts.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The evidence shows the characteristic operating with particular intensity in contexts of hostile relational proximity. 1Pe 2:12 (vc=14377 — VCG-03): "among the Gentiles" — the false accusation occurs within the shared social space of a minority community (believers) living among a majority culture (Gentiles); the proximity enables the social observation and accusation. Joh 18:30 (vc=14378 — VCG-03): the accusers have specifically observed and evaluated the accused — the false charge requires enough relational proximity to observe and make a judgment. VCG-01 (Rev 16:9/11/21) operates at the most extreme form of divine-human relational distance — yet even this is a direct encounter (God's judgment falling on those who curse him). The characteristic can operate across relational distance (verbal accusation from any social position) but is most intense in contexts of structured social opposition.

---

##### T4.5.2 — Does this characteristic operate within covenantal contexts only, or does it cross covenantal boundaries?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The characteristic crosses covenantal boundaries. The Proverbs evidence (VCGs 06, 07, 08, 09) frames wickedness as a universal moral category — the wicked person is addressed as a human type, not specifically as a covenant-community member violating covenant obligations. Job 9:22-24 (VCG-04, 10) frames the wicked as a cosmic category (earth delivered into their hands). The Psalms' structural contrast of wicked vs. righteous is articulated as a fundamental human-moral binary. Mal 3:18 (VCG-02) defines the wicked as those who do not serve God — which applies within and beyond the covenant community. Gen 18:23-25 (VCG-04) frames wickedness and righteousness as universal moral categories in Abraham's dialogue with God about Sodom (a non-covenant city). The characteristic is not covenantally restricted.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The characteristic crosses covenantal boundaries. The baseline constitutional evil (Mat 7:11; Luk 11:13 — VCG-02) is addressed to humans collectively — "you who are evil" — not to covenant community members specifically. Act 17:5 (vc=14452 — VCG-04): wicked men of the rabble — outside the covenant community. Mat 5:45 (vc=14437 — VCG-04): "evil persons" alongside "good" as universal moral categories receiving God's common providence. The characteristic is a universal human constitutional condition, not covenantally bounded. Notably, the Pauline letters address it within the covenant community — Eph 4:31 (VCG-05), Col 3:8 (VCG-05), 1Pe 2:1 (VCG-05) — showing that the characteristic also operates within the covenant community, requiring ongoing address even among believers.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The characteristic crosses covenantal boundaries. The Proverbs evidence (VCGs 01, 02, 03) applies to human moral character generally — the dishonest dealer (Deu 25:16 — VCG-01), the scoffer (Pro 24:9 — VCG-01), and the person with seven abominations in their heart (Pro 26:25 — VCG-02) are moral-character categories that apply universally. Pro 29:27 (vc=65959 — VCG-01): "the unjust man is an abomination to the righteous" — applies to any human community. The NT bdelugma (Luk 16:15; Tit 1:16; Rev 17:4-5; 21:27 — VCG-02/05) also crosses covenantal boundaries: Luk 16:15 is addressed to the Pharisees in a specific religious context but names a principle about divine moral assessment that applies universally. Rev 21:27 is eschatological — applying to all humanity at the end. The characteristic is concentrated in covenantal contexts but not limited to them.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The characteristic operates most intensively within the covenantal context — it is a covenantal betrayal (Deu 32:16 — VCG-02: jealousy is provoked within the covenant relationship). The Levitical and Deuteronomic evidence (VCGs 01, 02) is entirely covenantal — laws given to the covenant community. The reform narratives (VCG-03) address the covenant community's kings. The Ezekiel corpus (VCG-05) addresses the covenant people. However, the characteristic also applies to those outside the covenant: the nations' abominable practices (Deu 20:18; 18:9 — VCG-02) are named as abominable even for non-covenant nations — the category of divine revulsion at idolatrous practice is not covenantally bounded. The intensity of the characteristic's expression is concentrated within the covenant relationship (where it constitutes betrayal) but its moral category applies universally.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The characteristic crosses covenantal boundaries. The Psalms' evildoer-class (VCG-03, 24V) addresses iniquity as a universal human category — nations as well as Israel (Psa 59:5 — vc=38242 — VCG-03: "spare none of those who treacherously plot evil" — addressed to nations). Isa 59:7 (vc=38203 — VCG-02): "their feet run to evil" applies universally. The characteristic does have concentrated covenantal expression: Deu 28:20 (VCG-05) addresses Israel specifically; Isa 10:1 (VCG-02) addresses specific Israelite rulers. But the evildoer-type is recognised as a universal inner-character category, not a covenantally bounded one. The characteristic operates most intensively within covenantal contexts (where it constitutes specific betrayal) but is not confined to them.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The characteristic crosses covenantal boundaries. VCG-01 (Rev 16:9/11/21): those cursing God are the general population under eschatological judgment — not specifically the covenant community. Rev 13:6 (VCG-01): the beast's blasphemy is directed at God from a position entirely outside the covenant community. VCG-02: Rom 2:24 (vc=14357 — VCG-02): Gentiles blaspheme God's name because of Jewish believers' moral failure — the characteristic occurs across covenantal boundaries (Gentiles responding to covenant people's failures). VCG-03: 1Pe 2:12 (vc=14377 — VCG-03): Gentile opponents accuse the Christian community — the characteristic crosses from outside to inside the covenant boundary through hostile accusation. The characteristic operates universally across covenantal and non-covenantal contexts.

---

##### T4.5.3 — What does the evidence reveal about the relational scope of this characteristic — who is included and who is not?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The relational scope is universal — the characteristic applies to any human being, within or outside the covenant community. The evidence spans Sodom (Gen 18:23-25 — VCG-04), Egypt (Exo 9:27 — VCG-04 — Pharaoh's moment of conscience), Korah's community (Num 16:26 — VCG-04), kings and nations (Psa 9:5 — VCG-05 — "you have made the wicked perish"), Job's contemporaries (VCG-10 — the theodicy discussion), and the eschatological humanity (Dan 12:10 — VCG-05). The characteristic describes a human inner-being orientation that the entire 190-verse corpus treats as a universal moral category rather than a culturally specific or covenantally bounded one.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The relational scope is universal — the characteristic is the constitutional baseline of human inner nature as such (Mat 7:11; Luk 11:13 — VCG-02). Within that universal scope, the NT evidence particularly addresses the ecclesial-communal context: the letters to churches consistently name and address the characteristic (Eph 4:31; Col 3:8; 1Pe 2:1; Jam 1:21 — VCG-05; 1Cor 5:8 — VCG-05). This shows the characteristic's relational scope spans all humanity at the constitutional level while its most intense practical address in the NT is within the covenant-community context, where its presence among believers is a pastoral emergency requiring active response.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The relational scope is broad: the characteristic applies wherever there is a moral-relational framework in which inner character can be assessed. It spans: (1) the personal divine-human relationship (VCG-02 and VCG-03 — individual heart before God); (2) the covenantal community relationship (VCG-04 — Israel's communal abominations); (3) the human-social community (Pro 24:9 — VCG-01: scoffer abominable to mankind; Pro 29:27 — vc=65959: unjust person abominable to the righteous); (4) the cosmic-eschatological scope (Rev 21:27 — VCG-05 — nothing abominable enters the holy city). The relational scope is thus from the intimately personal to the universally eschatological, confirming the characteristic as operating across all levels of moral-relational reality.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The relational scope spans: (1) the intimate individual-divine relationship — the heart that goes after idols departs from the personal covenant relationship with God (Eze 6:9 — VCG-05); (2) the royal-institutional dimension — kings who install or purge abominations shape the entire national community (VCG-03); (3) the national-covenant community — the abominations fill the land (Jer 16:18 — VCG-04) and drive the divine presence from the sanctuary (Eze 8:6 — VCG-05); (4) the eschatological — the abomination of desolation is a cosmic-eschatological event (VCG-06). The scope moves from the personal heart to the cosmic event.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The relational scope spans: (1) the personal divine-human relationship — Psa 66:18 (VCG-04): cherished iniquity closes the divine ear; (2) the intimate neighbour relationship — Psa 28:3 (VCG-03): evil hidden beneath peace-speech toward neighbours; (3) the communal-civic level — Isa 10:1 (VCG-02): iniquitous decrees affecting the community; (4) the communal-embedded level — Psa 55:10 (VCG-01): "iniquity and trouble are within it" (the city); (5) the enemy-relational level — Psa 55:3 (VCG-01): trouble dropped upon the psalmist by personal enemies; (6) the generational level — Job 21:19 (VCG-04): iniquity stored up for children. The scope covers every level from the intimate individual to the transgenerational communal.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The relational scope is maximally wide: (1) vertical divine-human (VCG-01 — the human person against God); (2) horizontal community-level (VCG-03 — 1Pe 2:12: believers accused by Gentile opponents; 1Pe 3:16: slandered by those who revile); (3) individual person-to-person (VCG-02 — 1Cor 4:13: apostle slandered; Rom 3:8: false attribution to Paul); (4) institutional-legal (VCG-03 — Joh 18:30: formal legal charge; Act 25:5: official charge process); (5) eschatological-cosmic (VCG-01 — Rev 13:6; 16:9/11/21: cosmic-scale blasphemy under eschatological judgment). The characteristic operates at every level of the relational hierarchy from the intimately personal to the cosmic-eschatological.

---

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The evidence is not silent; relational scope and boundary are evidenced (T4.5.1–T4.5.3). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Relational scope and boundaries are evidenced (T4.5.1–T4.5.3). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Relational scope and boundaries are evidenced (T4.5.1–T4.5.3). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Relational scope and boundaries are evidenced (T4.5.1–T4.5.3). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Relational scope and boundaries are evidenced (T4.5.1–T4.5.3). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Relational scope and boundaries are evidenced (T4.5.1–T4.5.3). This prompt is satisfied.

#### T4.6 — Spiritual Beings Interface

##### T4.6.1 — Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating in relation to other spiritual beings — angelic or adversarial — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (S)

The verse evidence in the 190-verse corpus does not directly address the operation of wickedness-as-settled-person-identity in relation to angelic or adversarial spiritual beings. The characteristic is framed throughout as a human inner-being phenomenon in relation to God and other humans. No verse in the corpus directly implicates angelic or demonic mediation in the settling of this characteristic.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Yes — and this is the INTEGRATION_NOTE carry-forward. VCG-01 (13V) directly addresses the characteristic's operation in relation to cosmic-adversarial spiritual powers. Mat 6:13 (vc=14415 — VCG-01): "deliver us from evil" — evil as a power or domain from which divine deliverance is needed. Mat 13:19 (vc=14435 — VCG-01): the evil one as a supra-personal agent targeting the heart. Eph 6:12 (vc=14413 — VCG-05): "spiritual forces of evil in the heavenly places" — supra-human wickedness in the cosmic realm. 1Jo 5:19 (vc=14433 — VCG-01): "the whole world lies in the power of the evil one" — the cosmic-adversarial dimension is integral to understanding the scope of constitutional inner evil. The VCG-01 cosmic-evil sub-corpus is the M27 cross-register signal: these verses address a dimension of evil that is supra-personal and cosmic, not merely constitutional-individual.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The VCG-03 evidence addresses the divine-holy context within which abomination operates, but not specifically other spiritual beings. Eze 9:4 (vc=1698 — VCG-04) involves the angel instructed by the Lord to mark the grieving — angelic agency is present in the marking of those whose conscience recoils from abomination, but the angelic role is responsive to the divine-human moral situation rather than directly constituting the characteristic. The evidence does not show this characteristic as specifically mediated through or operating within angelic or adversarial spiritual agency in the same way VCG-01 in CHAR-2 evidenced the evil one.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Yes. The characteristic is fundamentally about allegiance to spiritual powers other than God. 1Ki 11:5 (vc=65898 — VCG-03): "Ashtoreth the goddess of the Sidonians" and "Milcom the abomination of the Ammonites" — foreign deities are the specific spiritual powers to whom the devotion-capacity is attached. Deu 32:16 (vc=65938 — VCG-02): "strange gods" — the characteristic involves allegiance to spiritual powers explicitly named as alien to the covenant relationship. Eze 8:5-17 (VCG-05): the Ezekiel vision shows idolatrous worship of specific figures (a creeping idol — Eze 8:10 context, women weeping for Tammuz — Eze 8:14 context, sun-worship — Eze 8:16 context) — these are specific spiritual beings/powers receiving the misdirected devotion.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Zec 10:2 (vc=38251 — VCG-01) provides the clearest spiritual-beings evidence: "household gods utter nonsense, and the diviners see lies; they tell false dreams and give empty consolation" — the iniquity of false spiritual guidance (household gods, diviners) operates in the context of spiritual beings whose deceptive counsel generates trouble and wandering. The a.ven vocabulary here names the emptiness-and-trouble produced by these spiritual-being-mediated deceptions. 1Sa 15:23 (vc=38185 — VCG-02): "rebellion is as the sin of divination" — the comparison of presumptuous self-will to divination links the characteristic's inner dynamics (the will asserting itself above God) to the adversarial spiritual realm of divination.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Yes. Jude 8 (vc=14354 — VCG-01): "blaspheme the glorious ones" — the "glorious ones" (doxas) are likely angelic or heavenly beings; the blasphemy is directed at these spiritual beings. This shows the characteristic operating directly in relation to angelic/heavenly beings as its targets. Rev 13:6 (vc=14356 — VCG-01): "blaspheming his name and his dwelling, that is, those who dwell in heaven" — the heavenly inhabitants are included in the target of the beast's blasphemy; the characteristic extends to the entire heavenly community. Jude 10 (vc=14355 — VCG-01): "blaspheme all that they do not understand" — including things that are heavenly/spiritual, beyond rational comprehension.

---

##### T4.6.2 — Is this characteristic a site of adversarial activity — something that can be attacked, distorted, or weaponised by adversarial spiritual powers?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (S)

The 190-verse corpus does not directly evidence adversarial spiritual engagement with wickedness-as-settled-person-identity. The wicked person's characteristic is framed as generated from within (T2.9.1 — "out of the wicked comes wickedness") and sustained by the person's own volitional commitment. The corpus is silent on demonic instigation or adversarial amplification of this characteristic. Note: the broader M10b cluster includes cosmic-evil content (M10b-B-VCG-01 — the evil one, which belongs to Characteristic 2), but that is outside Characteristic 1's evidence scope.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Yes. VCG-01 (13V) documents this directly. Eph 6:16 (vc=14428 — VCG-01): "the flaming darts of the evil one" target the inner person — the constitutionally vulnerable inner person is the target of adversarial attack. Mat 13:19 (vc=14435 — VCG-01): the evil one snatches away the word sown in the heart — the heart's inner state of insufficient understanding makes it a site of adversarial attack. 1Jo 5:18 (vc=14432 — VCG-01): the one born of God is shielded from the evil one's touch — implying that the unprotected inner person is accessible to the evil one. The constitutionally evil inner state creates a vulnerability that adversarial powers exploit.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (S)

The evidence does not directly address adversarial spiritual powers in relation to abomination-as-moral-character-failure. The characteristic is framed as arising from within human inner moral character (the crooked heart, the arrogant heart, the dishonest practice) — not as the result of adversarial spiritual attack or exploitation. The adversarial dimension that appeared in CHAR-2 (VCG-01 — the evil one targeting the heart) is absent from CHAR-3's 40-verse corpus. This silence is noted explicitly.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Yes. The idolatrous objects and the spiritual powers behind them (the foreign deities) function as adversarial influences drawing the heart away from God. Deu 7:25-26 (vc=1682/65927 — VCG-02): the idol ensnares and makes the person "devoted to destruction" — the idol-object as a spiritually dangerous entrapment. Deu 12:31 (vc=1683 — VCG-02): "every abominable thing that the Lord hates they have done for their gods" — the foreign gods are the beneficiaries of the misdirected devotion; they function as adversarial powers competing with the covenant God. The characteristic is therefore inherently a site of adversarial spiritual activity — the idol-objects and the spiritual powers they represent are drawing the human devotion-capacity away from God.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Yes, partially. Zec 10:2 (VCG-01) shows the spiritual-being dimension: household gods and diviners produce the a.ven (nonsense, empty consolation, false dreams) that leaves the community wandering without a shepherd — this is adversarial spiritual activity generating iniquity-as-trouble in the community. 1Sa 15:23 (VCG-02): rebellion/presumption compared to divination — the self-assertion of the human will against God's word is analogised to divination (an adversarial spiritual practice). The characteristic is not primarily framed as a site of adversarial attack in this corpus, but the VCG-01 evidence shows adversarial spiritual guidance (false prophets, household gods) as one channel through which a.ven trouble is generated in the community.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Yes. Rev 13:6 (vc=14356 — VCG-01) is the primary adversarial evidence: the beast (an adversarial figure) is the agent of sustained blasphemy against God, his name, his dwelling, and heaven's inhabitants. The beast represents the concentration of adversarial spiritual opposition to God expressed through speech. The characteristic is thus not merely a human moral failure but finds its most intense expression in the adversarial cosmic-eschatological figure of the beast whose primary weapon is blasphemous speech. The characteristic is constitutively adversarial in its VCG-01 dimension.

---

##### T4.6.3 — Is this characteristic communicated, strengthened, or mediated through angelic ministry in the evidence?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (S)

The evidence is silent on angelic ministry in relation to wickedness-as-settled-person-identity. No verse in the 190-verse corpus addresses angelic communication, strengthening, or mediation of this characteristic in either direction (angelic support for righteousness against wickedness, or angelic involvement in the characteristic's operation). This is explicitly noted as silence.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (S)

The 90-verse corpus does not evidence angelic ministry as a communicator, strengthener, or mediator of evil as constitutional inner nature. The adversarial dimension (VCG-01) addresses the evil one / spiritual forces of evil, not angelic ministry in the positive sense. No verse in the corpus shows angelic ministry in relation to this characteristic in either direction. This is explicitly noted.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The only angelic presence in the corpus is in Eze 9:4 (vc=1698 — VCG-04): the angel instructed to mark those who grieve over abominations. The angelic ministry here is protective toward those whose conscience recoils from abomination — not a mediation or strengthening of the characteristic itself but a divine response to it through angelic agency. The angelic role is the divine identification of those who do not share the abominable character. This is the sole evidence of angelic ministry in relation to this characteristic.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (S)

The 99-verse corpus does not evidence angelic ministry in relation to the characteristic (Eze 9:4 from CHAR-3's corpus — the angelic marking of the grieving — does not appear in CHAR-4's evidence set). The characteristic is not evidenced as communicated, strengthened, or mediated through angelic ministry within this corpus. This silence is noted.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (S)

The 79-verse corpus does not evidence angelic ministry in relation to iniquity as active scheming. No verse shows the characteristic as communicated, strengthened, or mediated through angelic activity. This silence is noted.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (S)

The 17-verse corpus does not evidence angelic ministry in relation to evil expressed through speech. The plagues in Rev 16 are administered by angels (Rev 16:2 etc. in the broader context), but the characteristic itself (blasphemy in response to the plagues) is not communicated, strengthened, or mediated through angelic ministry. The characteristic is generated entirely from within human or adversarial-cosmic volitional sources.

---

##### T4.6.4 — If the evidence is silent on the spiritual beings interface, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The evidence is silent on the spiritual beings interface for Characteristic 1 (T4.6.1–T4.6.3 above). This is noted explicitly. The spiritual-beings dimension is not part of the evidential territory this characteristic's corpus addresses.

## T5 — Transformation and Trajectory (21 prompts)

---

### T5

#### T5.1 — Nature of Transformation

##### T5.1.1 — Does this characteristic produce transformation in the person — and if so, does it change the person's condition, the person's orientation to their condition, or both?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The evidence shows that wickedness-as-settled-person-identity produces two types of transformation: (1) internal constitutional transformation — the sustained operation of the characteristic progressively consolidates the person's inner orientation and deepens their moral blindness (Pro 4:19 — deepening darkness; Isa 26:10 — incorrigibility under grace; Dan 12:10 — inability to understand at the eschatological moment). Both condition (the person's inner state — from partial to total moral closure) and orientation (the directional bent of the will — deepening away from God) are transformed. (2) The reversible transformation of the wicked person who turns: the Ezekiel corpus (VCG-07, Eze 18:21-27; 33:12-19) documents a transformation of orientation (the will turns from wickedness to justice) that produces a transformation of condition (life rather than death). The characteristic thus produces transformations in both directions depending on whether the volitional dynamic is hardening (deepening the characteristic) or reversing it (departing from it).

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The characteristic produces transformation primarily in the person's condition rather than orientation moment-by-moment. The tree-nature metaphor (Mat 7:17-18 — VCG-02) frames the characteristic as a condition — the diseased tree's condition determines its fruit. Transformation of the condition is what the evidence calls for: Heb 10:22 (vc=14426 — VCG-06) — the evil conscience sprinkled clean is a transformation of the conscience's constitutional condition; Act 3:26 (vc=14410 — VCG-05) — turning from wickedness through divine blessing is a transformation of the inner orientation away from the constitutional evil; Jam 1:21 (vc=14368 — VCG-05) — stripping away rampant wickedness and receiving the implanted word changes both the condition (emptied of the rampant wickedness) and the orientation (receptive to the word). The evidence shows the characteristic producing transformation of condition primarily, with consequent reorientation.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The characteristic produces transformation of both condition and orientation, depending on direction. In the deepening direction: sustained commission of abomination transforms the inner condition (conscience increasingly silenced — Jer 6:15; 8:12 — VCG-04 — "did not know how to blush") and the inner orientation (Pro 13:19 — vc=1687 — VCG-05: the will so bonded to evil that turning from it is experienced as abominable). In the redemptive direction: when memory is restored (Eze 36:31 — vc=1681 — VCG-04: "then you will remember… and you will loathe yourselves"), both condition (conscience reactivated) and orientation (self-loathing replacing self-justification) are transformed. Eze 14:6 (vc=65984 — VCG-04): "repent and turn away from your idols, and turn away your faces from all your abominations" — the commanded turning transforms both orientation (the will's direction) and condition (the person who has turned is no longer oriented toward abomination).

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The characteristic produces transformation of both condition and orientation. Hos 9:10 (vc=1632 — VCG-04): "they became detestable like the thing they loved" — condition is transformed: the person's own inner character-quality shifts toward the image of what they worship. Eze 11:21 (vc=1631/65982 — VCG-05): "heart goes after their detestable things" — orientation is transformed: the heart's directional faculty is re-oriented toward idols. The progressive deepening evidence (Eze 8:13; 8:15 — VCG-05: "still greater abominations") shows both condition (progressively more corrupted) and orientation (progressively more firmly directed toward idols) transforming together over time. The Ezekiel restoration (Eze 37:23 — VCG-05) also documents transformation of both condition ("I will save them and cleanse them") and orientation ("they shall not defile themselves anymore with their idols").

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The characteristic produces transformation of both condition and orientation. Condition: Psa 36:3 (vc=38234 — VCG-04): "he has ceased to act wisely and do good" — the person's condition shifts from wisdom-capable to wisdom-displaced; Pro 30:20 (vc=38222 — VCG-04): the conscience-deadened state is a transformed condition. Orientation: Psa 119:133 (vc=38227 — VCG-04): iniquity seeking dominion — the will's orientation progressively conforms to iniquity's direction; Pro 17:4 (vc=38219 — VCG-03): the evildoer's inner ear preferentially oriented toward wicked lips — an orientation-transformation. The transformative arc documented in T2.8.1 (worn inner path, conscience silenced) shows both condition (what the person is capable of) and orientation (what direction they face) being reshaped by sustained iniquity.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The characteristic produces transformation of both condition and orientation in VCG-01. Rev 16:9 → 16:11 → 16:21 (VCG-01): the sequence across three plague events shows progressive solidification — the will's anti-God orientation becomes more fixed, the condition of hardness deepens. The orientation is transformed in the direction of entrenched defiance: from potentially responding to judgment (initial contact) toward the settled state of cursing as reflex response. Condition: Jude 10 (vc=14355 — VCG-01): "destroyed by all that they, like unreasoning animals, understand instinctively" — the sustained characteristic produces a condition of self-destruction through sub-rational instinct: the person's constitutional condition is being destroyed by what they do not understand. For VCG-03's targets: the falsely accused's condition is one of maintained good conscience (1Pe 3:16 — VCG-03) — the counter-formation.

---

##### T5.1.2 — Is the transformation produced by this characteristic reversible or irreversible in the verse evidence?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The evidence presents both reversible and irreversible trajectories. The reversible trajectory is documented through the Ezekiel repentance corpus (VCG-07): Eze 18:21-22 — "if a wicked person turns away from all his sins… he shall surely live, he shall not die"; Eze 33:14-16 — the death-sentence is lifted when the wicked turns. The reversal is volitional, concrete (restitution acts — Eze 33:15), and effective (life results — Eze 33:19). The irreversible trajectory appears in: Isa 26:10 (VCG-05 — the wicked who cannot learn righteousness even under grace); Dan 12:10 (VCG-05 — "none of the wicked shall understand" — eschatological hardening); Pro 5:22 (VCG-06 — the bondage of the wicked's own cords). The evidence does not present a fixed point at which reversibility becomes definitively impossible, but the eschatological texts (Dan 12:10; Psa 9:5; Mal 4:3) imply a final termination after which reversal is no longer in view.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The evidence presents transformation as reversible in principle, through divine action. Act 3:26 (vc=14410 — VCG-05): "to bless you by turning every one of you from your wickedness" — divine blessing produces the turn from the constitutional evil; the characteristic is not permanently fixed. Heb 10:22 (vc=14426 — VCG-06): the evil conscience can be "sprinkled clean" — this is a real transformation of the constitutional condition. Tit 3:3 (vc=14367 — VCG-05) describes a "former" state of malice and envy now replaced — the transformation is evidenced as historically accomplished in the community being addressed. However, 2Ti 3:13 (vc=14451 — VCG-06) shows the trajectory without divine intervention: "from bad to worse" — the characteristic moves toward increasing irreversibility. The pattern is: reversible through divine transformative action; self-reinforcing toward increasing irreversibility without it.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The evidence presents transformation as reversible in principle through divine action. Eze 14:6 (vc=65984 — VCG-04) explicitly calls for turning from abominations — the reversal is commanded, implying it is possible. Eze 36:31 (vc=1681 — VCG-04): divine action restores memory, which produces self-loathing and conscience-reawakening — the transformation of the silenced conscience is reversible through divine initiative. The sustained silencing of conscience (Jer 6:15; 8:12 — VCG-04) represents the trajectory toward irreversibility — not an achieved permanent state but a deepening hardening. Rev 21:27 (vc=22 — VCG-05) and Eze 44:13 (vc=66003 — VCG-04) name eschatological-terminal consequences (permanent exclusion, permanent shame-bearing) that imply a final irreversibility at the eschatological horizon. The pattern is: reversible through divine action in the present; trajectory toward irreversibility without such action; eschatological finality at the terminus.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The evidence presents the transformation as reversible through divine action. Eze 37:23 (vc=65913 — VCG-05): "I will save them from all the backslidings in which they have sinned, and will cleanse them" — divine reversal of the characteristic's transformation. 2Ch 34:33 (vc=65946 — VCG-03): Josiah's removal of all abominations enabled sustained devotion — the communal transformation is reversible through reform. Jer 4:1 (vc=65903 — VCG-04): "If you return… If you remove your detestable things from my presence" — the condition for reversal is stated as achievable. The trajectory without divine intervention is toward irreversibility: Jer 44:22 (vc=65967 — VCG-04): the Lord "could no longer bear" — suggesting a threshold beyond which judgment rather than restoration becomes the primary trajectory. Reversible through divine action; moving toward irreversibility without it.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The evidence presents the transformation as reversible through divine action and human volitional response. Isa 55:7 (vc=38200 — VCG-02): "let the wicked forsake his way, and the unrighteous man his thoughts; let him return to the Lord, that he may have compassion on him, and to our God, for he will abundantly pardon" — reversal is both commanded and promised as achievable. Job 36:10 (vc=38215 — VCG-04): "He opens their ears to instruction and commands that they return from iniquity" — divine action enables reversal. Jer 4:14 (vc=38205 — VCG-02): "wash your heart from evil, that you may be saved" — the commanded washing implies reversibility. However, the terminus of the sustained trajectory (Psa 36:12 — vc=38233 — VCG-04: "evildoers lie fallen; they are thrust down, unable to rise") and Psa 92:7 (VCG-03: "doomed to destruction forever") describe a point of irrecoverability — irreversibility at the eschatological terminus of the trajectory without intervention.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The VCG-01 evidence presents the hardened-blasphemy trajectory as moving toward irreversibility. Rev 16:9/11/21 (VCG-01): three successive escalating judgments produce no repentance — the reversibility becomes progressively less available as each judgment deepens the hardening. The Revelation context (eschatological judgment) implies a final terminus: the plagues are the last judgments; if they produce no repentance, the trajectory is terminally fixed. However, for VCG-03: 1Pe 2:12 (vc=14377 — VCG-03): some false accusers "may see your good deeds and glorify God on the day of visitation" — partial reversibility is possible for at least some false accusers; their false speech is not permanently fixed. The distinction is between VCG-01's eschatological hardened trajectory (effectively irreversible at that terminus) and VCG-02/03's more reversible social-false-speech.

---

##### T5.1.3 — If the evidence is silent on transformation, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The evidence is not silent; both reversible and deepening-toward-irreversible transformations are documented (T5.1.1–T5.1.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The evidence is not silent on transformation; it is richly evidenced (T5.1.1–T5.1.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The evidence is not silent on transformation (T5.1.1–T5.1.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The evidence is not silent on transformation (T5.1.1–T5.1.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The evidence is not silent on transformation (T5.1.1–T5.1.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The evidence is not silent on transformation (T5.1.1–T5.1.2). This prompt is satisfied.

---

#### T5.2 — Sequence of Inner States

##### T5.2.1 — Does the verse evidence describe a sequence of inner states through which this characteristic moves the person — a before, during, and after?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Yes. The evidence from multiple VCGs maps a discernible sequence of inner states. Drawing on VCG-07 (directional orientation) and VCG-06 (instability and self-destruction), the sequence is: (1) Initial volitional entry — "do not enter the path of the wicked" (Pro 4:14) — the first stage is a choice; (2) Settled orientation — the person "walks in counsel of the wicked, stands in the way of sinners, sits in the seat of scoffers" (Psa 1:1 — a progressively deepening alignment); (3) Active God-exclusion — practical atheism consolidates (Psa 10:4; 10:13 — "all his thoughts are 'There is no God'"); (4) Inner instability and self-bondage — the characteristic generates its own cords (Pro 5:22), produces chronic dread (Pro 10:24), and inner torment (Job 15:20); (5) Final dissolution — "the wicked will be no more" (Psa 37:10), name rots (Pro 10:7), reduced to ashes (Mal 4:3). This sequence is not perfectly ordered in every verse but the pattern is discernible across the 190V corpus.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Yes. The evidence maps discernible sequential patterns. The deterioration sequence: (1) constitutional evil baseline (Mat 7:11 — VCG-02 — "you who are evil"); (2) settled inner malice and vice-saturation (Rom 1:29 — VCG-05 — "filled with all manner"); (3) defiled conscience making approach to God impossible (Heb 10:22 — VCG-06); (4) progressive deterioration (2Ti 3:13 — VCG-06 — "from bad to worse"). The remedial sequence: (1) exposure and conviction (Act 8:22 — VCG-05 — "repent of this wickedness"); (2) active stripping away (Jam 1:21 — VCG-05 — "put away all filthiness and rampant wickedness"); (3) receptive receiving (Jam 1:21 — VCG-05 — "receive with meekness the implanted word"); (4) cleansed constitutional state (Heb 10:22 — VCG-06 — "hearts sprinkled clean from an evil conscience"); (5) genuine approach to God restored.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Yes. VCG-04 (11 verses) is specifically the conscience-sequence evidence, documenting the characteristic's inner-state progression. The deepening sequence: (1) inner moral knowledge present but conscience beginning to be suppressed — Deu 27:15 (vc=65937 — VCG-04): the person sets up the idol in secret while knowing it is wrong; (2) abomination committed with partial conscience-engagement; (3) full conscience-silencing — Jer 6:15 (vc=1680 — VCG-04); Jer 8:12 (vc=1696 — VCG-04): "not at all ashamed; they did not know how to blush"; (4) accumulated weight — Eze 44:13 (vc=66003 — VCG-04): abominations as permanent burden; (5) eschatological exclusion — Rev 21:27 (vc=22 — VCG-05). The restoration sequence (Ezekiel): (1) divine action restores memory — Eze 36:31 (vc=1681); (2) self-loathing emerges; (3) repentance-command — Eze 14:6 (vc=65984); (4) turning from abominations.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Yes. The Ezekiel VCG-05 corpus (43V) documents the sequence with particular intensity. The deepening sequence: (1) initial volitional attraction and choice — Isa 66:3 (vc=1633 — VCG-04): "they have chosen their own ways"; (2) heart and soul attachment forming — Eze 11:21 (vc=1631 — VCG-05): heart going after detestable things; (3) eye-feasting habit entrenching — Eze 20:7-8 (vc=1634; 65911 — VCG-05): eyes feasting, unwilling to cast away; (4) moral gravity lost — Eze 8:17 (vc=65980 — VCG-05): treating abomination as trivial; (5) progressive deepening — Eze 8:13; 8:15 (VCG-05): still greater abominations; (6) constitutional transformation — Hos 9:10 (vc=1632 — VCG-04): becoming detestable; (7) memory lost — Eze 16:22 (vc=65985 — VCG-05): not remembering origins; (8) divine withdrawal — Eze 5:11 (vc=65969 — VCG-05); (9) judgment — Eze 5:9 (vc=65968 — VCG-05).

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Yes. The evidence documents a deepening sequence across the VCGs. (1) Initial volitional entry: Job 36:21 (vc=38216 — VCG-04): "this you have chosen rather than affliction" — the will chooses iniquity over the harder righteous path. (2) Active nocturnal devising: Psa 36:4 (vc=38235 — VCG-02): "plots trouble while on his bed" — the cognitive scheming mode is established. (3) Heart accumulating iniquity: Psa 41:6 (vc=38236 — VCG-04): "his heart gathers iniquity" — the condition of accumulation. (4) Wisdom displaced: Psa 36:3 (vc=38234 — VCG-04): "ceased to act wisely and do good." (5) Conscience deadened: Pro 30:20 (vc=38222 — VCG-04): "I have done no wrong." (6) Iniquity seeking dominion: Psa 119:133 (vc=38227 — VCG-04): the will increasingly under iniquity's control. (7) Terminal collapse: Psa 36:12 (vc=38233 — VCG-04): "fallen… unable to rise."

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Yes. VCG-01 documents the sequence with unusual explicitness. The Rev 16 sequence (vc=14352; 14350; 14353 — VCG-01): (1) First judgment (scorching heat) → cursing God's name + refusal to repent or give glory (Rev 16:9); (2) Second judgment (darkness, pain, sores) → cursing the God of heaven + refusal to repent of deeds (Rev 16:11); (3) Third judgment (catastrophic hail) → cursing God for the plague because it was so severe (Rev 16:21). The sequence shows: escalating judgment → escalating defiance, with each stage showing the will more fixed in its anti-God orientation. Jude 8 (vc=14354 — VCG-01): the prior state that enables blasphemy: sensory self-indulgence → authority-rejection → blasphemy — a three-stage inner sequence from indulgence through rejection to verbal defiance.

---

##### T5.2.2 — What are those states, and what does the sequence reveal about how this characteristic works?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The states are: (1) volitional alignment (Psa 1:1 stages — walking, standing, sitting with the wicked); (2) practical atheism (Psa 10:4 — God excluded from thought-life); (3) active harm-generation (VCG-03 directed hostility; VCG-08 speech-as-weapon; VCG-09 appetite-for-evil); (4) inner instability intensifying (VCG-06 — chronic dread, inner torment, self-bondage); (5) eschatological dissolution (VCG-05 — judgment, erasure of name, ashes). The sequence reveals that wickedness-as-settled-person-identity is a progressive deepening rather than a static condition: it moves from an initial volitional choice through increasingly settled inner states toward a terminus of dissolution. The sequence also reveals that the characteristic's internal logic is self-reinforcing — each stage makes the next stage more probable and the reversal more difficult.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The deterioration states are: constitutional baseline evil → accumulated vice-saturation → defiled conscience → progressive deterioration. The remedial states are: convicted of constitutional evil → active renunciation → receptive receiving of word → cleansed conscience → restored divine access. The sequence reveals two dynamics. (1) The deterioration dynamic is self-reinforcing and centrifugal: each stage deepens the constitutional condition without external intervention. (2) The remedial dynamic requires external initiative (divine blessing — Act 3:26; the sprinkled blood — Heb 10:22; the implanted word — Jam 1:21) at each stage — the transformation is not self-generated but grace-enabled. The sequences reveal the characteristic as constitutionally unable to reverse itself: it can deteriorate on its own momentum but requires external divine action to be reversed.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The deepening states are: knowing conscience (inner knowledge while setting up the abomination in secret — Deu 27:15 — VCG-04) → conscience-silencing (no shame or blushing — Jer 6:15; 8:12 — VCG-04) → accumulated inner burden (Eze 44:13 — VCG-04) → eschatological exclusion (Rev 21:27 — VCG-05). The restoration states are: divine memory-restoration → self-loathing (Eze 36:31 — VCG-04) → call to turn (Eze 14:6 — VCG-04) → restored relational access. The sequence reveals two key analytical insights: (1) the initial state is not conscience-absent but conscience-present-yet-overridden — the person in Deu 27:15 knows; (2) the conscience is the key inner faculty whose trajectory determines the sequence — its silencing deepens the abominable trajectory; its reawakening initiates the restoration trajectory. The sequence is conscience-driven.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The states: volitional choice → heart/soul attachment → eye-feasting habit → moral gravity lost → progressive deepening → constitutional transformation → memory suppressed → divine withdrawal → judgment. The restoration sequence (Eze 37:23; Jer 4:1 — VCG-04/05): divine action → cleansing → memory restored (Eze 6:9 — VCG-05) → self-loathing → removal of detestable things → return to covenant relationship. The sequence reveals that idolatrous abomination is a self-deepening trajectory: each stage makes departure more difficult (the eye-feasting habit reinforces the attachment; moral gravity lost removes the inner check; constitutional transformation reshapes character toward the idol). The restoration sequence requires divine initiative precisely because the self-deepening dynamic cannot be reversed from within.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The states: volitional choice → nocturnal devising established → heart accumulating iniquity → wisdom displaced → conscience deadened → iniquity's dominion → irrecoverable collapse. The restoration sequence: Job 36:10 (VCG-04): divine ear-opening → return from iniquity; Isa 55:7 (VCG-02): forsaking of way and thoughts → return to Lord → abundant pardon; Jer 4:14 (VCG-02): heart-washing → salvation. The sequence reveals that the characteristic is self-deepening: each state makes the next worse and makes voluntary departure less likely. The conscience-deadening state (Pro 30:20 — VCG-04) is particularly significant: once the conscience no longer registers wrongdoing, the person lacks the inner arresting signal that would initiate departure. Only divine intervention (Job 36:10 — ear-opening) can restart the departure-mechanism at that stage.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The deepening states in VCG-01: (1) Jude 8: self-indulgent sensory reliance → authority-rejection → blasphemy. (2) Rev 16:9: scorching judgment → curse God's name, refuse repentance/glory. (3) Rev 16:11: pain and sores → curse God, refuse repentance of deeds. (4) Rev 16:21: catastrophic hail → curse God because the plague is severe. The sequence reveals two critical findings: (a) The Jude sequence shows how blasphemy develops from prior inner conditions (self-indulgence, authority-rejection) — it is not spontaneous but prepared by prior inner postures; (b) the Rev 16 sequence shows that escalating divine judgment intensifies rather than reduces the defiance — the will becomes more, not less, hardened under pressure. This is the characteristic's most analytically distinctive feature: it is self-reinforcing under the very conditions designed to break it.

---
