**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The evidence is not silent; sequence is evidenced (T5.2.1–T5.2.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The evidence is not silent; sequences are identified (T5.2.1–T5.2.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The evidence is not silent on sequence (T5.2.1–T5.2.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The evidence is not silent on sequence (T5.2.1–T5.2.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The evidence is not silent on sequence (T5.2.1–T5.2.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The sequence is richly evidenced (T5.2.1–T5.2.2). This prompt is satisfied.

---

#### T5.3 — Mechanism of Change

##### T5.3.1 — What mechanism does this characteristic use to produce change in the person — discipline, encounter, gradual formation, sudden transformation, or something else?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The characteristic's primary mechanism of inner change is progressive self-consolidation through repetition and deepening volitional commitment. The evidence from VCG-06 and VCG-07 converges on this: Pro 5:22 (VCG-06) — "the iniquities of the wicked ensnare him, held fast in the cords of his sin" — each act of wickedness tightens the cord; Pro 10:16 (VCG-09) — "the gain of the wicked leads to sin" — the fruit of wickedness becomes its next fuel. The mechanism is a feedback loop: the inner disposition generates harmful acts, the harmful acts reinforce and deepen the inner disposition, and the deepened disposition is less accessible to correction (Isa 26:10 — "he does not learn righteousness"). The mechanism does not require dramatic encounter or discipline — it operates through the quiet accumulation of volitional commitment to the wicked way.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The deterioration mechanism is progressive self-consolidation through accumulation and spread. 2Ti 3:13 (vc=14451 — VCG-06): "from bad to worse" — each stage of deterioration feeds the next without an external input required. The leaven metaphor (1Cor 5:8 — VCG-05): leaven works by spreading through the whole batch; no additional external leaven is needed — the mechanism is internal propagation through existing constitutional material. Mat 12:45 (vc=65879 — VCG-06): the vacated inner space attracting seven more evil spirits — the mechanism here is vacuum-filling; the absence of positive inner occupation enables the characteristic's deepening. These three mechanisms (progressive self-reinforcement, leaven-spreading, vacuum-filling) are distinct modes of the same self-consolidating dynamic.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Three distinct mechanisms are documented. (1) Conscience-silencing through repeated practice: sustained commission of abomination without inner arrest progressively silences the conscience's shame-response (Jer 6:15; 8:12 — VCG-04: the trajectory from some shame to none). (2) Accumulated inner burden: the abominations become a weight that the person carries (Eze 44:13 — vc=66003 — VCG-04: "they shall bear their shame and the abominations that they have committed") — the weight of past abomination is a mechanical burden on the inner person. (3) Community saturation: the communal spread (Ezr 9:11 — vc=66005 — VCG-04: filled from end to end) shows a mechanism of environmental penetration where the abominations of others saturate the communal space and become a force that shapes subsequent persons within it.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Three distinct deepening mechanisms. (1) Visual-desire habit: Eze 20:7-8 (vc=1634; 65911 — VCG-05): eyes feasting on detestable things — repeated visual engagement with idol-objects reinforces inner attachment progressively; (2) Constitutional assimilation: Hos 9:10 (vc=1632 — VCG-04): "became detestable like the thing they loved" — the person is constitutionally shaped by what they worship; the mechanism is the spiritual-formative power of devoted attention to an object; (3) Communal-environmental embedding: Ezr 9:1 (vc=65949 — VCG-03): failure to separate from peoples with abominations — the social environment saturated with idolatrous practice shapes participants through communal formation; Deu 20:18 (vc=65932 — VCG-02): the nations teaching abominable practices — social teaching as the mechanism.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Three primary mechanisms. (1) Habitual practise deepening the worn path: Job 22:15 (vc=38210 — VCG-04): "the old way that wicked men have trod" — repeated practice deposits a worn inner trajectory that becomes the default; the more the path is trodden, the more ingrained it becomes. (2) Gradual conscience-silencing through repeated commission without arrest: Pro 30:20 (vc=38222 — VCG-04): the terminus of repeated iniquity without conscience-engagement. (3) Associational formation: Job 34:8 (vc=38214 — VCG-04): "travels in company with evildoers" — sustained chosen proximity to those who work iniquity shapes the inner person progressively toward the same character.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Two primary mechanisms of change (in the deepening direction). (1) Progressive will-hardening under judgment pressure: Rev 16:9/11/21 (VCG-01) — each divine judgment that fails to produce repentance deepens the will's hardening, leaving it more fixed in its defiant orientation. The mechanism is judgment-interaction: the divine judgment is the external stimulus; the will's defiant response reinforces and deepens its own hardness through each iteration. (2) Progressive cognitive regression through contempt-filling: Jude 10 (vc=14355 — VCG-01) — blasphemy directed at what is not understood reveals a mechanism of contempt substituting for understanding; each act of blaspheming what is not comprehended deepens the pattern of contempt-as-substitute-for-understanding, reducing cognitive operation toward the instinctual level.

---

##### T5.3.2 — Does the evidence distinguish between mechanisms in different contexts?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Yes. Two distinct mechanisms are documented. (1) The hardening mechanism (ongoing possession) — self-consolidating feedback (Pro 5:22; Pro 10:16), progressive perceptive closure (Pro 4:19; Isa 26:10; Dan 12:10), and deepening estrangement from God (Pro 15:29). (2) The reversal mechanism (potential departure from the characteristic) — which operates through the volitional turn in response to prophetic warning (Eze 3:18; 33:11), the acknowledgment of wickedness before God (Jer 14:20 — re.sha corpus, VCG-11), and the concrete acts of restitution (Eze 33:15). The hardening mechanism is quiet and internal; the reversal mechanism is dramatic, volitional, and requires external prophetic intervention (the divine call to turn — Eze 33:11; Isa 55:7). These are distinct mechanisms by context.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Yes. The evidence distinguishes: (1) the hardening mechanism (self-reinforcing deterioration — 2Ti 3:13 — VCG-06) for the person without divine intervention; (2) the leaven-spreading mechanism (1Cor 5:8 — VCG-05) for the community context — the characteristic spreads through social contagion within a community; (3) the vacuum-filling mechanism (Mat 12:45 — VCG-06) for the individual inner space that has been emptied of evil but not filled with good. The remedial mechanisms are also distinct: repentance and prayer (Act 8:22 — VCG-05), stripping away and word-reception (Jam 1:21 — VCG-05), and cleansing through sprinkled blood (Heb 10:22 — VCG-06) are different mechanisms for different aspects of the same transformation.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Yes. The individual mechanism is primarily conscience-silencing through repeated volitional commitment to abominable practice (VCG-04 — Jer 6:15; 8:12). The communal mechanism is environmental saturation — the abominations of a people fill their shared space and become the normative moral environment for subsequent generations (Ezr 9:11 — VCG-04). The worship-level mechanism (VCG-03) is the contamination of religious approach by inner corruption — the abominable inner person's act of approaching God makes the act itself additionally abominable. The restoration mechanism (Eze 36:31; 14:6 — VCG-04) is divine memory-restoration producing conscience-reawakening and the called-for volitional redirection. The mechanisms differ by context: individual-conscience, community-environment, worship-contamination, divine-restoration.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Yes. Individual mechanisms: visual-desire habit (Eze 20:7-8 — VCG-05) and constitutional assimilation (Hos 9:10 — VCG-04) — operating in the individual inner-being. Communal mechanisms: royal institutionalization (VCG-03 — the king's will installing abominations communally), social teaching (Deu 20:18 — VCG-02), and marital-relational influence (1Ki 11:5 — VCG-03). The restoration mechanisms are also distinct: individual (Jer 4:1 — VCG-04: individual removal of detestable things from the divine presence) and communal-royal (2Ch 34:33 — VCG-03: Josiah's comprehensive national removal). The mechanisms vary by whether the characteristic is operating at the individual inner-being level or the communal-institutional level.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Yes. The individual-internal mechanism (VCG-02/04): habitual nocturnal devising deepens the cognitive-scheming habit (Mic 2:1 — VCG-02 → established pattern). The social-associational mechanism (VCG-03/04): the company of evildoers shapes the inner character through relational influence (Job 34:8 — VCG-04; Psa 141:4 — VCG-04: inclined by company). The institutional-systemic mechanism (VCG-02): the professional writer of iniquitous decrees (Isa 10:1 — VCG-02) is shaped by their institutional role — the act of repeatedly writing oppression deposits an iniquity-orientation into the professional identity. The restoration mechanism (Isa 55:7 — VCG-02; Job 36:10 — VCG-04) is: divine instruction-opening + volitional response (forsaking, washing, returning).

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Yes. VCG-01 (eschatological judgment context): mechanism is judgment-driven will-hardening (Rev 16 — VCG-01) and contempt-filling cognitive regression (Jude 10 — VCG-01). VCG-02 (community conduct context): mechanism is conduct-shaped testimony — the moral state of the person produces the social speech consequence (Rom 2:24 — VCG-02: moral failure → God's name blasphemed); the mechanism is inside-out, from moral character to social-verbal effect. VCG-03 (social-legal false accusation context): mechanism is observation-and-verdict — the hostile observer evaluates and verbally charges (Joh 18:30 — VCG-03: accusers observe → false verdict delivered verbally). Three distinct mechanisms by VCG context.

---

##### T5.3.3 — If the evidence is silent on mechanism, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The evidence is not silent; mechanisms are documented (T5.3.1–T5.3.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The evidence is not silent on mechanism (T5.3.1–T5.3.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Multiple mechanisms are evidenced (T5.3.1–T5.3.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Multiple mechanisms are evidenced (T5.3.1–T5.3.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Multiple mechanisms are evidenced (T5.3.1–T5.3.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Mechanisms are evidenced (T5.3.1–T5.3.2). This prompt is satisfied.

---

#### T5.4 — Suffering and Affliction

##### T5.4.1 — Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating in relation to suffering or affliction — as a response to it, a product of it, or a context for it?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Yes. The characteristic's relationship to suffering is multi-directional in the evidence. (1) The wicked person as the cause of suffering: VCG-03 (directed hostility — 22V) documents the wicked imposing suffering on the righteous and vulnerable: Psa 17:9 ("deadly enemies"), Psa 37:14 ("to slay those whose way is upright"), Job 16:11 ("casts me into the hands of the wicked"), Jer 5:26 (predatory trapping). (2) The wicked person as the recipient of suffering: VCG-06 (21V) documents the wicked person's characteristic inner suffering: Job 15:20 ("writhes in pain all his days"), Psa 32:10 ("many are the sorrows of the wicked"), Pro 10:24 ("what the wicked dreads will come upon him"). (3) The theodicy frame: VCG-10 (9V) addresses the paradox that the wicked sometimes appear to suffer less than the righteous — Job 21:7 ("why do the wicked live and grow mighty?").

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The evidence shows the characteristic producing suffering in others and being the context in which the righteous suffer. Mat 5:11 (vc=14455 — VCG-04): "evil against you falsely" — the constitutionally evil person's speech produces false accusation and persecution of the righteous. Act 17:5 (vc=14452 — VCG-04): "formed a mob, set the city in an uproar, and attacked the house of Jason" — the constitutional inner evil produces social violence and suffering. 2Th 3:2 (vc=14450 — VCG-06): prayer to "be delivered from wicked and evil men" — the constitutionally evil are the source of the suffering from which deliverance is sought. The characteristic itself is not shown as operating in response to suffering; rather, it generates suffering in the social sphere. Luk 6:35 (vc=14444 — VCG-04): "God is kind even to the evil" — God's kindness toward the constitutionally evil is not framed as suffering for them.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The evidence shows suffering as a consequence of abomination rather than as a context that deepens or produces it. Jer 6:15 (vc=1680 — VCG-04): "they shall fall among those who fall; at the time that I punish them, they shall be overthrown" — the shameless abomination-commission is followed by divine punishment-suffering as consequence. Jer 8:12 (vc=1696 — VCG-04): "they shall fall among the fallen; when I punish them, they shall be overthrown" — same pattern: abomination without shame → judgment-suffering. Eze 44:13 (vc=66003 — VCG-04): "they shall bear their shame and the abominations they have committed" — the burden carried is a form of ongoing inner suffering (shame) as consequence of past abomination. The characteristic generates suffering (both divine judgment and inner shame-burden) as its consequence, rather than being shaped by encountered suffering.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The characteristic generates suffering as its consequence rather than being shaped by it. Eze 5:9 (vc=65968 — VCG-05): "I will do with you what I have never yet done" — unprecedented suffering as the consequence of accumulated abominations. Eze 6:11 (vc=65970 — VCG-05): "they shall fall by the sword, by famine, and by pestilence" — the standard judgment-suffering consequences. Jer 44:22 (vc=65967 — VCG-04): "your land has become a desolation and a waste and a curse" — comprehensive suffering of land-desolation as consequence. Eze 6:9 (vc=1697 — VCG-05): the suffering of exile enables the survivors' memory-restoration and self-loathing — judgment-suffering here is instrumentalised by divine action to produce conscience-reactivation and the beginning of restoration.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Yes. VCG-01 (7V) is specifically the evidence of the characteristic's relationship to suffering — the trouble and affliction that the characteristic generates in victims. Psa 55:3 (vc=38188 — VCG-01): trouble "dropped upon" the psalmist by enemies bearing grudges. Psa 55:10 (vc=38239 — VCG-01): "iniquity and trouble are within" the city — communal suffering from embedded iniquity. Hab 1:3 (vc=38194 — VCG-01): the prophet made to "see iniquity" and "idly look at wrong; destruction and violence are before me" — forced witness of suffering caused by iniquity. The characteristic produces suffering in others (VCG-01), not as a response to suffering but as its direct generative output.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Yes. VCG-01 is specifically the suffering-judgment context: Rev 16:9 (vc=14352 — VCG-01): scorching heat causing suffering → curse God; Rev 16:11 (vc=14350 — VCG-01): "cursed the God of heaven for their pain and sores" — the pain and sores are the suffering; Rev 16:21 (vc=14353 — VCG-01): hailstones causing suffering → "they cursed God for the plague of the hail, because the plague was so severe." The characteristic operates specifically as a response to suffering in VCG-01 — suffering is the trigger for the blasphemous expression. For VCG-02/03 targets: 1Cor 4:13 (vc=14351 — VCG-02): the slandered apostle suffers reduction to "the scum of the world" — the characteristic causes suffering in its targets.

---

##### T5.4.2 — Does suffering deepen, test, reveal, or produce this characteristic in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The evidence shows suffering primarily revealing the characteristic rather than deepening it. Psa 34:21 (VCG-03): "affliction will slay the wicked" — suffering in the form of divine judgment is the mechanism through which wickedness is exposed and terminated, not deepened. Isa 26:10 (VCG-05) is the most direct statement: even when the wicked person is shown favour (a form of grace-under-suffering), "he does not learn righteousness" — the characteristic is revealed as impervious to the corrective function that suffering-and-favour might otherwise serve. Dan 12:10 (VCG-05) — the purification process (refinement through suffering) separates the wise from the wicked rather than changing the wicked — suffering reveals the characteristic's settled intransigence at the eschatological level.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The evidence addresses suffering's relationship to the characteristic primarily through revelation. The constitutionally evil person's response to exposure by testimony (Joh 7:7 — VCG-04: hatred of the witness) and to divine common grace (Luk 6:35 — VCG-04: receiving God's kindness without change) reveals the characteristic's depth rather than changing it. Mat 18:32 (vc=14442 — VCG-06): the wicked servant who received mercy (a form of relief from the suffering of debt) responded with hardness rather than mercy — the experience of grace-relief reveals and exposes the constitutional evil rather than addressing it. The evidence does not show suffering producing the characteristic, but does show it revealing the characteristic's depth.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The evidence shows suffering as revealing the characteristic rather than producing it. The divine punishment (Jer 6:15; 8:12 — VCG-04) exposes and confirms the verdict on the shameless commission of abomination — it reveals the divine assessment rather than producing a new inner condition. Eze 36:31 (vc=1681 — VCG-04) shows that divine restorative action (which may include the experience of exile-suffering) restores memory and produces self-loathing — here suffering in the context of the exile is the backdrop for the memory-restoration that reveals the abominable past. The suffering that accompanies the abomination-verdict does not create new abomination but confirms and discloses the existing inner condition.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Suffering primarily reveals the characteristic (through divine judgment that confirms and executes the abomination-verdict) and instrumentally enables restoration (the exile-suffering that enables memory-restoration in Eze 6:9 — VCG-05). Judgment-suffering does not deepen the characteristic; it confronts and exposes it. The suffering of exile is the context within which Eze 6:9 (VCG-05) shows the survivors remembering God and feeling self-loathing — the suffering becomes the instrument of conscience-reactivation. Suffering thus tests and reveals the depth of the characteristic's hold and, under divine use, becomes the mechanism for beginning departure from it.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The evidence shows suffering as a consequence of the characteristic rather than as its cause. The suffering in VCG-01 is what the characteristic inflicts on victims, not what deepens the schemer's iniquity. However, Hab 1:3 (vc=38194 — VCG-01) shows the prophet's suffering through forced witness of iniquity as a form of suffering that reveals the characteristic: "Why do you make me see iniquity?" — the witness-suffering discloses the depth of the characteristic's social penetration. Job 36:21 (vc=38216 — VCG-04): "you have chosen [iniquity] rather than affliction" — the fear of affliction/suffering is what drives some persons toward iniquity as the easier path; suffering here functions as a test that the person has failed by choosing iniquity instead.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Suffering deepens the characteristic in the hardened blasphemer (VCG-01). Rev 16:11 (vc=14350 — VCG-01): "in pain and sores they cursed God" — the pain does not soften but intensifies the defiant speech; suffering reveals the depth of the characteristic (how hardened the will is) while simultaneously deepening it (each pain-curse cycle entrenches the will further). The suffering reveals what is already present (the hardened will) and deepens what it reveals (by providing the occasion for further entrenching expression). For VCG-03 targets: the suffering of false accusation tests and reveals the quality of the falsely accused's inner life — 1Pe 3:16 (VCG-03): the good conscience maintained under slander is tested and revealed by the experience.

---

##### T5.4.3 — If the evidence is silent on the relationship to suffering, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The evidence is not silent; suffering is multiply evidenced in relation to this characteristic (T5.4.1–T5.4.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The evidence is not silent; suffering is addressed in T5.4.1–T5.4.2 above. This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The evidence is not silent on suffering; its relationship to the characteristic is addressed above (T5.4.1–T5.4.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The evidence is not silent on suffering; it is addressed in T5.4.1–T5.4.2. This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The evidence is not silent on suffering; it is documented through VCG-01 and T5.4.1–T5.4.2. This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The evidence is not silent on suffering; it is central to VCG-01 (T5.4.1–T5.4.2). This prompt is satisfied.

---

#### T5.5 — Formation and Sanctification

##### T5.5.1 — Does the verse evidence show this characteristic participating in the longer arc of character formation and sanctification — shaping the person over time toward greater likeness?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The characteristic participates in character formation in a negative sense: it is the pattern of formation that moves in the opposite direction from sanctification. The Psa 1:1 progressive alignment (walking → standing → sitting with the wicked) is a counter-formation sequence — each stage deepens the wicked orientation. Pro 4:14-19 (VCG-07): "do not enter the path of the wicked… the way of the wicked is like deep darkness; they do not know over what they stumble" — this is an anti-formation warning, describing the trajectory of formation into wickedness as progressive moral blindness. Positively, the Ezekiel repentance corpus (VCG-07) does describe a reverse-formation process: the wicked person turning toward just action and restitution (Eze 33:15) — this is a re-formation from wickedness toward righteousness, evidencing that the characteristic's formation process can be reversed through the same mechanism (sustained volitional action) that consolidated it.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The characteristic participates in formation in a negative sense: it is what the formation process must address and replace. Tit 3:3 (vc=14367 — VCG-05) provides the most direct formation-arc evidence: "for we ourselves were once foolish, disobedient, led astray, slaves to various passions and pleasures, passing our days in malice and envy" — this is a before-state in a full formation narrative that continues (Tit 3:4-7 outside this corpus) with divine renewal. The "former" framing places constitutional inner evil as the pre-formation state from which sanctification departs. The NT letters consistently address the characteristic as what must be "put away" in the formation process: Eph 4:31 (vc=14365 — VCG-05), Col 3:8 (vc=14366 — VCG-05), 1Pe 2:1 (vc=14369 — VCG-05) — these are formation imperatives that explicitly name the constitutional evil as the starting condition that sanctification must work against.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The characteristic participates in the formation arc as the negative pole — what must be turned from for sanctification to proceed. Eze 14:6 (vc=65984 — VCG-04): "repent and turn away from your idols, and turn away your faces from all your abominations" — the command to turn from abominations is a formation-initiating moment; formation begins with the turn from the abominable. Eze 9:4 (vc=1698 — VCG-04): those who sigh and groan over abominations are marked for protection — their conscience-alive posture is itself a formation indicator: they are in the process of being formed away from the abominable toward the upright. Pro 3:32 (vc=1686 — VCG-02): the upright who are in God's confidence represent the formed-character state toward which the characteristic's departure leads.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The characteristic participates in the formation arc as the primary counter-formation trajectory. Hos 9:10 (vc=1632 — VCG-04): "they became detestable like the thing they loved" — formation by the idol: the person is being formed toward the idol's image through sustained devotion. This is formation, but anti-formation in the sanctification sense — being formed toward what is abominable rather than toward God's likeness. The corrective formation trajectory: Eze 37:23 (vc=65913 — VCG-05): "I will save them from all the backslidings… and will cleanse them; and they shall be my people, and I will be their God" — the divine formation project re-establishes the covenantal identity that idolatrous abomination had displaced. The reform-narratives (VCG-03) document the formation-correction process: removing the abominations enables sustained following of the Lord (2Ch 34:33 — VCG-03).

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The characteristic participates in the formation arc as the primary counter-formation trajectory. Job 22:15 (vc=38210 — VCG-04): "the old way that wicked men have trod" — formation by sustained iniquity-practice is named as a worn path; this is character-formation but in the wrong direction. Job 4:8 (vc=38186 — VCG-04): "those who plow iniquity and sow trouble reap the same" — agricultural formation metaphor: the character one cultivates determines the harvest one receives. The sanctification arc appears in the restoration calls: Isa 55:7 (vc=38200 — VCG-02): forsaking iniquitous thoughts and returning to God is the beginning of positive formation. Jer 4:14 (vc=38205 — VCG-02): washing the heart from evil is the cleansing initiating reformed character.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The characteristic participates in the formation arc as its negative trajectory — the formation of the hardened will. Jude 8/10 (VCG-01): the inner sequence (self-indulgence → authority-rejection → blasphemy) shows character formation in the direction of the characteristic: the person is progressively formed toward the blasphemous posture through prior inner choices. The Rev 16 sequence (VCG-01) shows the terminus of this formation: a will so formed toward defiance that judgment cannot penetrate it. For those shaped by counter-formation: 1Pe 2:12 (vc=14377 — VCG-03) and 1Pe 3:16 (vc=14380 — VCG-03): the formation of good conscience and honourable conduct is the sanctification arc that the characteristic's recipients are called to maintain — the counter-formation to the characteristic's impact.

---

##### T5.5.2 — What does the evidence reveal about the role of this characteristic in that longer arc?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The characteristic's role in the formation arc is that of the counter-trajectory: it is the direction of movement that sanctification must arrest and reverse. The evidence presents it as what the person becomes in the absence of God-directed formation — the default drift of the will when left without the corrective of divine instruction and prophetic call. Eze 13:22 (VCG-07): false prophets "encourage the wicked, that he should not turn from his evil way to save his life" — the false formation environment enables the wicked trajectory; the true formation environment (prophetic call to turn) is the corrective. The characteristic in the formation arc marks the terminus of the downward trajectory and the starting point of the reversal.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The characteristic's role in the formation arc is as the starting condition and the persistent counter-force. Formation must begin where the constitutional evil resides (the heart — Act 8:22 — VCG-05; the conscience — Heb 10:22 — VCG-06) and work against its self-perpetuating momentum (2Ti 3:13 — VCG-06). The formation arc requires ongoing vigilance because the characteristic is the constitutional baseline: even believers are addressed in these formation imperatives (Eph 4:31; Col 3:8; 1Pe 2:1), showing the characteristic remains a formation challenge throughout the sanctification process. The characteristic is the formation arc's permanent point of reference — what is being replaced, addressed, and countered throughout.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The characteristic's role in the formation arc is as the primary inner-being obstacle and starting condition. Eze 36:31 (vc=1681 — VCG-04): the restored memory of abominations producing self-loathing is a formation event — the conscience must be reawakened to abomination's weight before the person can be formed away from it. The formation arc in this characteristic runs: abomination (with or without conscience function) → conscience reawakening (through divine action restoring memory) → self-loathing and grief → volitional turning (Eze 14:6 — VCG-04) → departure from abomination → movement toward uprightness. The characteristic is the formation arc's starting problem, and conscience-reawakening is the formation pivot.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Idolatrous abomination's role in the formation arc is as the primary rival-formation process: the soul is formed by what it is devoted to (Hos 9:10 — VCG-04: becoming like what is loved). This rival formation produces: moral numbness (Eze 8:17 — VCG-05), memory suppression (Eze 16:22 — VCG-05), constitutional transformation toward the idol (Hos 9:10 — VCG-04), and progressive deepening (Eze 8:13; 8:15 — VCG-05). In the sanctification arc, this characteristic occupies the starting condition that formation must work against and the formation mechanism that must be reversed: stop being formed by the idol; begin being formed by God. The divine cleansing (Eze 37:23 — VCG-05) initiates the re-formation process.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The characteristic's role in the formation arc is as the counter-formation process that must be arrested and reversed for sanctification to proceed. Job 36:10 (vc=38215 — VCG-04): the divine opening of the ear is the formation-pivot moment — the transition from self-deepening iniquity to the beginning of return. Psa 125:5 (vc=38382 — VCG-03): "those who turn aside to their crooked ways the Lord will lead away with evildoers" — the continued formation in iniquity's direction terminates in separation from the community of the blameless. The sanctification arc requires active departure from the iniquitous formation-trajectory (Job 11:14 — VCG-04: "put it far away"; Jer 4:14 — VCG-02: "wash your heart"), showing that the characteristic's formation-power must be actively countered, not merely abandoned.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The characteristic's role in the formation arc is as the final terminal expression of the long formation of the hardened will. The Jude evidence (Jude 8 — VCG-01: self-indulgence → authority-rejection → blasphemy) shows that the characteristic is not a sudden onset but the culmination of a formation trajectory beginning with sensory self-indulgence. The Rev 16 sequence (VCG-01) shows the characteristic at the endpoint of that formation — where the will has been so consistently formed away from God that even maximum judgment cannot reverse it. In the sanctification arc, the characteristic marks the boundary of what formation away from God produces — and the counter-formation (good conscience, honourable conduct — 1Pe 2:12; 3:16 — VCG-03) is the alternative trajectory.

---

##### T5.5.3 — If the evidence is silent on formation and sanctification, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The evidence is not silent; the formation dimension is evidenced (T5.5.1–T5.5.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The evidence is not silent on formation; it is extensively evidenced (T5.5.1–T5.5.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The evidence is not silent; formation participation is evidenced (T5.5.1–T5.5.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Formation participation is extensively evidenced (T5.5.1–T5.5.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Formation participation is evidenced (T5.5.1–T5.5.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Formation participation is evidenced (T5.5.1–T5.5.2). This prompt is satisfied.

---

#### T5.6 — Eschatological Trajectory

##### T5.6.1 — Does the verse evidence point this characteristic toward an eschatological fullness — a future state toward which its present operation is oriented?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Yes. The evidence points wickedness-as-settled-person-identity toward an eschatological terminus — but one of dissolution rather than fullness. The eschatological evidence in VCG-05 is concentrated: Psa 9:5 — "you have blotted out their name forever and ever"; Psa 37:10 — "in a little while the wicked will be no more"; Isa 11:4 — "he shall kill the wicked" by the rod of his mouth; Mal 4:3 — "they will be ashes under the soles of your feet on the day when I act"; Dan 12:10 — the wicked "act wickedly" and "cannot understand" in the eschatological purification. The eschatological direction is termination — the characteristic reaches its ultimate consequence in the complete dissolution of the wicked person's existence and legacy. This is an eschatological fullness only in the sense that judgment is fully executed; there is no positive eschatological destiny for the characteristic itself.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The evidence points the characteristic toward an eschatological terminus of separation and judgment rather than positive fullness. Mat 13:49 (vc=14459 — VCG-04): "at the end of the age, the angels will come out and separate the evil from the righteous" — the eschatological terminus of the characteristic is separation. 2Ti 3:13 (vc=14451 — VCG-06): "evil people and impostors will go on from bad to worse" — the eschatological trajectory is progressive deterioration arriving at its terminus. The characteristic's eschatological fullness is the complete actualisation of its separation from the righteous — the sorting that is already occurring in the present (Joh 3:19-20 — VCG-04: loving darkness) is finalised eschatologically (Mat 13:49).

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Yes. The characteristic is pointed toward eschatological exclusion as its terminus. Rev 21:27 (vc=22 — VCG-05): "nothing unclean will ever enter it, nor anyone who does what is detestable or false, but only those who are written in the Lamb's book of life" — the characteristic's eschatological fullness is the complete and final exclusion of the abominable from the divine presence. Rev 17:5 (vc=65878 — VCG-05): Babylon the mother of abominations is the eschatological type of the system that generates and propagates abomination — its end is judgment. The Proverbs antithetical pattern (delight vs. abomination) points toward an eschatological resolution where the distinction is finalised: the abominable are excluded; the delightful (the upright) enter.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Yes. VCG-06 (5V) is the explicitly eschatological evidence: Dan 9:27 (vc=65914 — VCG-06), Dan 11:31 (vc=65915 — VCG-06), Dan 12:11 (vc=65916 — VCG-06) — the abomination of desolation as an eschatological peak-sacrilege event. Mat 24:15 (vc=65876 — VCG-06) and Mar 13:14 (vc=65877 — VCG-06) extend this eschatological reading. The characteristic's eschatological fullness is the abomination-of-desolation event — the maximal expression of idolatrous sacrilege that marks the terminus of the trajectory. Simultaneously, the restoration eschatology: Eze 37:23 (vc=65913 — VCG-05) points toward a future where the characteristic has been completely removed and the covenant relationship fully restored.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Yes. The characteristic is pointed toward eschatological judgment and elimination. Psa 92:7-9 (vc=38246/38247 — VCG-03): "evildoers flourish… doomed to destruction forever… all evildoers shall be scattered" — the "forever" and the certainty of scattering point toward a final elimination of the characteristic. Psa 94:23 (vc=38249 — VCG-03): "wipe them out for their wickedness; the Lord our God will wipe them out" — the final decisive act of divine wiping-out as the eschatological culmination. Psa 101:8 (vc=38226 — VCG-03): "morning by morning I will destroy all the wicked in the land, cutting off all the evildoers from the city of the Lord" — the city of the Lord from which evildoers are permanently excluded is an eschatological vision. The trajectory is toward a future in which the characteristic is entirely absent from the divine community.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Yes. The characteristic is oriented toward eschatological judgment as its trajectory. VCG-01 is itself situated within the eschatological judgment sequence of Revelation 16 — the characteristic's most extreme form occurs within the eschatological framework. Rev 16:9/11/21 (VCG-01): the plagues are the eschatological end-time judgments; the characteristic expressed under these judgments is at the eschatological terminus. Rev 13:6 (vc=14356 — VCG-01): the beast's blasphemy is an eschatological figure at the apex of cosmic anti-God defiance. 1Pe 2:12 (vc=14377 — VCG-03): "glorify God on the day of visitation" — the day of visitation is the eschatological moment when the false accusation is definitively reversed and truth is established.

---

##### T5.6.2 — What does the present experience of this characteristic anticipate about its future fullness?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The present experience of wickedness-as-settled-person-identity anticipates its future dissolution through internal signals already present. Pro 10:24 (VCG-06): "what the wicked dreads will come upon him" — the inner dread is a present anticipation of the future judgment the conscience cannot fully suppress. Isa 57:20-21 (VCG-02): the inner restlessness of the wicked ("like the tossing sea… no peace") is the present analogue of the complete dissolution that awaits. Job 15:20 (VCG-06): "the wicked man writhes in pain all his days" — the present inner torment is the beginning of the future judgment. The present experience of the characteristic therefore carries within itself anticipatory signals of its future termination — the characteristic is already self-consuming, already moving toward its own end, in the inner-experience of dread, want, and torment.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The present experience anticipates: (1) the deepening deterioration trajectory — 2Ti 3:13 (vc=14451 — VCG-06) shows the present "from bad to worse" as anticipating the eschatological terminus of that trajectory; (2) the evil conscience's present barrier to God — Heb 10:22 (vc=14426 — VCG-06) shows the present state of the evil conscience as anticipating its eschatological consequence (permanent separation from the holy God unless cleansed); (3) the present love of darkness — Joh 3:19 (vc=14448 — VCG-04) anticipates the eschatological settling into that preference (Mat 13:49 — separation of the evil). The present experience of the characteristic carries within it the seeds of its eschatological outcome.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The present experience of abomination anticipates: (1) the eschatological exclusion — Rev 21:27 (vc=22 — VCG-05): those who do what is detestable are excluded from the holy city; the present experience of exclusion from divine intimacy (Pro 3:32 — VCG-02) and from worship acceptability (VCG-03) anticipates this final exclusion; (2) the permanent weight of shame — Eze 44:13 (vc=66003 — VCG-04): bearing shame permanently anticipates the eschatological state where the shame-burden is not lifted; (3) the removal of abomination from the divine presence — the present divine revulsion (Pro 6:16 — VCG-05: God hates; Pro 11:1 — VCG-01: God finds it abominable) anticipates the eschatological act of exclusion. The present characteristic carries within it the seeds of its eschatological terminus.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The present experience of idolatrous abomination anticipates: (1) progressive escalation — Eze 8:13; 8:15 (VCG-05: "still greater abominations") — the present pattern of deepening anticipates its eschatological maximum; (2) divine-presence withdrawal — Eze 5:11 (vc=65969 — VCG-05): God's withdrawal from the defiled sanctuary anticipates the final eschatological separation; (3) the abomination-of-desolation event — the present historical desecrations (sanctuary defiled by idols — Jer 7:30; 32:34 — VCG-04) anticipate the eschatological desolation-event (Dan 9:27; Mat 24:15 — VCG-06). The present experience carries within it the seeds of the eschatological culmination: each act of idolatrous abomination advances the trajectory toward its maximum expression.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The present experience of iniquity as active scheming anticipates: (1) inevitable divine return of the accumulated iniquity — Psa 94:23 (VCG-03): the present accumulation will be returned as judgment; (2) the temporary nature of apparent flourishing — Psa 92:7 (VCG-03): present sprouting-like-grass anticipates permanent destruction; (3) the eventual complete collapse — Psa 36:12 (vc=38233 — VCG-04): "thrust down, unable to rise" — the present trajectory anticipates its terminus of irrecoverable ruin. The present experience of the characteristic is eschatologically loaded: each act of scheming builds toward the accumulated ruin that will be returned in full.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Present evil expressed through speech anticipates: (1) the eschatological maximum of blasphemy — the beast's sustained cosmic blasphemy (Rev 13:6 — VCG-01) as the concentrated endpoint of all human and adversarial defiant speech; present instances of blasphemous defiance participate in and anticipate this eschatological peak; (2) the eschatological reversal of false accusation — 1Pe 2:12 (vc=14377 — VCG-03): "glorify God on the day of visitation" — the false accusation's present impact is reversed in the eschatological moment when truth is established; (3) the condemnation of slander — Rom 3:8 (vc=14358 — VCG-02): "their condemnation is just" — the present slanderous misrepresentation carries within it the certain eschatological condemnation.

---

##### T5.6.3 — If the evidence is silent on eschatological trajectory, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The evidence is not silent; eschatological trajectory is richly evidenced (T5.6.1–T5.6.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The evidence is not silent; eschatological trajectory is addressed (T5.6.1–T5.6.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The evidence is not silent; eschatological trajectory is evidenced (T5.6.1–T5.6.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Eschatological trajectory is richly evidenced through VCG-06 (T5.6.1–T5.6.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Eschatological trajectory is evidenced (T5.6.1–T5.6.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Eschatological trajectory is richly evidenced through the Revelation and Petrine evidence (T5.6.1–T5.6.2). This prompt is satisfied.

---

#### T5.7 — Deposit Consequence

##### T5.7.1 — Where T2.8 has identified a constitutional deposit from sustained operation of this characteristic, what developmental consequence does that deposit produce over time?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

T2.8 identified three deposits: (1) self-reinforcing bondage (Pro 5:22 — "held fast in the cords of his sin"); (2) structural perversion of justice (Hab 1:4); (3) social-moral contagion risk (Num 16:26). The developmental consequences of these deposits: (1) The self-reinforcing bondage deepens over time — the wicked person becomes progressively less accessible to correction (Isa 26:10 — "he does not learn righteousness" even under grace; Dan 12:10 — the eschatological incapacity to understand). The deposit of bondage produces the developmental consequence of progressive volitional foreclosure. (2) The structural perversion of justice corrupts the community's legal and moral environment, making it progressively harder for justice to function (Hab 1:4 — "the wicked surround the righteous; so justice goes forth perverted"). (3) The social contagion risk (Num 16:26) produces developmental community corruption if the warning to distance is not heeded.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

T2.8 identified three deposits: (1) progressive deterioration (2Ti 3:13 — VCG-06); (2) expanding inner occupation (Mat 12:45 — VCG-06); (3) leaven-spreading through community (1Cor 5:8 — VCG-05). The developmental consequences: (1) The progressive-deterioration deposit produces escalating constitutional corruption — "from bad to worse" is not a stable state but an ongoing degradation trajectory. The deposit deepens with each stage, making each subsequent departure from the characteristic's grip more difficult without divine intervention. (2) The expanding-inner-occupation deposit produces a condition where the inner space becomes progressively more fully occupied by the constitutional evil — Mat 12:45 (VCG-06): the last state worse than the first shows the deposit accumulating toward maximum occupation. (3) The community-leaven deposit produces collective constitutional corruption spreading through communal relationships — 1Cor 5:8 (VCG-05) is the basis for the community's urgent response to expel the evil person (1Cor 5:13 — VCG-04).

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

T2.8 identified two primary deposits: (1) conscience-silencing (Jer 6:15; 8:12 — VCG-04); (2) accumulated shame-burden (Eze 44:13 — VCG-04); and a communal deposit (Ezr 9:11 — VCG-04). Developmental consequences: (1) The conscience-silencing deposit produces progressive incapacity for moral self-correction. Jer 6:15 and 8:12 (VCG-04) show the terminus: no shame, no blushing — the person has lost the inner faculty that would generate corrective response. Each subsequent act of abomination deepens the silencing deposit. (2) The shame-burden deposit (Eze 44:13 — VCG-04) produces permanent exclusion from sacred service — the abominations carried become a weight that bars relational access to the holy. (3) The communal-saturation deposit (Ezr 9:11 — VCG-04) produces a moral environment in which subsequent generations are formed within an abomination-saturated space, making reception of abominable norms the default rather than the exception.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

T2.8 identified two deposits: (1) constitutional character-transformation (Hos 9:10 — VCG-04 — becoming detestable like the idol); (2) land-defilement as collective deposit (Jer 16:18 — VCG-04; Eze 33:29 — VCG-05). Developmental consequences: (1) The constitutional transformation deposit produces a self-reinforcing degradation trajectory: the person who has become detestable (Hos 9:10 — VCG-04) finds idolatrous abomination increasingly natural and the covenant orientation increasingly alien. This development can reach the Eze 8:17 (VCG-05) stage where abomination is treated as trivial — full developmental normalisation of what is abominable. (2) The land-defilement deposit produces an environmental legacy that shapes the formation of subsequent generations within a morally contaminated space (Ezr 9:11 — vc=66005 — VCG-04 parallel, from CHAR-3 corpus but describing CHAR-4's land-fill pattern).

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

T2.8 identified three deposits: (1) conscience-silencing (Pro 30:20 — VCG-04), (2) worn inner path (Job 22:15 — VCG-04), (3) iniquity's dominion-seeking (Psa 119:133 — VCG-04). Developmental consequences: (1) Conscience-silencing deposit: produces the incapacity for self-correction; the person who has reached Pro 30:20 stage ("I have done no wrong") can no longer generate the inner moral signal that would initiate departure from iniquity. Each subsequent commission deepens the silence. (2) Worn path deposit: produces a habitual moral trajectory that becomes the path of least inner resistance; the worn path is increasingly difficult to leave because it is the established inner groove of the character. (3) Dominion-seeking deposit: produces progressive constraint on volitional freedom — the will becomes increasingly bound to iniquity's direction, narrowing the range of genuine volitional choice available.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

T2.8 identified a will-hardening deposit (Rev 16:9/11/21 — VCG-01: progressive hardening across three judgments). Developmental consequences: (1) The will-hardening deposit produces progressive incapacity for repentance — each iteration of blasphemous defiance under judgment deepens the deposit of hardness, narrowing the will's ability to orient toward repentance; at the terminus (Rev 16:21 — VCG-01), the deposit has produced a will that cannot bend even under catastrophic pressure. (2) The deposit produces cognitive regression — Jude 10 (vc=14355 — VCG-01): "destroyed by all that they, like unreasoning animals, understand instinctively" — the sustained contempt-as-substitute-for-understanding deposits a sub-rational cognitive posture that increasingly operates on instinct rather than rational moral comprehension.

---

##### T5.7.2 — Does the evidence indicate generational consequence — a deposit carried forward beyond the individual?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Eze 18:20 (VCG-07) explicitly limits generational moral-accountability consequence: "the son shall not suffer for the iniquity of the father" — the characteristic's moral weight is personalised, not automatically transmitted. However, Num 16:26 (VCG-04) — the contagious-sweeping-away risk of proximity to the wicked in community — implies a communal-generational consequence if wickedness is institutionally embedded. The tension in the evidence is between personal moral accountability (Eze 18:20 — no automatic generational moral inheritance) and social-structural consequence (Hab 1:4; Num 16:26 — the wicked person's sustained operation damages the environment in which the next generation grows). The evidence therefore presents limited personal-moral generational consequence combined with real social-structural generational consequence.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Mat 12:39/16:4 (vc=14416/14441 — VCG-02) and Luk 11:29 (vc=14446 — VCG-02) address "this evil generation" as constitutionally evil — the generational framing implies a collective, trans-individual dimension of the characteristic. The evil generation is addressed as a unit, not merely as aggregated individuals, suggesting the constitutional evil operates at a generational-collective level. 2Ti 3:13 (vc=14451 — VCG-06) — "evil people and impostors will go on from bad to worse" — frames the trajectory as an ongoing generational pattern of teachers following teachers in decline. The evidence does not address biological/DNA generational transmission specifically; it addresses the socio-cultural and spiritual transmission of the characteristic across generations through community and teaching.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Yes. Ezr 9:11 (vc=66005 — VCG-04) specifically addresses generational communal consequence: "the land… is a land impure with the impurity of the peoples of the lands, with their abominations that have filled it from end to end with their uncleanness." The abominations of preceding peoples have saturated the land and become the environment into which Israel is entering — a generational communal deposit that preceded Israel's arrival and shaped the moral-spiritual environment they would inhabit. This is not direct biological transmission but moral-environmental generational consequence: the abominations of predecessors shape the environment of successors. The Mal 2:11 (vc=66004 — VCG-04) faithless mixed devotion also has generational implications (the children of the faithless union introducing foreign god-allegiance into the covenant community).

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Yes, substantially. Eze 20:4 (vc=65994 — VCG-05): "let them know the abominations of their fathers" — the abominations of the fathers are a heritage requiring confrontation in the next generation. Eze 20:30 (vc=65912 — VCG-05): "Will you defile yourselves after the manner of your fathers and go whoring after their detestable things?" — the generational pattern of going after the fathers' detestable things is specifically named. Jer 16:18 (vc=65964 — VCG-04): the land filled with abominations is the environmental deposit of preceding generations that the current generation inhabits. The evidence is clear and direct about generational consequence: idolatrous abomination propagates across generations through the twin mechanisms of inherited patterns (Eze 20:30 — VCG-05) and environmental-land defilement (Jer 16:18 — VCG-04).

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Yes. Job 21:19 (vc=38209 — VCG-04): "God stores up their iniquity for their children" — explicit generational consequence is named: the accumulated iniquity of one generation is deferred to the next as an inherited burden. This is the primary generational-deposit evidence. The VCG-01 communal-trouble evidence (Psa 55:10 — vc=38239 — VCG-01: "iniquity and trouble are within it" — the city) shows that accumulated communal iniquity deposits a moral-environmental legacy that shapes subsequent inhabitants. The worn-path evidence (Job 22:15 — VCG-04: "the old way that wicked men have trod") implies a generational model: the path was established by predecessors and subsequent persons are warned not to follow it — the predecessors' iniquity has deposited a trajectory that the living must actively refuse.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (S)

The 17-verse corpus does not directly evidence generational consequence for evil expressed through speech. The characteristic's deposit is individual and cosmic/eschatological in scope (VCG-01: the hardened individual will; the eschatological population under judgment) but not specifically described as generational in transmission. Rom 2:24 (vc=14357 — VCG-02): the moral failure of those who represent God causes God's name to be blasphemed "among the Gentiles" — this has a communal rather than strictly generational social impact, but it is not specifically a generational transfer. Generational consequence is not directly evidenced.

---

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

T2.8 found deposits; T5.7 is therefore addressed (T5.7.1–T5.7.2) and closed.
