## T6 — Structural Relationships (24 prompts)

---

### T6

#### T6.1 — Co-occurrence

##### T6.1.1 — Which adjacent characteristics appear most frequently alongside this one in the verse evidence?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The verse evidence reveals four primary co-occurring characteristics. (1) Righteousness (M26 counterpart): the righteous/wicked contrast is the dominant structural feature of the corpus, present in virtually every VCG — Gen 18:23-25 (VCG-04), Psa 1:1-6 (VCG-04), Psa 37:10-21 (VCG-05/06), Pro 10-21 throughout (VCG-09), Mal 3:18 (VCG-02). (2) Pride (a constituent element — Pro 21:4; Psa 10:2; Isa 13:11 — VCG-03): pride co-occurs as the inner engine driving wickedness. (3) Justice/injustice (M28 or equivalent): the perversion of justice is a repeated co-occurrence — Isa 5:23 (VCG-05), Hab 1:4 (VCG-03), Pro 17:23 (VCG-09), Pro 17:15 (VCG-09). (4) Iniquity (M10b-E in the broader cluster context): ra.sha frequently co-occurs with terminology of iniquity — Psa 10:15 (VCG-05 — "wickedness"), Isa 13:11 (VCG-03 — "wicked for their iniquity"), Eze 3:18 (VCG-07 — "wicked way / wicked iniquity").

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Four primary co-occurring characteristics emerge from the 90-verse corpus. (1) The cosmic-evil / evil-one dimension (M27 cross-register — VCG-01, 13V): the cosmic adversarial context co-occurs extensively with the personal constitutional evil, showing they are not independent phenomena but structurally related — the whole world under the evil one's power (1Jo 5:19 — VCG-01) frames the context in which human constitutional evil operates. (2) Unrighteousness (adikia — 8V across VCGs 05/06): co-occurs with kakia and ponēria in the vice-saturation clusters (Rom 1:29 — VCG-05), showing the three terms habitually clustering as expressions of the same constitutional condition. (3) Pride (Jam 4:16 — VCG-06; Mat 20:15 — VCG-06): arrogance/envy as the affective expressions of constitutional inner evil. (4) Faithlessness (Heb 3:12 — VCG-06; 2Th 3:2 — VCG-06): the evil heart fused with the unbelieving heart — faithlessness as the characterising inner posture of constitutional evil.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Four co-occurring characteristics emerge. (1) Wickedness (CHAR-1 — ra.sha): Pro 15:9 (vc=1688 — VCG-01): "the way of the wicked is an abomination"; Pro 15:8 (vc=1678 — VCG-03): "the sacrifice of the wicked"; Pro 17:15 (vc=1690 — VCG-01): "he who justifies the wicked" — the wicked person/way is the most frequent co-occurring subject of abomination. (2) Pride (inner-being adjacent — Pro 16:5 — vc=1689 — VCG-02: arrogant heart; Luk 16:15 — vc=21 — VCG-02: self-justifying pride). (3) Dishonesty/deception (Pro 12:22 — vc=65955 — VCG-02: lying lips; Pro 11:1 — vc=65954 — VCG-01: false balance; Deu 25:16 — vc=65936 — VCG-01: dishonest practice) — deception as inner-character condition co-occurs frequently. (4) Conscience (VCG-04: the conscience in its silenced/awakened states is the most extensively co-occurring inner faculty, present in 11 of 40 verses).

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Four primary co-occurring characteristics emerge. (1) Iniquity/evil practice (M10b-E or M10 equivalent): Eze 7:3 (vc=65971 — VCG-05): "judge you according to your ways, and I will punish you for all your abominations"; Eze 18:12-13 (vc=65992-65993 — VCG-05): abomination listed among iniquity, robbery, oppression — iniquity co-occurs throughout. (2) Sexual immorality (M10c/adjacent): Eze 16:36 (vc=65986 — VCG-05): "lust poured out in your whorings with your lovers, with all your abominable idols" — whorings and abominations consistently co-occur in Ezekiel 16 and 23; Jer 13:27 (vc=65905 — VCG-04): "your abominations, your adulteries and neighings." (3) Violence (M02-adjacent): Eze 8:17 (vc=65980 — VCG-05): "fill the land with violence and provoke me still further" — abomination and violence consistently co-occur. (4) Unfaithfulness/harlotry (M10-adjacent): the Ezekiel whoring metaphor throughout VCG-05 — "whoring heart" (Eze 6:9), "whorings" (Eze 16:36; 16:43) — spiritual unfaithfulness as the co-occurring metaphorical characterisation.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Four primary co-occurring characteristics emerge. (1) Deceit/lying: Psa 7:14 (vc=38245 — VCG-02): iniquity "gives birth to lies"; Psa 36:3 (vc=38234 — VCG-04): "words of his mouth are trouble and deceit"; Psa 28:3 (vc=38232 — VCG-03): speak peace while evil in heart — deceptive speech consistently co-occurs with active iniquity-scheming. (2) Violence/bloodshed: Isa 59:7 (vc=38203 — VCG-02): "swift to shed innocent blood"; Hab 1:3 (vc=38194 — VCG-01): "destruction and violence are before me"; Hos 6:8 (vc=38196 — VCG-03): "Gilead is a city of evildoers, tracked with blood" — violence as the physical terminus of inner scheming. (3) Oppression of the weak: Psa 14:4 (vc=38229 — VCG-03): "eat up my people"; Isa 10:1 (vc=38191 — VCG-02): iniquitous decrees targeting the weak. (4) Pride/boasting: Psa 94:4 (vc=38250 — VCG-03): "all the evildoers boast" — arrogant speech co-occurs with the evildoer character.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Three adjacent characteristics appear. (1) Defiance of authority / rejection of divine order — Jude 8 (vc=14354 — VCG-01): "reject authority and blaspheme the glorious ones" — authority-rejection co-occurs directly with blasphemy as its paired expression; (2) Sensory self-indulgence — Jude 8 (vc=14354 — VCG-01): "relying on their dreams, they defile the flesh" — sensory indulgence and authority-rejection co-occur as the inner conditions that produce blasphemous speech; (3) Refusal of repentance — Rev 16:9 (vc=14352 — VCG-01): "they did not repent and give him glory"; Rev 16:11 (vc=14350 — VCG-01): "they did not repent of their deeds" — the absence of repentance is the most consistent co-occurring inner state throughout VCG-01; blasphemy and repentance-refusal are the paired positive and negative expressions of the hardened will.

---

##### T6.1.2 — What does the pattern of co-occurrence reveal about this characteristic's place in the inner-being landscape?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The co-occurrence pattern reveals that wickedness-as-settled-person-identity is a central hub characteristic rather than a peripheral one. Its consistent co-occurrence with righteousness (as structural opposite), pride (as inner engine), justice-perversion (as social expression), and iniquity (as companion characteristic) places it at the intersection of multiple inner-being dimensions simultaneously. The characteristic's prominence in Job, Psalms, Proverbs, and the Prophets — each with distinct co-occurrence patterns — confirms that it is a core category for the biblical analysis of the human moral interior, not a specific or bounded phenomenon. The co-occurrence with righteousness in particular shows that wickedness-as-settled-person-identity cannot be understood in isolation — it is constitutively relational, always defined against and in contrast to the righteous person.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The co-occurrence pattern reveals CHAR-2 as a hub characteristic — it co-occurs with the cosmic-adversarial frame (VCG-01/M27), with multiple specific vice-expressions (kakia, ponēria, adikia — VCG-05), with affective corruptions (pride, envy — VCG-06), and with faithlessness (VCG-06). The characteristic is not an isolated inner-being phenomenon but the constitutional condition from which all other negative characteristics flow. The vice-saturation cluster (Rom 1:29 — VCG-05: "filled with all manner of unrighteousness, evil, covetousness, malice…") shows the characteristic as the saturating condition within which a host of specific characteristics co-reside. This confirms CHAR-2 as a foundational condition rather than a specific characteristic — it is the constitutional ground from which specific evil characteristics emerge.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The co-occurrence pattern reveals CHAR-3 as the divine-verdict registration of inner moral conditions that are also addressed by other characteristics. Wickedness (CHAR-1), pride, dishonesty, and conscience-related states all appear in their own right as inner-being characteristics but CHAR-3 provides the divine-relational verdict on them: they are "abominable." This positions CHAR-3 as a meta-characteristic — a relational verdict category that operates over the top of other inner-being conditions rather than being a primary inner-being condition itself. The characteristic's placement in the inner-being landscape is as the divine-holiness response to multiple different inner-being failure conditions, which explains why it co-occurs with so many others.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The co-occurrence pattern reveals CHAR-4 as the epicentre of a moral-collapse cluster: it co-occurs with iniquity, sexual immorality, violence, and unfaithfulness — the full spectrum of moral failure. This positioning shows the characteristic as not merely one among several moral failures but as the root from which others proliferate: when idolatrous abomination establishes itself, the other characteristics follow. The pattern is consistent in Ezekiel VCG-05: abominations driving God away → resulting in violence, whorings, and iniquity filling the community. This positioning makes CHAR-4 analytically foundational — in the biblical moral-spiritual analysis, idolatrous devotion is the source from which broader moral collapse flows.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The co-occurrence pattern reveals CHAR-5 as the generative upstream source of multiple downstream expressions. Deceit is the speech-mode of the inner scheming (lies are born from iniquity — Psa 7:14 — VCG-02). Violence is the physical outcome of running to evil (Isa 59:7 — VCG-02). Oppression is the social expression of the predatory orientation (Psa 14:4 — VCG-03). Pride is the inner-affective companion of the boastful evildoer (Psa 94:4 — VCG-03). CHAR-5 is positioned upstream of these: the inner scheming generates the deceit, enables the violence, empowers the oppression, and is companioned by pride. This positioning makes CHAR-5 analytically foundational — it is the active inner process that produces the visible outputs named by adjacent characteristics.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The co-occurrence pattern reveals CHAR-6 as the terminal speech-expression of a cluster of hardened-will characteristics: authority-rejection + sensory indulgence + repentance-refusal → blasphemous speech. CHAR-6 is thus not the origin of the cluster but its verbal culmination — the point at which the hardened inner orientation finds its most explicit and socially operative expression through speech. Jude 8 (VCG-01): the authority-rejection and flesh-defilement precede and produce the blasphemy — CHAR-6 is downstream of those inner states. This positioning reveals CHAR-6 as the expressive terminus of a will that has already settled into defiance.

---

##### T6.1.3 — If no significant co-occurrence patterns emerge, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Co-occurrence patterns are significant and documented (T6.1.1–T6.1.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Significant co-occurrence patterns are evidenced (T6.1.1–T6.1.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Co-occurrence patterns are significant and documented (T6.1.1–T6.1.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Co-occurrence patterns are significant and documented (T6.1.1–T6.1.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Co-occurrence patterns are significant and documented (T6.1.1–T6.1.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Co-occurrence patterns are significant and documented (T6.1.1–T6.1.2). This prompt is satisfied.

---

#### T6.2 — Sequential Relationships

##### T6.2.1 — Does the verse evidence show this characteristic consistently preceding, following, or accompanying another characteristic in a sequence?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The evidence documents a sequential relationship: wickedness-as-settled-person-identity consistently precedes divine judgment. The sequence is: wickedness (settled inner orientation) → harm-generation (VCGs 03, 08, 09) → divine response (VCG-05 — judgment; VCG-02 — relational estrangement). This sequence is present throughout: Psa 9:5 (judgment erasing the wicked), Psa 37:10-17 (wicked present; then broken and gone), Isa 11:4 (the wicked killed by the righteous judge), Mal 4:3 (wicked as ashes). A second sequential pattern: pride precedes settled wickedness — Pro 21:4 (VCG-03: "haughty eyes and a proud heart… are sin"), Psa 10:2-4 (VCG-02/03: pride driving the God-exclusion that constitutes practical atheism). Pride appears to precede and enable the characteristic's consolidation.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Yes. The characteristic consistently precedes its outward expressions in a source-to-output sequence. Mat 12:34-35 (vc=14419-14420 — VCG-03): the evil heart (CHAR-2 constitutional condition) → corrupt speech (expressive output). Mar 7:23 (vc=14422 — VCG-03): constitutional inner evil → defilement through outward expression. Col 1:21 (vc=14424 — VCG-06): hostile mind (CHAR-2 cognitive expression) → evil deeds. The characteristic also consistently precedes divine judgment: Joh 3:19 (vc=14448 — VCG-04): "people loved the darkness…because their works were evil" — the constitutional evil preceding the judgment of condemnation in the light's arrival.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The characteristic consistently follows other inner-being conditions in a verdict sequence: wickedness → divine abomination verdict; pride → divine abomination verdict; dishonesty → divine abomination verdict. Pro 16:5 (vc=1689 — VCG-02): arrogance in heart → "is an abomination to the Lord." Pro 12:22 (vc=65955 — VCG-02): lying lips → "are an abomination to the Lord." The characteristic also consistently precedes judgment: Jer 6:15; 8:12 (VCG-04): abomination committed without shame → "they shall fall/be overthrown." The sequence is: inner moral condition → divine abomination verdict → divine judgment consequence.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The characteristic consistently precedes divine judgment in a causal sequence. Eze 5:9 (vc=65968 — VCG-05): "because of all your abominations I will do with you what I have never yet done" — abominations precede and cause unprecedented judgment. Eze 7:3 (vc=65971 — VCG-05): "punish you for all your abominations" — abominations precede punishment. Jer 44:22 (vc=65967 — VCG-04): abominations preceded land-desolation. The characteristic also consistently accompanies or precedes divine-presence withdrawal (Eze 5:11 — VCG-05: "I will withdraw"). There is also a sequence where idolatrous abomination precedes the constitutional transformation (Hos 9:10 — VCG-04: committed → became detestable).

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The characteristic consistently precedes divine judgment in a causal sequence. Deu 28:20 (vc=38439 — VCG-05): "evil of your deeds" → curses, confusion, destruction. Jer 44:22 (vc=38448 — VCG-05): evil deeds → land desolation. Psa 94:23 (vc=38249 — VCG-03): iniquity → divine return of iniquity as wipeout. The characteristic also consistently precedes its outputs: Psa 7:14 (vc=38245 — VCG-02): conceives → gives birth — the inner scheming precedes the born-iniquity. Mic 2:1 (vc=38217 — VCG-02): nocturnal devising → dawn performance. The characteristic also precedes the closing of the prayer-relationship (Psa 66:18 — VCG-04) and the loss of divine attention.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The characteristic consistently follows and accompanies hardened-will states. Jude 8 (vc=14354 — VCG-01): authority-rejection + flesh-defilement → blasphemy follows. Rev 16:9/11/21 (VCG-01): divine judgment (external) → refusal of repentance (inner) → blasphemy (verbal). The characteristic follows the will's refusal at every stage. The characteristic also consistently precedes or accompanies divine judgment escalation in the Rev 16 sequence: each blasphemy is followed by the next more severe judgment (Rev 16:9 → 16:11 → 16:21 — VCG-01), suggesting the blasphemy provokes or is followed by intensified divine response.

---

##### T6.2.2 — What does the sequence reveal — is the relationship causal, developmental, or correlational?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The pride-to-wickedness sequence appears causal: Psa 10:4 (VCG-02) — "In the pride of his face the wicked does not seek God" — the pride is the mechanism through which God is excluded, and the God-exclusion is constitutive of the wickedness. The wickedness-to-judgment sequence appears both developmental (the characteristic accumulates consequences over time — Pro 10:24 — "what the wicked dreads will come upon him") and causal (divine judgment is a principled moral response to the wickedness — Exo 23:7 — "I will not acquit the wicked"; Psa 11:6 — destruction is the appointed portion). The sequence from wickedness to judgment is the most consistently evidenced causal sequence in the corpus.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The source-to-output sequence (heart → speech; within → defilement) is causal: the constitutional inner evil causes the outward expressions. Mat 12:34 (vc=14419 — VCG-03): "for out of the abundance of the heart the mouth speaks" — the "for" (gar) signals causal explanation. Mar 7:23 (vc=14422 — VCG-03): "all these evil things come from within, and they defile" — the defilement is caused by the within-origin. The deterioration sequence (2Ti 3:13 — VCG-06 — "from bad to worse") is developmental — each stage causally produces the next. The characteristic is therefore causally and developmentally prior to its expressions, which confirms the constitutional framing: the condition (CHAR-2) causes the acts and orientations (expressions) rather than the reverse.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The sequence is causal. The inner moral condition (pride, dishonesty, wickedness) causally triggers the divine abomination verdict — the verdict is the response to the condition, not an independent event. The divine judgment that follows is also causally linked to the abomination verdict: Jer 6:15 (vc=1680 — VCG-04) states "therefore they shall fall" — the consequence is causally grounded in the abomination and its shameless commission. The whole sequence (inner condition → abomination verdict → judgment) is a causal chain in which each stage follows from the preceding. The characteristic is therefore analytically positioned in the middle of this chain — it is the relational verdict stage between inner condition and judgment consequence.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The sequence is causal throughout. The abominations cause the divine response (Eze 5:9 — VCG-05: "because of all your abominations…I will do with you"). The abominations cause the divine withdrawal (Eze 8:6 — vc=65976 — VCG-05: abominations "drive me far from my sanctuary"). The sustained abominations cause constitutional transformation (Hos 9:10 — VCG-04: "became detestable like the thing they loved"). The judgment-suffering causes memory-restoration (Eze 6:9 — VCG-05 — the exile survivors remember). The causal chain runs: idolatrous abomination → divine-presence withdrawal → judgment → exile → memory-restoration → self-loathing → possible return.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The sequence is primarily causal throughout. The inner scheming causes the born evil (Psa 7:14 — VCG-02); the evil deeds cause divine judgment (Deu 28:20 — VCG-05; Jer 44:22 — VCG-05); the cherished iniquity causes the closed divine ear (Psa 66:18 — VCG-04). The developmental dimension also applies (T5.2.1): the sequence of inner states (choice → devising → accumulation → conscience-deadening → dominion → collapse) is developmental — each stage develops from and depends on the prior. The dominant mode is causal: active scheming produces its consequences with moral necessity.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The Jude sequence (Jude 8 — VCG-01: self-indulgence → authority-rejection → blasphemy) is developmental/causal: each prior state enables and produces the next. The Rev 16 sequence (VCG-01) is both causal and revelatory: the judgment triggers the blasphemous response (causal: divine pressure → defiant expression) but also reveals what was already present (revelatory: the hardened will's pre-existing orientation is disclosed by the blasphemy). The condemnation of blasphemy in Rom 3:8 (vc=14358 — VCG-02) — "their condemnation is just" — shows the characteristic preceding its own judgment consequence: the slandering speech causally leads to just condemnation.

---

##### T6.2.3 — If no sequential pattern is evidenced, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Sequential patterns are evidenced (T6.2.1–T6.2.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Sequential patterns are evidenced (T6.2.1–T6.2.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Sequential patterns are evidenced (T6.2.1–T6.2.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Sequential patterns are evidenced (T6.2.1–T6.2.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Sequential patterns are evidenced (T6.2.1–T6.2.2). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Sequential patterns are evidenced (T6.2.1–T6.2.2). This prompt is satisfied.

---

#### T6.3 — Causal and Constitutive Relationships

##### T6.3.1 — Does this characteristic produce another characteristic in the verse evidence — and if so, which one, and by what mechanism?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The evidence shows wickedness-as-settled-person-identity producing multiple downstream characteristics: (1) inner instability and anxiety (VCG-06 — Pro 10:24 — dread; Job 15:20 — torment; Isa 57:20-21 — restlessness); (2) perceptive blindness (Pro 4:19 — moral blindness; Isa 26:10 — inability to see God's majesty); (3) chronic inner want and spiritual emptiness (Pro 13:25 — "belly of the wicked suffers want"); (4) social destructiveness (Pro 11:11 — city overthrown; Hab 1:4 — justice perverted). The most analytically important characteristic produced is the inner blindness/perceptive closure (T3.1) — the wicked person's characteristic generates its own perceptive impairment, which then makes reversal increasingly difficult. The characteristic also produces its own judgment-trajectory (VCG-05 — 30V of judgment evidence).

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Yes. The characteristic produces multiple downstream expressions. From VCG-03: corrupt speech (Mat 12:34-35; Luk 6:45 — produced by the evil heart-treasury). From VCG-05: the full vice-saturation catalogue (Rom 1:29 — produced by the constitutional evil that fills the person — "filled with all manner of unrighteousness, evil, covetousness, malice, envy, murder, strife, deceit, maliciousness"). From VCG-06: evil suspicions (1Ti 6:4 — produced by a conceit-inflated, understanding-devoid mind); progressive deterioration (2Ti 3:13 — produced by the self-reinforcing mechanism); the defiled conscience (Heb 10:22 — the evil conscience as the constitutional result of sustained inner evil). The characteristic produces the whole vice-catalogue of the inner person as its downstream expressions.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The characteristic produces: (1) divine relational exclusion — Pro 3:32 (vc=1686 — VCG-02): the devious person is excluded from divine confidence — the exclusion is produced by the abomination verdict; (2) divine judgment and its consequences — Jer 6:15; 8:12 (VCG-04): "they shall fall among those who fall; when I punish them, they shall be overthrown" — the divine punishment is produced by the abomination; (3) permanent shame-burden — Eze 44:13 (vc=66003 — VCG-04): the abominations they committed become a weight they bear permanently. The characteristic also produces — in the awakened conscience — self-loathing: Eze 36:31 (vc=1681 — VCG-04): self-loathing as the conscience's response to remembered abomination. These are the downstream outputs of the characteristic.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Yes. CHAR-4 produces: (1) constitutional character-deformation toward the idol — Hos 9:10 (vc=1632 — VCG-04): "became detestable like the thing they loved"; (2) moral gravity-loss — Eze 8:17 (vc=65980 — VCG-05): abomination treated as trivial; (3) divine-presence withdrawal — Eze 5:11 (vc=65969 — VCG-05): "I will withdraw"; (4) accompanying iniquities — Eze 18:12-13 (vc=65992-65993 — VCG-05): idolatrous eyes and abomination appear in the same iniquity-catalogue, implying the characteristic enables the full vice-cluster; (5) land-defilement — Jer 16:18 (vc=65964 — VCG-04): filled inheritance with abominations → land defilement. The characteristic generates a cascading consequence-chain rather than a single downstream output.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The characteristic produces: (1) deceit/lies as its born output — Psa 7:14 (vc=38245 — VCG-02): "gives birth to lies"; Job 15:35 (vc=38208 — VCG-02): "womb prepares deceit"; (2) oppression of others — Isa 10:1 (vc=38191 — VCG-02): iniquitous decrees produce systematic harm against the weak; Psa 14:4 (vc=38229 — VCG-03): eating up the people; (3) trouble-affliction for victims — VCG-01 (7V): the trouble that falls on the victim as the output of the schemer's iniquity; (4) the closing of the divine ear — Psa 66:18 (vc=38182 — VCG-04): cherished iniquity → no divine listening; (5) communal desolation — Jer 44:22 (vc=38448 — VCG-05): accumulated evil deeds → land desolation.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The characteristic produces: (1) social dishonour and reputational damage — 1Cor 4:13 (vc=14351 — VCG-02): slander reduces the apostle to "the scum of the world, the refuse of all things" — the defamatory speech produces a social-identity damage; (2) dishonour to God's name — Rom 2:24 (vc=14357 — VCG-02): blasphemy causes God's name to be "blasphemed among the Gentiles" — the conduct-caused blasphemy produces sustained social dishonour to the divine name; (3) condemnation — Rom 3:8 (vc=14358 — VCG-02): "their condemnation is just" — the slanderous speech produces its own just condemnation as consequence; (4) shame for the false accusers — 1Pe 3:16 (vc=14380 — VCG-03): good conscience and good behavior "may be put to shame" the revilers — the false accusation ultimately produces shame for those who made it.

---

##### T6.3.2 — Is this characteristic produced by another — and if so, which one?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The evidence suggests pride (Pro 21:4; Psa 10:2-4 — VCG-03) and practical-atheism/God-exclusion (VCG-02 — Psa 10:4; 9:17) as generative precursors, though the evidence does not establish a clean causal chain. Pride as an inner engine (VCG-03 — "arrogance drives the wicked," Psa 10:2) appears as a producing characteristic. The social alignment with wicked counsel (Psa 1:1 — VCG-04) also functions as a receptor-mechanism through which the characteristic is received. Eze 13:22 (VCG-07) shows that false prophetic enablement ("encouraging the wicked not to turn") functions as a maintaining-producing force for the characteristic's persistence. The evidence points to pride and God-exclusion as the primary upstream characteristics.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The evidence presents the characteristic as the constitutional baseline condition rather than as produced by another upstream characteristic within this corpus. Mat 7:11 (vc=14438 — VCG-02): "you who are evil" is addressed as a baseline fact. However, VCG-01 introduces a partial cosmic upstream: 1Jo 5:19 (vc=14433 — VCG-01) — "the whole world lies in the power of the evil one" — implies that the evil one's dominion over the world is a contributing environmental condition for the human constitutional evil. Mat 13:19 (vc=14435 — VCG-01): the evil one targets hearts that lack understanding, exploiting the constitutional vulnerability. The evidence suggests the cosmic adversarial dimension (M27 cross-register) as a partial upstream influence that exploits the constitutional condition rather than creating it from nothing.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Yes. The characteristic is produced by the inner moral conditions that trigger the divine revulsion verdict. In the evidence: wickedness (CHAR-1 — the way of the wicked — Pro 15:9 — VCG-01), pride (the arrogant heart — Pro 16:5 — VCG-02), dishonesty (lying lips — Pro 12:22 — VCG-02; false balance — Pro 11:1 — VCG-01), and crooked heart (Pro 11:20 — VCG-01) all produce the abomination-verdict. These inner conditions are the upstream characteristics; CHAR-3 is their divine-verdict downstream. Conscience-silencing (VCG-04) is a secondary upstream: the silenced conscience enables sustained commission of abomination without arrest, which deepens the abominable condition.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The evidence presents multiple upstream characteristics. Pride: Eze 7:20 (vc=65909/65975 — VCG-05): "pride" drives the conversion of beautiful ornament into idol-material — pride as the generating upstream characteristic. Lust/desire: Eze 16:36 (vc=65986 — VCG-05): "your lust was poured out" in idolatrous whorings — inner desire as the upstream driver. Covetousness: Deu 7:25 (vc=1682 — VCG-02): "you shall not covet the silver or gold on them" — covetousness as the entry mechanism. The failure to separate from idolatrous peoples (Ezr 9:1 — VCG-03 — upstream environmental enabler). These characteristics (pride, lust, covetousness, failure of covenant separation) are the upstream conditions that produce CHAR-4.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The evidence presents multiple upstream producing characteristics. (1) Volitional preference for easy path over affliction — Job 36:21 (vc=38216 — VCG-04): iniquity chosen "rather than affliction" — the failure of will under pressure of cost produces the entry into iniquity. (2) Associational formation — Job 34:8 (vc=38214 — VCG-04): company of evildoers shapes the person toward iniquity. (3) Pride/self-assertion — 1Sa 15:23 (vc=38185 — VCG-02): "presumption is as iniquity" — self-assertive will elevating itself above divine word produces iniquity-as-presumption. (4) Uncircumcised heart — Jer 4:4 (vc=38447 — VCG-05): evil deeds from an uncircumcised heart — the uncleansed heart as the upstream condition.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The characteristic is produced by: (1) authority-rejection — Jude 8 (vc=14354 — VCG-01): "reject authority and blaspheme" — the blasphemy is produced by the prior authority-rejection; (2) sensory indulgence and dreamlike self-reliance — Jude 8 (VCG-01): "relying on their dreams, they defile the flesh" — the sensory-indulgent inner posture produces the blasphemous expression; (3) hardened will refusing repentance — Rev 16:9/11/21 (VCG-01): the will's refusal to repent produces each instance of cursing; (4) moral failure in conduct — Rom 2:24 (vc=14357 — VCG-02): the moral failure of those representing God produces the social blasphemy of his name; (5) hostile malicious evaluation — Joh 18:30 (vc=14378 — VCG-03): the accusers' inner hostile judgment produces the false verbal charge.

---

##### T6.3.3 — Is this characteristic a constituent element of another, or does another characteristic constitute part of this one?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Pride functions as a constituent element within wickedness-as-settled-person-identity (Pro 21:4 — VCG-03: "haughty eyes and a proud heart, the lamp of the wicked, are sin"). The practical-atheism dimension (VCG-02) is a structural constituent — the God-exclusion is not merely a consequence but a constitutive feature of the settled wicked person. The iniquity dimension (the wicked person's inner scheming — some verses overlap with M10b-E) is also a partial constituent. Whether wickedness-as-settled-identity is itself a constituent of another broader characteristic is less clear from this evidence — it appears to be a primary category rather than a constituent of a yet-larger characteristic.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The VCG-01 cosmic-evil sub-corpus (13V — INTEGRATION_NOTE) represents the M27 (cosmic/concrete evil) characteristic constituting a partial context for CHAR-2's expression. The evil one's power (1Jo 5:19) and the evil age (Gal 1:4; Eph 5:16) constitute the cosmic environment within which the personal constitutional evil operates. Conversely, the vice-saturation VCG-05 (kakia, ponēria, adikia) shows specific characteristics (malice, wickedness, unrighteousness) as constituent expressions of the constitutional evil — they are the specific forms in which the general constitutional condition manifests. CHAR-2 is constituted by these specific vice-forms while simultaneously being the constitutional ground from which they flow.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The characteristic is constituted in part by multiple upstream inner-being conditions: wickedness (CHAR-1), pride, dishonesty, and the crooked heart are all constituent elements of the situations that trigger the abomination verdict — without these inner conditions, the abomination verdict would not be applied. In this sense, CHAR-3 is a compound verdict that draws its content from multiple other characteristics. CHAR-3 also constitutes the divine-relational dimension of those other characteristics: when CHAR-1 (wickedness) is assessed at the divine-holiness interface, it becomes CHAR-3 — abomination is CHAR-1 seen from God's perspective of active revulsion. The relationship is perspectival: CHAR-1 and CHAR-2 name the human inner condition; CHAR-3 names the divine-relational verdict on those conditions.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

CHAR-3 (moral-character abomination) shares the abomination-verdict category with CHAR-4 but constitutes a distinct register. CHAR-4 shares its vocabulary (to.e.vah, shiq.quts) with CHAR-3 — both are instances of the broader abomination category — but CHAR-4's distinguishing constituent is the idolatrous devotion dimension (the heart going after idols, the soul delighting in abominations). The idol-objects named as shiq.quts (foreign deities — 1Ki 11:5; 2Ki 23:13 — VCG-03) are constituent elements of the characteristic's content — they are the specific objects to which false devotion is attached. CHAR-4 is itself constituted by the conjunction of the devotion-capacity (from the image-bearing design) and the false-object (the idol) toward which it is misdirected.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The characteristic shares vocabulary and category with CHAR-1 (wickedness as settled person-identity using ra.sha vocabulary): both address the evildoer-person type but from different angles (CHAR-1 — settled identity; CHAR-5 — active scheming process). CHAR-5's VCG-03 evildoer class (24V) provides the person-type evidence that bridges to CHAR-1; the a.ven vocabulary is distinct from CHAR-1's ra.sha vocabulary, but the evildoer as a character-type overlaps. CHAR-5's VCG-05 (evil deeds register — ro.a) constitutes the expressed-deeds dimension of what CHAR-1 names as the settled wicked character — the deeds are the outward expression of the inner character both characteristics address. CHAR-5 and CHAR-1 are thus constitutively related as process (CHAR-5 — active scheming) and identity (CHAR-1 — settled character), with CHAR-5's VCG-03 and CHAR-1 sharing the evildoer-type.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The blasfēmeō vocabulary is flagged as sharing a cross-register with M06 (contempt / hostile speech / defiant rejection of authority — noted in §2). CHAR-6 and M06 share the speech-defiance domain: CHAR-6 analyses the inner wickedness expressed through speech; M06 analyses the contemptuous hostile speech act as a relational phenomenon. Part of what constitutes CHAR-6 (the contemptuous hostile speech content) is also constitutive of M06 — the characteristics share overlapping content from different analytical angles. The authority-rejection of Jude 8 (VCG-01) is itself a separate characteristic adjacent to CHAR-6 and constitutive of the condition that produces it.

---

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Causal and constitutive relationships are evidenced (T6.3.1–T6.3.3). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Causal and constitutive relationships are evidenced (T6.3.1–T6.3.3). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Causal and constitutive relationships are evidenced (T6.3.1–T6.3.3). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Causal and constitutive relationships are evidenced (T6.3.1–T6.3.3). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Causal and constitutive relationships are evidenced (T6.3.1–T6.3.3). This prompt is satisfied.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Causal and constitutive relationships are evidenced (T6.3.1–T6.3.3). This prompt is satisfied.

#### T6.4 — Vocabulary and Root Sharing

##### T6.4.1 — Does this characteristic share vocabulary terms with other characteristics in the programme?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Yes. The primary Hebrew term ra.sha (H7563) is shared with M10 (sin-act / forensic verdict register) — specifically in M10b-A-VCG-01 (the forensic-verdict 5V sub-corpus: Exo 23:7; Deu 25:1, 25:2; 1Ki 8:32; 2Ch 6:23). This is the INTEGRATION_NOTE carry-forward from Phase 5/6: ra.sha functions both as a person-type term (wickedness-as-settled-identity, M10b) and as a judicial-status term (the legally condemnable, M10). re.sha (H7562 — 9V in this characteristic) is the abstract noun that names wickedness as a condition — it likely shares vocabulary territory with M10b-E (iniquity) and M26 (righteousness — as structural opposite). mir.sha.at (H4849 — 1V) is unique to this characteristic in the programme. The ro.a verse (1Sa 17:28) shares vocabulary with M10b-E (ro.a evil-deeds corpus).

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Yes. Shared vocabulary: (1) ponēros (G4190) is the primary term shared with CHAR-1's cross-register (CHAR-1 uses ra.sha as primary; ponēros is the NT equivalent); ponēros in CHAR-4 (M10b-D) and CHAR-6 (M10b-F) also makes appearances in related clusters. (2) adikia (G0093) is the term shared most directly with M10 (sin-act / forensic register) — unrighteousness as both a forensic category (M10) and an inner constitutional condition (CHAR-2). (3) kakia (G2549) shares vocabulary with M26 (Righteousness) as its semantic opposite (kakia names badness as a quality; the structural opposite is agathos/righteousness). (4) ponēria (G4189) shares vocabulary with M27 cross-register (Eph 6:12 — VCG-05: "spiritual forces of evil" — the cosmic dimension of ponēria).

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Yes. (1) to.e.vah (H8441) is the primary term shared with M10b-D (idolatrous abomination — CHAR-4). Both M10b-C and M10b-D are sub-corpora of the full to.e.vah distribution; the term is shared across the two characteristics with the moral-character vs. idolatrous register being the distinguishing criterion. (2) ra.sha (H7563 — the wicked) co-occurs throughout VCG-01 and VCG-03 in this characteristic's corpus (Pro 15:8; 15:9; 17:15; 21:27) — the vocabulary of CHAR-1 appears within CHAR-3's evidence base. (3) bdelugma (G0946) and bdeluktos (G0947) are unique to this characteristic and CHAR-4 in the programme — they are the NT equivalents of to.e.vah for the abomination cluster.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Yes. (1) to.e.vah (H8441) is shared with CHAR-3 — both characteristics are sub-corpora of the full to.e.vah distribution, with CHAR-3 carrying the moral-character register and CHAR-4 carrying the idolatrous register. (2) shiq.quts (H8251, 25V in CHAR-4) is shared with M27 (concrete-abomination/idol-object) as the primary cross-register flag — shiq.quts specifically names the idol-objects as detestable, putting the vocabulary squarely in the M27 register of concrete abominations. (3) bdelugma (G0946, 2V — Mat 24:15; Mar 13:14 — VCG-06) is shared with CHAR-3's NT bdelugma verses and points toward M27 (the desecration-event register). The vocabulary shared between CHAR-4 and M27 is particularly significant: the shiq.quts vocabulary names the idol-objects themselves, making CHAR-4's inner-being dimension (devotion to idol-objects) directly connected to M27's concrete-object register.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Yes. (1) a.ven (H0205G) is shared with M27 (calamity/ruin) through the VCG-01 trouble-suffered register: Psa 55:3 (VCG-01), Psa 55:10 (VCG-01), Hab 1:3 (VCG-01), Zec 10:2 (VCG-01) — here a.ven names the trouble/calamity that falls on victims, which is M27 register. (2) ro.a (H7455, 13V VCG-05) — the evil-deeds sub-corpus shares vocabulary with M27 and adjacent clusters addressing the moral quality of deeds. (3) The evildoer vocabulary (po.al a.ven — "workers of iniquity") in VCG-03 connects with CHAR-1's ra.sha (wicked person) at the person-type level, though the terms are distinct. (4) The trouble/distress register of a.ven (VCG-01) shares with M03 (grief/sorrow) through Neh 2:2 and Ecc 7:3 (which are flag-only minorities in the corpus).

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Yes. (1) blasfēmeō (G0987, 11V) — the primary term shares with M06 (contempt / hostile speech), as flagged in §2. The blasfēmeō field covers what M06 analyses from the relational-contempt angle. (2) kakopoios (G2555, 5V — VCG-03) — "evil-doer" vocabulary connects with CHAR-1 (wickedness as settled person-identity, using ra.sha in Hebrew) and CHAR-2 (evil as constitutional inner nature, using ponēros/kakos in Greek). The kakopoios term in VCG-03 is specifically the charged-identity dimension — the evildoer as accusation-target — which bridges to the wickedness and evil characteristics through the common evil-doer person-type. (3) atopos (G0824, 1V — Act 25:5 — VCG-03) — a legal term with no significant cross-register sharing beyond its specific judicial context.

---

##### T6.4.2 — Does vocabulary sharing extend to root-level architecture — a shared root that generates terms across two or more characteristics?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The ra.sha root generates both ra.sha (the adjective/noun for the wicked person — H7563) and re.sha (the abstract noun for wickedness — H7562) — this is a root-level architecture shared within the characteristic's own vocabulary suite. The root RSH (resh-shin) generates the person-type and the condition-type simultaneously, which confirms the tight analytical connection between the person (ra.sha) and their characteristic condition (re.sha). At the cross-characteristic level, ra.sha in the forensic-verdict register shares root-architecture with the M10 (sin-act) cluster's legal vocabulary — the same root naming inner moral character AND legal guilt status is analytically significant: it implies that the biblical authors saw the inner moral orientation and the legal status as aspects of a single reality (the wicked person is the legally condemnable person because their inner character is the source of their culpability).

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The Greek vocabulary does not share a single unifying root in the same way as the Hebrew RSH root in CHAR-1. However, ponēros/ponēria share the root poneros (from ponos, "toil/hardship" — the word family originally named the painful laboriousness of evil before becoming a moral-quality term). kakia shares its root with kakos (bad, evil as quality), which generates kaka (bad things), kakopoios (evildoer — CHAR-6), kakologeō (to speak evil). The kakos root generates vocabulary used across M10b's CHAR-6 (kakopoios). The poneros root generates ponēros (CHAR-2 primary) and ponēria (also CHAR-2). These root families share vocabulary across characteristics in the cluster.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The Greek root bdeo (to stink) generates bdelugma (G0946 — abomination as noun), bdeluktos (G0947 — detestable as adjective), and bdelyssomai (G0948 — to detest, used in Rom 2:22 outside this corpus). This root family generates the NT abomination vocabulary consistently across both CHAR-3 and CHAR-4. The Hebrew to.e.vah (H8441) is a single-term root generating noun forms only — the root does not generate the same range of grammatical forms as the Greek bdeo root. The Greek architecture is thus more morphologically developed than the Hebrew, generating noun, adjective, and verb forms.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The to.e.vah vocabulary (shared with CHAR-3) operates at the noun level with no verb form in the corpus — the same single-noun root architecture as CHAR-3. shiq.quts (H8251) is a nominal form from the root sh-q-ts (to loathe, to regard as abominable) — the same root generates: shiq.quts (the detestable thing), shaqats (to abhor), and sheqets (loathed thing). This root architecture makes shiq.quts the object-noun (the detestable idol-thing) of a verbal root of loathing. The root-level analysis reveals that shiq.quts names the idol not as a neutral object but as an object-of-loathing — the idol is defined by its quality of being loathsome. This root architecture directly connects CHAR-4's idol-objects with the divine response of revulsion.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

a.ven (H0205G) is a root that generates nominal forms spanning emptiness, trouble, iniquity, and sorrow — a broad root architecture that connects CHAR-5 to M03 and M27 through shared root. The same root a-w-n generates a.ven's entire semantic range without additional derived forms; the polysemy is concentrated in the single term. ro.a (H7455) is a nominal from the root r-'-' (ra.a — to be evil/bad/harmful) — the same root that generates ra.sha (H7563 — the wicked person, CHAR-1's primary term). This root connection reveals that CHAR-5's evil-deeds vocabulary (ro.a) and CHAR-1's settled-identity vocabulary (ra.sha) share a root — the ra.a root generating both the quality-of-deeds dimension (ro.a) and the person-identity dimension (ra.sha).

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

blasfēmeō (G0987) — from blapto (to harm) + phēmē (speech, reputation). The phēmē root connects to other speech-vocabulary in the NT (euphēmia — good speech; dysphēmia — ill speech — in 1Cor 4:13 context). The blapto root (harm) connects to the harm-vocabulary field but not to a specific shared programme-vocabulary. kakopoios (G2555) — from kakos (evil) + poieo (do/make); the kakos root is shared with CHAR-2 (kakia — G2549, ponēria — G4189 — all from the bad/evil root). At root level, kakopoios (CHAR-6) and kakia/kakos (CHAR-2) share the ka- root of evil/bad — showing a root-level connection between evil expressed through speech (as charged identity — CHAR-6 VCG-03) and evil as constitutional inner nature (CHAR-2).

---

##### T6.4.3 — What does vocabulary sharing reveal about the conceptual relationship between characteristics?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The vocabulary sharing between ra.sha-as-person-type (M10b) and ra.sha-as-legal-status (M10 cross-register) reveals a conceptual relationship of derivation: the legal guilt status (M10) is derived from and grounded in the inner moral character orientation (M10b). The legal declaration "wicked" (M10b-A-VCG-01) names a status that is consequential upon the inner disposition — the forensic verdict follows from and confirms the moral character. This conceptual derivation has implications for understanding both clusters: the sin-act that generates legal guilt (M10) is not merely external behaviour but the outward expression of the inner moral person-orientation (M10b-A).

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The vocabulary sharing between adikia (CHAR-2) and the forensic-legal register (M10) reveals the same conceptual relationship as CHAR-1's ra.sha cross-register: constitutional inner unrighteousness (adikia as CHAR-2) is the inner condition from which moral-legal offense (adikia in the M10 forensic register) flows. The shared root expresses that the inner condition and its outward-legal expression are aspects of a single reality. The kakia/kakos root-sharing with CHAR-6 (kakopoios — evildoer) reveals that the inner settled badness (kakia — CHAR-2) and the outward evil-doing person-type (kakopoios — CHAR-6) are root-related — the constitutional badness (kakia) produces and characterises the evildoer (kakopoios).

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The to.e.vah vocabulary sharing between CHAR-3 (moral-character abomination) and CHAR-4 (idolatrous abomination) reveals that the biblical authors used a single concept-term (to.e.vah) to cover both moral-character and idolatrous violations — treating them as aspects of a single category of divine revulsion. The programmatic separation into CHAR-3 and CHAR-4 is analytically necessary (the inner-being content differs significantly) but the vocabulary sharing confirms that in the biblical mind the two registers are species of the same genus (that which provokes divine revulsion by violating divine holiness). The ra.sha vocabulary sharing within CHAR-3's corpus (Pro 15:8; 15:9; 17:15 — VCG-01 and VCG-03) confirms the conceptual relationship between CHAR-1 (wickedness) and CHAR-3 (abomination): the wicked person is specifically the person whose inner condition triggers abomination-verdict.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The to.e.vah sharing with CHAR-3 confirms that both characteristics are species of the same genus: divine revulsion at human moral-spiritual failure, with CHAR-3 addressing the moral-character register and CHAR-4 the idolatrous-devotion register. The shiq.quts sharing with M27 reveals that CHAR-4's inner-being dimension (the heart's devotion to idols) is directly linked to the concrete-object dimension (the idol as a thing of loathing): the inner devotion cannot be separated from the objects to which it attaches. The vocabulary connecting inner-being (to.e.vah as quality of the inner person's practice) with object-category (shiq.quts as the detestable idol-object) confirms that CHAR-4 describes a specifically object-directed inner attachment — the characteristic cannot be understood without reference to both the inner devotion and the external object to which it is misdirected.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The a.ven root sharing with M27 and M03 reveals that the biblical writers used a single vocabulary field (emptiness-trouble-iniquity) to cover both the agent's inner scheming and the victim's received affliction — these are opposite ends of the same harm-event, treated as aspects of the same concept. The ro.a/ra.sha root sharing confirms the conceptual relationship between CHAR-5 (active scheming process) and CHAR-1 (settled wicked identity): both are aspects of the same root concept of evil, with CHAR-5 naming the process and CHAR-1 naming the character-state that the process produces. The vocabulary sharing reveals these characteristics as analytically distinct but conceptually related aspects of a single moral-theological domain.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The blasfēmeō sharing with M06 confirms that CHAR-6 and M06 address the same speech-contempt domain from different analytical angles: CHAR-6 as the inner-wickedness expression; M06 as the contemptuous relational act. The kakopoios/kakos root sharing confirms the conceptual relationship between CHAR-6 (evil-doer as charged identity in VCG-03) and CHAR-2 (evil as constitutional inner nature): the person accused as kakopoios is accused of being what CHAR-2's person-type is constitutionally — the two characteristics are conceptually related through the same evil-doer concept at the person-type level.

---

#### T6.5 — Distinctions

##### T6.5.1 — Which adjacent characteristic most closely resembles this one — and what precisely distinguishes them?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The closest adjacent characteristic within M10b is Characteristic 5 (M10b-E — Iniquity as active inner scheming). Both address inner moral corruption and the wicked person's inner activity. The precise distinction: M10b-A (CHAR-1) describes the wicked person as an established type — a settled identity. M10b-E describes iniquity as an active generative process — evil being conceived, schemed, and enacted. CHAR-1's primary question is "who is this person at the inner-being level?" M10b-E's primary question is "what is this person actively doing inside?" The relationship is that the settled wicked person (CHAR-1) is the person whose characteristic internal activity is the scheming and generation of evil (M10b-E) — CHAR-1 names the identity, M10b-E names the activity that constitutes and expresses it.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

CHAR-1 (Wickedness as settled person-identity) is the closest adjacent characteristic — both address the evil inner person. The precise distinction: CHAR-1 (ra.sha) describes wickedness as a settled volitional identity — the person whose will has consolidated in a direction away from God. CHAR-2 (ponēros/kakia/adikia) describes evil as the constitutional condition that precedes and enables that volitional orientation — the structural state of the inner person from which corrupt choices flow. CHAR-1 is primarily volitional-directional ("the path the wicked walks"); CHAR-2 is primarily constitutional-structural ("the nature of the diseased tree"). CHAR-1 is an OT Hebrew characterisation of the person-type; CHAR-2 is a NT Greek characterisation of the structural condition. They are analytically related as tree-condition (CHAR-2) to tree-direction (CHAR-1).

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

CHAR-4 (Abomination — idolatrous abomination) is the most immediately adjacent and structurally similar characteristic — both use to.e.vah/bdelugma vocabulary, both involve the divine-revulsion verdict, and both address violations of divine holiness. The precise distinction: CHAR-3's abomination is directed at corrupt moral character and ethical failure (inner dispositions and practices — crooked heart, lying lips, dishonest commerce, perverted judgment). CHAR-4's abomination is directed at idolatrous devotion — the act of worshipping other gods, making and using idols. The distinction is of content: what is found abominable — moral character corruption (CHAR-3) vs. idolatrous allegiance (CHAR-4). CHAR-1 (wickedness as settled person-identity) is the second closest — the wicked person appears throughout CHAR-3's evidence as the subject of abomination, but CHAR-1 names the inner orientation while CHAR-3 names the divine-relational verdict on that orientation.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

CHAR-3 (Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character) is the most immediately adjacent and structurally similar characteristic. Both CHAR-3 and CHAR-4 use to.e.vah/bdelugma vocabulary; both involve the divine-revulsion verdict; both address violations of divine holiness. The precise distinction: CHAR-3's abomination is rooted in moral-character corruption (crooked heart, lying lips, perverted judgment, dishonest practice). CHAR-4's abomination is rooted in idolatrous devotion — the will's attachment to idol-objects rather than to God. The distinction is one of content: what is abominable — inner moral-character corruption (CHAR-3) vs. misdirected devotion to false gods (CHAR-4). Both produce divine revulsion; the inner-being mechanism differs: CHAR-3 is primarily about moral character; CHAR-4 is primarily about volitional devotion-direction.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

CHAR-1 (Wickedness as settled person-identity) is the most immediately adjacent. Both CHAR-5 and CHAR-1 address the evildoer as a person-type, both involve the inner moral character producing evil outcomes, and both accumulate into a settled inner condition. The precise distinction: CHAR-1 addresses wickedness as a settled person-identity (ra.sha vocabulary — the settled orientation of the will as defining the person's identity). CHAR-5 addresses iniquity as an active inner process of scheming and generating evil (a.ven vocabulary — the ongoing cognitive-volitional activity of devising harm). CHAR-1 names what the person is; CHAR-5 names what the person's inner life does. The distinction is between the settled identity (CHAR-1) and the active generative process (CHAR-5).

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

CHAR-1 (Wickedness as settled person-identity) is the most immediately adjacent in terms of the inner-character source — both CHAR-1 and CHAR-6 address the wicked inner character's expression, but CHAR-1 names the settled identity and CHAR-6 names the speech-expression of that identity. The M06 cross-register (contempt/hostile speech) is the closest in terms of the speech act itself. The precise distinction from CHAR-1: CHAR-1 names the settled dispositional wickedness (the ra.sha inner orientation); CHAR-6 names the specific mode of expression through speech — blasphemy, slander, and false accusation as the verbal instruments of inner wickedness. The distinction from M06: M06 names the contemptuous relational act; CHAR-6 names the inner wickedness that the contemptuous act expresses. CHAR-6 sits between CHAR-1 (inner source) and M06 (relational act) as the expression-linkage.

---

##### T6.5.2 — Where the evidence shows apparent overlap, what is the precise boundary?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The precise boundary is between person-type (CHAR-1) and activity-type (M10b-E). When a verse uses ra.sha (person term — H7563), it is naming the wicked person as a type regardless of the specific activity being described. When a verse uses a.ven (iniquity/trouble — H0205G), it is naming the inner generative activity (scheming, plotting, conceiving evil). The boundary is lexical and conceptual: ra.sha is the person; a.ven is what that person is generating. The overlap appears in VCG-03 (CHAR-1 — the wicked person plotting, Psa 37:12) and M10b-E-VCG-02 (iniquity as scheming, Psa 36:4) — both locate inner scheming, but CHAR-1's VCG-03 is framed around the person-type ("the wicked"), while M10b-E addresses the generative process without necessarily naming the person-type.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The overlap is most visible in the person-identity VCGs of both characteristics — CHAR-1's VCG-04 (settled deep character of persons) and CHAR-2's VCG-04 (evil as settled deep character) address the same persons using related language. The precise boundary: in CHAR-1, the ra.sha verses address the wicked person as someone whose inner orientation is directed away from God (Psa 36:1 — transgression speaking as inner voice; Eze 33:11 — a way that can be turned from). In CHAR-2, the ponēros/kakia verses address the evil person as someone whose inner structure produces evil as constitutional output (Mat 7:17-18 — diseased tree cannot produce good fruit). The boundary is: CHAR-1 describes what the person has chosen and consolidated; CHAR-2 describes what the person is constituted as at the structural level.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The Deu 27:15 (vc=65937 — VCG-04) verse is the most boundary-challenging: a secretly made idol is named as abominable, placing it near CHAR-4's idolatrous register. The verse is assigned to CHAR-3 because its inner-being content focuses on the conscience: "sets it up in secret" — the secrecy reveals that the heart knows the act is wrong even while the will proceeds. The primary inner-being contribution is conscience-suppression rather than idolatrous devotion per se. Similarly, Isa 41:24 (vc=65960 — VCG-05) and Isa 44:19 (vc=65961 — VCG-05) involve idol-choices but their primary inner-being content is the absence of discernment and the quality of the will's choice — assigned to CHAR-3 for their conscience/discernment content. The boundary is: if the primary inner-being content is the moral-character quality of the person making the choice, CHAR-3; if the primary content is the idolatrous devotion itself, CHAR-4.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The boundary verses in this characteristic's corpus that touch CHAR-3 territory: Eze 18:12 (vc=65992 — VCG-05): "lifts up his eyes to the idols, commits abomination" — here abomination is listed alongside oppression and robbery, combining CHAR-4's idolatrous dimension with CHAR-3's ethical-violation dimension. The boundary is: if the primary inner-being content is devotion to a false god or idol-object, CHAR-4; if the primary content is a moral-character quality (pride, dishonesty) independent of idol-attachment, CHAR-3. The overlap verse Eze 18:12 (VCG-05) is assigned to CHAR-4 because the immediate context ("lifts up his eyes to the idols") is idolatrous. The boundary is content-based: the idol-attachment as the abomination's anchor determines CHAR-4; the moral-character quality as the anchor determines CHAR-3.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The overlap appears most clearly in VCG-03 (24V — evildoer class), where the evildoer-type appears as a character-identity category rather than as an active scheming description. Verses like Psa 92:7 (vc=38246 — VCG-03: "evildoers flourish… doomed to destruction") describe the evildoer's trajectory without specifically naming active scheming — these could also serve CHAR-1. The boundary: if the primary inner-being content is the active inner process of devising, conceiving, and plotting (VCG-02 — the scheming mode), CHAR-5; if the primary content is the settled identity/orientation of the wicked person without specific attention to the generative process, CHAR-1. VCG-03 sits at the boundary and serves CHAR-5 because the evildoer class is understood as constituted by the active working of iniquity (VCG-03's "workers of evil" language — Psa 6:8; 59:2; etc. — emphasising active habitual practice).

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The boundary with M06: Jude 8 (VCG-01): "reject authority and blaspheme the glorious ones" — the authority-rejection is the M06-adjacent element (contemptuous defiant rejection); the blasphemy of the glorious ones is the CHAR-6 element (evil expressed through speech directed at spiritual beings). The boundary is: if the primary inner-being content is the contemptuous relational stance of rejection/defiance, M06; if the primary content is the speech act as the vehicle of inner wickedness, CHAR-6. The boundary with CHAR-1: if the primary content is the settled wicked identity of the person, CHAR-1; if the primary content is the speech-expression of that identity, CHAR-6. VCG-03's kakopoios (evildoer as charged identity) sits at the CHAR-1/CHAR-6 boundary — it is used in VCG-03 specifically as a charged verbal accusation (CHAR-6), not as a description of the person's actual settled identity (CHAR-1).

---

##### T6.5.3 — Is the distinction between this characteristic and its nearest neighbour one of degree, kind, direction, or constitutional level?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The distinction is primarily one of kind: CHAR-1 is a person-type characteristic (who the person is), while M10b-E is an activity-type characteristic (what the inner person generates). They address different analytical questions about the same inner reality. The distinction is not of degree (one is not more or less wicked than the other) or constitutional level (both operate at the same heart/soul/mind level) or direction (both are outwardly oriented in their consequences). It is a categorical distinction between identity and activity as analytical frames for the same inner-being domain.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The distinction is primarily one of kind and constitutional level. Kind: CHAR-1 is a person-identity category (the wicked person as a type), while CHAR-2 is a structural-condition category (the evil constitutional nature as the condition from which the person-identity flows). Constitutional level: CHAR-1 operates at the level of the settled will and its directional orientation; CHAR-2 operates at the deeper constitutional level of the generative inner architecture that precedes and shapes the will's options. The distinction is not of degree (more or less wicked) or direction (different moral directions) but of analytical depth: CHAR-2 describes the constitutional condition; CHAR-1 describes the settled orientation that the condition makes probable.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The distinction from CHAR-4 is one of kind: different contents of what is found abominable (moral character corruption vs. idolatrous allegiance), not different degrees or constitutional levels of the same content. Both CHAR-3 and CHAR-4 operate at the same constitutional level (the inner person's character and allegiance before God) and both involve the same divine-revulsion response mechanism — what differs is the object of the divine revulsion. The distinction from CHAR-1 is one of direction and perspective: CHAR-1 describes wickedness from the human-inner side (the settled orientation of the will away from God); CHAR-3 describes the same reality from the divine-relational side (the verdict of revulsion on that orientation).

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The distinction from CHAR-3 is one of kind: different contents of what is abominable (idolatrous devotion vs. moral-character corruption), not different degrees of abomination. Both operate at the same constitutional level (inner person before God) and both involve the same divine-revulsion mechanism. What differs is the object that triggers the divine revulsion: misdirected devotion to idols (CHAR-4) vs. morally corrupt inner character (CHAR-3). The distinction is categorical/kind, not gradational/degree, directional, or level-based.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The distinction is one of kind: different aspects of the same moral domain (wickedness/evil) are named. CHAR-1 names the settled dispositional identity; CHAR-5 names the active generative process. Both operate at the same constitutional level (inner person before God) and in the same moral domain. The distinction is not gradational (CHAR-5 is not more evil than CHAR-1 or vice versa) nor directional (both involve inner-to-outer movement) nor level-based (both are at the inner constitutional level). It is a categorical distinction between what the person is (CHAR-1) and what the person's inner life does (CHAR-5).

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The distinction from M06 is one of analytical angle (not degree, kind, or level): same speech-contempt phenomenon analysed from the inner-expression angle (CHAR-6) versus the relational-act angle (M06). The distinction from CHAR-1 is one of mode: CHAR-1 names the inner identity; CHAR-6 names one specific expressive mode of that identity (through speech). This is a mode-distinction rather than degree, kind, or level — the same inner wickedness can be named as settled identity (CHAR-1) or as speech-expression (CHAR-6); both are correct from their respective analytical angles.

---

#### T6.6 — Shared Verse Anchors

##### T6.6.1 — Does any verse in this characteristic's evidence base also function as a primary anchor in another characteristic's study?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The most analytically significant shared anchor is Psa 36:1 (vc=42567 — M10b-A-VCG-02 anchor candidate), which is also a potential M26 (Righteousness) anchor given its structural importance for understanding the relationship between God-fear and wickedness. Eze 33:11 (vc=42701 — M10b-A-VCG-07 anchor) is highly likely to function as a key anchor in M11 (repentance or moral turning) given its concentrated statement of the divine desire for the wicked to turn. Gen 18:23-25 (vc=42643/42644 — M10b-A-VCG-04) likely serves as an anchor for M26 (Righteousness) given the structural importance of the righteous/wicked distinction for the righteousness characteristic. Job 34:10 (vc=15525 — M10b-A-VCG-11) is a structural anchor for any study of divine holiness or moral perfection.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Several significant shared anchors are identifiable. Mat 12:34-35 (vc=14419-14420 — VCG-03) is highly likely to serve as a primary anchor for any cluster addressing the heart as a generative source (the treasury-of-heart principle has implications across multiple inner-being clusters). Mar 7:22-23 (vc=14409/14473/14422 — VCGs 03/05) is a primary anchor candidate for any cluster addressing the vice-catalogue from the heart — the heart as the origin of all moral defilement (Mar 7:23) is broadly significant. Heb 10:22 (vc=14426 — VCG-06) is significant for any conscience-focused cluster — the evil conscience as barrier to God and the cleansed conscience as enabling approach are central to any study of conscience (potentially M22 or equivalent). Rom 1:29 (vc=14336-14338 — VCG-05) is a primary anchor for multiple vice-saturation studies.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Probable shared anchors: Pro 3:32 (vc=1686 — VCG-02) is a strong candidate as a primary anchor for any study addressing the relational intimacy of divine confidence — the contrast between "abomination to the Lord" (exclusion) and "upright are in his confidence" (inclusion) is foundational for understanding divine-human relational intimacy. Pro 15:8 (vc=1678 — VCG-03) is a strong anchor candidate for any study of worship integrity — the wicked person's sacrifice as abomination captures the worship-inner-character interface precisely. Eze 9:4 (vc=1698 — VCG-04) is a candidate for any conscience-study — the mark given to those who grieve over abominations is a central conscience-function evidence point. Jer 6:15 and 8:12 (vc=1680; 1696 — VCG-04) are candidates for any conscience-silencing study.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Probable shared anchors: Eze 11:21 (vc=1631 — VCG-05) — "whose heart goes after their detestable things and their abominations" — is a strong candidate as an anchor for any study addressing the heart's directional faculty. Hos 9:10 (vc=1632 — VCG-04) — "they became detestable like the thing they loved" — is likely a significant anchor for any study on the formative power of devotion (the person is shaped by what they love), which has implications across many positive characteristics as well. Dan 9:27 / Mat 24:15 (vc=65914; 65876 — VCG-06) are anchors for eschatological studies within M27. Deu 7:25 (vc=1682 — VCG-02) is a candidate for any study on covetousness or the ensnaring power of attractive objects.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Probable shared anchors: Psa 66:18 (vc=38182 — VCG-04): "if I had cherished iniquity in my heart, the Lord would not have listened" — is a strong anchor for any study of prayer, divine hearing, or the conditions of approach to God. Psa 7:14 (vc=38245 — VCG-02): "conceives evil… pregnant with mischief… gives birth to lies" — is a candidate for any study on the inner generative process of evil or on the relationship between inner moral condition and deceptive speech. Mic 2:1 (vc=38217 — VCG-02): "devise wickedness on their beds; when the morning dawns, they perform it" — is a candidate for any study on the relationship between cognitive planning and bodily execution. Isa 59:7 (vc=38203 — VCG-02): "thoughts are thoughts of iniquity; feet run to evil" — is a candidate for any study on the cognitive-volitional link to violent action.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Probable shared anchors: Jude 8 (vc=14354 — VCG-01) is likely an anchor for M06 (contempt/hostile speech/defiant rejection of authority) — the authority-rejection and blasphemy of the glorious ones serves both characteristics. Rev 13:6 (vc=14356 — VCG-01) is the most concentrated beast-blasphemy evidence, likely serving any eschatological/apocalyptic study. Joh 18:30 (vc=14378 — VCG-03) is a high-significance anchor for the christological narrative — the false charge against Jesus is foundational for understanding false accusation in the NT. 1Pe 2:12 (vc=14377 — VCG-03) is likely an anchor for any study of conduct, testimony, and the relationship between behaviour and God's honour.

---

##### T6.6.2 — What does the shared anchor reveal about the relationship between the two characteristics?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The Eze 33:11 shared anchor (potential M11 repentance anchor) reveals that the wicked person's possible turning is constitutively connected to the characteristic of repentance: the Ezekiel corpus's call to the wicked to turn is simultaneously a definition of wickedness (as a reversible volitional direction) and a description of repentance (as the characteristic movement away from wickedness toward life). The Gen 18:23-25 shared anchor (potential M26 righteousness anchor) reveals that righteousness and wickedness are definitionally co-present — you cannot define one without the other; they are structurally interdependent characteristics. The Psa 36:1 shared anchor reveals the connection between wickedness-as-settled-identity and the absence of God-fear as a characteristic.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The Mar 7:22-23 shared anchor reveals a structural relationship between CHAR-2 (evil as constitutional inner nature) and any heart-generative characteristic: the heart that produces evil (CHAR-2) is the same faculty whose generative function, when rightly ordered, produces other characteristics. The shared-heart-generative-function reveals CHAR-2 as the corruption of a faculty that is, when uncorrupted, the generative source of positive inner-being characteristics. Heb 10:22's shared conscience anchor reveals the structural relationship between CHAR-2 and the conscience characteristic: the evil conscience (CHAR-2's impact on the conscience) is the specific inner state addressed by the new covenant's cleansing, connecting CHAR-2 to any cluster studying the conscience's restoration.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Pro 3:32 as a shared anchor (if it serves CHAR-3 and any divine-intimacy characteristic) reveals that abomination is the antithesis of divine-relational intimacy — the two characteristics (abomination as exclusion and divine-confidence intimacy) are structural polar opposites constituted by the same verse. Pro 15:8 as a shared anchor reveals the relationship between CHAR-3 and any worship-integrity characteristic: the corrupt inner person's approach to God is a specific instance of the abomination category, showing that worship becomes a site of abomination when the worshipping person's inner character is abominable. Eze 9:4 as a shared conscience anchor shows that the grieving conscience is a marker of both abomination-awareness (CHAR-3) and conscience-function (whichever characteristic conscience falls under in the programme).

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Hos 9:10 as a potential shared anchor reveals the relationship between CHAR-4 (idolatrous abomination) and any characteristic addressing character-formation: the principle "became like the thing they loved" applies inversely to positive characteristics — those who love God are formed toward God's likeness. The shared anchor reveals that the formation mechanism (devotion shapes character) operates for both positive and negative outcomes; CHAR-4 documents its negative operation while positive characteristics will document its positive operation. Eze 11:21 as a shared anchor reveals the heart's directional faculty as a site of both covenant fidelity (heart going after God) and idolatrous defection (heart going after idols) — a faculty that appears across multiple characteristics.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Psa 66:18 as a shared anchor (if it also serves prayer-relationship studies) reveals that the prayer/divine-hearing relationship is directly damaged by inner cherished iniquity — the two characteristics are in a negative causal relationship: iniquity-scheming blocks prayer; prayer-relationship requires released iniquity. Psa 7:14 as a shared anchor (if serving speech/deception studies) reveals that active inner scheming and deceptive speech are not merely co-occurring but causally linked — the scheming generates the deceptive speech as its born output. Mic 2:1 as shared anchor (cognitive-to-bodily studies) reveals the tight coupling between cognitive planning and immediate bodily execution in the characteristic's inner-outer movement.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Jude 8 as a shared anchor with M06 reveals that authority-rejection and blasphemous speech are two faces of the same inner disposition: the contemptuous defiance of M06 finds its speech-expression in CHAR-6's blasphemy. They are not merely co-occurring but causally linked in the same verse: the authority-rejection generates the blasphemous expression. Joh 18:30 as a shared anchor with christological studies reveals that CHAR-6's false-accusation mode is embedded in the pivotal moment of Christ's trial — the characteristic of false accusation is christologically significant as the verbal instrument through which the innocent was condemned. 1Pe 2:12 as a shared anchor with conduct/testimony studies reveals that the social-testimonial dimension of conduct is the antidote to false accusation: honourable conduct addresses the characteristic's social impact.
