#### T6.7 — Dimensional Sharing

##### T6.7.1 — How many of this characteristic's confirmed analytical dimensions are shared with another characteristic in the programme?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (G)

Full dimensional-sharing data requires completed Phase 9 analysis across all M10b characteristics (and comparison with other clusters), which is not available at this stage. What can be noted from the evidence: the volitional dimension (primary classification — T1.8.1) is likely shared with M26 (Righteousness — also volitional in its primary dimension), M10b-E (Iniquity — volitional scheming), and M11 (repentance/turning — the volitional reversal). The affective dimension (T1.8.3 secondary) is likely shared with M03 (Grief), M01 (Fear), and M04 (Joy) given the characteristic's engagement with the affective faculty. The full dimensional-sharing picture is a G — gap requiring cross-cluster synthesis data.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (G)

Full dimensional-sharing data requires completed Phase 9 analysis across all M10b characteristics and cross-cluster comparison, which is not yet available. Partial picture from the evidence: the constitutional-structural dimension is likely unique to CHAR-2 within M10b (CHAR-1 is volitional-directional; CHARs 3-6 are specific-domain characteristics). The affective secondary dimension (envy, pride — Mat 20:15; Jam 4:16 — VCG-06) is likely shared with M01 (Fear), M02 (Anger), M03 (Grief), M04 (Joy) as all engaging the affective faculty. The cognitive secondary dimension (Col 1:21; 1Ti 6:4 — VCG-06) is likely shared with M15 (Wisdom) as its structural opposite. Full synthesis deferred to Session D.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (G)

Full dimensional-sharing data requires completed Phase 9 analysis across all M10b characteristics and cross-cluster comparison, which is not yet available. Partial picture: the relational-moral primary dimension (divine revulsion as the constitutive response) is likely unique to CHAR-3 within the programme — no other characteristic identified so far has the divine-relational verdict as its primary dimension. The secondary dispositional dimension (crooked heart, arrogant heart) is likely shared with CHAR-1 (volitional-dispositional) and CHAR-2 (constitutional-structural). The conscience secondary dimension is likely shared with whichever programme cluster specifically addresses conscience. Full synthesis deferred to Session D.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (G)

Full dimensional-sharing data requires completed Phase 9 analysis across all M10b characteristics and cross-cluster comparison, not yet available. Partial picture: the volitional-devotional primary dimension appears unique to CHAR-4 within M10b — no other characteristic has the volitional-devotional misdirection as its primary dimension. The affective secondary dimension (soul-delight in abominations — Isa 66:3) is likely shared with M04 (Joy) as its structural opposite — the soul that delights in abominations rather than in God. The constitutional-formative secondary dimension (Hos 9:10 — becoming like the idol) is likely shared with any characteristic addressing character-formation by sustained devoted attention. Full synthesis deferred to Session D.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (G)

Full dimensional-sharing data requires completed Phase 9 analysis across all M10b characteristics and cross-cluster comparison, not yet available. Partial picture: the cognitive-volitional-generative primary dimension appears distinctive to CHAR-5 within M10b — no other completed M10b characteristic has the active cognitive-scheming-and-generating process as its primary dimension. The dispositional-character secondary dimension is likely shared with CHAR-1. The accumulated-condition secondary dimension may be shared with M10c or M10 characteristics. Full synthesis deferred to Session D.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (G)

Full dimensional-sharing data requires completed Phase 9 analysis across all M10b characteristics and cross-cluster comparison, not yet available. Partial picture: the volitional-expressive primary dimension appears unique to CHAR-6 within M10b — no other completed M10b characteristic has the will's expression through speech as its primary dimension. The will-hardening that emerges in CHAR-6's VCG-01 shares the volitional hardening dimension with CHAR-1. Full synthesis deferred to Session D.

## T7 — Lexical, Literary, and Scientific Analysis (20 prompts)

---

### T7

#### T7.1 — Lexical and Semantic Analysis

##### T7.1.1 — What are the primary Hebrew and Greek terms for this characteristic — and what do their root meanings reveal?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Primary Hebrew terms: ra.sha (H7563, 179V) — the adjective/noun for the wicked person; re.sha (H7562, 9V) — abstract noun, wickedness as condition; mir.sha.at (H4849, 1V) — collective noun, wicked-woman-type. Secondary: ro.a (H7455, 1V — 1Sa 17:28). The RSH root (resh-shin-ayin) is the generative root. RSH connotes a fundamental moral wrongness or badness — it is not primarily a legal term in its root but a character-quality term designating the person whose inner moral orientation is bad, wrong, or wicked. The root generates ra.sha (the wicked person), re.sha (wickedness as abstract condition), and rasha' (the verb "to act wickedly" — the root's verbal form, as in Dan 12:10: "the wicked shall act wickedly"). At the root level, RSH is a moral-character assessment: the person defined by what is fundamentally wrong in their inner orientation. No Greek term is primary for CHAR-1 — this characteristic is predominantly a Hebrew-OT phenomenon; the Greek evidence base for M10b belongs primarily to Characteristics 2 (ponēros, kakia) and 6 (blasfēmeō, kakopoios) rather than to CHAR-1.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

This characteristic is exclusively NT Greek in its evidence base (90V — no Hebrew OT verses assigned; this is the key vocabulary distinction from CHAR-1). Primary terms: ponēros (G4190, 63V) — from the root ponos (toil, hardship, pain) — originally naming what is laborious or painful, which developed into a moral-quality term for what is evil in its character, harmful in its effects, and wicked in its inner orientation. kakia (G2549, 11V) — from kakos (bad, evil as a quality) — naming settled inner badness, malice, and ill-will as a character trait. adikia (G0093, 8V) — from a- (not) + dikē (justice, right) — naming the structural condition of not-rightness; unrighteousness as the constitutional state of being at odds with the right order. ponēria (G4189, 7V) — from the same root as ponēros but a feminine abstract noun naming wickedness, villainy, active malice as a condition. faulos (G5337, 1V) — from an alternative root meaning cheap, worthless, bad — applied to morally deficient deeds. Root meanings reveal: the characteristic is named from both the painful quality of evil (ponos root) and the structural wrongness (a-dikē) — it is evil as what is constitutionally deficient and wrong.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Primary Hebrew: to.e.vah (H8441, ~35V) — the primary abomination term covering both moral-character (M10b-C = CHAR-3) and idolatrous (M10b-D = CHAR-4) registers. The root etymology of to.e.vah is uncertain — possibly connected to a verb meaning to loathe or turn away from with revulsion. At root level, to.e.vah names that which provokes active turning-away in revulsion — the opposite of what attracts or draws near. Primary Greek: bdelugma (G0946, 4V — Luk 16:15; Rev 17:4; 17:5; 21:27) — from bdeo (to stink); names what is repugnant through its stench-quality, the morally-putrid. bdeluktos (G0947, 1V — Tit 1:16) — the adjectival form: the detestable, the stench-bearing person. The root revelation: Hebrew to.e.vah emphasises the relational dimension (what prompts revulsion and turning-away); Greek bdeo root emphasises the sensory-disgust dimension (what stinks, what is putrid). Together they name abomination as both relationally rejecting and sensory-revolting.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Primary Hebrew: to.e.vah (H8441, ~72V idolatrous sub-corpus) — see CHAR-3 T7.1.1 for root analysis. Applied to the idolatrous register, to.e.vah names the divine revulsion at idolatrous practices (Deu 12:31 — VCG-02: "every abominable thing that the Lord hates they have done for their gods"). shiq.quts (H8251, 25V) — from the root sh-q-ts (to loathe, abhor). The shiq.quts root generates: shiq.quts (noun — the detestable idol-thing), shaqats (verbal — to abhor, to make/regard as unclean). Root meaning: that which is loathed, the object of abhorrence. Applied to idols, shiq.quts names the foreign deity or idol-object specifically as an abhorrent thing — not merely wrong but inherently disgusting. 1Ki 11:5 (vc=65898 — VCG-03): "Milcom the abomination (shiq.quts) of the Ammonites" — the foreign deity is named by its quality of being loathsome. Primary Greek: bdelugma (G0946, 2V — Mat 24:15; Mar 13:14 — VCG-06) — from bdeo (to stink) — the sacrilegious desolation event as what stinks in the moral-spiritual register.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Two primary Hebrew terms; no NT Greek terms in this corpus. a.ven (H0205G, 66V) — the root a-w-n denotes emptiness, nothingness, and trouble. At root level, a.ven names that which is morally empty-yet-harmful: the scheming of the wicked is empty of genuine moral substance (futile, hollow — the "worthless" quality of the evildoer in Pro 6:12 — VCG-03: "a worthless person, a wicked man") while simultaneously generating genuine trouble and harm. The root reveals a dual quality: inner moral vacuity paired with outward harmful productivity. ro.a (H7455, 13V evil-deeds sub-corpus) — from the root r-'-' (ra.a — to be evil, bad, harmful). The root names what is intrinsically bad in quality — not merely wrong by rule but harmful in essence. Applied to deeds (VCG-05), ro.a names the moral quality of acts whose inner source is wickedness: Jer 25:5 (vc=38445 — VCG-05): "evil way and evil deeds" — the way and the deeds both carry the ra.a quality. Root revelations: a.ven = empty-and-troubling; ro.a = intrinsically bad in quality.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

No OT Hebrew terms appear in the 17-verse corpus (exclusively NT Greek). Three Greek terms carry the characteristic. blasfēmeō (G0987, 11V) — from blapto (to harm, injure) + phēmē (speech, reputation). Root revelation: blasfēmeō names injurious speech — speech that harms a person's or God's standing/reputation. The root combines the harm-concept (blapto) with the speech-concept (phēmē) — the compound names exactly what the characteristic is: speech that harms. Rev 13:6 (vc=14356 — VCG-01): "utter blasphemies against God" — the verbal harm directed at the divine. kakopoios (G2555, 5V) — from kakos (evil/bad) + poieo (do/make): the evil-doer; the one whose actions are morally bad. Root revelation: the term names a person by the moral quality of their acts — the one who "makes bad." atopos (G0824, 1V — Act 25:5 — VCG-03) — from a (not) + topos (place): "out of place," irregular, improper. Root revelation: wrongdoing as that which is "out of place" in the moral-social order — a spatial-order metaphor for moral irregularity.

---

##### T7.1.2 — What is the grammatical range of the primary term (noun, verb, adjective, participle) — and what does that range reveal about how the characteristic operates?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

ra.sha (H7563) functions grammatically as both adjective ("wicked" — attributive to person) and noun ("the wicked [person]"). The verbal root rasha' appears in Dan 12:10 ("the wicked shall act wickedly" — vc=42664). This grammatical range reveals that the RSH root describes both what the person is (nominal/adjectival: the wicked man, the wicked as a class) and what they do (verbal: to act wickedly). The co-presence of adjectival/nominal and verbal forms confirms that wickedness in this tradition is both a person-type (what they are) and an activity (what they do) — though the nominal/adjectival usage is dominant in the corpus (179V of ra.sha and 9V of re.sha vs. the single verbal instance), confirming that the characteristic's primary reference is the person-identity rather than the act.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

ponēros (G4190) functions as: (1) adjective — "evil persons" (Mat 5:45 — VCG-04), "evil thoughts" (Mat 9:4 — VCG-03), "evil generation" (Mat 12:39 — VCG-02), "evil eye" (Mat 6:23 — VCG-03), "evil conscience" (Heb 10:22 — VCG-06); (2) substantive noun — "the evil one" (Mat 6:13 — VCG-01), "the evil" (Rom 12:9 — VCG-06), "evil people" (2Ti 3:13 — VCG-06); (3) neuter substantive — "evil things" (Luk 6:45 — VCG-03). This grammatical range reveals that ponēros operates across all the major grammatical categories of attribution (adjective describing a faculty/person/generation), hypostatisation (substantive noun naming the evil one or evil as a force), and abstract reference (naming evil things). The range confirms that ponēros is the most flexible and comprehensive of the characteristic's terms — naming the quality, the person, the cosmic force, and the abstraction.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

to.e.vah (H8441) functions exclusively as a noun in the 40-verse corpus — it names the category of abomination as a substantive ("an abomination to the Lord," "abominations"). There is no verbal form used in this corpus. The noun-only function reveals that the characteristic is primarily a categorical designation — it names a type of violation, not an action-verb. In contrast, the Greek bdelugma (G0946) is a noun (abomination as a thing/category), while bdeluktos (G0947) is an adjective applied to persons (Tit 1:16 — "they are detestable"). The grammatical range thus spans: noun (naming the category — to.e.vah, bdelugma) and adjective (naming the person-type who embodies the category — bdeluktos). The absence of a verbal form in the primary Hebrew term suggests abomination is conceived as a state or category rather than an act — the verdict that something is abominable, not the act of making it so.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

to.e.vah (H8441): noun-only in the corpus — the abomination as a category or quality. shiq.quts (H8251): noun-only in the corpus — the detestable idol-object as a substantive thing. The verbal root sh-q-ts does not appear in the CHAR-4 corpus, though it generates the nominal shiq.quts. This noun-only pattern across both primary Hebrew terms reveals that the characteristic is conceived as naming things (categories, objects, practices) rather than as naming actions. To.e.vah names the category of divine revulsion; shiq.quts names the specific detestable objects that provoke it. The absence of verbal forms in the corpus (no "to abominate" verb in use here) confirms that the characteristic names states and objects, not the act of performing abomination — the act belongs to M10c/M10.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

a.ven (H0205G) functions in the corpus primarily as a noun — naming iniquity as a substantive condition, object, or quality. The phrase po.al a.ven ("workers/doers of iniquity") treats a.ven as the object of the verb "to work" — showing iniquity as something that can be actively worked/produced. This noun-as-object-of-activity grammatical pattern confirms the characteristic's generative mode: iniquity is what is actively produced by the po.al ("workers"). The plural "abominations" (a.vanim) and compound constructions (Isa 59:7: "thoughts of iniquity") extend the range. ro.a (H7455) functions exclusively as a noun naming the quality-of-evil in the deeds, always in construct state: "evil of your deeds" (Deu 28:20 — VCG-05), "evil of their deeds" (Jer 23:2 — VCG-05) — a genitive construction naming the evil quality as a property of the deeds. The noun-quality range confirms ro.a as naming the moral character of expressed acts rather than an inner state or process.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

blasfēmeō (G0987) appears as a verb in all its occurrences in this corpus. The verbal form is significant: blasphemy is an act, not merely a state or quality — the verb names the speech event as an ongoing, enacted process. Rev 13:6 (vc=14356 — VCG-01): "opened its mouth to utter blasphemies against God, blaspheming his name" — both the infinitive and participial forms of the verb appear, showing sustained blasphemous action. The verb-only occurrence confirms the characteristic as constitutively an enacted speech-event rather than a static condition. kakopoios (G2555) appears as a noun (person-type term) in all five VCG-03 occurrences — the evildoer-person-type as a substantive category. atopos (G0824) appears as an adjective in Act 25:5 — "anything wrong (atopos) about the man" — modifying the act as "out-of-place."

---

##### T7.1.3 — What is the semantic range of the primary term — across what breadth of meaning does it operate?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

ra.sha's semantic range spans three registers evidenced in the 190-verse corpus: (1) inner moral character — the person whose deep inner orientation is wicked (the dominant register, ~174 of 179V); (2) legal-forensic status — the guilty, condemnable party in a judicial proceeding (M10b-A-VCG-01, ~5V: Exo 23:7; Deu 25:1, 25:2; 1Ki 8:32; 2Ch 6:23); (3) behavioral description — the man-in-the-wrong in an observed conflict (Exo 2:13 — VCG-04, a transitional instance). The semantic range thus spans from the deepest inner moral orientation (dominant) to the outer-observable behavioral instance to the socially-legally adjudicated status. This breadth reflects the Hebrew integrated anthropology: inner character and outer status and observable behaviour are aspects of a single moral reality, all named by the same term.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

ponēros's semantic range across the 90-verse corpus spans: (1) moral-quality of persons — "evil persons" (Mat 5:45; Act 17:5 — VCG-04); (2) moral-quality of thoughts — "evil thoughts" (Mat 9:4 — VCG-03); (3) constitutional-baseline of human nature — "you who are evil" (Mat 7:11 — VCG-02); (4) moral-quality of deeds — "your works were evil" (Joh 3:19 — VCG-04); (5) cosmic-adversarial power — "the evil one" (Mat 6:13; 1Jo 5:19 — VCG-01); (6) environmental-moral characterisation — "the evil age" (Gal 1:4 — VCG-01), "the evil days" (Eph 5:16 — VCG-01); (7) legal-category — "evil crimes" (Act 18:14 — VCG-06, minimal inner-being content). The range spans personal (individual moral quality), constitutional (human nature baseline), cosmic (the evil one), environmental (evil age), and legal-categorical (evil crimes) — a remarkably broad semantic span for a single term.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

to.e.vah's semantic range in this characteristic (CHAR-3 — moral sub-corpus only) spans: (1) inner character-qualities — the crooked heart (Pro 11:20 — VCG-01), arrogant heart (Pro 16:5 — VCG-02), wicked thoughts (Pro 15:26 — VCG-02), lying lips (Pro 12:22 — VCG-02); (2) habitual practices — dishonest commerce (Deu 25:16 — VCG-01; Pro 11:1 — VCG-01; Pro 20:10; 20:23 — VCG-01), perverted judgment (Pro 17:15 — VCG-01); (3) corrupted religious approach — worship by the inwardly corrupt (Pro 15:8; 21:27 — VCG-03; Isa 1:13 — VCG-03; Pro 28:9 — VCG-03); (4) conscience-related states — accumulated abominations (Eze 44:13 — VCG-04); (5) identity-constitutive categories — Pro 6:16 (divine declaration); Rev 17:5; 21:27 (NT eschatological). The range is wide: from specific acts (false balance) to inner-character conditions (arrogant heart) to identity-categories (mother of abominations). The breadth confirms the characteristic is a verdict-category, not a single specific vice.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

to.e.vah in the idolatrous register spans: (1) practices that are abominable (Deu 18:9 — VCG-02 — "abominable practices of those nations"), (2) acts that make the doer abominable (Deu 18:12 — VCG-02 — "whoever does these things is an abomination to the Lord"), (3) accumulated abominations of the community (Eze 5:9 — VCG-05 — "all your abominations"), (4) the relational event of provoking God (Deu 32:16 — VCG-02 — "with abominations they provoked him to anger"). shiq.quts spans: (1) foreign deity named as detestable (1Ki 11:5 — VCG-03 — Milcom the shiq.quts), (2) idol-objects installed in sacred space (Jer 7:30 — vc=65904 — VCG-04 — "detestable things in the house"), (3) idols seen by the eyes (Eze 20:7 — vc=1634 — VCG-05 — "detestable things your eyes feast on"). The range spans from named deities to practices to accumulated communal acts to relational-covenantal betrayal.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

a.ven's semantic range in the CHAR-5 corpus spans: (1) active scheming/devising (VCG-02): Mic 2:1 (vc=38217) — "devise wickedness"; Isa 32:6 (vc=38181) — "heart busy with iniquity"; (2) the evildoer as a character-type (VCG-03): Psa 5:5 (vc=38237) — "all evildoers"; (3) stored/harboured inner condition (VCG-04): Psa 66:18 (vc=38182) — "cherished iniquity in my heart"; (4) trouble-caused-in-victims (VCG-01): Psa 55:3 (vc=38188) — "they drop trouble upon me." The semantic range is thus unusually wide: a.ven covers the active inner-scheming agent (VCG-02), the character-class of those who habitually do it (VCG-03), the stored inner condition (VCG-04), and the trouble that falls on victims (VCG-01). This broad semantic range is what generates the polysemy requiring VCG-01's separate structural handling in the INTEGRATION_NOTE.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

blasfēmeō's semantic range in the CHAR-6 corpus spans: (1) direct sustained defiant blasphemy against God/heavenly beings (VCG-01): Rev 13:6; 16:9/11/21; Jude 8/10; (2) social defamation causing dishonour to God's name through conduct-failure (VCG-02): Rom 2:24; (3) false verbal attribution of a morally bankrupt teaching (VCG-02): Rom 3:8; (4) harmful speech toward legitimate freedom (VCG-02): Rom 14:16; 1Cor 10:30; (5) received slander reducing the recipient to refuse (VCG-02): 1Cor 4:13. The range is wide: from direct cosmic-scale defiant contempt for God (Rev 13:6 — VCG-01) to the social consequence of conduct-failure causing name-dishonour (Rom 2:24 — VCG-02) to received slander in community context (1Cor 4:13 — VCG-02). The verbal harm (blapto root) is present throughout but the target (God vs. persons), the agent (hardened will vs. community conduct), and the mode (direct vs. indirect) vary significantly.

---

##### T7.1.4 — Does the vocabulary include terms that distinguish distinct aspects of this characteristic — disposition versus act, received versus given, condition versus quality?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Yes. ra.sha (H7563) primarily names the disposition and the person-quality. re.sha (H7562) primarily names the condition — wickedness as an abstract state that the person is in. The verbal root rasha' (Dan 12:10) names the act. This three-part vocabulary suite (person-as-quality: ra.sha; condition: re.sha; act: rasha') mirrors the analytical distinctions of the programme: the person-identity (ra.sha = CHAR-1), the abstract condition (re.sha = VCG-11), and the act of wickedness (rasha' = M10 cross-register in the forensic VCG). The vocabulary thus does not simply conflate person, condition, and act — it distinguishes them through different morphological forms of the same root.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Yes. The vocabulary suite distinguishes: (1) condition vs. quality — adikia (G0093) primarily names the structural condition of being constitutionally unrighteous; ponēros primarily names the quality (evil as an attribute of persons, thoughts, deeds); kakia names the settled inner-badness as a residual deposit; (2) general vs. specific expressions — ponēros names the general evil quality; ponēria names the specific active malice/wickedness; (3) inner vs. outer — kakia (inner settled disposition — Eph 4:31 — VCG-05) vs. faulos (outward deeds — 2Cor 5:10 — VCG-06 — evil deeds evaluated at judgment); (4) abstract vs. concrete — adikia is the most abstract (structural wrongness), ponēros is the most concrete (applied to specific persons, thoughts, deeds).

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The vocabulary distinguishes aspects through the types of objects to which to.e.vah is applied rather than through distinct vocabulary forms. Acts: dishonest commercial practice (Deu 25:16 — VCG-01), making an idol secretly (Deu 27:15 — VCG-04), bringing sacrifice with evil intent (Pro 21:27 — VCG-03). Dispositions/qualities: the crooked heart (Pro 11:20 — VCG-01), the arrogant heart (Pro 16:5 — VCG-02), wicked thoughts (Pro 15:26 — VCG-02), lying lips (Pro 12:22 — VCG-02). Person-type: "the devious person is an abomination" (Pro 3:32 — VCG-02), "the scoffer is an abomination" (Pro 24:9 — VCG-01). The vocabulary applies the same term (to.e.vah) across act, disposition, and person-type — revealing that the biblical writers treated these as aspects of a single moral-relational category rather than distinct categories requiring distinct vocabulary.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Yes. to.e.vah distinguishes: (a) quality of the person/practice ("is an abomination to the Lord" — predicate structure naming quality); (b) the accumulated condition ("all your abominations" — the corpus of practices naming a collective state). shiq.quts specifically distinguishes the object-aspect: it names the idol as the detestable thing — the concrete object rather than the practice or quality. The two terms together cover: the quality of divine revulsion at idolatrous practices (to.e.vah) and the specific category of detestable objects toward which inner devotion is misdirected (shiq.quts). The vocabulary distinguishes the relational-verdict dimension (to.e.vah) from the object-dimension (shiq.quts).

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Yes. The two primary terms distinguish the inner condition from the expressed quality. a.ven (H0205G) names the inner condition: the iniquity harboured in the heart (Psa 66:18 — VCG-04), the plotting on the bed (Psa 36:4 — VCG-02), the evildoer as person-type (VCG-03). ro.a (H7455) names the quality of expressed deeds: "the evil of your deeds" (Deu 28:20 — VCG-05), "evil way and evil deeds" (Jer 25:5 — VCG-05). The po.al a.ven construction ("workers of iniquity" — VCG-03) distinguishes the act-dimension (po.al = active doing) from the condition-dimension (a.ven = what is held/possessed). Together, the vocabulary covers: inner condition (a.ven harboured), active process (a.ven devised/plotted), character-type (po.al a.ven — habitual worker), and expressed quality (ro.a of deeds).

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Yes. blasfēmeō (verb) names the act of harmful speech — the enacted event. kakopoios (noun) names the evildoer-identity — the person-type characterised by doing evil, which functions in VCG-03 as the accusation-target identity. The two terms together distinguish: the act of harmful speech (blasfēmeō) and the harmful identity attributed through accusation (kakopoios). VCG-02 further distinguishes given/received: 1Cor 4:13 (vc=14351 — VCG-02): "when slandered [blasfēmeoumenoi — passive], we entreat" — the passive form of blasfēmeō names the received-slander experience. Rom 2:24 (vc=14357 — VCG-02): blasfēmeitai — passive: "God's name is blasphemed" — the passive forms in VCG-02 distinguish the received-blasphemy experience from the active-blasphemy generation of VCG-01.

---

##### T7.1.5 — Does the vocabulary include a term for the structural opposite or absence of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Yes. The structural opposite is tsaddiq (H6662 — righteous) and its related forms. Throughout the corpus, ra.sha and tsaddiq appear as the explicit polar pair — Gen 18:23-25 (VCG-04), Psa 1:5-6 (VCG-04), Psa 11:5 (VCG-04), Mal 3:18 (VCG-02), and throughout the Proverbs antithetical couplets (VCG-04, VCG-09 throughout). The vocabulary for the opposite (righteousness, M26) is as fully developed as the vocabulary for the characteristic itself — the polar pair co-develops in Hebrew moral vocabulary. The absence-term for wickedness is also re.sha's own reversal: the absence of wickedness is not a separate term but is expressed through the departure from wickedness (the Ezekiel corpus uses "turn from his wickedness" — Eze 18:21-27; 33:11-19 — the structural absence is the turning from).

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Yes. Multiple terms name the structural opposite. agathos (good — Mat 12:35 — VCG-03: "the good person out of his good treasure"; Mat 5:45 — VCG-04: "on the evil and on the good") is the direct antonym of ponēros in the corpus. dikaiosynē (righteousness) is the structural opposite of adikia — Rom 6:13 (vc=14340 — VCG-06) presents "instruments for righteousness" as the opposite of "instruments for unrighteousness." The cleansed conscience (Heb 10:22 — VCG-06) is the structural opposite of the evil conscience. Sincerity and truth (1Cor 5:8 — VCG-05) are named as the structural opposite of malice and evil (old leaven). The vocabulary for the structural opposite is as developed as the vocabulary for the characteristic itself.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Yes. The antithetical structure of the Proverbs evidence consistently pairs the abomination with its opposite: ratson (H7522 — delight, acceptance) is the structural opposite at the divine-response level. Pro 11:1 (vc=65954 — VCG-01): "a false balance is an abomination to the Lord, but a just weight is his delight." Pro 11:20 (vc=1677 — VCG-01): "crooked heart is an abomination; those of blameless ways are his delight." Pro 15:8 (vc=1678 — VCG-03): "the sacrifice of the wicked is an abomination; the prayer of the upright is acceptable (ratsah)." The structural opposite of abomination is what is delightful and acceptable to God — ratson/ratsah. At the human inner-being level, the opposite is uprightness (yashar — Pro 11:20), blamelessness (tamim), faithfulness (Pro 12:22: "those who act faithfully").

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Yes. The structural opposite is named in the reform narratives through the acts that oppose the characteristic: 2Ch 34:33 (vc=65946 — VCG-03): removing all abominations → "all who were present in Israel serve the Lord their God" — exclusive covenant service is the structural opposite. Jer 4:1 (vc=65903 — VCG-04): "remove your detestable things from my presence" → "if you return, O Israel, to me you should return" — return to God is the structural opposite of idolatrous abomination. The opposing vocabulary is ratson (delight/favour) and ratsah (acceptable) — what is acceptable to God is the structural opposite of the abominable; shalom (covenantal peace) as the relational state the opposite of the rupture produced by abomination.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Yes. The structural opposite appears through antithetical vocabulary in the corpus. "The blameless" (tamim — Psa 18:25 and implied in Psa 10:29 — VCG-03: "way of the Lord is a stronghold to the blameless"). The righteous/upright as the structural opposite person-type implied by Psa 5:5 (VCG-03: boastful/evildoers cannot stand before God — implying those who can). Job 4:8 (VCG-04): plowing iniquity contrasts implicitly with plowing righteousness. The most explicit structural-opposite vocabulary is Isa 55:7 (vc=38200 — VCG-02): the wicked/unrighteous who forsake their ways → the Lord who will pardon; the pardon-relationship requires the righteous-way orientation as its context. The structural opposite vocabulary is the lexical field of tsaddiq (righteous), tamim (blameless), and yashar (upright).

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Yes. The structural opposite of blasfēmeō is explicitly named in the Rev 16 context. Rev 16:9 (vc=14352 — VCG-01): "they did not repent and give him glory (doxazō)" — giving glory (doxazō) is the structural opposite of blaspheming. 1Pe 2:12 (vc=14377 — VCG-03): "glorify God on the day of visitation" — same: doxazō as the structural opposite. Rom 2:24 (vc=14357 — VCG-02): God's name blasphemed — the structural opposite is God's name honoured/glorified. The glory-vocabulary (doxa, doxazō) is the consistent structural opposite throughout the corpus: what the characteristic withholds (glory) is precisely what the opposite gives.

---

##### T7.1.6 — Does the vocabulary include a person-type term — a term for the one who habitually possesses or exercises this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Yes — this is the definitional feature of ra.sha (H7563). Ra.sha is itself the person-type term: "the wicked [person]" as a recognized moral-anthropological category. The person-type vocabulary is unusually rich in this characteristic: ra.sha (the wicked individual), the plural resh'im (the wicked as a class — present throughout Psalms and Proverbs), re.sha (the abstract condition naming the class), and mir.sha.at (H4849 — the wicked woman collective). The person-type vocabulary is the dominant form of the characteristic's lexical expression — it is first and foremost a person-type vocabulary, which is the primary evidence that wickedness-as-settled-person-identity is the correct analytical category for this characteristic.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Yes. ponēros functions as a person-type term across multiple contexts: "evil persons" (Mat 5:45 — VCG-04), "evil people" (2Ti 3:13 — VCG-06), "the evil one" as a cosmic person-type (Mat 6:13 — VCG-01), "wicked and evil men" (2Th 3:2 — VCG-06), "wicked servant" (Mat 18:32 — VCG-06; Mat 25:26 — VCG-06). 1Cor 5:13 (vc=14465 — VCG-04): "purge the evil person from among you" — person-type term used for community action. The person-type function of ponēros confirms that the characteristic, like CHAR-1, has a person-identity dimension — the evil person is a recognisable type. The distinction from CHAR-1: ponēros person-type is primarily NT and constitutional; ra.sha person-type is primarily OT and volitional-directional.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Yes. bdeluktos (G0947, Tit 1:16) is specifically the person-type term: "they are detestable, disobedient, unfit for any good work" — the term designates the abominable person as a type. In the Hebrew corpus, the person-type is constructed through the predicate structure rather than a dedicated term: "the devious person is an abomination" (Pro 3:32 — VCG-02), "the scoffer is an abomination" (Pro 24:9 — VCG-01). The equivalent of a person-type term is embedded in the abomination statement itself. Rev 17:5 (vc=65878 — VCG-05) creates the person-type at cosmic scale: "the mother of prostitutes and of earth's abominations" — the identity constituted entirely by generating abomination.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The shiq.quts vocabulary partially generates a person-type: Deu 18:12 (vc=1685 — VCG-02): "whoever does these things is an abomination to the Lord" — the person who practises divination and occult arts becomes personally abominable, not merely the practice. The to.e.vah predicate structure names the person-type through the "is an abomination to the Lord" construction. No dedicated person-type noun is coined for the habitual idolater within this corpus — the person-type is constructed through the predicate abomination-verdict applied to the person. The closest person-type evidence is Hos 9:10 (vc=1632 — VCG-04): "they became detestable like the thing they loved" — the community collectively becomes the person-type of the abominable through sustained idolatrous devotion.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Yes. The evildoer vocabulary is one of the richest person-type terminations in the programme. po.al a.ven (H6466 + H0205G — "workers/doers of iniquity") is a person-type construction appearing throughout VCG-03: Psa 6:8 (vc=38243 — VCG-03): "workers of evil"; Psa 59:2 (vc=38241 — VCG-03): "those who work evil." Pro 6:12 (vc=38223 — VCG-03): "a worthless person, a wicked man" — ish beliyya.al + ish a.ven as person-type designation. Isa 31:2 (vc=38199 — VCG-03): "evildoers" and "workers of iniquity" as named classes. The person-type vocabulary is unusually developed in this characteristic, comprising VCG-03's full 24-verse corpus — the evildoer-as-person-type is constitutive of the characteristic's presentation.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Yes. kakopoios (G2555, 5V — VCG-03) is the person-type term: "evil-doer" or "one who does evil" — the person defined by the moral quality of their acts. In VCG-03, kakopoios functions as the identity attributed through hostile accusation: 1Pe 2:12 (vc=14377 — VCG-03): "when they speak against you as evildoers (kakopoious)" — the kakopoios is the specific person-type identity that the accusing speech imposes on the falsely accused. The person-type term reveals the social-identity dimension of CHAR-6: evil expressed through speech can attribute a person-type identity to the innocent, making the false accusation an identity-creating speech act with serious social consequences.

---

##### T7.1.7 — Does the vocabulary include a supplication or seeking term — a term for the act of seeking this characteristic from another?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (S)

The vocabulary of this characteristic does not include a specific supplication term — a term for the act of seeking wickedness from another. This is expected: wickedness-as-settled-person-identity is not a characteristic one seeks from another as one might seek grace, wisdom, or peace. The relevant seeking vocabulary in the evidence belongs to the reversal direction: Ise 55:7 (VCG-07 — "let him return to the Lord, that he may have compassion on him") — the seeking vocabulary addresses the turn from wickedness toward God, not the seeking of wickedness itself. The absence of a supplication-seeking term is analytically coherent with the characteristic's nature.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (S)

The vocabulary does not include a term for seeking evil as constitutional inner nature from another. Mat 6:13 (vc=14415 — VCG-01): "deliver us from evil" contains a supplication term (deliver — rhyomai) but it is a supplication for protection from the characteristic rather than for the characteristic itself. The characteristic is not one sought from another — it is the constitutional baseline already present, from which deliverance is sought. The absence of a seeking term is analytically coherent with the characteristic's nature as a constitutional baseline condition rather than a received gift.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (S)

The vocabulary does not include a term for seeking or desiring abomination from another. Abomination is not a characteristic one seeks from another — it is a divine verdict applied to inner moral conditions. The one seeking-adjacent appearance is the call to turn from abominations (Eze 14:6 — VCG-04 — "repent and turn away from your abominations") which is a command away from the characteristic rather than a seeking toward it. No supplication-seeking term is present.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (S)

The vocabulary does not include a term for seeking idolatrous abomination from another. Idolatrous abomination is not a characteristic one seeks as a gift; it is entered through attraction to idol-objects and the will's choice. The evidence shows the characteristic as received through learning (Deu 20:18 — VCG-02), through relational entanglement (1Ki 11:5 — VCG-03), and through visual-desire feeding (Eze 20:7 — VCG-05) — none of these are supplication-seeking forms. The absence of a seeking term is analytically coherent: one does not seek idolatrous abomination as one seeks wisdom or grace.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (S)

The vocabulary does not include a term for seeking or desiring iniquity-as-scheming from another. Iniquity as active scheming is not sought as a gift; it is generated from within (VCG-02) or received through social formation (VCG-04 — association with evildoers). The absence of a seeking term is analytically coherent: one does not petition for the capacity to scheme evil; one cultivates it or drifts into it through volitional choices and relational influences. No supplication-seeking form is present.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (S)

The vocabulary does not include a term for seeking blasphemy or evil speech from another. The characteristic is not a gift that one seeks; it is generated from within the hardened will (VCG-01) or received as unwanted hostile speech (VCG-02/03). No supplication-seeking form is present. The absence is analytically coherent: no one petitions for the capacity to blaspheme or to be slandered.

---

##### T7.1.8 — What does the relationship between the OT Hebrew vocabulary and the NT Greek vocabulary reveal about continuity or development of this characteristic across the Testaments?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

For Characteristic 1, the OT Hebrew vocabulary (ra.sha, re.sha — 189 of 190 verses) overwhelmingly dominates; there is only 1 ro.a verse (1Sa 17:28) as a secondary Hebrew contribution. There are no NT Greek verses assigned to Characteristic 1. This vocabulary distribution reveals that wickedness-as-settled-person-identity is a primarily OT Hebrew anthropological category. The NT vocabulary for the equivalent domain is distributed across Characteristic 2 (M10b-B — ponēros, kakia — constitutional inner nature) and other characteristics. The OT-to-NT development appears to be: the OT concentrated the settled wicked-person analysis in the ra.sha vocabulary; the NT distributed that analysis across multiple Greek terms (ponēros for the evil person, kakia for entrenched inner badness, etc.) without a single dominant NT equivalent for ra.sha. This suggests a NT diversification of the OT person-type vocabulary.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The relationship reveals a significant developmental shift. CHAR-1 (wickedness as settled person-identity) is primarily OT Hebrew (ra.sha — 179V of 190 in CHAR-1) — the OT concentrated the evil-person analysis in the person-type vocabulary. CHAR-2 (evil as constitutional inner nature) is exclusively NT Greek (90V — no OT Hebrew verses assigned) — the NT developed a new analytical register for the constitutional dimension of human evil. The development reveals a deepening of the anthropological analysis: the OT named the wicked person as a type; the NT analysed the constitutional condition from which the wicked person-type emerges. The NT's distinctive contribution is the constitutional-depth analysis — "you who are evil" as a baseline statement about human nature (Mat 7:11; Luk 11:13 — VCG-02) is NT-specific and has no direct OT equivalent in this programme's evidence corpus.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The relationship reveals both continuity and intensification. Continuity: the content of what is abominable is consistent — the NT bdelugma passages address the same moral inner-being conditions as the OT to.e.vah moral sub-corpus: Luk 16:15 (vc=21 — VCG-02) names self-justifying pride as abomination before God, directly paralleling the OT heart-pride abominations (Pro 16:5 — VCG-02). Tit 1:16 (vc=27 — VCG-02) names the profession-works disconnect as abomination, extending the OT worship-integrity register (VCG-03). Intensification: the NT bdelugma/bdeluktos terms add the sensory-disgust dimension (stench-quality) that the Hebrew to.e.vah lacked at the root level. The NT also extends the category eschatologically: Rev 21:27 (VCG-05) — the final exclusion of the abominable from the holy city is an eschatological development of the OT's local exclusions from divine presence (Eze 44:13 — VCG-04).

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The relationship reveals primarily continuity with NT extension to apocalyptic/eschatological deployment. Continuity: the OT's to.e.vah and shiq.quts identify idolatrous abomination as the category of divine revulsion at false devotion — this is consistent throughout OT. The NT's bdelugma (G0946 — Mat 24:15; Mar 13:14 — VCG-06) takes the same category and deploys it in the eschatological-apocalyptic register: the abomination of desolation as the culminating sacrilege event. The OT shiq.quts vocabulary (naming idol-objects as detestable — used 25V in CHAR-4) has no direct NT Greek equivalent in this corpus — the NT bdelugma verses are event-naming rather than object-naming. The NT development: from OT naming of specific idol-objects and practices as detestable to NT naming of an eschatological sacrilege event as the culminating abomination.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The characteristic is exclusively OT Hebrew in its evidence corpus: all 79 verses are OT, with no NT Greek terms appearing. This is a distinctive feature that requires analytical note. The absence of NT Greek evidence suggests either: (1) the NT addresses the same inner-being content through different vocabulary (ponēria/adikia/kakon — the CHAR-2 NT vocabulary in M10b-B); or (2) the characteristic's specific a.ven polysemy-field does not have a direct NT Greek equivalent that was extracted into this corpus. The exclusively OT character of the evidence confirms that CHAR-5 is a primarily OT-vocabulary characteristic. Cross-cluster NT engagement with the same content (active scheming of evil) would be located in the ponēros/ponēria word-family documented in CHAR-2's evidence. The relationship between the two testaments for this characteristic requires cross-cluster synthesis (Session D) rather than within-corpus analysis.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The characteristic is exclusively NT Greek in its evidence corpus — no OT Hebrew terms are extracted. This is a distinctive feature: the characteristic as defined (blasfēmeō, kakopoios, atopos) is specifically a NT-period vocabulary construction. The OT concept that corresponds most closely is the lashon hara (evil tongue) tradition and the Hebrew terms for curse (qalal), slander (rakhil), and false witness (ed shaqer) — but these are not present in this corpus. The exclusively NT character suggests that the specific conceptual formulation of blasphemy as the hardened will's speech-expression (VCG-01) and the false-accusation dynamic of the NT minority community (VCG-03) are NT-specific forms of a broader biblical concern. The OT-NT relationship would require cross-cluster analysis to address fully.

---

##### T7.1.9 — Is there a term newly coined in the NT period for this characteristic — and if so, what does that coinage reveal?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (S)

No NT term is present in Characteristic 1's evidence base (T7.1.8). The characteristic is exclusively OT Hebrew. This prompt is therefore not applicable; the silence is noted explicitly. The NT coinage question is better addressed in Characteristic 2's analysis (ponēros, kakia, ponēria carry the NT equivalents of this characteristic's domain).

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

ponēria (G4189) appears to be a term more prominent in the NT period than in the LXX, though not coined de novo. Its use in Mar 7:22 (vc=14409 — VCG-05: listed in the heart's vice catalogue) and Rom 1:29 (vc=14411 — VCG-05: "filled with all manner of unrighteousness, evil, covetousness, malice") names a settled inner wickedness as an active, malicious orientation — a specific naming of the characteristic's most volitional and active expression. kakia (G2549) in the Pauline corpus is used with particular precision to name the deep-seated hostile inner residue requiring removal (Eph 4:31 — VCG-05; Col 3:8 — VCG-05; 1Pe 2:1 — VCG-05) — this usage pattern is distinctly NT. The NT's coinage precision (kakia for deep hostile residue; ponēria for active malice; adikia for constitutional wrongness; ponēros for broad evil quality) reveals a more differentiated vocabulary for the constitutional dimension than the OT's ra.sha family.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

bdeluktos (G0947, Tit 1:16 — VCG-02) is the most specific NT contribution: the adjectival person-type form naming the detestable person. While bdelugma and its root appear in the LXX as equivalents of to.e.vah, bdeluktos appears primarily in NT usage. Its coinage (or distinctively NT application) reveals a development from the Hebrew noun-form (to.e.vah naming the abomination-category) to a Greek adjective naming the abominable person-type directly. This development reveals the NT's interest in the person who is abominable, not merely the category — Tit 1:16's naming of the detestable person (bdeluktos) as the one who professes God but denies him by works is a person-type designation that the OT to.e.vah system handled through predicate structures ("the devious person is an abomination") rather than through a dedicated person-type adjective.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

"The abomination of desolation" (bdelugma tēs erēmōseōs — Mat 24:15; Mar 13:14 — VCG-06) is a specific compound term not found in the OT Hebrew and appearing in the LXX of Dan 9:27 (bdélygma erēmōseōs). Its NT use is not a new coinage but a direct citation of Daniel — the term pre-exists in the LXX. However, the NT's application of the Danielic formula (Mat 24:15 referencing Dan's prophecy as not yet fulfilled) represents an interpretive extension: the abomination of desolation as a still-future eschatological event at the time of Jesus's address. The coinage-as-eschatological-extension reveals the characteristic's NT development toward an apocalyptic-culmination deployment.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (S)

No NT Greek terms appear in this characteristic's 79-verse corpus. The question of NT-period coinage is therefore not answerable from this evidence base. If the same inner-being content (active scheming of evil, conceiving and birthing harm from within) is addressed in the NT, it would be through the ponēria/adikia/kakos vocabulary of CHAR-2's evidence base. No NT coinage within this corpus is noted. This silence is analytically informative: the characteristic's content may be absorbed into a broader evil-nature vocabulary in the NT rather than maintaining distinct scheming-specific terminology.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

blasfēmeō (G0987) is not newly coined in the NT but receives new theological depth in the NT period. Its application to the hardened will's eschatological defiance (Rev 16:9/11/21 — VCG-01) and to the cosmic beast-figure (Rev 13:6 — VCG-01) extends the term into eschatological-cosmic territory that is distinctively NT. kakopoios (G2555) appears primarily in 1 Peter and John 18 in the NT — its concentration in the persecution-context of minority communities under false accusation is a distinctively NT social-political setting. atopos (G0824) as a legal term (Act 25:5 — VCG-03) is used in the NT in a legal-juridical setting. The NT's distinctive contribution is not new coinages but the eschatological-cosmic extension of blasfēmeō vocabulary and the community-defence context of kakopoios.

---

##### T7.1.10 — What does the full vocabulary arc reveal about this characteristic's complete semantic range?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The full vocabulary arc (ra.sha person-type, re.sha abstract condition, mir.sha.at collective, rasha' verbal act, tsaddiq structural opposite, plus the ro.a adjective-of-badness) reveals that this characteristic's semantic range is comprehensive at the person-moral-identity level: it names the person, the person's inner condition, the collective of such persons, the act that expresses the condition, and the structural opposite that defines it by contrast. The arc is self-contained and fully developed within the Hebrew OT vocabulary — it does not require NT Greek supplementation to be analytically complete. The OT has built a complete moral-anthropological vocabulary for the wicked person as an inner-being type. The characteristic's semantic range is therefore as wide as the full RSH-root vocabulary suite plus the contextually associated terms (tsaddiq as opposite; iniquity terms as co-occurring conditions).

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The full vocabulary arc (ponēros + kakia + adikia + ponēria + faulos) reveals a semantic range that spans: evil as a broad moral quality (ponēros — most comprehensive), evil as settled hostile inner residue (kakia — most constitutional), evil as structural wrongness (adikia — most relational to the moral order), evil as active malicious wickedness (ponēria — most volitionally aggressive), and evil as morally worthless deeds (faulos — most behavioural-evaluative). Together these five terms cover the full spectrum from constitutional condition to specific expression, from inner residue to outward act, from structural wrongness to active malice. The vocabulary arc is complete: it provides a lexical map of the constitutional inner evil at every level from its deepest structural reality (adikia) through its settled character (kakia) to its broadest qualitative expression (ponēros).

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The full arc (to.e.vah + bdelugma + bdeluktos) reveals a semantic range spanning: (1) the divine-verdict category (to.e.vah as the standard term for what provokes divine revulsion); (2) the sensory-disgust quality of that revulsion (bdelugma — what stinks morally); (3) the person-type who embodies the abominable quality (bdeluktos); (4) the inner-character content that triggers the verdict (crooked heart, arrogant heart, lying lips, dishonest practice, perverted judgment, corrupt worship); (5) the relational consequence of the verdict (exclusion from divine intimacy, unacceptable worship, eschatological exclusion). The vocabulary arc is complete from the category (to.e.vah), through its quality (bdelugma), to its embodiment (bdeluktos), to its consequences (exclusion at multiple levels).

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The full arc (to.e.vah as abomination-verdict on idolatrous practice + shiq.quts as the detestable idol-object + bdelugma as the sacrilegious desolation-event) reveals a semantic range spanning: (1) the divine-verdict on idolatrous practices (to.e.vah — what the practices are before God); (2) the specific objects of misdirected devotion (shiq.quts — the idol-objects as detestable things); (3) the relational-covenantal betrayal dimension (to.e.vah in Deu 32:16 context — abominations provoking jealousy); (4) the eschatological-sacrilegious event (bdelugma — the abomination of desolation). The arc moves from the individual inner attachment (the heart going after shiq.quts objects) through communal practice and divine-verdict (to.e.vah) to cosmic-eschatological culmination (bdelugma tēs erēmōseōs). The vocabulary arc covers the full scope of the characteristic from inner devotion to eschatological judgment.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The full arc (a.ven spanning emptiness-iniquity-trouble + ro.a naming evil-quality-of-deeds + po.al a.ven naming the evildoer-person-type) reveals a semantic range covering: (1) the inner moral vacuity that generates harm (a.ven's root meaning of empty-yet-troubling); (2) the active cognitive-volitional scheming process (a.ven in VCG-02 — devising, plotting, conceiving); (3) the evildoer as a recognisable habitual-character class (po.al a.ven in VCG-03); (4) the accumulated inner condition (a.ven harboured — VCG-04); (5) the expressed quality of harmful deeds (ro.a — VCG-05); and (6) the trouble that lands on victims (a.ven in VCG-01). The vocabulary arc is remarkably comprehensive: from the root emptiness through the inner process to the character class to the accumulated condition to the expressed deeds to the victim's received trouble. The entire harm-cycle — from inner vacuity to social impact — is captured within the a.ven/ro.a vocabulary field.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The full arc (blasfēmeō as harm-speech + kakopoios as evil-doer person-type + atopos as legally irregular wrongdoing) reveals a semantic range covering: (1) the defiant cosmic-scale speech of the hardened will against God (blasfēmeō — VCG-01); (2) the social-communal defamation of God's name through moral failure and misrepresentation (blasfēmeō — VCG-02); (3) the hostile false accusation of the innocent as evildoers (kakopoios — VCG-03); (4) the formal legal charge of wrongdoing (atopos + kakopoios — VCG-03). The vocabulary arc covers the full range from cosmic-eschatological defiance of God (Rev 13:6; 16:9/11/21) through social community defamation (VCG-02) to intimate legal-charge false accusation (VCG-03). The characteristic operates across all scales of social reality — cosmic, communal, and judicial.

---

#### T7.2 — Verse and Literary Interpretation

##### T7.2.1 — What is the function of this characteristic's primary term within its primary verse — what role does it play in the sentence and argument?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Taking Psa 36:1 (vc=42567 — M10b-A-VCG-02 anchor) as the primary verse: "Transgression speaks to the wicked (ra.sha) deep in his heart; there is no fear of God before his eyes." Here ra.sha functions as a dative-relational noun naming the addressee of transgression's inner speech — it is not an active subject but the characterised recipient of an inner-voice event. The function is descriptive-classifying: the verse uses ra.sha to identify the type of person to whom this inner dynamic pertains. This classifying function of ra.sha — naming the type of person for whom this is the inner condition — is representative of its dominant function across the corpus. In the Proverbs antithetical couplets (Pro 10:6, 10:11, etc.), ra.sha functions as the negative comparison-term in a moral-quality pair.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Taking Mat 7:11 (vc=14438 — VCG-02: "you who are evil, know how to give good gifts") as the primary verse for ponēros: the term functions as a predicative adjective in the second-person address ("you who are evil" — hypers ponēroi ontes) — it functions as a constitutional description of the human addressees, not a moral accusation about specific acts. The grammatical form (present participle — "being evil") is particularly significant: it is continuous, describing a state that is ongoing, not episodic. The function is diagnostic and constitutive — it identifies the constitutional state of the human hearers as the given context within which the argument about God's better giving operates. The verse's logic is a fortiori: if the evil-constitutioned humans can still give good gifts, how much more can God. ponēros here functions as the term that names the baseline anthropological condition from which the argument proceeds.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Taking Pro 3:32 (vc=1686 — VCG-02) as the primary anchor candidate: "for the devious person is an abomination to the Lord, but the upright are in his confidence." to.e.vah functions here as the predicate noun in a comparative antithetical statement — it names the relational status of the devious person before God as abomination-status. The function is diagnostic and relational: the term does not merely describe a moral quality but names the relational position of the person in relation to God. The antithetical parallel ("the upright are in his confidence") reinforces the relational nature of the term by contrasting it with the opposite relational status (intimate confidence). The function of to.e.vah in this primary verse is therefore: relational verdict (naming the status of the devious before God), diagnostic (identifying the specific inner condition that triggers the verdict — devious/crooked inner way), and antithetical (defining by contrast with its opposite).

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Taking Eze 11:21 (vc=1631 — VCG-05) as the primary anchor: "those whose heart goes after their detestable things (shiq.quts) and their abominations (to.e.vah), I will bring their deeds upon their own heads." Here shiq.quts functions as the direct object of the heart's going-after — naming the idol-objects as the specific destinations of the misdirected devotional movement. to.e.vah functions as an associated category expanding on what the shiq.quts involves (they are not just detestable objects but abominations in the full divine-verdict sense). The grammatical function is object-of-devotion (shiq.quts) and verdict-category (to.e.vah) combined in a single verse. The verse's overall argument: the heart's directional faculty going after abominable objects → the deeds that result → divine judgment bringing those deeds back on the person. The terms function as the diagnostic statement of the inner condition that triggers judgment.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Taking Psa 36:4 (vc=38235 — VCG-02) as the primary anchor candidate: "He plots trouble [a.ven] while on his bed; he sets himself in a way that is not good; he does not reject evil." Here a.ven functions as the direct object of "plots" (verbalised) — naming what is planned and produced through the scheming process. The function is: named content of the scheming act. a.ven is what the inner person is plotting; it names both the content of the plot (iniquity/trouble) and the harmful quality of the planned output. The verse's structure — plotting a.ven (inner) → setting himself in a wrong way (directional orientation) → not rejecting evil (volitional refusal) — shows a.ven at the productive heart of a three-part inner-being description. The term functions as the generative target of the cognitive-volitional scheming act.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Taking Rev 16:9 (vc=14352 — VCG-01) as the primary anchor candidate: "They were scorched by the fierce heat, and they cursed [blasfēmeō] the name of God who had power over these plagues. They did not repent and give him glory." Here blasfēmeō functions as the main verb of the subject's active response — naming the specific verbal act (cursing God's name) that is the primary content of the sentence. The term carries the full weight of the verse's analytical disclosure: it names what the hardened will does in the moment of judgment. The function is primary-verb disclosure: the term is not background or incidental but the central predicate that defines the verse's inner-being content. The name of God as the object of the verb shows what specifically is targeted — God's name-reputation-honour is the thing the term harms.

---

##### T7.2.2 — What literary form carries the primary verse evidence (narrative, psalm, wisdom, prophecy, epistle, apocalyptic) — and what does that form require for responsible interpretation?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The 190-verse corpus spans multiple literary forms. Wisdom literature dominates numerically (Proverbs antithetical couplets — VCGs 06, 08, 09 — perhaps ~80V; Job theodicy dialogue — VCG-10 — 9V). Psalms lament, praise, and wisdom poetry carry VCGs 02, 03, 04, 05 (~60V). Prophetic literature (Isaiah, Jeremiah, Ezekiel, Habakkuk, Zephaniah, Malachi) carries VCGs 05, 07 (~30V). Narrative carries VCG-04 and VCG-01 (~18V). Each form requires distinct interpretive care: the Proverbs antithetical couplets are generalising wisdom observations about characteristic patterns — they describe typical patterns, not invariable laws (the theodicy-challenge of Job VCG-10 explicitly complicates the Proverbs pattern). The Ezekiel prophetic-pastoral material (VCG-07) is direct divine address to historical Israel — its volitional urgency ("turn!") is different in register from the Proverbs observation ("the wicked falls by his own wickedness").

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The 90-verse corpus spans three primary literary forms. (1) Sayings/discourse of Jesus (Synoptic Gospels — VCGs 02, 03, 04 — ~30V): Mat 7:11 (vc=14438), Mat 12:34-35 (vc=14419-14420), Mat 15:19 (vc=14414), Luk 6:45 (vc=14421), Mar 7:22-23 (vc=14409/14473/14422). These require interpretation within the context of Jesus's teaching — they are often Q-material or Markan tradition; the a fortiori argument structure (Mat 7:11; Luk 11:13) and the treasury-of-heart teaching are core Synoptic anthropological claims. (2) Pauline epistles (VCGs 05, 06 — ~35V): Rom 1:18-29 (vc=14336-14338), Eph 4:31 (vc=14365), Col 3:8 (vc=14366), 1Cor 5:8 (vc=14363/14412), 2Ti 3:13 (vc=14451). These are communal address — formation imperatives requiring careful attention to paraenetic context. (3) Johannine corpus (VCGs 01, 04 — ~18V): Joh 3:19 (vc=14448), 1Jo 5:19 (vc=14433), 1Jo 2:13-14 (vc=14429-14430). These require attention to Johannine dualism (light/darkness; from God/from the evil one).

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Four primary literary forms carry the characteristic's 40-verse corpus. (1) Wisdom aphorism (Proverbs — VCGs 01, 02, 03, and partial 05 — ~24V): antithetical two-line constructions stating what is abominable and what is its opposite. These require recognition of the generalising pattern — Proverbs aphorisms describe typical patterns rather than invariable laws, and the antithetical structure requires both poles to be held simultaneously. (2) Prophetic oracle (Jeremiah, Ezekiel — VCG-04 — ~12V): divine address to Israel about communal abominations and conscience-state. These require attention to the historical context of pre-exile (Jeremiah) and exile (Ezekiel) and the difference between prophetic diagnosis (Jer 6:15; 8:12) and prophetic call (Eze 14:6) and prophetic restoration (Eze 36:31). (3) Apocalyptic (Revelation — VCG-05 — 3V): cosmic and eschatological deployment of the abomination category. These require recognition of the symbolic-visionary register. (4) NT epistle (Tit 1:16 — VCG-02): direct pastoral address.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Four primary literary forms carry the characteristic's 99-verse corpus. (1) Law (Leviticus, Deuteronomy — VCGs 01, 02 — ~20V): categorical prohibitions and warnings — these require interpretation as divine boundary-marking, not casuistic case law; the categorical form ("you shall not") names the absolute prohibition without specifying every scenario. (2) Historical narrative (VCG-03 — 17V): the reform narratives require historical-contextual reading; the moral assessment ("he did what was evil… according to the abominations of the nations") is evaluative commentary on documented events. (3) Prophetic oracle (VCG-04 — 14V; VCG-05 — 43V): prophetic address to Israel — requires attention to the historical context of the prophetic moment and the speaker-audience relationship. The Ezekiel VCG-05 is prophetic-visionary (the tour of abominations — Eze 8-11); it requires recognition of the visionary register without literalising the narrative details. (4) Apocalyptic (VCG-06 — 5V): the Daniel and Synoptic abomination-of-desolation passages require eschatological-typological reading.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Three primary literary forms. (1) Psalm/lament (dominant — VCGs 01, 03, 04): the Psalter's evildoer corpus addresses the characteristic from the perspective of the psalmist as victim or as righteous observer seeking divine intervention. These forms require reading as prayer-address to God — the evildoer is described from the pray-er's vantage point; the language is often vivid and experiential rather than systematic. (2) Wisdom/aphorism (Proverbs, Job — VCGs 02, 03, 04): generalising statements about the inner character of the wicked and the consequences of iniquity. These require recognition of the generalising pattern (Proverbs) and the dialogic context (Job — speeches by various characters whose reliability varies). (3) Prophetic oracle (Isaiah, Jeremiah, Ezekiel, Micah, Habakkuk — VCGs 01, 02, 04, 05): prophetic address condemning specific iniquitous acts. These require attention to the specific historical-prophetic situation and the speaker-audience relationship.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Three literary forms carry the 17-verse corpus. (1) Apocalyptic (Revelation — VCG-01 partial: Rev 13:6; 16:9/11/21): cosmic visionary narrative describing eschatological events. These require recognition of the symbolic-visionary register: the beast is a typological figure, not a specific historical person; the plagues are eschatological events. Responsible interpretation requires holding the visionary-symbolic frame while taking the inner-being content seriously. (2) Epistle (Pauline — VCG-02: Rom 2:24; 3:8; 14:16; 1Cor 4:13; 10:30; and Petrine — VCG-03: 1Pe 2:12/14/3:16/4:15; Jude — VCG-01: Jude 8/10): direct pastoral-theological address. These require attention to the specific community context and the speaker-audience relationship. (3) Narrative (Gospel/Acts — VCG-03: Joh 18:30; Act 25:5): juridical-narrative context of formal trial proceedings.

---

##### T7.2.3 — What is the logical structure of key arguments in the verse evidence — what are the premises and conclusions?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Two dominant logical structures: (1) The antithetical comparison (dominant in Proverbs — VCGs 06, 08, 09): premise: the righteous and the wicked are distinct moral types; inference: they have different inner states and different consequences. The form is consistent: "the righteous [positive state], but the wicked [negative equivalent]" — e.g., Pro 10:6 ("blessings on the righteous, but the mouth of the wicked conceals violence"). The logical conclusion is always that the inner character determines the outcome. (2) The divine-moral indictment (dominant in Psalms and Prophets — VCGs 02, 05): premise: the wicked have a specific inner orientation (God-exclusion, pride, directed hostility); inference: this orientation constitutes moral liability; conclusion: divine judgment is warranted and will come. Psa 9:5-17 (VCG-05) is a concentrated instance of this structure.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Three dominant logical structures. (1) A fortiori (Mat 7:11; Luk 11:13 — VCG-02): premise: humans are constitutionally evil; humans can still give good gifts; conclusion: God, who is not constitutionally evil, gives far better gifts. The constitutional evil of humans is the negative premise from which the positive argument about God's better character proceeds. (2) Source-to-output (Mat 12:34-35; Luk 6:45; Mar 7:23 — VCG-03): premise: the inner treasury of the heart is evil; conclusion: the speech and deeds that flow from it are necessarily evil. The constitutional condition determines the output — the "for" (gar) in Mat 12:34 makes the logical connection explicit. (3) Nature-determines-fruit (Mat 7:17-18 — VCG-02): premise: a diseased tree is constitutionally unable to produce good fruit; conclusion: an evil inner nature cannot produce genuinely good moral output. The constitutional condition is the determinative category.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Three dominant logical structures. (1) Antithetical comparison (dominant in Proverbs — VCGs 01, 02, 03): premise: a specific inner condition (crooked heart, false balance, lying lips) is abominable to God; implicit conclusion: its opposite (blameless way, just weight, faithful speech) is delightful. The logical structure reveals the characteristic as defined through contrast. (2) Consequential-judgment (dominant in VCG-04): premise: abomination was committed without shame; therefore: divine judgment will fall. The logical structure is causal: shameless commission → divine punishment. (3) Inclusive categorical (VCG-05 — Pro 6:16): premise: God hates six things, seven are abomination to him; unstated content enumerated in following verses. The logical form is a categorical declaration followed by enumeration of contents — the category is established before its contents are filled in.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Three dominant logical structures. (1) Command-basis structure (Deuteronomy — VCG-02): "you shall not [practice abomination] because [God hates it / the nations were expelled for it / it makes you abominable]." The logic is: prohibition → basis (divine hatred + expulsion precedent). Deu 18:12 (vc=1685 — VCG-02): "whoever does these things is an abomination to the Lord; and because of these abominations the Lord your God is driving them out." (2) Because-therefore structure (Ezekiel — VCG-05): "because of all your abominations [I will do X]" — the judgment is logically grounded in the prior abomination. Eze 5:9 (vc=65968 — VCG-05): "because of all your abominations I will do with you what I have never yet done." (3) Cause-transformation structure: Hos 9:10 (vc=1632 — VCG-04): commitment to abomination → constitutional transformation ("became detestable like the thing they loved"). Each logic structure confirms the causal relationship between idolatrous abomination and its consequences.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Three dominant logical structures. (1) Because-therefore judgment (dominant in VCG-05): "evil deeds → divine judgment": Deu 28:20 (VCG-05): "because of the evil of your deeds, because you have forsaken me → curses, confusion, destruction"; Jer 44:22 (VCG-05): evil deeds and abominations → land desolation. The logic is causal-judicial. (2) Generative-productive logic (VCG-02): "conceives → pregnant → gives birth" (Psa 7:14 — VCG-02): the inner process logically entails its harmful output. The logic is generative-productive: inner state necessarily produces outer output. (3) Character-consequence logic (VCG-03/04): "evildoers flourish → doomed to destruction" (Psa 92:7 — VCG-03): the character produces consequences despite temporary appearance of flourishing. The logic is developmental-consequential.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Three dominant logical structures. (1) Judgment-response logic (VCG-01): judgment falls → defiant speech response → no repentance: Rev 16:9 (VCG-01): "scorched → cursed God → did not repent." The logic is consequential-revelatory: judgment reveals what the will already is by provoking its defiant response. (2) Conduct-testimony logic (VCG-02): moral conduct → social speech consequence: Rom 2:24 (VCG-02): "because of you [moral failure] → God's name blasphemed among Gentiles." The logic is indirect causation: inner moral state → social speech outcome. (3) False-charge-counter-charge logic (VCG-03): false accusation → honourable conduct → eventual shame for accusers: 1Pe 2:12 (VCG-03): "speak against you as evildoers → see your good deeds → glorify God." The logic is reversibility: the false verbal charge is eventually overturned by visible evidence.

---

##### T7.2.4 — What contextual setting carries the primary verse evidence (judicial, liturgical, covenantal, communal, eschatological) — and what does that setting reveal?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Three primary contextual settings: (1) Judicial/forensic — the wicked as the legally guilty party (VCG-01, 5V: Exo 23:7; Deu 25:1-2; 1Ki 8:32; 2Ch 6:23). The INTEGRATION_NOTE carry-forward is most relevant here: these forensic uses are the cross-register with M10. (2) Covenantal/prophetic — the wicked as those who have broken covenant relationship with God and face prophetic call to turn (VCG-07, VCG-02, VCG-05 — concentrated in Ezekiel and the Psalms of divine address). (3) Wisdom/communal — the wicked as a human moral type observed within social life, whose patterns of inner character and consequence are documented for instruction (Proverbs — VCGs 06, 08, 09). The contextual diversity across judicial, covenantal, and wisdom settings shows the characteristic is not confined to a single institutional setting but is a general moral-anthropological category operative across all three.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Three primary contextual settings: (1) Communal/ecclesial formation — the largest body of evidence (Pauline letters, VCGs 05/06) addresses believers in community — the constitutional inner evil is named in the context of ongoing formation imperatives within established churches. The communal setting reveals the characteristic as a pastoral concern within the covenant community, not merely an external moral category. (2) Apocalyptic/eschatological — the separation of evil from righteous at the end of age (Mat 13:49 — VCG-04), the cosmic evil-one's dominion (1Jo 5:19 — VCG-01), and the progressive deterioration of evil people (2Ti 3:13 — VCG-06) all carry eschatological-frame settings. (3) Conflict/challenge — Jesus addressing the Pharisees (Mat 12:34-35; Luk 11:39 — VCG-03/05), the entrapment attempts (Mat 22:18 — VCG-05), and the community expulsion of the evil person (1Cor 5:13 — VCG-04) all carry conflict-context settings.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Three primary contextual settings. (1) Wisdom-communal instruction (Proverbs — VCGs 01, 02, 03): the commercial market (false weights — Deu 25:16; Pro 11:1; Pro 20:10; 20:23 — VCG-01), the judicial court (Pro 17:15 — VCG-01 — perverted judgment), and the worship/ritual context (Pro 15:8; 21:27; 28:9; Isa 1:13 — VCG-03). These settings reveal the characteristic as operative across all the practical domains of daily life (commerce, justice, worship), not confined to religious or ritual contexts. (2) Covenantal-prophetic address (Jeremiah, Ezekiel — VCG-04): the covenant community's communal moral state addressed by the prophets — the conscience of Israel collectively is the concern. (3) Eschatological/cosmic (Revelation — VCG-05): the final-judgment exclusion context. The breadth of contextual settings (commerce to court to worship to covenant community to eschatological) confirms the characteristic as operating across all levels of human moral-relational life.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Three primary contextual settings. (1) Covenantal-legal (Leviticus, Deuteronomy — VCGs 01, 02): the boundary-law context of divine statutes defining Israel's holy distinctness from surrounding nations. The covenantal setting reveals the characteristic as a specifically covenantal-betrayal category. (2) Royal-historical (reform narratives — VCG-03): the political context of kings whose wills shape national covenant fidelity or infidelity. The royal-historical setting reveals the characteristic as having an institutional-political dimension — it is embedded in political structures as much as in individual inner lives.
