(3) Prophetic-judicial (Jeremiah, Ezekiel — VCGs 04, 05): the prophetic confrontation context where accumulated idolatrous abominations reach the threshold requiring divine declaration and judgment. The prophetic-judicial setting reveals the characteristic as the subject of the divine legal case against the covenant community.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Four primary settings. (1) Judicial-divine (Psalms of complaint/imprecation — VCG-03): the divine court is the setting in which evildoers are brought before God and their iniquity judged — Psa 94:23 (VCG-03): divine bringing-back of iniquity; Psa 5:5 (VCG-03): God's court before which evildoers cannot stand. (2) Wisdom-instructional (Job, Proverbs — VCGs 02, 04): the classroom and counsel setting where iniquity is named and warned against — Job 4:8; 11:14; 36:10/21 (VCG-04). (3) Prophetic-confrontational (Isaiah, Jeremiah, Micah — VCGs 01, 02, 05): the prophetic oracle setting in which specific communities or rulers are confronted with their iniquity. (4) Personal prayer/lament (Psalms — VCGs 01, 03, 04): the prayer setting where the righteous pray for protection from and release from the influence of evildoers.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Three primary contextual settings. (1) Eschatological judgment setting (Revelation VCG-01): the end-time context of divine plagues falling on an unrepentant humanity under cosmic judgment. This setting reveals the characteristic at maximum intensity — the most extreme possible divine pressure producing the most extreme possible defiant speech. (2) Community-conduct setting (Pauline VCG-02; Petrine VCG-03): the NT church community living as a minority within Gentile society, managing the social testimony of their conduct and the false accusations of hostile neighbours. This setting reveals the characteristic in its social-communal dimension. (3) Judicial-legal setting (VCG-03: Joh 18:30; Act 25:5): formal trial proceedings where false charges are formally delivered. This setting reveals the characteristic's institutional dimension — evil speech institutionalised through legal process.

---

##### T7.2.5 — Does any verse function as the primary anchor for this characteristic — the verse that most fully and directly expresses its essential character?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Psa 36:1 (vc=42567 — VCG-02) is the primary anchor candidate: "Transgression speaks to the wicked deep in his heart; there is no fear of God before his eyes." This verse most directly and simultaneously names: (a) the inner constitutional location of the characteristic (the heart's deepest governance layer); (b) the characteristic's defining inner mechanism (the transgression-voice displacing God-fear); (c) the defining absence that constitutes practical atheism (no fear of God); (d) the inner-governance structure of the settled wicked person (transgression as the ruling voice). No other single verse in the 190V corpus combines all these analytical elements as economically. Pro 21:10 (vc=42554 — VCG-09) is a secondary anchor: "the soul of the wicked desires evil" — the most direct soul-level location statement. Eze 33:11 (vc=42701 — VCG-07) is a tertiary anchor: the divine desire for the wicked to turn, naming the characteristic as a reversible volitional direction.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Mat 12:35 (vc=14420 — VCG-03) is the primary anchor candidate: "The good person out of his good treasure brings forth good, and the evil person out of his evil treasure brings forth evil." This verse simultaneously names: (a) the constitutional-structural condition of the inner person (the evil treasury); (b) the active-generative dynamic (brings forth — ekballō — the person actively draws from and produces); (c) the symmetry between good and evil inner natures as mirror structural conditions; (d) the inevitable output relationship between the constitutional condition and the person's expressions. No other single verse in the corpus so precisely and economically captures the constitutional-generative essence of the characteristic. Mar 7:23 (vc=14422) is a secondary anchor: "All these evil things come from within, and they defile a person" — the most direct inside-origin statement.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Pro 3:32 (vc=1686 — VCG-02) is the primary anchor candidate: "for the devious person is an abomination to the Lord, but the upright are in his confidence." This verse uniquely combines: (a) the inner-character location of the abominable quality (devious — whose inner way is crooked); (b) the relational verdict (abomination to the Lord — divine revulsion); (c) the relational consequence (excluded from divine confidence); and (d) the structural opposite (upright in divine confidence). No other verse in the 40-verse corpus simultaneously names the inner character condition, the divine verdict, the relational consequence, and the opposite in a single antithetical unit. Pro 11:20 (vc=1677 — VCG-01) is the closest secondary anchor: "those of crooked heart are an abomination to the Lord, but those of blameless ways are his delight" — explicitly locating the abomination in the heart and naming the opposite as delight.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Eze 11:21 (vc=1631 — VCG-05) is the primary anchor candidate: "But as for those whose heart goes after their detestable things and their abominations, I will bring their deeds upon their own heads, declares the Lord God." This verse uniquely combines: (a) the constitutional heart-level location ("whose heart goes after"); (b) both primary vocabulary terms in their characteristic register (shiq.quts — detestable things; to.e.vah — abominations); (c) the directional language ("goes after") naming the characteristic's volitional-devotional dimension; and (d) the consequence (deeds returned on their heads). A secondary anchor: Hos 9:10 (vc=1632 — VCG-04): "they became detestable like the thing they loved" — uniquely names the constitutional-transformation consequence of sustained idolatrous attachment.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Psa 36:4 (vc=38235 — VCG-02) is the primary anchor candidate: "He plots trouble while on his bed; he sets himself in a way that is not good; he does not reject evil." This verse uniquely combines: (a) the characteristic's central action (plotting/scheming — the nocturnal premeditation); (b) the constitutional location (the bed — the person's intimate private space, showing scheming as a nocturnal inner habit); (c) the directional commitment (sets himself in a way that is not good — the will's orientation); and (d) the volitional refusal to arrest (does not reject evil — the defining inner stance). No other verse simultaneously names all four elements: the scheming act, its constitutional-temporal location, the directional will-commitment, and the volitional refusal. Secondary anchor: Isa 32:6 (vc=38181 — VCG-02): "his heart is busy with iniquity" — uniquely names the heart's productive busyness as the constitutional location.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Rev 16:9 (vc=14352 — VCG-01) is the primary anchor candidate: "They were scorched by the fierce heat, and they cursed the name of God who had power over these plagues. They did not repent and give him glory." This verse uniquely combines: (a) the maximum-pressure context (divine eschatological judgment); (b) the characteristic's core act (cursed God's name — blasfēmeō as primary verb); (c) the will's constitutive refusal (did not repent); (d) the structural opposite (give him glory — withheld); and (e) the self-reinforcing-under-pressure dynamic (judgment deepens rather than breaks the defiance). Rev 13:6 (vc=14356 — VCG-01) is the secondary anchor: "opened its mouth to utter blasphemies against God, blaspheming his name and his dwelling" — the most concentrated single-verse portrait of sustained cosmic blasphemy.

---

##### T7.2.6 — What does the primary anchor verse reveal that no other verse reveals?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Psa 36:1 reveals uniquely that the wicked person has an inner governance structure in which transgression functions as an active speaking voice within the heart. No other verse in the 190V corpus so directly names wickedness as an inner speech-act — a voice deep in the heart. This reveals that the characteristic operates not merely as a disposition or orientation but as an active inner authority structure: transgression is not merely present in the wicked person but speaks, instructs, and governs. The verse also uniquely pairs the inner voice with the external perceptual consequence: "there is no fear of God before his eyes" — the inner voice of transgression produces an outer perceptual absence of God. This inner-to-outer consequence is uniquely compressed in Psa 36:1's formulation and is not replicated at this density in any other verse of the corpus.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Mat 12:35 (vc=14420 — VCG-03) uniquely reveals: the bi-directional structural symmetry between the constitutionally good person (good treasury → good output) and the constitutionally evil person (evil treasury → evil output). No other verse in the 90-verse corpus explicitly constructs both sides of the constitutional equation simultaneously. This symmetry reveals that CHAR-2 is not merely the absence of the good constitutional condition but its structural mirror opposite — the constitutionally evil person has an inner treasury of evil that is the precise structural parallel of the constitutionally good person's treasury of good. The active verb "brings forth" (ekballō) also uniquely names the characteristic as generatively active — the person draws from the treasury and actively brings evil forth — confirming the characteristic as a producing condition, not merely a deficiency.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Pro 3:32 (vc=1686 — VCG-02) uniquely reveals the relational intimacy dimension of the structural opposite: "the upright are in his confidence" (sod — council, intimate circle). The abomination-verdict produces not merely non-abomination (a neutral state) but its positive polar opposite: intimate access to God's counsel. No other verse in the corpus names the precise positive relational content that is the opposite of being abominable — other antithetical pairs name "delight" (Pro 11:20; 11:1) or "acceptable" (Pro 15:8) but only Pro 3:32 names the intimacy of divine confidence (sod) as the relational state to which uprightness leads. This reveals that abomination's relational consequence (exclusion) is not merely spatial exclusion but the loss of a specific quality of intimate relational access.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Eze 11:21 (vc=1631 — VCG-05) uniquely reveals the heart as the active subject of idolatrous movement — "heart goes after." No other verse in the 99-verse corpus so precisely names the heart's directional faculty as the agent that actively pursues the detestable things. The phrase "heart goes after" captures both the inner-being location (heart) and the active-directional movement (going after) — showing that idolatrous abomination is not a passive state but an active pursuit of the inner faculty. The verse also uniquely pairs both primary vocabulary terms (shiq.quts and to.e.vah) in a single verse, connecting the detestable-object dimension and the abomination-verdict dimension in a single statement of the characteristic's constitutive elements. The judgment statement ("bring their deeds upon their own heads") further shows the verse's comprehensive scope: inner condition → named objects → divine verdict → consequence.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Psa 36:4 (vc=38235 — VCG-02) uniquely reveals the temporal-spatial location of the characteristic's scheming: the bed, at night. No other verse in the 79-verse corpus situates the scheming with such specificity: the bed is the place of rest, intimacy, and private thought — the iniquity-schemer turns the restorative space of the night into a workshop for devising harm. The bed-scheming shows the characteristic as not merely a public or professional failing but as constitutive of the person's most private hours — the inner life at its most unguarded is occupied with iniquitous planning. This temporal-spatial specificity (bed-at-night) is the unique revelation of the primary anchor verse: iniquity penetrates even the private restorative spaces of the inner life.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Rev 16:9 (vc=14352 — VCG-01) uniquely reveals the self-reinforcing-under-pressure dynamic: the characteristic is not merely resistant to divine pressure but intensifies under it. Scorching divine judgment → more defiant cursing. This dynamic is not evidenced by any other verse in the corpus: the other VCG-01 verses (Jude 8/10) show the characteristic's inner preconditions; the other Rev 16 verses (16:11/21) confirm the pattern; but only Rev 16:9 presents the initial moment of the characteristic's triggered expression under judgment. The verse uniquely reveals that divine judgment is not merely the context of the blasphemy but the specific trigger that activates it — the characteristic uses divine judgment as its occasion for expression rather than as a corrective that arrests it.

---

#### T7.3 — Human Science Frameworks

##### T7.3.1 — Which human science framework (psychology, moral philosophy, developmental psychology, sociology, anthropology, or other) is most useful as an interpretive lens for this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Moral psychology — specifically the study of moral character, character formation, and moral identity — is the most useful framework. The characteristic is defined as a settled person-identity organised around wickedness, which maps directly onto the moral-psychology domain of character as a stable dispositional structure that shapes perception, cognition, motivation, and behaviour across contexts. Secondary frameworks: developmental psychology's work on character formation and deformation (the characteristic is progressive and formative — T5.2.1), and clinical psychology's understanding of dark-triad personality patterns (narcissism, psychopathy, Machiavellianism — which parallel some of the characteristic's constitutive elements: pro-21:4 pride, Psa 37:12 predatory plotting, Pro 12:5 deceptive counsel). Social-moral philosophy's concept of evil as a character-orientation (Aristotle's concept of the vicious person — hexis kakia) is also relevant to the Hebrew understanding of ra.sha as a stable inner orientation (hexis/disposition) toward wickedness.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Theological anthropology and personality psychology (specifically the concept of deep character structures or character traits) are the most useful frameworks. The constitutional-structural framing of CHAR-2 (the diseased tree whose nature determines its fruit — Mat 7:17-18) maps onto personality psychology's concept of character as a stable dispositional structure that shapes behaviour across contexts — what Paul Costa and Robert McCrae's five-factor model would call the trait-level of personality, or what virtue ethics (Aristotle's hexis) would call habituated character. More specifically, the NT's analysis of the evil treasury in the heart (Mat 12:35) maps onto depth psychology's concept of the unconscious as a reservoir from which mental contents are drawn — the heart-treasury operates below the level of conscious deliberate choice, shaping what the person "brings forth" as natural output. Object relations theory (Melanie Klein) is also relevant: the constitutional inner evil with its hostile-suspicious cognitive outputs (1Ti 6:4 — VCG-06) and the community expulsion dynamics (1Cor 5:13 — VCG-04) parallel the object-relations analysis of internal bad objects shaping relational dynamics.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Moral psychology and emotion science — specifically the psychology of disgust and moral condemnation — are the most useful frameworks. The characteristic is constitutively affective-relational: it names divine revulsion (an emotion-analogue) in response to specific moral violations. The contemporary psychology of disgust (Paul Rozin, Jonathan Haidt) is highly relevant: disgust is the emotion characterised by a specific sensory-revolting quality (nausea, repulsion), a motivation to expel or distance oneself from the disgusting object, and a judgment of the disgusting object as contaminated or polluted. The Greek bdelugma's derivation from bdeo (to stink) maps directly onto disgust psychology's oral-sensory-disgust origin. The OT to.e.vah's relational (to the Lord) framing maps onto moral disgust — the disgust response directed at moral violations rather than sensory contaminants. Moral foundations theory (Haidt) identifies disgust/purity as one of six moral foundations — CHAR-3 is the biblical expression of the purity/sanctity moral foundation.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Attachment theory (psychology) and the anthropology of religion are the most useful frameworks. Attachment theory: the characteristic's core dynamic — the heart going after idol-objects (Eze 11:21 — VCG-05), the soul delighting in them (Isa 66:3 — VCG-04), and the constitutional transformation toward the image of what is loved (Hos 9:10 — VCG-04) — maps precisely onto attachment theory's understanding of how devoted relational orientation shapes the attached person. Idolatrous abomination is a form of misattachment: the devotion-capacity attached to an object incapable of the reciprocal relational fulfillment it was designed for. The anthropology of religion: scholars of religion (e.g. Jonathan Smith, William Robertson Smith) have extensively studied the logic of sacred boundaries and the pollution/purity dynamics in ancient Near Eastern religion — shiq.quts as the detestable idol-object belongs to this purity/boundary-violation register that comparative religion documents widely.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Moral psychology (particularly research on moral disengagement and self-justification) and cognitive science of planning/scheming are the most useful frameworks. Moral disengagement (Albert Bandura): the theory that harmful actors deploy specific cognitive mechanisms to disengage their moral standards from their harmful conduct — justifying harm, blaming victims, displacing responsibility — maps directly onto the characteristic's conscience-bypassing features (Pro 30:20 — VCG-04: "I have done no wrong"; Psa 14:4 — VCG-03: "no knowledge"). The planned evil (Mic 2:1 — VCG-02; Psa 36:4 — VCG-02) with its nocturnal devising followed by dawn execution maps onto cognitive science's analysis of premeditated harmful behaviour — the cognitive-planning phase that distinguishes premeditated from impulsive harm.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Social psychology of reactance (Jack Brehm) and the psychology of moral disengagement (Bandura) are the most useful frameworks. Psychological reactance theory: reactance is the motivational state that occurs when a person perceives their freedom as threatened or eliminated — the response is to assert the threatened freedom more strongly, including through oppositional behaviour. The Rev 16 sequence (vc=14352; 14350; 14353 — VCG-01) maps directly onto reactance: divine judgment → perceived threat to autonomy → defiant assertion of anti-God stance through blasphemous speech. The more severe the judgment, the more intense the reactance (Rev 16:21: "because the plague was so severe" → more cursing). Moral disengagement (Bandura) also applies to the false-accusation register (VCG-03): the accusers disengage from moral consideration of the accused's actual character through dehumanising labelling (kakopoios — evildoer).

---

##### T7.3.2 — Where the human science framework illuminates the verse evidence — making a finding more coherent or complete — what does it reveal?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

Moral psychology's concept of moral disengagement illuminates Psa 36:1 and the practical-atheism cluster (VCG-02): the mechanism by which the wicked person excludes God from their thought-life (Psa 10:4 — "all his thoughts are 'There is no God'") parallels the psychological mechanism of moral disengagement — the cognitive strategy by which persons neutralise the moral restraints that would otherwise constrain harmful behaviour (Bandura's framework). The progressive perceptive blindness documented in Pro 4:19 and Isa 26:10 is illuminated by moral psychology's evidence that habituated moral disengagement progressively reduces the person's capacity to perceive and respond to moral information. Character-formation theory illuminates the progressive consolidation sequence (T5.2.1) — the Psa 1:1 walk-stand-sit progression is a character-formation sequence in which each stage deepens the orientation.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

Character-trait psychology illuminates the constitutional-baseline claim (Mat 7:11 — VCG-02: "you who are evil") as analogous to the empirical finding that deep character structures are stable across time and contexts — the constitutional evil is not situationally triggered but context-invariant, exactly as character traits are. The tree-nature metaphor (Mat 7:17-18 — VCG-02) is illuminated by character research showing that attempting to change surface behaviour without addressing deep character structure produces temporary change at best. The progressive-deterioration dynamic (2Ti 3:13 — VCG-06 — "from bad to worse") is illuminated by personality psychology's finding that character consolidates over time through reinforcement — the evil constitutional condition deepens through its own exercise. The heart-treasury's inside-out model (Mat 12:34-35 — VCG-03) is illuminated by depth psychology's concept of the unconscious as generative of conscious output.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

Disgust psychology illuminates the characteristic at several points. (1) The antithetical pairing of abomination with "delight" (Pro 11:1; 11:20 — VCGs 01/02) is illuminated by the psychology of disgust's finding that disgust and delight are polar opposites operating through the same evaluative system — what disgusts occupies the negative pole of the same dimension as what delights. (2) The social-contamination aspect (Ezr 9:11 — VCG-04: abominations filling the land) is illuminated by disgust psychology's finding that disgust involves a contagion-sensitivity — the disgusting thing spreads its contaminating quality to what it contacts. (3) Jer 6:15 and 8:12 (VCG-04 — no shame or blushing) are illuminated by the psychology of shame suppression: sustained commission of morally disgusting acts can desensitise the shame response, eventually rendering it non-functional.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

Attachment theory illuminates: (1) Hos 9:10 (VCG-04): "became detestable like the thing they loved" — attachment theory documents that sustained devoted attachment to an object shapes the attached person toward the image of what they attend to; the biblical text articulates a specific negative instance of this general principle; (2) the visual-desire loop (Eze 20:7-8 — VCG-05: eyes feasting on detestable things) — attachment theory's analysis of how sustained visual attention reinforces and deepens attachment is confirmed by the biblical evidence; (3) the difficulty of departure (Eze 20:8 — VCG-05: unwilling to cast away) — attachment theory's evidence that secure attachment (even misdirected) is difficult to relinquish without a stronger alternative attachment offers illumination.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

Moral disengagement theory illuminates: (1) Pro 30:20 (VCG-04): "I have done no wrong" — Bandura's mechanism of "moral justification" or "advantageous comparison" is the cognitive process through which the person reclassifies their iniquitous act as acceptable or even positive. The verse names the terminus of this process; (2) Psa 14:4 (VCG-03): "no knowledge" among evildoers — moral disengagement produces genuine cognitive blindness to the moral dimension of one's acts; (3) the nocturnal plotting (Psa 36:4 — VCG-02; Mic 2:1 — VCG-02) — cognitive science of criminal planning documents that premeditation involves emotional distancing from the anticipated victim, which matches the impersonal, predatory character of the scheming.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Reactance theory illuminates VCG-01 at multiple points. Rev 16:9 (VCG-01): the scorching judgment functions as a coercive threat to autonomy → the reactance response is defiant cursing of the source of the threat (God). Rev 16:21 (VCG-01): "because the plague was so severe" → the severity of the perceived coercive threat intensifies the reactance response (more cursing) — precisely what reactance theory predicts: stronger coercion produces stronger reactance assertion of the threatened freedom. Jude 10 (vc=14355 — VCG-01): contemptuous blasphemy of what is not understood — moral disengagement through ignorance-contempt: the person disengages morally from what they do not comprehend by treating it with contempt rather than acknowledgment. The framework also illuminates Joh 18:30 (VCG-03): the false accusers disengage morally from honest evaluation of Jesus through the dehumanising label kakopoios (evildoer).

---

##### T7.3.3 — Where the verse evidence and the human science framework diverge, what does the divergence reveal?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The most significant divergence: the verse evidence treats the wicked person's inner orientation as both volitionally chosen and morally accountable (Eze 18:20-27 — personal wickedness "upon himself"; the forensic-verdict VCG-01 — God will not acquit the wicked). Human science frameworks for similar inner patterns (dark triad personality; moral disengagement) tend toward explanatory frameworks that reduce moral accountability — the dark-triad patterns are partially attributed to early developmental factors and neurobiological profiles, which mitigates the sharp personal-moral-accountability claim of the verse evidence. The divergence reveals that the verse evidence operates with a non-reductionist anthropology: the wicked person is fully accountable because they are volitionally constituted as the wicked person (Eze 18:20 — "the wickedness of the wicked shall be upon himself"). The scientific framework's tendency toward mitigating accountability is in tension with the evidence's consistent affirmation of personal moral responsibility.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The most significant divergence: the verse evidence presents the constitutional inner evil as the universal baseline of human nature (Mat 7:11: "you who are evil" addressed universally to human hearers), while personality psychology presents character as variable — some persons have more trait-aligned character structures than others; no personality model designates all humans as constitutionally evil. The verse evidence's universalist claim (all humans are constitutionally evil, not merely some) diverges from the empirical observation that persons vary enormously in their moral character quality. This divergence reveals the verse evidence's theological-anthropological commitment to a post-creation fall-condition that is universally human — the constitutional evil is not a trait variation but a species-wide structural condition. The science framework cannot account for or confirm the universalist theological claim; the theological claim operates at a different analytical level.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The most significant divergence: the human science framework (Haidt's moral foundations theory) treats the purity/sanctity foundation as one cultural variable among six — different cultures weight the disgust/purity foundation differently, and many contemporary Western moral frameworks consider this foundation as less morally fundamental than harm or fairness. The verse evidence presents the divine abomination verdict as absolute and non-culturally-relative: Pro 16:5 (vc=1689 — VCG-02) — "everyone who is arrogant in heart is an abomination to the Lord; be assured, he will not go unpunished" — the verdict is not culturally contingent. This divergence reveals the characteristic as operating on a different plane than cultural moral psychology: it names not what humans find disgusting (which varies culturally) but what God finds abominable (which is presented as absolute and invariant). The disgust-science framework is a useful illuminating lens but cannot account for the absolute-divine character of the verdict.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The most significant divergence: attachment theory treats all secure attachments as developmentally appropriate and beneficial within their contexts — it does not categorically judge attachment to objects as wrong. The verse evidence presents idolatrous attachment to non-divine objects as categorically abominable — not because attachment per se is wrong but because the devotion-capacity is designed for God and is constitutively injured by attachment to what is not God. This divergence reveals the characteristic as operating within a theological anthropology that has a specific telos for the devotion-capacity: it was made for God. No attachment to any created object can fulfil this telos; all such attachment is therefore constitutively misdirected, whatever its psychological qualities. The theological claim (the devotion-capacity has a specific object it was created for) cannot be derived from the human science framework and represents the evidence's most distinctive contribution.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The most significant divergence: moral disengagement theory treats the mechanisms as universal cognitive-psychological processes applicable to all humans under certain conditions. The verse evidence presents iniquity as a volitional, morally culpable choice: Job 36:21 (vc=38216 — VCG-04): "this you have chosen rather than affliction" — the iniquity-schemer chose their path; God holds them accountable. The human science framework cannot ground the accountability dimension — it explains the mechanism but not the culpability. The verse evidence also presents God's active hatred of evildoers (Psa 5:5 — VCG-03) as a morally serious relational response that has no parallel in psychological frameworks which treat harmful behaviour as a problem to be explained rather than as an offence against a morally serious agent. The divergence reveals the characteristic as operating within a moral-theological anthropology that includes genuine culpability and divine-relational consequence — dimensions beyond the psychological framework's scope.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

The most significant divergence: reactance theory treats the defiant autonomy-assertion as a universal and value-neutral psychological response to perceived freedom-threat — it does not make moral judgments about whether the reactance is justified or unjustified. The verse evidence presents the blasphemous defiance as absolutely unjustified and morally culpable: Rom 3:8 (vc=14358 — VCG-02): "their condemnation is just" — the justness of condemnation presupposes moral culpability. The reactance framework explains the psychological mechanism (why defiance intensifies under pressure) but cannot explain why the defiance is morally wrong or why the pressure (divine judgment) is legitimate. The verse evidence's theological claim — that divine judgment is morally warranted and that defiance in the face of it is culpable — is beyond the framework's scope. The divergence reveals the characteristic as requiring a theological-moral anthropology that the psychological framework cannot supply.

---

##### T7.3.4 — Does the human science framework surface any aspect of this characteristic that the verse evidence has not yet addressed — and does that absence require further verse investigation?

**[CHAR-1] Wickedness as settled person-identity** (E)

The human science framework surfaces the question of early developmental origins of the wicked character — specifically, what environmental, relational, or neurobiological factors contribute to the formation of this inner orientation in a human being. The verse evidence is largely silent on developmental origins (T2.9.1 — the characteristic is presented as internally generated from within the person's volitional choices, not as environmentally determined). The science extract (Section 3 — Evil/Wickedness) would address this gap; the verse evidence alone does not elaborate on developmental-psychological pathways into the wicked person's characteristic. This is not a gap that requires further verse investigation (the verse evidence is not addressing this question), but it is an aspect of the human science domain that enriches understanding of how the characteristic comes to be settled in a person's inner life.

  → PASS. Writing final Self-check.

**[CHAR-2] Evil as constitutional inner nature** (E)

The human science framework surfaces the question of the developmental origins of the constitutional evil condition in individual human lives — specifically, how early relational and environmental experiences contribute to the formation of the "evil inner treasury" in a given person's heart. The verse evidence treats the constitutional evil as the universal starting condition without addressing the developmental-psychological pathways through which it is shaped or intensified in individual cases. Developmental psychology's evidence that early attachment experiences, parenting environments, and developmental trauma significantly shape the person's inner character architecture is not directly addressed in the 90-verse corpus. This is not a gap requiring further verse investigation (the verse evidence is making a theological-anthropological claim at the species level, not a developmental claim at the individual level) but it is an aspect of the human-developmental picture that enriches understanding of how the constitutional condition manifests with varying intensity in different persons.

**[CHAR-3] Abomination — divine revulsion on moral character** (E)

The disgust psychology framework surfaces the question of how the disgust response relates to in-group/out-group dynamics. Disgust psychology research shows that disgust is often activated most strongly against perceived in-group violations (violations by members of one's own moral community are felt as more disgusting than violations by out-group members). The verse evidence shows a strong covenantal-community dimension (Eze 44:6-7; Mal 2:11 — VCG-04 — Israel's own abominations addressed by the prophets), consistent with this pattern — the most intense prophetic concern is for abominations within the covenant community. However, the characteristic also applies universally (Deu 25:16 — all who act dishonestly; Pro 29:27 — the unjust person as abomination to the righteous generally). The science framework surfaces the in-group/out-group dimension as a potentially interesting analytical question, but the verse evidence's universal scope limits how far that framework applies. No further verse investigation is required.

**[CHAR-4] Idolatrous abomination** (E)

The attachment theory framework surfaces the question of how early developmental attachment experiences shape the later capacity for idolatrous versus covenant devotion. The verse evidence addresses the characteristic primarily at the adult community level (Israel's communal idolatrous attachment) rather than at the developmental level of how the devotion-capacity is formed in individuals across their life-history. The developmental question — what early relational experiences make a person's devotion-capacity more vulnerable to idolatrous misdirection — is not addressed in the 99-verse corpus. This is not a gap requiring further verse investigation (the corpus is making a prophetic-covenantal claim, not a developmental-psychological one) but it is an aspect of the human-science picture that enriches understanding of individual variation within the communal idolatrous pattern.

**[CHAR-5] Iniquity as active inner scheming and evil generation** (E)

The moral disengagement framework surfaces the question of which specific disengagement mechanisms are most operative in iniquity-as-scheming. The verse evidence describes the terminus (no knowledge — Psa 14:4; "I have done no wrong" — Pro 30:20) and the practices (nocturnal devising, deceptive speech) but does not enumerate the specific cognitive steps by which moral disengagement occurs. Bandura's taxonomy (moral justification, euphemistic labelling, victim attribution, dehumanisation, etc.) provides a more granular analysis of the cognitive pathway than the biblical evidence offers. This is a surface-but-not-address aspect: the disengagement mechanisms are operative in the evidence (their effects are documented) but their step-by-step cognitive architecture is not described in the verse evidence. No further verse investigation is required — this is a genuine gap between the level of analysis the evidence provides and the level the psychological framework analyses at.

**[CHAR-6] Evil expressed through speech** (E)

Reactance theory surfaces the question of how the blasphemer's sense of threatened autonomy develops prior to the Rev 16 judgment events — what earlier experiences of divine authority as constraining produced the pre-formed reactance that then explodes into blasphemy under judgment. The Jude 8 sequence (VCG-01: sensory self-indulgence → authority-rejection → blasphemy) provides a partial answer, but the prior formation of the reactance-prone inner posture is not fully addressed in the 17-verse corpus. This is a surface-but-not-address aspect: the pre-formation of the defiant inner posture is implied (Jude 8 — VCG-01) but the developmental psychology of how authority-rejection forms over time is not detailed. No further verse investigation is required — the corpus's level of analysis is prophetic-theological, not developmental-psychological.
